## 3807

3807

By the grace of Hashem, Days of Selichos, 5715
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, R' Boruch, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 25th of Elul, with the enclosure.

1) Regarding the Megillah: Our custom, according to the instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, is to shake the Megillah twice while reciting "the [Megillah] scroll" and "this second scroll of Purim." (In the *Hayom Yom*, the word "this" was omitted, and this has been corrected in the *Likkutei Minhagim* at the end of the list of Esther printed by Kehot.)

2) Regarding my note on the wall calendar of the Kollel, where I wrote that "v'kasveinu b'sefer" is an error: My intention was that it is one of two things: a) Either the word "hachayim" must also be included, as is written in *Ketzos HaShulchan*, chapter 21, paragraph 4; or b) that it is sufficient to say only the word "v'kasveinu." This is also the implication in *Derech HaChaim*, and it is the simple logical conclusion.

3) Thank you for your notes regarding the text "aptenu" or "artzenu."

4) Regarding the notes on the vocalization of the *piyutim* in the Machzor for Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur: There is much to be checked in this vocalization. It appears that there are many errors due to mistakes by the typesetter who went over them without paying attention. Once an error has been made, it persists, and it is a pity that for the time being there is no expert to attend to this.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all who are yours: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings.

Regarding my addition in Mincha of Rosh Hashanah of the word "Shabbos": It is correct that my intention was to exclude a fast day, since we read a Haftorah then. This is simple.

Regarding your comment on the *piyut* of Neilah, "Anu l'Hashem v'eineinu l'Hashem," from *Sukkah* 53b: It is a mitzvah to find a justification for the established text. It can be said that this is why they changed the text from the language of the Mishnah there, and placed the word "v'eineinu" first, to create a break and indicate that it is a different matter. It can also be said that a congregation is different (see *Bach* in *Orach Chaim*, chapter 61; *Pri Megadim* and *Machatzis HaShekel* there, ad loc., *Magen Avraham*, subsection 9). I have since seen it noted that this is discussed in *Responsa She'eilas Shalom*, second edition. I do not have it at hand.

## 3808

3808

B"H, Days of Selichos, 5715
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished R' Alter Moshe, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

...In response to the comments in your letter:

1) Regarding what you wrote concerning the *Luach Kolel* on the matter of *Vayechal* and *Aneinu* — this is indeed the halachic ruling of the Tzemach Tzedek (Responsa *Shaar HaMiluim*, section 8; see also his ruling in *Orach Chaim*, section 566; Responsa *Chasam Sofer*, *Orach Chaim*, section 157; *Maharam Schick*, section 289; *Sdei Chemed*, *Pe'as HaSadeh*, *Asifat Dinim*, *Ma'areches Beis HaMikdash*, section 2, subsection 3, as I noted all of this in *Yalkutei Minhagim* printed at the end of the *Eicha* list, from where this instruction was copied into the *Luach*. The *Luach* is not a place for citing sources). One may also note the Responsa *Tzafnas Paneach* by the Rogatchover Gaon, Part 2, section 31.

2) Regarding reciting *Mashiv HaRuach* during Shacharis even after having heard the announcement (in my opinion, this applies only if one is not davening in another minyan, contrary to the doubt raised in *Biur Halacha*; but this is not the place to elaborate) — this is also the ruling in Responsa *She'ilas Shalom*, Second Edition, end of section 197, based on the Yerushalmi, concluding: "This is simple and clear." The *Biur Halacha* evidently did not see the aforementioned sefer, as he did not mention it.

3) On Erev Shabbos Chanukah, one must have enough oil to burn for at least a half-hour after sunset — this is as stated in the *Luach*.

I would like to know what difficulty you find in this.

4) Regarding why we do not finish the verse in *Devarim* (9:7) when reciting the *Zechiros* — it can be said that this is to minimize the disparagement of Yisrael, similar to what is written in Responsa *Chasam Sofer*, *Orach Chaim*, section 10. Yet, the difficulty remains regarding the *Zechirah* of *Matan Torah*.

It seems clear that the answer is like that of Responsa *Maharam Schick*, *Orach Chaim*, section 124: it is different in such a case, as the intention is not to read a verse or a passage, but rather to recall a concept, and one is merely utilizing the elegance of the scriptural phrasing, similar to what the *Magen Avraham* writes at the beginning of section 282, and in *Yoreh Deah* 284 regarding *sirtut* (scoring lines for writing).

5) Inserting the thread into the hole from the side — regarding *Tallis Gadol*, the Alter Rebbe writes in his *Siddur*: "After he has made the upper knot properly."

6) Regarding what you noted in the aforementioned matter concerning clarifying the length and width — see the halachic ruling of the Tzemach Tzedek in *Orach Chaim*, section 11.

3809

4 Tishrei, 5716
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

Although I receive news about you from time to time, I was pleased to receive your letter now. However, it is understood that I am not satisfied with the state of mind reflected in it—namely, your despondency over the fact that, in your opinion, you do not see the fruits of your toil and labor among the youth.

While it is understood that complete satisfaction on the part of an activist and worker does not necessarily lead to the best results—as it is liable to weaken one’s energy, since the *yetzer* tempts him to say, "You have done enough and succeeded; now let others come and continue"—the other extreme, that is, a feeling of despair and even strong despondency, has results that are undesirable and even more harmful than the results of the first extreme, because the slackening caused by it is much greater.

Regarding the substance of the matter—that the youth into whom you have invested so much labor are nevertheless being swept away by the secular tide—it is a firm principle that effort does not return **empty**, even if it does not always succeed to the extent one aspires and hopes for. Furthermore, very often the results are seen only after time, for many reasons. Frequently, it is delayed until the educated and influenced individual settles into family life; at that point, he is not subject to as many changes, he takes into account his entire past and his present situation, and then the period in which he received influence from a certain person in a certain place enters into this calculation and can tip the scales toward the good.

Moreover, consider the story of Rabbi Akiva, one of the greatest *Tanna'im* and a pillar of our *Torah Shebaal Peh*. Our Sages tell us that for forty years he was a teacher, an influencer, an educator, and a leader, and he had twenty-four thousand students—students on his own level, meaning that given their level of knowledge and character, their teacher and *mashpia* needed to be a person of Rabbi Akiva’s stature. For a certain reason, they all died, *Rachmana litzlan*, and the *Torah* was in danger of being forgotten from Israel. Yet, Rabbi Akiva established five students, and they restored the entire *Torah Shebaal Peh* and disseminated it among Israel in their time and generation, and it was handed down from generation to generation until it reached us, our children, and our children’s children forever.

It is simple that our *Torah* is not merely a book of stories, but rather *Torah* in the literal sense—a word meaning instruction (*hora'ah*)—where every matter within it teaches and provides guidance for every individual. In particular, the aforementioned story is a living example that a person must utilize his talents to the fullest extent possible. Any phenomenon he encounters in this work should not be allowed to cause him any lowering of spirit. Even if it is, *chas v’shalom*, as described above—where the labor of several years seems to the eyes of flesh to have been lost in vain—he must continue his holy work with energy and joy. In the end, he will certainly succeed. Even if it is possible, as mentioned above, that he did not succeed with a large number or they did not bear fruit, he will succeed with a small quantity with an extraordinary success that will fill all the lack and satisfy him for all the labor he has labored. As the verse cited by our Sages in the aforementioned story says: "In the morning sow your seed, and in the evening do not withhold your hand, for you do not know which will succeed."

Certainly, a feeling of bitterness should be aroused over every individual who deviates from the straight path, the path of *Torah* and *mitzvos*, even if this deviation is only for a few days and in minor matters, for every single moment is precious and every single action is of great value. This feeling of bitterness should especially be present in the educator and *mashpia*. However, the conclusions to be drawn from this bitterness are that one must certainly add courage to the work he has done until now, to improve it and complete it. For the general rule is: there is nothing that stands before the will. This applies not only regarding new students and new people to influence, but also regarding those in whom his influence is not yet visible, or is hidden from the eyes of flesh—and even with greater intensity.

One must also take into account that the path of compromise does not succeed in general, and especially among the youth. Their argument is simple: if it is possible to make a compromise for a third or a fourth, it is also possible to increase it and make a compromise for half or more. Furthermore, if a matter can tolerate compromises, that itself is proof that it is not the truth. For the ways of falsehood are many, but the way of truth is **one**. Although one sees that it is impossible to transform a student all at once and make him a complete person, and that change is possible only slowly and from the easy to the difficult, nevertheless, at the time of the outreach itself, the explanation must be clear: the things demanded of him are not **everything**, and they do not exhaust the perfection, for every individual is obligated in all 613 *mitzvos*. It is just that, considering his situation, one begins with him in such-and-such a matter, since he is not yet capable of receiving everything at once. Furthermore, the truth does not tolerate duality. Regarding our people, one nation in the land, any duality is far from it, even if for a short period it is accepted for various reasons. Just as we have only one *Elokus*, so too we have only one *Torah*, which is holy—just as in the first commandment, "I am the L-rd your G-d," so too in **all** the other letters and words from its beginning to its end. One should not fear that the youth will not accept this, for we see the opposite in practice: it is precisely the revealed truth, without compromises, that is accepted by them, even if in their practical lives they have not yet reached the level to withstand all the trials encountered in human life.

The central point of all the above lengthiness is that every individual who possesses influence, especially in the field of proper education, must work with all his energy and ability in this holy work. Although he is forbidden to give up even on the worst of his students, he is also forbidden to slacken his hands from his work—the work of Heaven—if he sees a lack of success in his labor. In the end, words that come from the heart enter the heart, and in the course of time, he will see good fruit from his labor.

It is understood that if in all human affairs one needs help from Heaven, all the more so in the work of education, where the forces opposing Hashem and His *Torah* fight against this with all means and methods. To add to the help from Heaven, one must strive through the perfection of oneself and in one's own matters. This matter, in its simple sense in daily life, is consistent with our *Torah*, the *Torah* of life and its *mitzvos*, and this is not a contradiction to working with others; on the contrary, one assists the other.

It will gladden me if I receive a letter with news from you that you are continuing your work with the desired influence in your circle and environment—influence in the spirit of *Yisrael Saba* with energy that grows from time to time. My hope is strong that after not a long time, you will also be able to bring tidings that fruits are seen in your work.

In these days of the beginning of this year, I wish to offer, in the accepted and traditional formula, a good and sweet year, a year of success in personal matters and success in the desired direction in your work in general matters. My thanks are offered in advance if you will convey these wishes to those you influence and your students, especially those who visited with you.

With blessing.

## 3410

B"H, 4 Tishrei, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the Fast of the Seventh [Month]—may it soon be transformed in our days into joy and gladness—as you requested, I will mention you for the opening of the heart and the opening of the mind. The advice given for such matters is already known, based on the words of our Sages, of blessed memory, that the measure of Hashem is "measure for measure." When one influences another to open their mind and heart to the study of our holy Torah—and especially the inner dimension of the Torah, the *ilana d'chaye* (tree of life)—then, in that same measure, it is measured out to him. Furthermore, many times over, he is influenced with what he himself needs in these very areas, in addition to the fact that "the reward of a mitzvah is a mitzvah," and "one mitzvah leads to another." May it be the will of Hashem that you bring good news regarding this soon.

Enclosed is a general letter which I am sure will interest you, as well as an English translation so that, if you see fit, you may show it to your dear children, may they live. May Hashem grant you success in bringing good news in this as well.

With the blessing of *Chasimah v’Gmar Chasimah Tovah*.

## 3111

B"H, 4 Tishrei, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the teachers of the Beis Rivkah school in Kfar Chabad, may they live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 27 Elul... I have a strong hope that, just as you write, you will continue to gather strength in the education of the students of the institution, until its positive influence in the spirit of the *Yisrael Saba* is evident even outside its walls, as is fitting for daughters of Israel. There is nothing that can stand before the will, especially since we are currently in the days regarding which it is said, "Seek Hashem **when He is found**, call upon Him **when He is near**," a time when every request for help from Hashem Yisbarach and every *tefillah* is more readily accepted and achieves its effect. May it be His will that you bring good tidings regarding all of this very soon.

With a blessing for a *chasimah v'gmar chasimah tovah* for each and every one of you, and for outstanding success in your work—the work of Heaven, which is the matter of pure and holy education—through which you also fulfill your inner purpose, in the language of the *Mishnah*: "I was created to serve my Maker."

And with a blessing for good news.

## 3412

B"H, 6 Tishrei, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the G-d-fearing, honorable, and distinguished man, a man of energy and character, a man of many accomplishments in Torah and its mitzvos, R' Yitzchak Meir, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive the news that the well-known matter in the shul and beis medrash has been rectified, and even before the start of the year—the days when a large congregation gathers there. This adds to the inherent value of the rectification itself, as it also involves the matter of publicly strengthening Yiddishkeit, which is a form of Kiddush Hashem. As is well known, precisely in matters that the masses treat lightly, one’s conduct according to Torah must not involve entering into compromises (despite the various and strange arguments that this is the only way to draw hearts of people distant from pure Yiddishkeit). On the contrary, one must explain the matter as it is and add a safeguard. As the Sages of blessed memory taught in a few words, showing the path for anyone to whom the word of Hashem is precious: "He found a breach—and he built a fence in it." If one sees that mitzvos are being treated lightly, one must, on the contrary, add a fence. And this applies not only to the most severe prohibitions punishable by stoning (Eruvin 6a), and not only to a prohibition that is a novelty and whose entire essence is not accepted (Chullin 111a), but even to a rabbinic prohibition (Eruvin 100b).

May it be the will of Hashem that for many more years you will succeed in mending breaches and strengthening the house of Israel, especially among the younger generation, the future of the people.

Although, to my regret, rumors have reached me that there is less interest in activities among the youth than in previous years. I would be happy to learn that this rumor is baseless, or at least that it was merely a passing matter, and that you are continuing to increase your energy in influencing the youth to instill in them a pure fear of Heaven. May it be the will of Hashem that in time you will also instill in them a spirit of joy in the service of Hashem, as emphasized by the Baal Shem Tov regarding the verse "Serve Hashem with joy," which is a definitive halacha in the Rambam at the end of Hilchos Lulav.

With respect and a blessing for success in the above, and with a blessing for a *chasimah v’gmar chasimah tovah*.

## 3333

B”H, 7 Tishrei, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Rosh Hashanah, in which you complain about your state of sadness and bitterness, and that you despair many times, etc., etc.

It is surely unnecessary to elaborate on the fact that despair is one of the stratagems and ruses of the Yetzer Hara, which seeks to incite and lead him astray, Heaven forbid, from serving his Creator. And if, regarding laziness and heaviness, our Alter Rebbe says (Tanya, Chapter 26) that one should overcome them easily and they will fall, etc., then all the more so is this true regarding despair, Heaven forbid.

And although it is understood that one must fight against bad habits as much as possible, on the other hand, despair and its derivatives are forbidden by the Torah. It is also understood through human reason that there is no cause for despair, as is explained in many places, among them Tanya, Chapter 27 and onwards—please study it there. You should divert your mind from such thoughts, which do not add anything at all to the avodah of Torah and mitzvos, and fight the war of Hashem, as is explained in Tanya there. Just as in the conquest of the Land in the literal sense it is said, "Little by little I will drive them out," so too is the matter in spirituality. We have been promised that, in the end, we will win the war, especially those who have merited to taste the teachings, guidance, and customs of Chassidus. Any thought that one does not belong to such avodah, etc., is the opposite of sound reason, and essentially the opposite of the instructions and commandments of our Torah, the Torah of life.

... With blessings for persistence in your studies in Nigleh and Chassidus, and in the avodah of tefillah, and to fulfill through this the commandment of the Ribono shel Olam, "Serve Hashem with joy," and for a good sealing and final sealing.

With blessings.

P.S.
I trust you are keeping the three daily shiurim that are equal for every soul, established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in the Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, as is well known.

## 3414

B"H, 7 Tishrei, 5716
Brooklyn.

Bas Sheva, may she live,

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter from Erev Rosh Hashanah, in which you ask how you can effectively exert influence in your environment to increase Yiddishkeit, Torah, and mitzvos.

It is surprising that you even ask this, for just as you surely feel that you are influenced by your friends—and as every person is influenced by their environment, in the words of our Sages, "Many are the companions one makes"—then how much more so can propaganda regarding Torah, mitzvos, and the inner dimension of Torah and its soul—which is the teachings, guidance, and customs of Chassidus—penetrate and influence many times over, for the measure of good is greater.

There are two general points to this outreach:

1) That you yourself serve as a living example in your conduct and affairs of what a daughter from a Chassidic home is.

2) Through explaining, in terms suited to their understanding, matters of Chassidus and Chassidic stories—of which you will find a rich and diverse wealth in the *Sichos* and *Likutei Diburim*—and by speaking about this time and again, we are certain that such words are accepted and will have their effect, provided they are words that come from the heart.

It would be appropriate for you to consult on this with the leaders of N'shei u'Bnos Chabad in Jerusalem, may it be built and established, and they will guide you regarding the practical application.

With blessings for a *Chasimah v'Gmar Chasimah Tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

***

**Bas Sheva, may she live:** Lazrov, Jerusalem.

## 3855

B"H, 7 Tishrei, 5716
Brooklyn.

Rabbi Yehuda Segal, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

...Regarding what you wrote about whether it is permitted for a student to mention his Rebbe by name while adding a title of honor — the details and the various opinions on this are explained in Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah, 242:15 and the commentaries there.

It is known that the custom of Chassidim regarding Admurim is to be stringent in this matter, even when not in their presence.

Seemingly, as mentioned above, the law permits this straightforwardly. However, one could suggest a basis for this pious custom, and furthermore, one could suggest that it is not merely a stringency, based on what is written there in paragraph 16: that the concern is that it should not be "in the manner of the common people." If one were to treat his Admur according to the aforementioned permission, "in the manner of the rest" of his teachers, this would fall into the category prohibited in paragraph 16. And what difference does it make whether this is in greeting, in speech, or in writing?

As for the verses "My lord Moses," "Abba Chalafta," and the like — **which is** the basis for the permission in paragraph 15 — in those instances, Joshua did not call **any** person by the name "my lord," and Rabbi Yehuda did not call any person by the title "Abba." This is simple. And there is no need to elaborate further. I have written at length on this elsewhere.

#### ***3855***

**Rabbi Yehuda Segal:** Tel Aviv. Perhaps this is the same individual as in letter 4045.

**Regarding what you wrote:** Written in the margins of a secretariat letter to him.

## 3855*

B"H, 7 Tishrei, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 3 Tishrei, in which you write regarding... and what has crossed the mind of someone, that witchcraft, Heaven forbid, was performed against her, etc., and you ask my opinion on this.

Tell the woman in question to completely divert her thoughts from this entire matter. She should take upon herself to be careful in the mitzvos of Hashem, may He be blessed and exalted, in general, and especially in the mitzvos entrusted to women, primarily the laws and statutes of taharas hamishpachah—niddah, hefsek taharah, and immersion in a strictly kosher mikveh, not from the city’s water supply, etc. She should also increase her hachnosas orchim according to her ability. Her husband should have his tefillin checked, as well as the mezuzos in their home, to ensure they are kosher according to the law. Every weekday, before davening Shacharis, he should give a few coins to tzedakah. When they decide to fulfill all of the above with a whole heart and begin doing so immediately, then the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He, will protect them from all trouble and distress, Heaven forbid, and they will raise their children to Torah, chuppah, and maasim tovim.

With blessings for a *chasimah v’gmar chasimah tovah* and for good tidings regarding all the above.

## 3816

B"H, 11 Tishrei, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and industrious in communal affairs,
R' Menachem Zev, may he live, Halevi

Shalom u’Bracha!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from Erev Yom Kippur, in which you write regarding the customs concerning the Arba Minim. Thank you for this list, although in practice it is difficult to establish exactly what a specific person’s custom was, especially when one did not hear the reasoning from him personally, and in such minute detail—it is possible that in some instances it was merely a matter of happenstance, etc.

Regarding what you wrote about the pronunciation of the Name [Hashem], it is indeed puzzling, for according to the simple explanation, it belongs to what precedes it and not to what follows it. It requires further study why one would change this during the *ninuim* (shaking of the Lulav), especially since the Name Havayah is the attribute of *rachamim*, and *rachamim* inclines toward *chesed* and the South.

With blessings for a *Gmar Chasima Tova* and for *Zman Simchaseinu* in both material and spiritual matters alike.

## 3717

B"H, 11 Tishrei, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R' Pinchas Leibish, may he live.

Shalom u'Bracha!

In response to your letter of 4 Tishrei, I trust that my letter with blessings for the New Year has already reached you.

As you requested, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for a good and sweet year. Since you are acting as a shaliach to bring their request, you should surely explain to them what is written in several places—and a passage regarding this is also transcribed in the *Hayom Yom*—concerning the methods of *hiskashrus*. For *hiskashrus* is the conduit for receiving blessings. First and foremost is the observance of the three *shiurim* that are equal for every soul, the *takanah* established by the one who awakens us, my father-in-law, the Rebbe: the well-known *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*. Regarding the women, may they live, [the practice is] giving *tzedakah* before lighting candles every *Erev Shabbos* and *Erev Yom Tov*. And for everyone, [this includes] having their *tefillin* and *mezuzos* checked in their homes to ensure they are *kosher* according to *din*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above and for a *Gmar Chasimah Tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

***

3717

R' Pinchas Leibish: [Residing in] Herzliya.

In the *Hayom Yom*: See also letter 484 below.

## 3818

B"H, 12 Tishrei, 5716
Brooklyn

To the Avreich Shalom Leib, may he live,
Shalom and Blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter from last week, in which you write about your state of mind in your new location, and that you have organized a minyan for davening, etc.

Surely you will not be satisfied with this alone; you should also organize a group for the study of our Torah, the Torah of life, which is the protection for every single one of the Bnei Yisrael wherever they may be, for it is our life and the length of our days. When you exert yourself in this as is fitting, you will succeed, for words that come from the heart enter the heart. Certainly, the Tzeirei Agudas Chabad will assist you to the best of their ability, especially if there is a need for seforim, pairs of tefillin, or the like. Who knows—perhaps this is the very purpose of your being placed in that specific location and environment: to bring the hearts of the Bnei Yisrael closer to our Father in Heaven. For this purpose, all the effort, energy, and time are worthwhile. You are surely familiar with the story regarding the Mashpia R' Yosef of Beshenkovitch and the Ba'al Teshuvah R' Shlomo Leib—in the writings of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which was printed in the introduction to the sefer *Pokeiach Ivrim*. The way of Hashem is measure for measure, only many times over. May He open your heart and mind to fulfill your role, as the Mishnah states, "I was created to serve my Creator," with proper health and an expanded mind.

Please convey my regards and holiday greetings to your friends in your area. May it be the will of Hashem that, similar to the mitzvah of Sukkah—where the mitzvah encompasses the entire person from head to foot, including their garments and even their shoes—and furthermore, that a person is elevated and fulfills a mitzvah through eating in the Sukkah, as well as drinking, sleeping, and so on (everything done in the Sukkah, as the Sages say, "dwell as you live"), may each and every one of them merit and succeed in recognizing the truth: that the ability given to **every** person to serve their Creator is not only during davening and Torah study, but "in all your ways know Him." This matter depends only on one's will; if one truly desires it, they will eventually realize that it is an easy service, for He only asks according to our capacity.

With blessings for a happy holiday and to hear good news regarding all that was mentioned above.

## 3,319

B"H, 12 Tishrei, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the G-d-fearing, honorable, and distinguished R' Chananya, may he live.

Shalom and blessing!

In response to your letter, in which you write about your position—that you work as a guard in office buildings, sometimes by day and sometimes by night:

I have heard several times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding the conduct of people in such positions: they would keep matters of Torah learned by heart in their memories, and while at their posts, they would review them. It would be appropriate that, to the extent possible, you also conduct yourself in this manner. The matters of Torah should be Tehillim, Mishnayos, and—how much better—at least one chapter of Tanya; and the more one increases, the more praiseworthy it is.

As you requested, I will mention you and your family—whom you write about—at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. In this year, which we are just beginning, may Hashem grant you success in utilizing the time now in the best possible way, and in the course of time, to achieve a good arrangement for yourself and your family, may they live, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

Surely you are aware of the three daily study portions established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for every person—in Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—which are well-known; in any case, you should observe them from here on out.

With holiday blessings.

***

**R' Chananya:** Lugasi, Jerusalem.

## 3821

B"H, 12 Tishrei, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned individual, engaged in communal needs, Rav Meir, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your question regarding the fact that you saw my letter printed in a newspaper, and you are concerned that newspapers are not treated with the proper care, especially since this letter contained statements of our Sages and a verse of Scripture.

The practice of the great leaders of Israel in our countries in the past—and this was also the practice of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, during his time in the United States—is that when necessary, he would publish words of inspiration in newspapers and the like, even if they contained quotations from our Sages or verses of Scripture. Although, naturally, they would exercise caution where possible—namely, by not writing the Divine Name in its full form, etc. We follow this same caution even in what is printed in booklets and the like, and even in letters written in the vernacular, based on what is explained in the *poskim* that there is holiness even in names written in foreign languages.

The teaching of our Sages regarding the verse, "And his banner [diglo] over me is love," is already well-known: "And his skipping [dilugo] over me is love"—He skips over the mention of the Name—**love**.

With blessings for a *Gmar Chasimah Tovah* and for the joy of the holiday.

***

**Rav Meir:** Amsel, Brooklyn.

**Teaching of our Sages regarding the verse:** Shir HaShirim 2:4; Shir HaShirim Rabbah 2:13.

## 3823

3823

B"H, 17 Tishrei, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and engaged in communal needs,
R' Chaim Tzvi, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from the end of Elul, in which you ask why Anash, may they live, refrain from reciting the Thirteen Principles (Ikkarim) every day, and why they are not mentioned in the Siddur of our Alter Rebbe.

1) The first question is answered by your second: since they are not mentioned in the Siddur of our Alter Rebbe, we do not recite the Principles.

2) As for the reason why our Rebbe did not include them in his Siddur, I have not received an explicit tradition on this. However, one may suggest, merely by way of conjecture, several reasons for their omission from the davening:

a) The purpose of davening—as explained in the Gemara—is the arrangement of praises to the Makom and the request for a person’s needs. Reciting "Ani Maamin" does not fall into either of these categories.

b) In general, regarding matters of davening, any addition to what was established by the Anshei Knesses HaGedolah and brought down by the Rishonim requires proof to justify its adoption. In other words, whoever introduces a new formula or recitation into the communal davening **must** provide clear proof and a foundation for it; the burden of proof is not on the one who refuses to accept the addition. It is well known how meticulous they were regarding every word and letter in the text of the davening, and how many allusions are contained therein. Even those who do recite the Thirteen Principles do so after the davening, and even this requires proof. The proof is already known from our Rebbe, the Arizal, as brought in the beginning of *Etz Chaim*, Shaar 1, which states: "He did not desire any of the *pizmonim* or *piyutim* composed by the Acharonim, only those composed by the Rishonim... which were established according to the path of Truth."

"But these Acharonim, who did not know the path of Kabbalah, do not know what they are saying and err in the order of their speech without any knowledge at all..." Therefore, as mentioned above, one must be cautious regarding additions. Scripture explicitly states (Koheles 5:1), "For G-d is in heaven and you are on the earth; therefore, let your words be few." See the commentary of the Ibn Ezra there. If a person wishes to increase his prayers and supplications, he can increase his recitation of Tehillim, etc., the "pleasant singer of Israel."

3) All of the above—aside from section (a)—concerns additions to davening in general. Regarding the Thirteen Principles in particular, they are **not** brought in the Siddur of the Arizal, nor in many prayer books of the Rishonim. It requires study to find who first established their daily recitation. Furthermore, it is known that several of the great figures of Israel were not comfortable with the notion of designating a portion of the mitzvos as "principles" while others are not. Moreover, even regarding the count of the Principles, not everyone agrees with the opinion of the Rambam that they are thirteen in number, and these matters are well known.

4) It has not escaped my notice that the *Sefer Mishmeres Shalom* cites the holy Rabbi, R' Pinchas of Koritz, that it is a *segulah* for livelihood to recite the *Parshas HaMan* and the Thirteen Principles early in the morning. It is simple, however, that matters of *segulah* stated for a specific place or time are not part of the standard davening formula for the entire Jewish people, nor is this instruction necessarily applicable in all places and at all times.

By the way, "when your wellsprings spread outward" is the answer of Melech HaMashiach.

Due to the holiness of the festival, the Rebbe shlita did not sign this himself, and I am signing on his behalf,

The Secretary

P.S. The book *Doveres Shlomo* was received, and many thanks. Enclosed is a check for the shipping costs.

## 3825

B"H, 17 Tishrei, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Erev Yom Kippur, along with the enclosure. I trust you have already received my letter with blessings for the year.

I feel a sense of joy on one hand, that you have decided to endeavor, bli neder, and with extra effort, to fulfill my wishes regarding the matters of the Reshet, and to be a faithful shaliach in contributing to its progress, improvement, and so on. However, I feel a sense of weeping on the other hand, that all of this is stated in the future tense.

If in all matters of holiness every moment is precious, as is brought in many seforim, how much more so in the field of education for young Jewish boys and girls. Every moment that passes without the greatest possible positive action, they are receiving influence from the "other side" and from the winds blowing in the street.

And although our Sages of blessed memory said that one does not cry over the past, it is understood that what is brought in many places—that a resolution for the future is made simultaneously with regret for the past—is because a resolution for the future is difficult if one does not recognize the truth regarding the past. Consequently, this is not "crying over the past," but rather a double and triple request regarding the future.

If one takes into account the opinion of such-and-such a person regarding vital matters in the private affairs of an individual and his household—matters where, on the face of it, the decision was entrusted from Above to the person himself—then how much more so should one take into account the opinion of that person regarding general matters. Especially since he is not a party to the situation, and can therefore judge the state of affairs without bias or bribery, unlike those who are on the scene and in the thick of the action.

May it be Hashem’s will that in your next letter you will bring me good news regarding all that has been mentioned above, as well as the other matters mentioned in your letter.

With holiday blessings.

Due to the holiness of the festival, the Rebbe shlita did not sign personally.

I sign on his behalf,

The Secretary

## 3330

B"H, 18 Tishrei, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs,
Mr. S.B., known as Dr. Ullman, may he live.

Shalom u’Bracha!

I have received your letter of September 29, as well as the reprint you sent; thank you.

Regarding what you wrote—that the Reformers, etc., lack no resources, whereas the same cannot be said for the side of holiness—and you conclude with the words, "Why should a living man complain," suggesting that perhaps it is enough that he is alive:

It is unnecessary to elaborate on the simple fact that this conclusion is refuted, and the history of the Jewish people over thousands of years proves it. In the words of the verse, "Why does the way of the wicked prosper?" Our Sages of blessed memory explained that even Moshe Rabbeinu, the teacher of all Israel, grappled with this dilemma. Yet, despite this, he received the Torah at Sinai and transmitted it, and so on, down to our generation and the generations to come—an eternal Torah. The word *Torah* comes from the root *hora'ah* (instruction), and its eternal nature means that in every place and at every time, these instructions are binding and provide merit. Among these instructions is the ruling of the Mishnah at the end of Kiddushin: "I was created to serve my Maker." This is a constant commandment in every place and at every moment of a person’s life. This service is possible only through the path that the Creator of the world has paved for us: to spread the "candle of mitzvah, the Torah of light, and the light of Torah"—which is the inner dimension of the Torah—within one’s own "four cubits," and through this, to influence one’s own body and animal soul, as well as one’s immediate and even distant surroundings.

As for all the questions that confuse and sometimes even conceal and obscure—the vast majority of them, through appropriate exertion, depth of study, and with Siyata Dishmaya, find their answer and resolution. And even if a person has not yet reached that level—especially considering that, as is evident to the senses, those who are "men of ascent" and possess such intellectual grasp are few—this does not exempt him in the slightest from fulfilling his role day by day. Since the Ribono shel Olam demands this of him, He has certainly provided him with the powers to fulfill this role beforehand, and the matter depends solely on his will. Just as no question confuses one regarding the fulfillment of the body’s needs—eating, drinking, and so on—all the more so, **in and of itself**, should no question confuse one regarding the fulfillment of the needs of the source of the body’s vitality, which is the neshamah, through its spiritual nourishment: the Torah and mitzvos.

With blessings for success in all of the above and for good tidings.

Due to the sanctity of the festival, the Rebbe shlita did not sign personally.

I sign on his behalf,

The Secretary

## 3833

B”H, 19 Tishrei, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing and accomplished, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R’ Yitzchak, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter from Erev Sukkos, in which you raise a point regarding the date on my letter—that it was written during the days of Selichos and the specific day was not detailed—my intention is simple, as the purpose of dating a letter and the like is:

1) To indicate when the writing took place, which is relevant for secondary matters—similar to the expression of our Sages regarding “fruits” [in legal documents], etc. In this regard, it is understood that the more precise the date, the more it serves this purpose, to the extent that in Jerusalem they would even record the hours.

2) Or, it relates to the content of the letter, in accordance with the teaching of our Sages that “merit is brought about on a day of merit.” In such a case, the date depends on the duration of that merit—whether it is a single day or a period that is shorter or longer. In that instance, it is appropriate to emphasize the period rather than the specific day, similar to what is written, “And the days were the days of the first ripe grapes,” where “days” is in the plural (see Targum Yonasan there).

Since in my letters of blessing the second aspect is primary—and it is appropriate that the recipient of the letter also emphasize this—I wrote the date as “the days of Selichos,” as it is through these days that the *Kesivah V’chasimah Tovah* comes.

With respect and blessing.

29 Due to the sanctity of the festival, the Rebbe shlita did not sign personally, and I am signing on his behalf.

**R’ Yitzchak:** Hutner. Additional letters to him appear above in Vol. 7, 1868, and in the references noted there.
See below, 4115.

## 3834

19 Tishrei, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, expert in Torah and G-d-fearing, engaged in communal affairs, etc., Moreinu HaRav Shlomo Yosef Zevin, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Shuvah:

1) Regarding what I mentioned, that in our generation the opinions prohibiting grafted *esrogim* have multiplied, etc., and you note that the opinion of the prohibitors has long been known:

My intention was to refer to the early *Acharonim* who **permit** grafted *esrogim*, upon whom the prominent lenient authorities rely (and not because of the permissive stance of authors in our current generation). If they had seen the reasoning and arguments of the prohibitors in their own time, it is questionable whether their permission would have been formulated as it appears in their books. In any event, one cannot escape the element of doubt. The main point is that the entire basis for permission is in a situation where a non-grafted *esrog* cannot be obtained, which is not the case in our time. As for the advice you write to add that "this applies if the *esrogim* are kosher"—this is the same phrasing used in the *kol korei* (public proclamation) of the Agudas HaRabonim here.

This is similar to what I wrote regarding the book *Shevisas HaYam*, and even more so: a book is intended for a *ben Torah* and a person of understanding, whereas a *kol korei* is not. Before publishing, one must consider how the readers will interpret it; the intent of the signatories is less relevant. Surely you will also agree that when reading the *kol korei*, the reader’s takeaway is the central point. In the present case, the point is that one should take the *esrog* about which the *kol korei* was written. The conditions mentioned are, at best, written in vague language, and to such an extent (as they wrote here... "that the *esrogim* be kosher") that there is **no** practical benefit in this at all regarding the actual practice. It only serves so that they can argue in the Heavenly Court, "I have saved my own soul."

If the *kol korei* had only reached people who would study it—not just read it—and who would contemplate the vague phrasing "kosher *esrogim*" (meaning those presumed to be non-grafted), and who would take into account that only a few orchards in Eretz Yisrael are certified as such (as even the orchard owners from Eretz Yisrael who are here have said, and as is also apparent from the letters of *Anash* on this matter), then this would actually decrease the number of people buying these *esrogim*—**and significantly so** (the opposite of the intent of those requesting the publication of the *kol korei*). For as is apparent from the aforementioned accounts, the *esrogim* that have certification are a minority of a minority.

Regarding what I wrote in my letter about the matter of one who cooks on Shabbos: It is obvious that I did not raise this based on the principle of a *mitzvah* performed through a transgression, nor because it is equivalent to the case of "one who cooks for his fellow" mentioned in the *Gemara*—where it was done in the past without any command or assistance from him, etc. Rather, in the present case, it is a matter of the present and future, and involves assistance from the fellow to the one cooking, and even more than that—*v'dai l'meivin* (a word to the wise is sufficient). I used this language because it is the standard terminology, and also because in the present case, it appears to be a Torah prohibition, etc. There is no need to dwell on the corruption, especially during the *Moed*.

You have surely received my letter with blessings for the year.

With blessings for the *Chag*,

Due to the sanctity of the *Moed*, the Rebbe Shlita did not sign personally.

On his behalf,

A. Quint
Secretary

***

[Additional letter from the year 5715—to which the preceding letter refers]

10 Elul, 5715
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, expert in Torah and G-d-fearing, Moreinu HaRav Shlomo Yosef Zevin, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from the 3rd of Elul, you have surely received my two previous letters. Regarding what you wrote about so-and-so traveling here, and about the *kol korei* letter concerning the *esrogim* of Eretz Yisrael: out of respect for you, and so that you do not say that I passed over your letter without the proper attention, I am responding to this as well: How is it possible in the *atra* (domain) of the Rav—that is, the Rebbe the *Tzemach Tzedek*—and especially for his descendants, to act in opposition to what he ruled in his *Responsa Orach Chaim*, Siman 64? Especially since *maaseh rav* (the practice of the master) is well known, and it is known how dismissed the issue of grafted *esrogim* was in the house of the Rav. The vast majority—and one could say (though perhaps it is not worth publishing) that the remainder is a minority of a minority, not just a minority—of *esrogim* brought from Eretz Yisrael are grafted. I am astonished that anyone can take upon themselves the *breitkeit* (breadth/boldness) to issue a *kol korei* to tens of thousands of Jews to recite a blessing over *esrogim* from such-and-such a land without first declaring that one must verify that it is not grafted. And even those who permit grafted *esrogim*, surely in this generation, after the opinions of those who disagree with them have been clarified, **they would not permit it except when no others are available**. Even in this year, when an *esrog* is only taken from the second day onwards, there is the additional issue of *safek bracha* (a doubtful blessing), which according to many opinions also involves the prohibition of "do not take [Hashem's name in vain]." Furthermore, it is impossible to declare this year that it is only because it is a Rabbinic matter, unlike in the coming year.

And if all the above were not enough for us, there is an additional matter, which because of the publicity involved is even more severe: the vast majority of *esrogim*, and generally all religious articles from Eretz Yisrael brought here, are transported on ships belonging to various agencies in Eretz Yisrael that also travel on Shabbos. According to information from those who have traveled on them, and the sailors as well, they conduct themselves on Shabbos regarding the operation of the ship just as on weekdays, which involves the prohibitions of *hav'arah* (kindling), *kesivah* (writing), etc., and this is done with great public display. Even more so on cargo ships where there are no outsiders present besides the sailors. I must say that I am appalled by the silence of the Chief Rabbinate regarding this alarming matter. Furthermore, the fact that there is an official Rabbinic supervision there—though I do not know clearly if it is from a private Rabbi or the Chief Rabbinate—the public in the United States receives this as supervision from the Chief Rabbinate, as if the supervisor is their representative. Consequently, this is not merely silence, but the granting of a *hechsher*. The public does not distinguish whether this *hechsher* is for the kitchen or for the entire ship. A proven sign of this is that G-d-fearing and observant people travel on these ships based on the aforementioned assumption.

I have seen the book *Shevisas HaYam* which discusses this question, and I do not know if it is so naive, or if it is intentionally misleading the public, G-d forbid. For everything stated in this book is irrelevant to the question as it exists **in reality**. A simple reader of his book has no doubt; on the contrary, the book is written in such language that there should be no doubt that it refers to ships traveling from Eretz Yisrael to here. It is obvious that all the leniencies that exist regarding a ship have no place in the present case, since the ship can rest the entire Shabbos, and even with the addition of *mechul al hakodesh* (adding from the profane to the holy), and there is no danger in this (except for exceptional cases, which for now, as it appears from the newspapers regarding the weather conditions in the area of the ship's travel, has never happened **even once**!). Especially since the ship is delayed several times during its journey anyway, and this is only a question of money, and the main point—the question of the will not to desecrate Shabbos.

Regarding the passengers and the merchandise transported on the ship: when there is an option to travel on a ship where the work is done by a non-Jew, where is the permission to have it done specifically by a Jew? Especially since they also perform tasks that are only for maintaining order, where there is not even a question of financial loss. It seems that the author of this book is also a member of the Chief Rabbinate, and as is apparent from the book, he labored over this problem, but afterwards, regarding the public—*er hot tsugetshepet a heiter tsum davar ha'asur bifshitut* (he tacked on a permission to something that is simply forbidden).

It is enough to ask someone who traveled on these ships from Eretz Yisrael, whose stories would make one's hair stand on end. It is hard to believe that a person who went into all the minute details of the ship's operation did not think to ask about this as well. Even though his book contains several conditions—and preconditions—for his permissive rulings, as mentioned above, this *avvarenish* (warning) has no place, since the practice of many months and years is known to be the opposite of all the conditions. This is a book written for a practical halachic ruling, not for theoretical pilpul. Regarding the present case, even if you were to say that there are those who say that grafted *esrogim* have "no doubt," when they are brought—and the same applies to other merchandise—on the aforementioned ships, the issue of "one who cooks for his fellow on Shabbos," etc., is added.

Incidentally, it is surely known to you as well that thousands, and perhaps even more, *mezuzos* have been received here, and apparently *tefillin* as well, which are photographic reproductions on paper, etc. All of this goes together under the slogan of "settling the land," etc. In matters such as these, I am reminded of the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, which was said to him—apparently in the year 5687—regarding such matters. When they challenged his position, arguing that when extinguishing a fire one does not distinguish whether the water is fit for drinking and clear or not, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, replied that this is true, but one must be extremely careful not to extinguish the fire with kerosene. *V'dai l'meivin*.

Incidentally, it is surely known that about sixty years ago or more, a *kol korei* was prevalent in Russia regarding the *esrogim* of Eretz Yisrael, with many signatories. At that time, the question of grafted *esrogim* was not as prevalent, and simply, the question of Shabbos did not exist, and they were also confident regarding the matters of *shemitah* and *maaseros*. Nevertheless—even though I do not have the *kol korei* in hand—those from Lubavitch did not sign it. It is also worth noting that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and as I heard also from his father (the Rebbe Rashab), never issued any letter or *kol korei* that contained anything akin to granting a *hechsher* on matters of holiness and the like.

I have written all the above, even though, seemingly, three or four lines would have sufficed, out of the abundance of my speech and my pain over the alarming situation. We see with our own eyes the fulfillment of the Sages' words: "There is no day that its curse is not greater than the previous one"—regarding the terrible situation in Eretz Yisrael. I am reminded of the uproar that occurred regarding what was done with the children of Tehran, even though they are nothing compared to what is being done with the children of Morocco, through a disgraceful contract signed also by the representatives of the right-wing parties, who agree to concede up to 75 percent. Thank G-d that thanks to the elections they have begun to backtrack from this agreement, and the same applies to the matter of the conscription of women, and mainly... in those matters where they are even more reckless, where they eat pig meat, abominations, and mice, and are literally doing the exact opposite from one extreme to the other.

In these days of mercy, as the *Likkutei Torah* (Re'eh 32b) states, "The King is in the field" (not a place of human habitation, but a place of the Divine), and then anyone who wishes to go out to greet Him is permitted to do so, and He receives everyone with a smiling countenance and shows a smiling face to everyone. May it be the will that through *is'arusa d'le'eila* (arousal from above), a spirit of purity will be poured upon each one of us to see the good in others, etc., until everyone becomes one group to do Your will with a whole heart.

With blessings for a *Kesivah V'Chasimah Tovah* and good news in all the above specifically.

P.S. It is strange that apparently due to his silence, the matter of printing the books and manuscripts of the late Rabbi Rivlin is not progressing.

## 3836

B"H, 25 Tishrei, 5716
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

It was a pleasure to receive your regards through the esteemed Chossid, who is involved in communal needs, R' Moshe Eliyahu Gerlitzky, as well as the *pidyon nefesh* that he delivered, which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding what you write, that you feel "crushed under your burden," this is not surprising, for it is written that "Hashem created [the world] to do," to rectify. It is also stated that "Hashem formed (*va-yitzer*)—with two *yuds*—the *yetzer tov* and the *yetzer hara*." Therefore, "when you see the donkey of one who hates you"—when you look with careful scrutiny at your own "donkey," which is your body—you will see that it "hates" the *neshamah* that yearns for *Elokus* and spirituality. Furthermore, you will see that it is "crushed under its burden"—the burden that the *Ribono shel Olam* placed upon the body so that it might be refined through *Torah* and *mitzvos*, yet the body is sluggish in fulfilling them. And perhaps it may enter your heart to "refrain from helping it"—that it will be able to fulfill its mission—thinking that if you begin with self-affliction to break your materiality, that is the way to let the light of *Torah* dwell within. But this is not the way; rather, "you shall surely help him"—to clarify and refine the body, not to break it through self-affliction (one of the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, copied in *Hayom Yom*).

From this, it is understood and simple that one must not, *chas v'shalom*, fall into despair over this. For the reason for this is that the *Ribono shel Olam*, who is the ultimate good, does not want a Jewish person to receive what he needs—whether in material or spiritual matters—as "bread of shame." Therefore, it was arranged in Creation as it is written: "See, I have set before you today life and good, etc.," for immediately afterward it adds, "and you shall choose life." It is explained in *Chassidus* that a request to the *Ribono shel Olam* is also a granting of strength and an addition of power to fulfill that request. You are surely aware of this, and it is worthwhile for you to contemplate this once again, as stated in *Tanya* in several places, and in particular in Chapter 27 regarding the two types of *nachas ruach* before Him above, and see there from Chapter 34 onward, where the contemplation of all that is said there leads one to perform his *avodah* all his days with great joy, etc.

Enclosed is a copy of my general letter for *Rosh Hashanah*. In addition to the blessing in my letter for *Rosh Hashanah*, I reiterate them here for long life and good years, that you should succeed in strengthening and spreading *Yiddishkeit* in your surroundings, with health and true peace of mind.

With blessings,

## 3337

3337

B"H, 25 Tishrei, 5716
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I received the initial news in due time, and subsequently the good tidings that the surgery of your wife, may she live, Mrs. [Name], went well and was successful. May it be the will of Hashem, the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders, that she returns to her full strength soon, and from here on may you hear only good and kindness.

It is already known how we interpret the statement of our Sages that "any year that is poor at its beginning becomes wealthy at its end." The distinction lies in the state of affairs before the *tekiyos* and the *tefillos*, and the state after them. For before them, one is still in a state of *din* and judgment, whereas through the *tekiyos* and *tefillos*, one brings about that the Holy One, Blessed be He, rises from the throne of *din* and sits upon the throne of mercy, and all of the Jewish people, your people, are all written and sealed immediately in the book of the righteous. Throughout the year, every single day performs its task of creating vessels for the drawing down and receiving of the good that was decreed for one on Rosh Hashanah. The vessels for this are the matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, one of which is influencing others. Especially for one whom Hashem has graced with the talent to educate, he should utilize every possibility to its fullest to raise students who are G-d-fearing, who study Torah and observe *mitzvos*. The merit of the many assists him and draws down an abundance of blessing and success regarding himself and all his household, may they live.

With blessings, awaiting good tidings.

## 3,338

B"H, 26 Tishrei, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the Bnos Chabad of [City Name],

Blessings and peace!

I received your letter with pleasure, albeit with a slight delay, and I was pleased to read that you have strengthened your work with the school students through various activities.

It is my hope that even though you write that you paused this work for a short time, you have already begun anew, with renewed strength and increased vigor—befitting the demands of the hour, which are ever-increasing.

It is understood and simple that my intent here is not only regarding your activities with the aforementioned students, but, to no lesser degree, regarding yourselves, through corresponding avodah.

The interpretation of Chassidic teaching regarding the verse that calls a person a **"walker"** (one who moves) is already well-known—for this is his function and a sign of the vitality within him, that from the day of his birth he grows and develops.

We see tangibly that this depends solely on the **will** of the person, for the **ability** is always in a person’s hands to improve upon their standing and situation of yesterday, and so too from day to day.

And if this applies to all people, it applies all the more so to the younger generation, whose vigor has not yet been utilized and is still bubbling within them, and whose initiative is greater.

However, caution is required regarding the direction and the matters in which they utilize this vigor and strength, especially in places and matters where light and darkness are intermingled. It is necessary to consult and clarify with those who stand "on the sidelines," who can judge matters without the bias of self-love and personal agendas.

Furthermore, one’s outlook on life must be insulated by Torah and permeated with a spirit of yiras shamayim; then, often, one instinctively feels and distinguishes between the straight path and a deviation from it, even if one cannot explain it intellectually.

May Hashem grant each of you, in the year you have just entered, the merit to succeed in all the above, and to serve as a living example and a guide for others as well.

With blessings for great success,

[The Rebbe]
Who awaits good news, detailed as necessary.

## 3440

3440

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc., R' Tzvi, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the 21st of Tammuz, in which you write that you are a native of Lubavitch and retain memories of the period when you were in Lubavitch—the era of the Rebbe Maharash and his son, the Rebbe Rashab—both regarding Lubavitch itself and the guests who visited from time to time.

It would be appropriate if you could commit these memories to writing, as there are very few who still remember the events of those days in their entirety, as well as the character types of the guests, the members of the court, and so on. Even if not everything written is suitable for publication, preserving it in writing is worthwhile. Surely, portions of these notes could be utilized for matters that are published in print, although it is understood that one cannot know this clearly in advance. Naturally, one must be certain that the recorded matters correspond to reality, especially since several decades have passed, and a matter that is not constantly on a person’s mind is not always remembered exactly as it was. Surely, in your memory as well, there are matters about which you have no doubt regarding their description, as well as those about which you are somewhat uncertain or unsure of certain details; it would be best if you note this in your records as well.

It is understood that I would be very interested in seeing these records, as I am collecting material for the history of Lubavitch, especially for that period which has not yet found its chroniclers—the history of Chassidus during the era of the Rebbe Maharash and the beginning of the era of his son, the Rebbe Rashab. Thank you in advance.

As per your request, a pocket-sized Tanya is being sent to you separately, and I trust you will confirm its receipt.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

***

## 3841

3841

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Mar-Cheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 26 Tishrei, in which you ask regarding:

a) Unwanted thoughts.

The advice for this is well-known: a little light dispels much darkness. Therefore, one should be immersed in thoughts of Torah and tefillah, and be proficient in reciting by heart chapters of Mishnayos, chapters of Tanya, and—even better—maamarim of Chassidus that are easy to understand. All of this helps one to free oneself from improper thoughts.

b) What to do when every action is done with an ulterior motive (pniyah).

One must be very careful regarding this. Often, when the yetzer hara wants to prevent a Yid from doing a good deed, it attempts to do so by convincing him that he is acting out of an ulterior motive, and that therefore it would be better for him not to do it at all. This is the opposite of the ruling of our Sages, of blessed memory: "A person should always engage in Torah and mitzvos, even if not for their own sake, for from doing them not for their own sake, one comes to do them for their own sake." Therefore, even though it is self-understood that one must strive for the end result that every action be done without any ulterior motive, in the meantime, if the action itself is a good thing, one must not, chas v'shalom, refrain from doing it, as stated above.

Regarding the above in general, it is a great help toward receiving siyata d'shmaya when one influences friends and one’s environment to bring them closer to Yiddishkeit in general, and to Chassidus in particular. This is tzedakah in spirituality, and of this it is said, "And tzedakah exalts a nation," as explained in Torah Or, at the beginning of Parshas Bereishis.

With blessings for success in Torah study with joy and yiras shamayim,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

***

3841

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 17, p. 500.

## 3443

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, involved in communal needs, R' Nosson Dovid, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 1st of Menachem Av, and I was pleased to read that you have been lecturing to the public on matters of Yiddishkeit. It goes without saying that it is insufficient to lecture to them only once a year. As is known, the avodah of "once a year"—which in terms of **time** refers to the Holy of Holies, Yom Kippur, and in terms of **place** refers to the literal Holy of Holies, through the High Priest who is called "holy of holies" (*Divrei HaYamim I 23:13*)—is effective only when there are preparations throughout the year, in addition to the preparation for Yom Kippur itself.

And although it is explained that every Jew, by virtue of his soul—which is literally a part of Elokus from above, transcending time and place—can accomplish in any place, at any time, and at any moment, in a manner similar to the High Priest’s avodah on Yom Kippur in the Holy of Holies, through the proper *avodah* of changing one's essence, it is understood and simple that this does not, G-d forbid, exempt one at all from avodah throughout the entire year. As the Zohar states, "Every single day one performs one's work" (*Zohar III 94b*), and "if one day is missing, one garment is missing" (*Zohar I 224a*). This is all the more so regarding influencing others, who are not always in one's presence and are not always prepared to receive the influence. May Hashem grant you success in bringing good tidings in this as well.

With blessings.

## 3444

3444

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5716
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Shochet and Bodek,
Gabbai of the Lubavitcher Shul in Lubavitch

Peace and Blessing!

At the conclusion of the month of Tishrei—the month that encompasses the entire year, which is "sworn" with all goodness in order to draw it down throughout the entire year—I hereby double my blessings: that for many more years you will continue to serve as Gabbai of the Lubavitcher Shul in Lubavitch in a Chassidic spirit. May this be realized through your efforts—with success—to increase the number of congregants and elevate their quality by establishing regular shiurim in the shul, both in Nigleh and in Chassidus, as is customary in the shuls of Bnei Yisrael, and especially in Chabad shuls. And surely it is possible to arrange these shiurim in a way that will not disrupt the schedules of the Yeshiva.

It is already well known how our Sages of blessed memory extolled the virtue of uniting the shul and the beis medrash together (Berachos 8a), and the merit of the community depends upon him.

With blessings for success in all of the above, in good health and with Chassidic nachas, together with your wife, may she live, and all your children, may they live,

**M. Schneerson**

## 3845

## 3846

B"H, 1st of Mar-Cheshvan, 5716

This depends only on the talent that awakens and acts in this regard. And one whom Hashem has graced with a writer’s pen, through which his words reach thousands upon thousands of the children of Israel, has a capacity that is many times greater—and along with this, the responsibility and the merit as well.

It is understood and simple that the work and effort with others does not, Heaven forbid, exempt one from the work upon oneself. As it is written, "When you see the naked, you shall cover him, etc."—and the exposition of our Sages of blessed memory on this verse is well known, that it also refers to matters of Torah and mitzvos, and the verse concludes: "And do not hide yourself from your own flesh."

With a blessing for success in all that is mentioned above.

## 3447

For if you exert your full capacity in this, you will achieve immediate victory, and if not, it may unfortunately be prolonged. However, it has already been promised to each and every one of us that no one shall be cast away from Him, for the Creator takes pride in all of them, as they are the work of His hands in which He takes pride. It is only that free choice has been granted to each and every one so that they may test their strengths and reveal the inner point within them through their own efforts. The very recognition and contemplation that victory is certain adds strength and fortitude in conducting this struggle and in concluding it speedily. I would appreciate it if you would share good news regarding the aforementioned in the near future.

## 3848

3848

B"H, 3rd of MarCheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding the order of the past month of Tishrei, which is the general month for the entire year, and the *himsachos* (drawings-down) within it affect the manner and every detail of the entire year. Even so, *teshuvah* is always effective, and there is nothing that can stand before the *ratzon* (will). Furthermore, there is *teshuvah* of all kinds, as is explained in *Chassidus*—that it is not necessarily regarding a matter of sin and iniquity in the literal sense, but rather "sin" (*chet*) in the sense of a lack (*chisaron*), and on a more elevated level, a returning (*shuvah*) to the source, as is explained in *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Haazinu*, and see also *Likutei Torah*, *Maamar* beginning with the words "Mah Tovu."

May Hashem grant you success in bringing good tidings regarding all of the above, with true *harchavas hada'as* (breadth of mind).

With blessings.

## 3849

3849

B"H, 3rd of Mar-Cheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from Erev Sukkos, recounting the praises of Hashem and His kindness to mankind, and the wonders you witnessed regarding the delay of your trip, etc. May it be the will of Hashem that this "Psalm of Thanksgiving" [Mizmor L'Todah] continues to radiate light throughout the entire year. The concepts of Mizmor L'Todah are explained in the Chassidic discourses of the Alter Rebbe and the Mitteler Rebbe; it would be appropriate for you to study them with the proper depth, as it is written, "And we will render for bullocks the offering of our lips."

I trust you participated in the farbrengens of anash during the days of favor and joy of the month of Tishrei—the general month for the entire year, the month saturated with all good.

With blessings.

## 3850

B"H, 3rd of Menachem Av, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...And let it be known that all of the above is of no value compared to the primary matter, which is the necessity of establishing a family life. This is clearly explained in our holy Torah, the Torah of life, and it is also evident to the senses that it is not good for man to be alone; any further elaboration on this simple matter is superfluous.

However, since everything requires *siyata d’shmaya*, especially regarding *zivugim*—as it is written, "A house and wealth are an inheritance from fathers, but a prudent wife is from Hashem," and especially regarding a second *zivug* which is according to one’s deeds—he must therefore increase, as soon as possible, his study sessions in *Toras HaNigleh* and *Chassidus*. This includes the keeping—*bli neder*—of the three daily *shiurim* for every soul, established by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zy"a*, in *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*, as is well known. He should also set aside a few coins for *tzedakah* every weekday before *davening*, and it is also appropriate that his *tefillin* be checked. May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant him success and bring him good tidings regarding all that has been mentioned.

Regarding what you wrote at the end of your letter, that you did not write until now because there were no good things to report, etc.—this not only fails to answer the difficulty, but on the contrary, it only compounds it. For a student of *Tomchei Temimim* to be in *Eretz Yisrael, tichyeh*, and act contrary to the demands of the hour—especially in our generation, this orphaned generation—by not engaging in the dissemination of Yiddishkeit in general, and the dissemination of the teachings of *Chassidus*, its guidance, and its customs in particular, is unacceptable. He must engage in this, at the very least from now on, to the best of his ability and even more than that. When one does so, the verdict from Above is known, and one sees success. May it be His will that, at the very least, from here on out this will be rectified, and little by little, he will also make up for what was lacking in the years that have passed.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 3851

B"H, 3rd of Menachem Av, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Chol HaMoed Sukkos: In such matters, one should increase the letters of Torah and tefillah, and increase efforts in matters of chinuch and similar areas that involve the "sweat of a mitzvah." It is understood that this must be done with simcha and complete bitachon in Hashem, as it is written, "Serve Hashem with simcha." The Tzemach Tzedek’s response regarding this matter is well-known and is printed in the Shaar HaMiluim, Part II.

May Hashem grant you the merit to increase your strength to the point of the "sweat of a mitzvah" in your holy work in the chinuch of the children of Yisrael, so that they may be "the seed blessed by Hashem." The attribute of the Ribono shel Olam is "measure for measure," and may it be so many times over. May you and your wife derive true Chassidishe nachas from all your descendants, may they live and be well.

With blessings.

## 3852

B"H, 3rd of Menachem Av, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., R' Ze'ev Tzvi, may he live.

Shalom u'Bracha!

In response to your letter, in which you ask for the interpretation of the phrase "receiving the Torah with joy and with inwardness (pnimiyus)," specifically whether it refers to the inwardness of the Torah or the inwardness of the student.

It is self-evident that just as the word "with joy" means that the student should study with joy, so too, regarding the word "with inwardness," the intention is that the student should absorb it into his own inwardness.

Regarding what you wrote concerning a printing error in the Tanya, I do not know which edition you are studying from. In any case, many of the printing errors were corrected in the editions of the Tanya from the year 5760 and onwards, and several others were corrected in the edition of the Tanya printed here (which were also sent in large quantities to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established).

Regarding the interpretation of points that you sometimes find difficult in your study of Tanya, there are many of Anash and Temimim located in Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established. You should present these matters to them, and discussing them together will illuminate the concepts.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary
