## 3854

B"H, 4th of Menachem Av, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote about the young man who wishes to daven in a place of greater yiras shamayim, etc., and his father does not agree to this—the ruling is already explicit in the sefer Chamudei Daniel (cited in Pischei Teshuvah in Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah, end of siman 240) that he is not obligated to listen to his father in this matter. However, it is obvious that he must conduct himself in a manner of respect and in the ways of peace.

## 3855

B"H, 4th of Menachem Av, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh, in which you write that you did not understand what I meant regarding the avodah of... whether to refrain, etc.

It is obvious that it is not my intention to prevent anyone from good activities, especially regarding the chinuch of the younger generation. Rather, I wrote that they are **neglecting** their primary avodah and their role because of this. For in my opinion, their primary role—as I have written many times—is saving the youth from falling into the hands of the *le'u'z* and establishing them in a way that they will receive proper chinuch. As for all other matters that come their way, only if they can be done in a manner **that will not detract** from the fulfillment of their primary role, then *yishar cheilam* and fortunate is their portion.

And even though in general it is difficult to decide and to act upon refraining from a good activity, even if it is not directly incumbent upon one, this too is demanded of us (provided, as mentioned above, that the reason is because one is occupied at that very time, and also prior to that, with a mitzvah that is **his own** mitzvah and is not being performed by others)...

I was pleased by what you wrote regarding the activities of your wife, *tichye*, and may it be the will of Hashem that you both fulfill the words of our Sages, "we increase in holiness," with proper health and true peace of mind.

With blessings.

## 3859

B"H, 4th of Menachem Av, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you write about not having the time or the focus of thought, etc.—this is precisely the point I am making: since you do find the time and the focus of thought for matters that the *nefesh hasichlis* understands, why is this not the case **at all** regarding matters that the *nefesh elokis* understands? To elaborate on such a simple matter would be superfluous.

Regarding what you wrote about the reasons for the lack of increased *shalom*, etc., within [the community], etc., and how the situation would change for the better if there were a person whom everyone agreed upon, etc., etc.—

The fact is that each and every one of us has been given our own *avodah*—at a time suitable **for them**, in a place suitable, and with matters suitable. This is explicitly written (Koheles 3:11) and is a fundamental principle of faith. Furthermore, *l’fum gamla shichna* (the burden is according to the camel), and as explained in *Toras HaChassidus* (which is also understood by human intellect), we have been given the powers to fulfill **this** *avodah*. Therefore, thinking about how things would be if they were different is merely theoretical speculation that does not relate **at all** to practical action. Moreover, it is liable to weaken one’s energy in improving the current situation, as is clearly evident. It is certain that even in the current state of affairs, the choice remains in the hands of all those involved to fulfill the scriptural verse, "See, I have set before you... and you shall choose life." Furthermore, since everyone involved belongs to *Toras HaChassidus*—to a greater or lesser degree—and it is the "light within the Torah" and its inner dimension, their *avodah* is easier. May it be His will that you bring good tidings soon regarding all that was mentioned above.

With blessings.

## 3857

B"H, 5 Menachem Av, 5716
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To my friend, the G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, and distinguished [man], our teacher R' Avraham Dovid, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I received the happy news that some time ago there was a farbrengen in which you participated and recited a maamar da"ch, and that those who heard it were very satisfied.

May it be the will of Hashem that this serves as a good beginning for you to start utilizing your talents and the knowledge you acquired while in Tomchei Temimim, etc., for the benefit of others as well. This is something that is essential in all places and at all times, as Rabbi Akiva said, "And you shall love your neighbor as yourself — this is a great principle of the Torah." It is already well-known what the Alter Rebbe writes in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 16, based on the Gemara in Nedarim 72b, regarding physical tzedakah—and the same applies to spiritual tzedakah—all the more so now.

Certainly, there are many opportunities within the Chabad organizations that are in need of such things, and there are possibilities to utilize your talents to an ever-increasing degree. It would be a pleasure for me to receive good news from you regarding this, and may it be the will of Hashem that it happens soon, for time is a loss that cannot be recovered...

## 3859

3859

B"H, 5th of MarCheshvan, 5716

Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 25th of Tishrei (as well as to your letter of the 20th of Elul, which I had not yet answered), although my heart is gladdened by the activities you describe, they are—as you yourself write—not at all commensurate with the capacity and possibilities that exist in the world today, and especially in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established.

If we were meritorious, we would learn from the side of holiness. In the current situation, one can see this from what is being done on the "other side"—namely, among the leftist individuals and parties. Their success stems from the fact that they adopt methods and utilize strengths that the Torah of Chassidus demands for avodah in holiness. These are: vitality, enthusiasm, acting without regard for one’s own logic and opinion, discipline in following the directives of those above them (and only afterwards contemplating the reasons), unity in a single group to realize the required goals, and the sacrifice of personal interests—and even what they consider to be their spiritual interests—for the benefit of the collective, etc., etc.

If they have reached such a point in their affairs—even though their source is the "netherworld" and ultimately they will return to their source, the Source of Life and vitality—how much more so should this be true in our own affairs, and especially in the camp of the Chassidim. For the Nasiim, just as they "stood and served" here, so too do they "stand and serve" on high, drawing down additional blessing and success below for all the institutions, activities, and those involved in them. Yet, to our sorrow and regret, we do not utilize this blessing and success except occasionally and in a measure that is disproportionately small. And this is not due to reasons that are significant even in the eyes of human intellect, but rather because we are submerged in matters of "a mess of pottage" and forget the birthright, or because of matters of division of hearts, following the motto, "Let it be neither mine nor yours." Meanwhile, day comes and day goes, etc., etc. The proof of the truth of all the above is that wherever even a "little finger" (to use the language of the Midrash, Koheles Rabbah, at its beginning) has been applied, an extraordinary success has been seen that was not anticipated beforehand, to the point that in many cases the verse has been fulfilled: "When Hashem favors a man's ways, He makes even his enemies at peace with him."

It is understood that my intention here is not directed only to you personally, but to all of Anash... Nor is my intention to preach morality or cry out about the past, but rather with the hope that perhaps these words of mine will awaken them to dedicate themselves to the avodah as it should be done. Then, they will go forth and seek and acquire tens, hundreds, thousands, and myriads of Bnei Yisrael for the Torah of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs, until "the small one shall become a thousand," etc.

I trust you have already received the letter from the secretariat regarding the branch of Agudas N'shei U'Bnos Chabad in Bnei Brak.

It is surprising that you do not mention the "activities of the Arba Minim." I refer to the custom here—and I believe also by Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, last year—of inviting passersby on the street and the like to make a blessing on the Arba Minim. This year, they added here, primarily, visits to convalescent homes and the like, and it was a great success. Perhaps you will fill me in on the next opportunity.

## 3860

3860

B"H, 5th of MarCheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, occupied with communal needs,
R' Alexander Sender, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

It is surprising that since your letter of the 17th of Elul, there has been no news from you. Yet, the month from which we are departing (and as is known the interpretation in Chassidus—that they become a level of "walking/progressing") is the general month for the entire year, and it is "satiated with all good," as is explained in the Midrash. However, it is incumbent upon a person to fulfill what is said, "Open wide your mouth," to create wide vessels. It is explained in Chassidus that these are not merely a quantitative expansion, but also a qualitative expansion—meaning, vessels of an entirely different nature. May it be the will [of Hashem] that the only deficiency here is in writing, but not a deficiency in action during the days of favor and awakening of Tishrei, and may they be drawn out over the entire year through a true expansion of the mind.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 3862

B"H, 8 Marcheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, engaged in communal needs,
R' Aharon Mordechai, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, which you began writing on Erev Sukkos, in which you write regarding the establishment of courses for teachers (and I fear that since you do not mention anything about the study days [yimei iyun] that were supposed to take place during the month of Tishrei, that this also did not come to fruition this time).

It is understood that the establishment of courses for teachers from Anash is a very correct thing indeed. However, it requires consideration whether, in the current situation, it is necessary that there be a special course for them run by Anash. Perhaps it is possible to find among the already existing courses ones that are suitable for them, especially since when they speak with the administration of the courses regarding the special requirements of Anash and explain that the matters concern a group of a certain number, they will certainly agree to arrange special lectures for them if they need it, or changes to their study program, etc. In addition to the expenses being incomparably lower, there is an additional benefit in this—and this is the main point—that when they study together with other people, the studies will certainly be absorbed more easily, and there will be no necessity to combine in one class those who are not so compatible due to their small number, etc., etc. And another point in this, which is also important: since they will be interested in already existing courses, it will certainly be possible to begin the studies sooner, unlike if they were to establish a special course.

By the way, regarding what you write about the number of study hours mentioned above, seemingly it requires consideration: from where will they find so much free time, since each one of them is busy? And it is certainly superfluous to emphasize once again that all of the above does not diminish **at all** the **greatest** necessity that the teachers of Anash improve their qualifications as much as possible and as soon as possible. The discussion is only regarding the manner in which it is possible to realize this matter as soon as possible and in the best way.

With blessings for success in all that is mentioned above, and awaiting good tidings.

***

**R' Aharon Mordechai, may he live and be well:** Zilberstrom, Jerusalem. Additional letters to him—above Vol. 11, 3703, and in the references in the notes there. Below, 4267.

## 3863

B"H, 8 Marcheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the end of Tishrei, in which you write about the ways in which you can continue studying Chassidus and conducting yourself according to its guidance and customs—specifically, that it should not be too widely known, and that you would not need to study Chassidic texts for an hour or two every day.

Regarding the first matter, you must decide for yourself—that is, to gauge in which manner you will progress more in *yiras shamayim* and Chassidus, and conduct yourself accordingly. However, regarding the second matter, where you limit the time you spend studying the words of the Living G-d, the *pnimiyus haTorah*: while it is understood that studying some amount is better than not studying at all, the very approach to the Torah of Hashem that involves limiting oneself so as not to study a certain part of our holy Torah for a significant amount of time is, G-d forbid, contrary to the honor of the Torah. 

Although it is not required that every single person study specifically several hours a day in Chassidic texts—as per the well-known statement of our Sages regarding the Torah in general, that those who are constrained by circumstances fulfill their obligation with one chapter in the morning and one chapter in the evening—they must still know that this is only due to their constraints, because through Divine Providence they have not yet merited having more free time to occupy themselves with His wisdom, may He be blessed. But to say, G-d forbid, that this is their desire and their chosen order, etc.—to elaborate on such a simple matter is unnecessary. It is already well-known what is explained in *Kuntres Eitz Chaim* by the Rebbe (Rashab) *n.e.*, that in this time, the primary battle of the *yetzer* is against the study of *pnimiyus haTorah* (which has been revealed in our days in the teachings of Chassidus)...

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 3864

3864

B"H, 8th of Mar-Cheshvan, 5716

Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Beracha:

You have surely received a timely answer to the question in your previous letter.

Regarding what you write about your brother, may he live and be well: the reason he did not respond to my writing that his tefillin should be checked—it is self-evident that this reason only reinforces the suggestion that his tefillin should be checked as soon as possible, especially the parshiyos, to ensure they are certainly kosher. This should be done as soon as possible. It is also self-evident that it is absolutely necessary for him to put them on every weekday for at least a few minutes.

Hashem Yisbarach desired that a Yid should fulfill mitzvos of his own choosing (b’vchiraso), not under compulsion. This applies to your brother as well. However, it must be explained to him that when a remedy is prescribed to a sick person, it makes no sense to wait until one has first studied the science of medicine, become a doctor after several years, and understood how the remedy works, only then to take the medicine. Especially since the more one delays using the remedy, the further one moves away from recovery—and consequently, from understanding things as they truly are in reality. May Hashem Yisbarach grant success so that you and your friends find the appropriate words to set him on the path that is good for him, both b’gashmius and b’ruchnius.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 3865

B"H, 9 MarCheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Cheshvan, in which you write regarding your situation concerning the avodah of a person to his Creator, and that you desire to establish a hiskashrus and are requesting details regarding your conduct for the future.

It is understood and simple that from a distance, it is not the matter to provide detailed instructions, as the matter depends on the nature of the soul of each individual and the conditions of the time and place in which they are found (except as an emergency instruction when it is necessary). In your case, the premise and foundation—which is also the manner of receiving the Torah in its entirety—is sufficient: the precedence of "we will do" to "we will hear." This applies likewise to all parts of the Torah, including the pnimiyus haTorah, its guidance, and its customs. In order to bring this kabalas ol into practice in daily life, you must set fixed shiurim in the study of Chassidus, investigate the customs of Chassidim and conduct yourself accordingly, participate in farbrengens, and the like. You should consult regarding the details with a mashpia of Chassidus at Yeshivas Toras Emes in Jerusalem (may it be rebuilt and established), or, if possible, at Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod.

You surely know of the three daily shiurim that are equal for every soul, established by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, and you should keep them at least from this point forward.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 3866

B"H, 9 Menachem Av, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, refined, and involved in communal needs, etc.,
R' Moshe Pinchas, may he live, HaKohen

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter—your report regarding the farbrengen of Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Noach,

Although I generally derived pleasure from the aforementioned, and may the strength of all the organizers, those who put in the effort, and the participants—they and their families, may they live—be bolstered; may they all be blessed,

Yet, I am greatly surprised and astonished at some of the anash who do not pay attention to the maamar and the well-known mission of "when your springs spread outward" (*l'chsheyafutzu ma'ayanosecha chutzah*). What kind of "spreading" is it when one sees the same familiar faces at Chabad farbrengens and gatherings? As is evident from the results—for the time being, nothing is being done in this direction. And how long shall this continue?

It is clear that my intention is not to complain about the past, but rather to awaken [you] regarding the future—regarding the Melaveh Malkah farbrengens that are coming up, the Shabbos Mevarchim farbrengens, etc.

And in accordance with the well-known saying of the esteemed Chossid and Tzaddik, etc., etc., R' Hillel of Paritch, that in all his deeds his intention was that through them there would be an increase regarding Chassidus, etc.

And to you, sir, and your colleagues, and to each and every one of the anash who initiates and continues the organizing of farbrengens and the like—I say to you: continue and increase, specifically in this regard.

And then we will merit the conclusion—speedily in our days with the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu—when the mission will be fulfilled: "And the earth shall be full of the knowledge of Hashem, etc."

And "the vessels of service, when full, sanctify" (or at the very least—his intention is to fill them), and "the remainder" (*veyosir*)—we call them "full," with a holiness that comes from the vessels themselves, and a complete holiness—in addition to the holiness of the *oros* (lights) which exist on their own.

For this is precisely the purpose and perfection of creation, as is explained in many places in Chassidus.

With blessings for good tidings regarding the above.

***

3866
Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 20, p. 610, and completed according to the secretariat’s copy.

R' Moshe Pinchas: Katz. Additional letters to him—above, Vol. 11, 3746, and in the references noted there.

Vessels of service: Bamidbar Rabbah 13:14: "A bowl corresponding to the sea, a basin corresponding to the dry land; both are full, etc."

Full, sanctify: Zevachim 88a.

His intention is to fill them: Menachos 8a.

The remainder, etc.: Menachos 88a.

From the vessels: Tosefta Taharos, first chapter, 4.

Complete holiness: Based on Rambam, Hilchos Pesulei HaMukdashin 3:6.

Saying: See also below, letters 3928, 3973, 4079.

## 3867

3867

B"H, 9 MarCheshvan, 5716

Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 2 Rosh Chodesh Cheshvan, and it is understood that what you write—that the "leaven in the dough" of Eretz Yisrael is causing a delay—is noted.

It is well known that our Sages ruled that the air of Eretz Yisrael is pure and its land is pure; if leaven is found, it is not in the dough of Eretz Yisrael, and a word to the wise is sufficient. Furthermore, the ruling of our Sages that "the burden is commensurate with the camel" applies both to the residents of Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) and to Anash, the Chassidim and the Temimim. To elaborate on such an obvious matter would be superfluous...

3868

B"H, 10 Marcheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn

To the G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, and distinguished R' Yisrael Tzvi, may he live, Halevi.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to read what you wrote in your letter regarding your outreach efforts during your time in reserve duty. It is understood that the fact that you conclude by saying you wrote to Eilat and received no reply does not exempt you at all from continuing in this work. You must write, and write again, and send them appropriate printed materials as well, if only to awaken the point of Yiddishkeit within them and bring it to actual, internal expression, as explained in Chassidic discourse.

Regarding your question as to how to respond when people tell you that science supposedly has proof that the world has existed for more than 5,715 years, and whether this can be reconciled with the well-known statement of our Sages that the Holy One, Blessed be He, would build worlds and destroy them—the interpretation of this statement of our Sages is not so. It refers to spiritual worlds, as our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe explains based on the writings of the Arizal in *Torah Or*, Parshas Shemos (page 51d). As for the claim that science has proof of the aforementioned, this is an absolute falsehood. Science has **no proof** of this whatsoever; it has only **theories** built upon **shaky foundations**. It is difficult to explain this at the length required in a letter, but the point is that what is found in scientific textbooks regarding the aforementioned—that the world has existed for many billions of years, etc.—bases this theory on the following:

Since (under the conditions existing **today**—heat, atmospheric pressure, wind movement, the amount of various materials found on the earth's surface, etc., etc.) a certain number of years is required for every hundred cubits of height of sand that accumulates on a riverbank, and since there are mountains made of this very sand that are several miles high, then (assuming that they, too, were accumulated from grains of sand by such a river, and that the aforementioned conditions have not changed throughout all these thousands of years) it would require such-and-such number of years. This calculation arrives at a figure much higher than 5,715.

However, when you ask them where the grains of sand came from, they have no answer. When you ask them—just as you assume that grains of sand were formed on a plain, it is possible to say that the **mountains** were formed all at once—they also have no answer to this. And when you ask them how they know that five thousand years ago all the conditions—the water, the winds, the river, etc.—were exactly as they are now, they have no answer for that either. And when you ask them, in addition to this, if we assume their proof is scientific, how is it possible that the results of research regarding the duration of the world's existence—according to the science of astronomy, according to the science of archaeology, according to the science of geology, and according to the science of radioactivity—contradict one another **from one extreme to the other**? That is—for example—one conclusion is that it is **impossible** for it to be **more than half a billion** years, and a second conclusion is that it is **impossible** for it to be **less than two billion** years, and so on.

These contradictions are clear proof that all these investigations are nothing more than **theories** built on thin air. And this is not the place to elaborate further.

I trust you utilized the days of the month of Tishrei—the general month from which we draw inspiration and joy for the entire year—to influence your surroundings, and you will write about this on the next occasion.

With blessings.

## 3870

B"H, 10 Mar-Cheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Especially since, according to the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov regarding *hashgacha pratis* over every single detail of a person’s life—and particularly regarding Torah and *mitzvos*—it is obvious that all of these [individuals] have been given the strength to rectify the situation, each according to his own circumstances. For our Sages of blessed memory have said, "According to the camel is the burden" (*Sotah* 37a), and the instruction of our holy Nasi is already well-known: "One action is better than a thousand sighs."

As for what you wrote—that they will not listen and will not act in accordance with the instruction—we have no way of knowing this. As our Sages of blessed memory famously said, "If it is revealed **before You**..." (*Shabbos* 55a), which proves that it is difficult for a human being to know this with certainty. This is especially true when we are speaking of those who, to a greater or lesser extent, have benefited from the "light of Torah"—that is, the teachings of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs...

Based on all of the above, it is understood that the improvement and rectification of the situation depends primarily on those who are on the scene. And whoever is greater than his fellow—whether in wisdom or in years—his responsibility, and likewise his merit, is greater. Our Sages of blessed memory have already ruled that the *mitzvah* of *tochachah* (reproof) applies until [the point of being struck] (*Erchin* 16b), and those who are doing the reproving are still far from that point. Our holy Rebbeim, the leaders of Chabad, have already elaborated on the manner of *tochachah*, that it must also be done in ways of pleasantness, and so on. To elaborate on such a simple matter would be superfluous...

With blessings for good news.

## 3872

B"H, 10 MarCheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter from the 2nd of Cheshvan, along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed therein. As you requested, it will be read at an *eis ratzon* at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Since all of Israel are responsible for one another, and there is the added bond of family, know that the more you increase your diligence and persistence in learning, your *avodah* of *tefillah*, and your performance of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*, the more Hashem’s blessing will increase in the matters you wrote about in the aforementioned *pidyon nefesh*. May Hashem grant you the merit and success to share good news regarding this.

I have just received your letter from the 17th of MarCheshvan, along with the four *pidyonos nefesh* that will be read at an *eis ratzon* at the holy *tziyun*. Regarding what you write in your letter about your state of mind—the matter has already been addressed, and explained, in the *Tanya Kadisha*, Chapter 26, 27, and onwards. You can see tangibly that your thoughts about yourself are leading you to *bitul Torah* and to the absurd conclusion that you should leave the *yeshiva*. It is clear from this that these thoughts come from the *yetzer hara*, whose entire purpose is to fight against a person’s spiritual and material well-being using arguments that have no basis in sound reason. Their entire existence is only because "Hashem your G-d is testing you," and when one makes the effort and stands firm in the test, the person himself sees how their entire illusory existence vanishes. You should divert your mind from all these thoughts—without even entering into a *shakla v'tarya* about them, but rather through the "light" approach (for even a little light pushes away much darkness)—and ask your *rosh yeshiva* or *mashpia* to arrange your studies properly, and you should act according to their instructions. May Hashem grant you success.

## 3875

B"H, 14 Menachem Av, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote about reviewing Chassidus: The giving of the Torah was conditional upon the fact that the greatest part of a person’s deeds should be performed through his own free choice, as it is written, "And you shall choose life," and not merely by way of commands and decrees. Rather, one must choose this because it is the decree of the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He. The same applies to the review of Chassidus. The procedure is not that instructions should be sent from here to those you mention in your letter that they should review Chassidus in the shuls. Rather, it is incumbent upon them, through an *is'arusa d'lesata*, to organize a gathering and to obligate—or rather, to grant the merit to—each and every one of them in this most exalted matter. May Hashem grant them success.

With blessings for *parnassah* and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 3777

B"H, 14 Mar-Cheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, engaged in communal needs, R' Tzvi Hirsch, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

It is surprising that since you left, we have had no news from you. Even though the matter of "Yaakov went on his way" has begun—meaning that you have taken with you all the matters of the month of Tishrei, the seventh month, which is "sworn" with all goodness—and you are now influencing this goodness upon the matters of the rest of the months of the year, I am certain you will fill this void at the earliest opportunity. You should also send a clipping from the newspapers there in which words of *hisorerus* and the like were printed.

Enclosed is a clipping from the *Morgen Journal* regarding the books from the *She'eris HaPleita* collection that were distributed to various locations. I would like you to take an interest in this, similar to what some of *anash*, may they live, have done in other places. They have initiated discussions—usually in an informal manner—to exchange books that are rare and are not found in that specific collection, and which, obviously, are not being studied in countries such as Australia, Brazil, etc., for books from Kehot. The rare books should be sent to the library here, where they will be of benefit to many. The benefit in this is twofold: first, that rare books will not lie in a corner like something that has no one to look after it; and second, that there will be an opportunity in those places to see Kehot’s books of Chassidus and the like, or at least *Siddurim*, etc., which will undoubtedly lead to an increase in those who daven, or at the very least, those who read and take an interest. I rely on your understanding as to how to bring this matter to fruition, and *d'l* (a word to the wise is sufficient). It is understood that the expenses for shipping, packing, etc., along with a great thank you, will be covered from here.

With blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

It is possible that she is lacking certain things in the food and drink you are giving her, and that is the reason for her lack of appetite.

## 3881

B"H, 14 Menachem Av, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the eve of Thursday, in which you write the various reasons regarding the proposal to accept the position of *mashgiach* at the yeshiva...

Now, even if we assume that you are correct in part of your explanation—that your nature is not suited to be a *mashgiach* because of your trait of shyness, and that the students will feel too close to you, which will consequently diminish discipline, etc.—all these matters can be corrected by you to a great extent. Since, in my opinion, the time has come to begin taking an interest in settling down and, in time, family life, happy is your portion if you can combine material livelihood with spiritual livelihood—that is, that your position should be in the "tent of Torah." Especially when the offer is in a yeshiva of *Torah Temimah*, where both the revealed and the hidden aspects of Torah are permeated with *yiras shamayim*. It is obvious that this is not an easy task or matter, but then again, other forms of livelihood are not easy in the time of *Golus* either; rather, they have additional trials that are not present in this matter. Elaborating on this simple point is superfluous. You should stop the back-and-forth deliberation regarding matters that do not require such contemplation, and instead, you will be able to utilize your power of *iyun* and *hisbonenus* in the areas where it is actually needed. Regarding the influence on the students, you should view yourself as a *shaliach* of the founder and director of the yeshiva, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nevag"m, zy"a*, and you have nothing to do but prepare your *keilim* to receive the influence and success that is being bestowed upon you.

It is understood that all of the above does not concern the question of salary. You should find out how much others in similar positions at their yeshivos receive, and you need not make concessions regarding yourself, except perhaps for the first few weeks until you become accustomed to your work. Regarding what you write about the learning you are lacking, the matter has already been addressed in *Torah Or*, *Bereishis*, at the beginning, by our Nasi, the Alter Rebbe: that through *tzedakah*, one's mind and heart become a thousand times more refined.

With blessings that you should see the situation as it truly is, and consequently decide as mentioned above, for the best for you in both material and spiritual matters alike, and may it be with success.

P.S.
You wrote that you handed [something] to me before you traveled; I have read it. Many of the matters about which you write will be corrected through your engagement in *meleches hakodesh*—to bring the hearts of the children of Israel closer to our Father in Heaven by inflaming them with the study of our Torah, the *Toras Chaim*, which of course includes the revealed Torah as well. This will facilitate and hasten the rectification of other matters as well, through *avodah* in the appropriate manner and in the appropriate areas.

## 3885

3885

B"H, 15 Menachem Av, 5716
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To our brothers, the children of Israel, who love and cherish Torah and mitzvos,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby send my blessing to all the activists of the Yeshiva, the supporters, and the participants in the preparation for the annual celebration of the Merkaz HaYeshivos Tomchei Tmimim Lubavitch, which is scheduled to take place, G-d willing, on Sunday, Parshas Vayigash, the 3rd of Teves, upcoming.

I greet the friends of the Lubavitcher yeshivos in connection with the privilege they have merited to have a share in supporting one of the greatest fortresses of Torah and yiras shamayim of our time.

Together with this, I send my call—in accordance with the teaching of our Sages that one should only urge those who are already diligent—and I emphasize the special obligation that rests upon all those who understand the vital importance of a yeshiva in general, and the Lubavitcher yeshivos in particular.

Like all matters of Torah and mitzvos, their work for the Lubavitcher yeshivos must be **with alacrity (zerizus)**. As is known, this quality of zerizus was planted by Avraham Avinu in all Jews until the end of all generations. Furthermore, it must be in an **increasing** measure, like every living thing, for the sign of vitality is growth and development.

And as our Sages said: "We elevate in matters of holiness."

In particular, a special privilege and obligation rests upon the lead activists, the initiators and guides, the "doers and makers," upon whom the success of a yeshiva endeavor depends to a great extent.

They must create the necessary momentum of dedication and mesiras nefesh, so that everyone will fulfill their duty according to their strengths—both their revealed strengths and their hidden strengths—and thereby ensure the continued existence and expansion of the Merkaz HaYeshivos Tomchei Tmimim Lubavitch.

By recognizing this great privilege and fulfilling this holy obligation, everyone will merit the blessing of our holy Rebbes, the founders of the Tomchei Tmimim Lubavitch yeshiva, who are constantly arousing great mercy for the supporters of the yeshiva.

May you be blessed with the threefold blessing of children, life, and abundant sustenance, in addition to the blessing of "those who support it are fortunate."

With a blessing for success in all of the above.

#### ***3885***

Published in Likutei Sichos, Vol. 21, p. 479.

## 3886

B"H, 16 Mar-Cheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

It was a pleasure to receive your letter of 7 Cheshvan, in which you write about the good activities of the students of Tomchei Temimim—reviewing Chassidus and performing the mitzvah of the Arba Minim at the proper time, etc. May it be the will of Hashem that the statement of our Rebbe HaZaken on the verse "And tzedakah exalts a nation" be fulfilled in each and every one of them: that their minds and hearts become refined a thousand times over, as explained in the beginning of Torah Or and in Likutei Torah for the three parshiyos in the gloss there.

Regarding what you wrote—that these matters require dedicating time that could have been utilized for one's own learning, and similarly regarding the proposal for the yeshiva to take part in the education of the younger classes in the Tomchei Temimim yeshiva—the greatness of these matters requires no explanation or elaboration. On the other hand, it is also understood that a yeshiva student must learn with persistence and diligence. Both pursuits are good; as for how much time to dedicate to each, not all times and individuals are the same. Therefore, you should consult together with the Rosh Yeshiva and the Mashpia. May it be the will of Hashem that He direct their hearts toward Heaven, for then they will succeed in both matters together.

Regarding what you wrote—that there are avreichim who do not want to go and review Chassidus—it is a matter of wonder and astonishment that students of Tomchei Temimim would lack the desire for this, as it is the opposite of the will of our holy Nesi'im. From this, it is understood that by lacking this desire, they are lacking in their own spiritual standing even more than in the standing of those they are meant to influence. They should gather together and make good resolutions regarding this, for then they will surely have the strength to maintain them, in accordance with what is explained in the maamar beginning with the words "Hechaletzu."

May Hashem grant you the merit to share good news regarding all that was mentioned above.

With blessings.

## 3887

B"H, 16 Cheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Michel Yehoshua, may he live and be well,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I was pleased to receive the news that your son, Amiel, may he live and be well, will be entering the yoke of mitzvos on Thursday, Parshas Vayeira. I hereby express my wishes to you and your wife, may you live and be well, that your son, may he live and be well, will always recognize that his Bar Mitzvah day is the **beginning** of his acceptance of the yoke of Torah and the yoke of mitzvos, and that he will go from strength to strength in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of its mitzvos in his daily life.

Since he will surely be called to the Torah on the upcoming Shabbos, Parshas Vayeira, and will recite the *Boruch Shepatrani*, it is fitting to note that this Parsha contains the source for what our Sages of blessed memory stated (Midrash Rabbah, Parshas Toldos 53:10) regarding the Bar Mitzvah of Yitzchak Avinu—the first Bar Mitzvah celebration—which contains a lesson for all generations, as the word "Torah" comes from the word *hora'ah* (instruction). Our Sages related that the greatest of the nations were present at Yitzchak’s Bar Mitzvah feast, including Og, who mocked the Bar Mitzvah and the future of the Jewish people—a small minority among many nations. The Holy One, Blessed be He, said to him, "By your life, you will see thousands of thousands and myriads of myriads descending from his children’s children."

There have always been those who claimed, and continue to claim, that a way of life according to the Torah serves to eliminate and weaken the strength of the Jewish people, etc. Yet our Sages taught that, on the contrary, the way of Torah is the path of life and eternity, the path of success in both spiritual and material matters.

With blessings,

## 3889

3889

B"H, 18 Menachem Av, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from the eve of Thursday. It is surprising to note the small number of students. I have already expressed this to many of anash for several years: one must exert every possible effort to increase the number of students—both boys and girls—in a proper educational institution. This is especially true when we see that, ultimately, through the students, one also influences the improvement of the parents' situation, in addition to saving the students themselves from an undesirable education. Elaborating on this simple matter is unnecessary. We have also seen tangibly that an increase in the number of students not only does not worsen the financial situation of the yeshiva and educational institution, but on the contrary, it actually improves it.

May Hashem grant you success in bringing good news regarding this soon, for there is nothing that can stand before the will.

Enclosed is the *Kovetz Lubavitch* that was published not long ago. Surely you will utilize its content to influence your surroundings, and the merit of the many depends upon you.

With blessings for success.

## 3890

B"H, 19 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the avreich Shalom Leib, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, which is already with the military rabbinate, describing your role and the fact that you are not in one fixed location, but rather changing your location, etc.—it is certainly unnecessary to awaken you to the great importance of ensuring that food is kosher according to law and custom. Especially since, in addition to it being one of the fundamental mitzvos, it is explained that non-kosher food, Heaven forbid, clogs the heart and the mind, and consequently diminishes a person’s capacity and ability to absorb matters of Torah and mitzvos, and even those mitzvos that human intellect acknowledges. This is alluded to in the Tanya, beginning of Chapter 8. You can surely utilize this role to also explain to those you encounter the great importance of being careful specifically with kosher food.

Beyond all this, it is also understood that you should not be satisfied with your aforementioned official role. Rather, you must take advantage of the fact that you come into contact with many avreichim for whom you might be the only one whose words they will accept regarding Yiddishkeit. Therefore, you must awaken them to the "rock from which they were hewn," the children of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov, and explain and clarify to them that regardless of their status and situation until now, in one hour and in one moment, they are obligated—and it is their privilege—to be kosher Yidden in their day-to-day lives, **in the fullest** sense of the word. You will certainly find in the maamarim of Chassidus and in the holy sichos many points and expressions that will assist you in explaining the above. We are already assured that the involvement of Chassidim in these matters is blessed with success, provided that it conforms to the words of our Sages: "Words that come from the heart enter the heart."

May it be the will of Hashem that you do all of the above to the best of your ability. This will also add to the blessing of the Ribono shel Olam and your success as an individual, so that the verse "and do not hide yourself from your own flesh" may be fulfilled, enabling you to go from strength to strength in the study of Torah and the performance of His mitzvos with hiddur.

With blessings, and with regards to his friends, may they live, who will desire to fulfill [these matters], and then they will succeed in fulfilling the command of the Creator of the world, "And your camp shall be holy, so that He, your G-d, may walk in the midst of your camp, etc." (Devarim 23:15).

## 3891

B"H, 19 Menachem Av, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Erev Shabbos along with its enclosure, and I am enclosing the booklet, the contents of which you will surely be able to utilize regarding the matters we have discussed several times in our conversations of *hisorerus*, etc.

Now, although it seems that my words below do not always have the effect I intend, I must say, at the very least in brief, that I see your involvement in the strengthening and development of the *beis medrash* is not at all in accordance with what the matter requires. It is essential for your own personal benefit—not to mention the benefit of the *beis medrash*, etc.—that you change this attitude from one extreme to the other. That is to say, you should set aside all the calculations and grievances you have against the *baalei batim*, etc., and look at the matter in its true light: namely, that this is your *avodah* in *ruchniyus* and your *avodah* in *gashmiyus*. If the *baalei batim* are helping you in this, you must show them gratitude; and if someone is not helping you as you would like, it is understood that this is no reason to neglect a matter that concerns you and your family—may they live. It is also obvious that there is no place for keeping score with others or being angry, when the matter is not someone else’s, but your own. Much more could be said on this, etc.

With blessings for success in the above.

## 3892

B"H, 19 Menachem Av, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and involved in communal needs, R' Tzvi, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

Following your longest silence, your letter of 17 Cheshvan was received. Even in it, the reason for your silence is not to be found. Most importantly, you do not even mention in this letter how you utilized the days of the month of Tishrei—the month that encompasses the entire year and is saturated with all good. It is incumbent upon a person to draw this goodness into the rest of the months of the year. I hope that this is merely a deficiency in writing and reporting, and that all these matters were indeed accomplished in their entirety.

Regarding what you wrote—that there is no minyan in the shuls in the evening—it would be worthwhile to make an effort to rectify this. This is not merely a question of *tefillah* in a *tzibbur*; it is also about the stability and strength of the *beis medrash*, as the *baalei batim* and neighbors, etc., must know that the *beis medrash* is open as frequently as possible. You are surely aware of the requirement in previous generations, and the aspiration that a *beis medrash* should be open all day and all night, so that the entire vicinity knows that if one has a few free minutes, one should dash into the *daled amos* of *tefillah*, look into a *sefer*, etc. The magnitude of this matter in spirituality, and even its influence on daily life, we have seen and continue to see tangibly.

On one hand, I was pleased by what you wrote regarding the various *shiurim*. However, it is surprising that I do not find a *shiur* in the *halachos* required for daily life. As I have written to several of *anash*, ultimately, "This is the whole of man: fear Hashem and keep His *mitzvos*."

Regarding what you wrote about the topic of *Me'orei Yisrael*, you are surely aware that in *HaShmuessin* and *Talks*, several *maamarim* have been printed on this subject...

Enclosed is the *Kovetz Lubavitch* that was published not long ago. Surely you will utilize its content to bring merit to the many, and the merit of the many is dependent upon you.

With blessing.

## 3893

B"H, 21 Menachem Av, 5716
Brooklyn.

In response to your letter, in which you write that you are preparing, G-d willing, to receive semicha.

May it be the will of Hashem that you contemplate deeply, *aliba d’nafshi*, the matter of semicha—that a person receives the power of Torah to teach and to distinguish between the *assur* (forbidden) and the *muttar* (permitted). The *assur* is bound and shackled by the *kelipos*, having no ascent until the time of the end, while the *muttar* is that which can be elevated through the *avodah* of man, as explained in *Tanya*. May this contemplation set you on the straight path to *asukei shema'tasa aliba d'hilchasa* (derive the halachic conclusion from the study) and to judge with truth, *emes la'amito*. It is already known from the ruling of the *Mishnah* how one arrives at this: that the fear of Hashem must precede one’s wisdom, for only then does one’s wisdom endure.

Surely you have fixed times for the study of *Chassidus*, the "light of the Torah," which illuminates the study of the *Nigleh* as well, making it easier to align with the intent of the Giver of the Torah.

With blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 3894

B"H, 22 Marcheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Peace!

In response to your letter of 14 Cheshvan, in which you write that this year you are not as interested as you were last year in teaching the students in your class, because they do not have the same capacity to absorb the material as the previous class.

Understandably, the opposite is true: this matter should provide even more enthusiasm and interest than usual to bring these students to the proper level. For this is the whole purpose of man—to rectify his portion in the world in accordance with the talents that Hashem Yisbarach has bestowed upon him. Especially when one has a talent for chinuch and influence over youth, this is the very purpose of one’s creation: to increase light in the world by spreading "the mitzvah is a candle and the Torah is light." And "according to the effort is the reward"—it is precisely these students, whose talents are not as developed, who are the "beautiful portion" through which to fulfill the will of the Creator and the attribute of Hakadosh Baruch Hu, "measure for measure," but many times over. When one fulfills the will of Hashem Yisbarach—even though the yetzer hara tries to convince one that it is a difficult task—Hakadosh Baruch Hu then fulfills the will of the person, granting his heart's good desires.

May it be Hashem’s will that with added strength and vitality, you will take an interest in improving the state of the class, that they will rise from level to level, and that you will see good fruit in your work. And "one mitzvah leads to another," so that you will soon be able to report that the students are making great strides, and that Hashem Yisbarach has enabled you to find your good zivug, good in gashmius and good in ruchnius alike.

With blessings for good tidings and with respect.

## 3895

B”H, 22 Marcheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from some time ago regarding the various ways in which the state of education in the kosher institutions in your area could be improved, but noting that the administrators of these institutions are not particularly pleased when others interfere in their affairs.

It is simple, however, that since the welfare of the students—both boys and girls—is the primary concern, one must find pleasant ways and peaceful methods to do everything possible to improve the curriculum, the methods of education, and so on. The parable is already well-known: a correction that seems minor at the time of planting a seed can sometimes change the tree that grows from that seed from one extreme to the other; the application of this parable is understood. From this, it is also understood that regardless of which educational institution one favors more, one must improve the situation in all institutions where one’s influence reaches, as our Sages of blessed memory said: "He who has eaten garlic and his breath is foul, let him eat more garlic [and eat again, so that his breath will not be noticed]".

Regarding what you heard from so-and-so about a proposal for some students from the Yeshiva here to come to study, etc.: in matters such as these, the aforementioned person must approach the official administration of the institution here in a formal manner. This obligates the administration more to fulfill all the conditions that will be stipulated, and consequently, the proposer will consider in advance what to propose, etc. It seems that some time ago, contact was already made with the administration here regarding this.

I trust that upon your return home, you shared in a timely manner the points discussed during the farbrengen here. May it be the will of Hashem that these matters lead to practical action, as it is written: "Fear Hashem and keep His mitzvos, for this is the whole man."

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 3896

B.H., 23 MarCheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 19 Cheshvan and the enclosure.

As you requested, I will mention you and your entire family—may they live—at a time of favor at the holy resting place of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for a year of success. One of the aspects of this is that every single day must accomplish its own work—the work appropriate for that day and the work of that specific individual—for the capabilities, and consequently the required work, of each person are not the same.

You are surely familiar with the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, which is also transcribed in the *Hayom Yom*, that despite the great value of the matter of baking bread—for bread sustains the heart of man (*enosh*—even a simple man)—if someone has the ability to be a diamond cutter, he does not fulfill his obligation at all by occupying himself with baking bread.

He wrote this in a letter to one of the *Temimim* in response to his informing him that he had established *shiurim* in *nigleh*, and so on.

From this, the directive for each of us—and you are included in this—is simple: no matter how much one might truly value his work in strengthening Yiddishkeit in general, he does not fulfill his obligation through that alone at all. Since you have merited to be raised in the home of Chabad Chassidus, and have also tasted to a certain degree—and perhaps even a significant degree—of the teachings of this Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs, whose foundations include the spreading of the *maayanos* (specifically) outward (specifically), and the approach of Chabad Chassidus is already known—that every matter must be done in a way that it is absorbed internally—yet in the vast majority of the articles written by you in the newspaper, I have not yet found that you are occupied with fulfilling this internal and spiritual task.

It is understood that I do not necessarily mean that you should utilize the newspaper in this direction, for there are many paths to this *avodah*, and the person doing the work must choose the most effective and lasting path. My intention in the above is only to say that I have not heard that you are utilizing your talents in other ways, and even in your aforementioned articles, they have not yet been utilized for the spreading of the *maayanos* outward. I am confident that with even a slight amount of contemplation, you will find several ways to act with your talents specifically in this matter, in line with the *derashah* of our Sages, "Honor Hashem with your wealth (*mehoncha*)"—do not read it as *mehoncha*, but as *mechonecha*, from what He has endowed you with (*mechonecha*).

May it be Hashem’s will that you contemplate this soon, and consequently begin this soon, and may it be with success. And according to the measure of the *Ribono shel Olam*, which is measure for measure, this will add to the *nachas chassidish* that you and your wife—may they live—receive from all your children, and from yourselves as well.

With blessings.

## 3897

3897

B"H, 23 MarCheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 19th of MarCheshvan, which caused me some surprise as I read it, for it was written with a tone of *kapdanus* (strictness) regarding so-and-so. Even though our Sages of blessed memory have said that Kohanim are prone to *kapdanus*, surely, apart from the fact that one need not begin one’s *avodah* as a Kohen specifically with this trait—as there are many other matters that take precedence—why utilize *kapdanus* toward another person? A person is closer to himself, and this is especially true when the person in question is not a distant "other," but rather the very person who completes him and makes what is "not good" into something that is "good."

Perhaps you still remember what I said to you regarding so-and-so, that the matter of *shalom bayis* also impacts one’s *parnassah*, as stated in the Mishnah at the end of Maseches Uktzin, and in *Likutei Torah* at the end of *Parshas Berachah*. If one is required—according to Torah—to make an effort in natural matters upon which *parnassah* depends, then how much more so must one make an effort in those matters dictated by Torah upon which *parnassah* and longevity depend. To elaborate on this is simple, yet superfluous; I have only come to awaken and illuminate the fact that such matters, even if they appear insignificant and small in the eyes of men, are precisely the touchstone of how much so-and-so is a Chossid, as is explained and understood from several *sichos*.

May it be the will of Hashem that very soon you will inform me that you have begun **to work** on yourself in this direction, and then you will also merit to inform me that you are seeing success in this *avodah*.

With blessings to hear good news regarding all that was mentioned above, and also regarding the expansion of your *parnassah*.

## 3898

B"H, 24 Menachem Av, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 9 Cheshvan, in which you describe your state of mind and your bitterness, and in which you seek an answer, concluding with the question: "Is there still a teshuvah?"

There is no room for this question. As our Sages ruled, there is nothing that stands before teshuvah. This is also proven by the fact that the Anshei Knesses HaGedolah ordained for **every** single Jew to say in their davening, "Bring us back to You, and we shall return," followed immediately by the blessing, "Forgive us." This is recited with the mention of Hashem’s Name and Kingship; if there were any doubt, Heaven forbid, regarding the matter, the rule of "doubt in blessings—be lenient" would apply. Therefore, there is no doubt here at all, as is explained at length in Iggeres HaTeshuvah by our Alter Rebbe, Chapter 11.

Regarding your question as to what the path to teshuvah is: this, too, is simple. It must consist of regret for the past, and primarily, a resolution for the future, conduct that aligns with this resolution, and fulfillment in practice—in "doing good" that one is obligated to do, and in "turning away from evil" regarding the mitzvos of Hashem that one must not transgress. Certainly, to know all of this, it is understood that one must study the halachos required for daily life and review them until the study leads to action. And for siyata d'shmaya, it is essential that every day, after morning davening, you say some chapters of Tehillim, and also set a regular time for studying Chassidus, which illuminates a person's path in life. May Hashem grant you success.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe Shlita

## 3899

B”H, 24 Cheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Your letter of 19 Mar-Cheshvan has been received.

Regarding what you wrote about the idea of moving to live in... — on the face of it, it is a very sound idea. However, in the present case: a) A new residence must be with her full consent and without any coercion of your wife, may she live. b) One must not compromise the quality of the children’s chinuch, may they live. c) Since you are away from home for several hours a day and she, may she live, is necessarily left at home — there must be relatives or friends in close proximity to your residence. It seems to me that as far as you are concerned, none of these conditions are currently met.

It would be worthwhile for you to compare your letters from... and see clearly to what extent your writing is unfounded and leads to a lowering of spirit, and surely also a lack of vitality in your holy work. From this, you should learn for the future that if the Yetzer Hara comes again and tries to frighten you about how you will fulfill your obligation, etc., etc. — you should not even pay attention to his words, and instead utilize your time and energy in your holy work of bringing the hearts of the Children of Israel closer to our Father in Heaven, and specifically with joy. As mentioned above.

3900

With blessings that you choose your beautiful portion, which is your gateway for all elevations from below to above and for all draws from above to below, and may you do this with joy and a glad heart.

## 3901

3901

B"H, 25 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter with the enclosed *pidyon nefesh*, which will be read at the *eis ratzon* at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zya".*

Regarding what you write—that you are unable to accomplish anything in any matter—Heaven forbid to say such a thing. For the Torah is eternal, and it was given specifically to every single individual of Israel. As is known, this is one of the reasons why the Ten Commandments—and especially the first and second commandments, which contain the entire Torah—were stated in the singular. From this, it is understood that you, too, have the merit to engage in *hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah*—the teachings of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs.

While it is understood that the methods of dissemination depend on the time and place, in every time and place there exists the ability and the possibility for dissemination. Our Sages of blessed memory said, "You have labored and you have found." Furthermore, the attribute of the *Ribono shel Olam* is *middah k'neged middah* (measure for measure): when one increases the spiritual health of their environment, the *Hashem* increases, many times over, the spiritual—and also the physical—health of the person who engages in this.

May the *Hashem* lengthen your days and years, and may He strengthen and increase the light that is your portion in the world, with *harchavas hada'as*.

With blessings,

## 3803

B"H, 26 Menachem Av, 5716
Brooklyn.

## 3896

B"H, 29 Mar-Cheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn.

The minutes also mention and prompt the actions that were decided upon. According to the common practice, from time to time, certain clauses of the decisions that were adopted should be publicized in order to give them greater validity; the standard way to do this is by posting them on a wall or the like...

May it be done in an orderly fashion and with the appropriate expansion, as it is written, "And I will walk in a broad place," even in terms of quantity.

And in keeping with the avodah and the spiritual mission of spreading the wellsprings outward, you will surely endeavor that even those who for the time being are still "outside" will participate in the celebration and the farbrengen in great numbers. It is a established principle regarding the words of our holy Nesi'im that they will be heard and recalled at the time of the farbrengen, so that they will effect a change in each and every one of the participants, for their words are alive (leben) and, consequently, they also bring to life (machen lebedig)—and with true life.

Awaiting good tidings.

## 3807

3807

B"H, 29 Mar-Cheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent communal worker, R' Avraham Chanoch, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

...Your letter of 11 Mar-Cheshvan has been received. I am writing now because, as we are entering the month of redemption, we must plan well in advance how to utilize the auspicious days of Shabbos and the following Sunday, the bright day of 19 Kislev, for the purpose of *hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah*—within the framework of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, the Yeshiva, the village, and so on. Since it is human nature to be more enthusiastic when things are done through *is'arusa d'lesata* (initiative from below), I do not wish to write about this in detail to all the various institutions. I will, however, touch upon the general point, and I am certain you will find the ways and means to inspire all of the above in good time, so that matters may be arranged in the best possible way.

From this, it is understood that one must strive in the aforementioned, and on the contrary, the number of visitors during this *eis ratzon* (time of favor) should be increased and expanded. Regarding perfumes—a matter of *makif* (encompassing light)—our Sages have said that one who passes through a perfumery absorbs its scent, for it is impossible otherwise. How much more so is this true regarding Chassidus, its Torah, its guidance, and its customs, which are both *pnimiyus* (internal) and *makif* (encompassing) at once; one absorbs not only the scent, but also internal matters. And if, for the time being, one does not see this with physical eyes, one must examine and search to see where the deficiency lies—*v'da lecha* (and to the wise, a word is sufficient).

It is surely unnecessary to remind you regarding writing in the newspapers, and it would be very good to include the children's newspapers as well, in connection with the days of 10 and 19 Kislev, the fifth candle of Chanukah, and so on.

Surely you will arrange for radio broadcasts regarding these auspicious days, and connect and conclude the narrative of the past with the *b'po'al mamash* (actual reality) and the "therefore" regarding the present. Also, record the main *farbrengen*, as was done last year.

Regarding what you wrote about material for the upcoming publication, surely you will utilize the *farbrengens* and the accounts shared by the guests from Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) who visited here, the national convention of N'shei U'Bnos Chabad, the 19 Kislev *farbrengen*, and so on. And, of course, based on the ruling of our Sages that it is a *mitzvah* to publicize those who perform *mitzvos*, the simple reason being that this creates "jealousy among scholars that increases wisdom."

## 3808

3808

B"H, 29 Mar-Cheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, who occupies himself with communal needs, the G-d-fearing, etc.,
Eliezer shlita, Pinchas shlita, Chaim Shamaryahu shlita

Greetings and blessings,

In response to your letter of 21 Cheshvan, along with the enclosure—the bylaws of the Tiferes Dos Chessed Tzedakah (Tadchatz) organization and the letter from its board, in which you write regarding the plot of land in Tel Aviv, etc., and ask for my opinion:

1) Based on experience regarding matters in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt speedily, if there is any form of shared ownership, one cannot be secure against future aggravation. Therefore, it does not seem right to me that the plot should be registered not only in the name of Agudas Chabad, but also in the name of Tadchatz. Especially since it is also incomprehensible: if they have no desire to involve themselves at all, and if they will have no part in the building, what benefit will they gain from the plot being in their name as well? It serves only as a potential opening for someone to claim that they, too, are an owner, etc. And even if the current board members are beyond suspicion in such matters, the building and its usage are intended for long, good years; consequently, one must take into account the possible changes in the leadership of the aforementioned organization. Most importantly, there is no logical basis for why they would insist on this demand. It is understood that their rights should not be diminished in the slightest—and consequently, the donors of the mitzvah who gave the plot as a gift should be publicized, and this should be printed on all forms—but one should not leave room for ownership, as mentioned above. Since the building will surely cost a significant sum, if it is built on a plot in which others have a share, it is liable to lead to many frictions, etc., and a word to the wise is sufficient.

2) It would be appropriate not to limit yourselves specifically to the matter of a yeshiva on this plot. Especially according to your letters, which you have repeated time and again—that it is difficult to obtain students in Tel Aviv, and it is almost impossible, etc. (surely you have kept copies of your letters). It is understood that to invest tens of thousands of liras in a building and then bring students from Lod just to fill the building—it is doubtful whether this is worthwhile. [Missing line] ...of Agudas Chabad, Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, and N'shei U'Bnos Chabad, etc., etc.

3) All of the above is a last resort, but it is understood that the most correct path is for the Tadchatz organization to agree to sell the plot, and to invest this money in buildings in Kfar Chabad and in all the aforementioned merits, where it will be written that this was done with their money, etc., etc.

Awaiting a detailed letter in connection with the above, and thanking you in advance,

**M. Schneerson**

## 3809

B"H, 29 Mar-Cheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished chossid, who engages in communal needs,
Rabbi Refael Nachman, may he live and be well, HaKohen

Shalom u’Bracha!

I was pleased to receive your letter informing me of your improved health, and may it be Hashem’s will that you go from good to better.

It is surprising that you do not write in detail whether any action was taken in any direction regarding the *p’nimiyus* and the words that the guests from Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, surely conveyed upon their return. As has been discussed at *farbrengens* many times, and also this past Shabbos Mevarchim, "idle words" (*devarim batelim*) do not necessarily mean only when one speaks about trivial matters. Rather, it is also meant literally: if one speaks with a certain intention and goal, and that intention and goal are not realized, then the words automatically become "idle words." The intention and goal of a *farbrengen* and words of *hisorerus* is that they should lead to a "therefore" and to actual deed, and not merely provide *nachas ruach* at the time the words are heard—*az es gefelt der vort* (then the word is appreciated). May it be Hashem’s will that I merit and succeed in receiving good news regarding this.

I conclude with the good news that on Erev Shabbos Bereishis, you brought your grandson, Aharon Menachem, may he live and be well, into *cheder*. May it be Hashem’s will that from a "five-year-old for Mikra," he grows to be a "ten-year-old for Mishnah," and a "thirteen-year-old for Mitzvos," etc., as the Mishnah rules.

And regarding the good news that on Monday, 25 Mar-Cheshvan, you brought your grandson, Yosef Simcha, may he live and be well, into *cheder*—may it be Hashem’s will that he grow to be a Chassid, a G-d-fearing person, and a *lamdan*.

May you and your wife, may you live and be well, derive much Chassidishe *nachas* from your children, your sons-in-law, and all your descendants, may they live and be well.

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 3812

3812

B”H, 29 Mar-Cheshvan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...On this occasion, I wish to urge you regarding the fact that it is not evident from any of your letters that you are dedicating your time and energy to *hashpaah* within your own home—that is, upon your wife and children, *shichyu*, and through pleasant ways and matters of *kiruv*.

I am writing the word "dedicate" precisely, for this is a matter of *kedushah*, as it pertains to the existence of a *am kadosh*.

A verse does not depart from its plain meaning: "And you shall teach them to your children," as is also explained in the *halachos* of *Talmud Torah*. This is especially so given the well-known *sicha* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *n.e.*, which begins with the point that just as one is obligated to put on *tefillin* every day, so too is one obligated to dedicate time to *hashpaah* upon his wife and children, etc., etc.

It is understood that one cannot fulfill this obligation with matters of "sharp" Chabad intellect or *oros* without *keilim*, at the expense of others. Ultimately, this is also at one’s own expense. May *Hashem* grant you success in serving as a **living** example in this matter for your friends and acquaintances as well.

It is understood that one should not be distressed over the time required for these activities, because, as mentioned above, through this one sanctifies the time, and a *mitzvah* draws after it another *mitzvah* and *kedushah*.

I await good news regarding **everything** mentioned above.

#### ***3812***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 21, p. 432.

**Well-known sicha:** See above, Vol. 5, letter 1591, and the references in the notes there.

## 3813

3813

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 8th, with the enclosure, in which you also write that Mrs. ... told you that she does not know if she will be able to fulfill the practice of putting money into a tzedakah box every day.

You should explain to her that this does not mean she should give more than she is able to, but rather that instead of giving the total amount all at once, she should give it in small increments every day. While for the tzedakah fund itself there is no difference whether she gives it all at once or in multiple installments, for the person giving the tzedakah, there is **a great** difference, because one must accustom oneself to giving tzedakah every day. Just as a person makes expenditures for the things that **he** needs and **wants** every day, so too must one make expenditures every day for the things that Hashem Yisbarach—through which the prayers and requests of the person are [answered]—wants and commands us to give, which is the matter of giving tzedakah. And what is even better—one must rely on Hashem Yisbarach every day, not just once every many days. You will surely find the appropriate words to explain this to her: that tzedakah—regardless of the amount, whether more or less—should be given every day (naturally, excluding days when one is not permitted to handle money, Shabbos and Yom Tov). And I thank you for your efforts in this matter.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe Shlita,

Secretary

Published in Likutei Sichos, Vol. 9, p. 295.

## 3814

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 27th of Cheshvan, along with the list enclosed therein.

Regarding what you wrote about the state of your health, as well as the difficulty in the holy work of educating the children of Yisrael in Torah and mitzvos: these two matters are interdependent. If you would listen to my advice, you should endeavor with all your might to be master over your nerves and to accept all matters with calmness. This is especially true when you contemplate that everything is by Divine Providence, and you should not view your surroundings as if they are seeking ways to hinder or obstruct your steps—even if there were some basis for such a feeling. It is already a known ruling of our holy Torah that "as in water, face answers to face," and so on. When your outlook changes to an "ayin tovah" (a good eye), it will be "as in water, face answers to face," and this will also serve to improve your general state of health. Furthermore, this will make the work of chinuch easier for you, as is clearly evident in many people and in many cases similar to this.

Enclosed is what was published recently, and surely you will merit to bring merit to the many, for the merit of the many depends upon you.

With blessings.

## 3815

3815

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, Mr. A. Friedrich, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I am surprised that for quite some time I have not received any news from you. If, according to the accepted custom, this is a sign that everything is in order and at peace, and therefore there is nothing to write about, that applies only to personal matters. However, regarding communal matters, according to the ruling of our Sages, one must always ascend in holiness; therefore, there is always something to write about concerning new developments.

This is especially true now that we have recently entered the new year, and one must re-establish all schedules and fixed times for learning. For one to whom Hashem Yisbarach has given the talent to be able to influence others, this is one of his primary, essential, and vital tasks.

In particular, I wish to urge you to continue and expand your lectures for women. Through this, one strengthens and influences the improvement of their families’ Yiddishkeit in general, and the upbringing of their sons and daughters in particular. Even when children conduct themselves in a Torah-true manner, unfortunately, in the vast majority of cases, there is a lack of knowledge regarding the laws and customs. Furthermore, the mothers lack the knowledge to be able to answer the many questions that arise in children through their peers and various other reasons and circumstances.

Our Sages have already said that one only urges those who are already diligent. Therefore, I hope to receive from you good tidings regarding the development of this matter, as well as other matters. Hashem Yisbarach will surely grant His reward, which is measure for measure, but many times over—an addition of "a candle is a mitzvah, Torah is light," and the light of Torah, which is the inner dimension of the Torah—in your own family, and he himself included.

Awaiting good tidings.
