## 3817

3817

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

It is surprising that since your letter before Rosh Hashanah, no news has arrived from you, especially regarding how you utilized the days of the month of Tishrei—the general month for the entire year, which is saturated with all good—and it is incumbent upon a person to draw this good into the remaining months of the year. I am certain you will make up for this at the next opportunity.

Regarding what you wrote then about a detailed schedule for the study of Nigleh and Chassidus: in general, one requires both *limud l’iyuna* (in-depth study) and *limud l’migras* (study for fluency/review). *Limud l’migras* should consist of the weekly Parshah, a tractate from the division of Shas, and the Halachos required for daily life in Nigleh. In Chassidus, *limud l’migras* should be the weekly Parshah (Torah Or in the winter, and Likutei Torah in the spring and summer) or the Kuntreisim printed for specific times. As for *limud l’iyuna*, both in Nigleh and in Chassidus, one should study wherever one’s heart desires, as per the well-known statement of our Sages. The specifics—how much time each day and when—naturally depend on the individual’s circumstances, and therefore you should consult with your friends among Anash in your location.

Regarding your question as to what field you should engage in: it is understood that if Hashem has graced you with the talent for education and for influencing others, you should utilize this gift. In order to utilize it to the greatest and best extent, if at all possible, it is worth the effort that your material livelihood also come from this. Regarding the recipient, it does not make such a great difference whether one is doing it *lishmah* (for its own sake) or also for the sake of one’s own livelihood. As is well known from the statement of our Sages (Sifrei, Teitzei 24:19) that if one loses a coin and a poor person finds it, it is considered an act of Tzedakah. It is obvious that all of the above is in addition to the three daily *shiurim* that are equal for every soul, established by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—in Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—which I am certain you are keeping.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 3818

B"H, 1 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and diligent in communal affairs, R' Aryeh, may he live:

Shalom u'Bracha!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from Monday, and regarding what you wrote concerning the story about medical matters and the structure of the skull: It seems you are referring to what I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory:

His father, the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory, was approached by one of the members of his household with great excitement, saying that he had just read about a new discovery regarding the path of the nerves in the head. The Rebbe, of blessed memory, replied that this matter is already found in the Chassidic writings of the Mitteler Rebbe, son of the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch. He took out the volume of writings and showed him the passage inside. He concluded by saying that the Mitteler Rebbe knew this not because of his expertise in medical matters, but because he knew the matters as they are in the "Supernal Man," for the "lower man" is in His image and likeness.

And one is obligated to speak in the language of his teacher, so I must add what my father-in-law, the Rebbe, added: that the remark from this member of the household occurred at the time when the Rebbe Rashab was drying his hands for netilas yadayim. He was not at all pleased that he was being approached with conversation at that moment; therefore, at the time of the remark, he merely looked at the speaker, and only after the blessing of Hamotzi did he answer as mentioned above.

And a matter mentioned in passing teaches us: that there is a kavanah required not only during the recitation of the blessing of the netilah, but also during the drying, and consequently, the speech of another is a distraction.

Enclosed is the *Lubavitch* collection that was published recently; I am certain it will interest you, and may you merit to share its contents with the many, for the merit of the many depends upon you.

With blessings.

***

3818

R' Aryeh: Levin, Jerusalem. Additional letters to him - see above, Vol. 11, 3697, 3771.

That I heard: See Sefer HaMaamarim 5710, p. 140.

## 3819

By the Grace of Hashem, 2 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs, a man of noble character, a scion of a noble lineage, etc., R’ Sh.Z. Shazar, may he live.

Shalom u’Bracha!

To my surprise, I received a copy of the correspondence regarding the dining hall in Kfar Chabad. The content indicates that at the meeting held regarding the construction of the dining hall, with the participation of the representatives of the offices, it was determined that due to the rise in the cost of building materials and labor, the construction would cost several thousand liras more than originally planned. Consequently, they decided to build a smaller structure!

Now, in addition to the well-known principle in Kabbalah that *Tzimtzum* is the source of *dinim* (judgments), in general, it is not my way to downsize, G-d forbid, but rather the opposite—to expand.

According to my perspective, it is the duty of every person to strive to increase the good, not to leave it as it stands, and certainly not to diminish it. As our Sages expressed it so succinctly: "We increase in holiness."

I am confident that you will also agree with my opinion that it is not appropriate to downsize a project that, in its entirety, costs tens of thousands of liras, simply because of a price increase of a few thousand liras due to the rising cost of building materials, etc.

Knowing that the agricultural school in Kfar Chabad is your initiative, and that you have nurtured this enterprise from its inception—in addition to the many efforts you have invested in the development of the village in general—I believe it is your merit that this matter, too, should be brought to its proper resolution through you. That is why I am writing to you about this.

Nevertheless, if it is **absolutely** impossible to increase the loan for the agricultural school to carry out the plan in its entirety, I am prepared, as a last resort, to urge *anash* to conduct a special fundraising campaign—even though, according to the payment terms from Chabad’s side, the time for repayment is still in the future—to raise the surplus for the dining hall caused by the rise in the cost of building materials, etc., in accordance with the aforementioned letter. The responsibility is mine, and, with the help of Hashem, it will be settled before the completion of the building.

I was pleased to learn from R’ B.G. that you participate in a public *shiur* on Maseches Bava Metzia. You are surely aware of my instructions at the beginning of the year—at the start of the study term in the Chabad yeshivos—that the higher classes should study Maseches Bava Metzia. For this reason, we specifically printed this tractate with an addition: *chiddushim* (novellae) in *nigleh* by the Rebbe, the Tzemach Tzedek, as well as his *maamar* for the beginning of the tractate and his *maamar* for its conclusion. I have instructed that three copies of this tractate be sent to you in a separate package. Naturally, the first is for you, the second for the head of the study group, and the third for the *shiur* participant. I am troubling you with their delivery, as I hope that through this, you will have the opportunity—and certainly the words that come from the heart—to explain to them the concept of "two holding a garment" based on the points in the Tzemach Tzedek’s *maamar* printed in the supplement. I ask your forgiveness for the trouble. The supplement, which was also printed separately, is being sent to you by airmail.

To conclude on a positive note: as the bright day of 19 Kislev, the day of the liberation of our Alter Rebbe, approaches—a day regarding which the Rebbe Rashab adds the explanation, "The festival that redeemed our **soul** in peace, and the light and vitality of our **soul** was given to us"—my hope is that when you participate in the *farbrengen* in Kfar Chabad on this auspicious day, as has been your good custom for several years, you will bring along many of those you influence. So that they, too, may enjoy the radiance of the light of this *farbrengen*, which will surely affect them and leave an impression on the days, weeks, and months that follow. If one who passes through the shop of a perfumer cannot help but absorb its scent, then all the more so with participation in a Chabad *farbrengen*, whose essence is as its name implies—that it should penetrate inwardly, not just in the emotion of the heart, but that it should also conquer the Chabad intellect in the mind. My hope is strong that they will absorb not only the "scent" but also internal matters, and the merit of the many depends on you.

With respect and a blessing for success in all of the above.

## 3921

And regarding what [you] write about losing hope, chas v'shalom—a Jewish daughter must not say such a thing, for Hashem Yisbarach is Kol Yachol—He can do everything—and He wants every Yid to have good, not only in ruchniyus but also truly in gashmiyus.

## 3822

B"H, 2 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the honorable Rav, G-d-fearing, diligent in Torah, R' Ephraim Zev, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter bringing the good news of the wedding of your son, may he live, on Wednesday, the 15th of Kislev, the coming year.

May it be the will of Hashem that it be for good fortune, a *mazal tov*, in a good and successful hour, and that it be the building of a home in Israel, an everlasting edifice built upon the foundations of Torah and *mitzvos*, as they are illuminated by the "light of Torah"—which is the *pnimiyus haTorah*. May Hashem fulfill the requests of your heart, that you may derive much *nachas* from him, and that he may continue to labor in the "tent of Torah."

With blessings of *mazal tov, mazal tov*.

On this occasion, I acknowledge with thanks the receipt of the *sefer*—*Mechilta* with the commentaries *Kav HaMidah* and *Har Ephraim*. Out of affection for the work, even though I lack the time and leisure, I have at least leafed through its pages in haste, and I have transcribed some notes below. The words of our Sages regarding the verse "Es Vahav b'Sufah" are well known.

**Har Ephraim**

**Section 1:** The prophecy of Chananyah ben Azur (*Sanhedrin* 89a). Its status is like one who prophesies what was said to his colleague (to Yirmiyahu), since it was derived via *kal v'chomer* from what was said to Yirmiyahu. Yet, even though he prophesied generally—without saying that it was said to him—one cannot interpret his words as prophesying what was said to Yirmiyahu, since Yirmiyahu had not yet learned that *kal v'chomer*.

The forced explanation is understandable. On the contrary, it seems to me the opposite: that even if he intended to refer to Yirmiyahu’s prophecy, the *halachic* ruling would not be so. *V'kal l'havin*.

But there is no need for all this forced reasoning, for the premise itself is flawed. Even if we were to say that in every case where one speaks generally and does not say "to me," we judge it favorably—assuming he meant to say "Thus said Hashem to the other prophet" and not to himself—in the case of Chananyah, it is impossible to interpret that he meant to say so, for this prophecy came to his colleague, the prophet Yirmiyahu, as it is written (*Yirmiyahu* 28:1), "Chananyah... spoke **to me**." And this is simple.

**Kav HaMidah, 60b:** The *Mechilta* states that "on that day" Yehoshua was anointed. It is implied and reasonable to say that this was in the fortieth year, at the conclusion of Moshe’s reign.

However, it is impossible to interpret the *Mechilta* this way, for immediately following the words of Rabbi Yehudah that "on that day..." come the words of Rabbi Elazar HaModa'i, that this was a **hint** given to Moshe that he would not enter the Land. There is no place for a hint in the fortieth year, after it had already been stated explicitly.

And one cannot say that this is the point of dispute between Rabbi Elazar and Rabbi Yehudah—as to when the passage was said—for if so, the main point is missing from the text.

In general, there is no necessity to interpret "Yehoshua was anointed" as being with the anointing oil and for kingship (and where would the anointing oil have been then?). Rather, it is a term for appointment to authority, similar to how Rashi explains *Shemos* 29:29. [And whoever wishes to interpret it specifically as kingship—even so, the aforementioned difficulty remains, for Shlomo was anointed during David’s lifetime and by his command. But then the question arises: what room would there be after that for the request, "Let Hashem... appoint a man over the congregation"?]

The dispute between Rabbi Yehudah and Rabbi Elazar is straightforward: whether "and place [it] in his ears" (mentioned three times) is a command for an appointment or merely a hint given to Moshe.

- Regarding what is written in *Har Ephraim* there—note what is written in *Chizkuni* on the verse.

**Har Ephraim at the end of the sefer, 121a:** He explains the *Mechilta* here according to the *Mechilta d'Rashbi*. This is evidence to the contrary, as the difference in terminology between the two places—"the Kohanim say" versus "the Yisraelim say"—indicates a difference in the subject matter.

The explanation of the *Mechilta* is simple: that they would be permitted to perform the labors that are permitted in the *Mikdash*, while the prohibition of labor on Shabbos would remain in effect for the other labors. And these constitute the **overwhelming** majority of the thirty-nine *melachos*.

The wonderment of the *Zayis Ra'anan*—I have not merited to understand.

***

**3822**

**R' Ephraim Zev:** Garbuz, Jerusalem.

**Prophecy of Chananyah ben Azur:** Further discussion on this prophecy is explained in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 9, p. 115.

**With the anointing oil for kingship:** See *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 23, p. 190.

3823

B"H, 2 Kislev, 5716

Greetings and Blessings!

When one resolves firmly that he must be fitting for the "rock from which he was hewn," he will certainly be granted an increase of success in his efforts and in rising higher in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of *mitzvos*, and the merit of his ancestors will assist him.

## 3924

B"H, 3 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Your letter from the end of Tishrei reached me in due course. Even if we were to assume that you are correct in all the matters you write about, and in your interpretation of them, the practical conclusion and the resulting feeling of despair are completely rejected and unfounded.

This is especially true since the aforementioned premise is also incorrect. As has been explained, your words would be true if the soul were the only one praying, etc. See *Iggeres HaKodesh*, end of Epistle 25, *Torah Or*, the *maamar* beginning "Shir HaMaalos," and many other places. Based on all of this, it is clear that, on the contrary, the very matters and the state of mind you describe have the potential to arouse a great and powerful *hisorerus*. It is understood, however, that even for this, one requires *siyatta d'shmaya*—even more so than for other matters.

The advice for this is to give *tzedakah* to others—meaning, to bring them closer to *Torah* and *mitzvos* and to the *pnimiyus* of *Torah*. When you do so, you are also drawn closer from Above.

The confusion and the back-and-forth arguments regarding this are a detriment to *Torah* and *mitzvos*, and not merely a waste of time without benefit; on the contrary, there is actual harm in it.

You must compel yourself to keep the *yeshiva* schedule and to influence all your peers to do the same—through your speech, and even more so by being a living example of how a *Tamim* should conduct himself. You should also increase your resolve in drawing others closer.

When the *yetzer hara* comes again with a suggestion to engage in back-and-forth arguments and debates, do not enter into any of it. Explain to it that you are a servant—and even if you were, *chas v'shalom*, a Canaanite slave who might prefer his own freedom—you have not a single moment free for your own affairs, aside from the service of the Master. You are not permitted to waste your time, even on arguments regarding your service to the Master.

Regarding your question about the specifics of how to arrange your studies and their schedule: you are in the Tomchei Temimim *yeshiva*. This should not only be a physical presence in a physical place; you must be present there in your essence as well. This simply means that you must follow and do as the *rosh yeshiva* and the *mashpia* of the *yeshiva* direct.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned, and it is already known that our Sages have ruled: "Whatever is straightforward is superior."

## 3925

B"H, 3 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

We acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 8th of Cheshvan. You have surely received my letter by now, which also contains answers to a significant portion of the issues you write about in this letter. I would add that one should certainly not be impressed—and certainly not feel a sense of despair—by the fact that communal activists sometimes slacken in their efforts, using the well-known excuse that "there is nothing to be done," etc. (It is already known that the hint for *amla* [excuse] is *emes-lo* [truth-no/not truth]).

It is known that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, interpreted the statement of our Sages regarding the era of *Ikvesa D'Meshicha* at the end of Maseches Sotah—which is repeated there several times—that "we have no one to rely upon but our Father in Heaven." Although the context there refers to the shortcomings and curses of that era, he explained that for a Jewish person to sit idly by and justify himself by saying that there is nothing to do but rely [on Hashem], etc., is the very opposite of Torah, and consequently, he falls into the category of the curses of the era of *Ikvesa D'Meshicha*.

It is surprising that you, having been involved in communal work for several years, have been affected by the aforementioned. Surely this is merely a passing mood, and you will proceed to increased effort and *hisorerus*.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 3827

3827

2, 5 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, who engages in the needs of the community, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R’ Yosef, may he live.

Shalom u’vracha!

In response to your letter, which I received on Rosh Chodesh Kislev... it gave me pleasure to read of your activities with your students during the days of Sukkos. Surely you do not content yourself with such activities only during the month of Tishrei, but also seek opportunities throughout the other eleven months of the year. The necessity for this is evident, as it is tangible that one can accomplish much more with youth through indirect means—needless to say, through a farbrengen and a meal—than through direct methods, and to elaborate on this further is unnecessary.

Regarding what you wrote, that the number of students is decreasing because members of Anash are moving their residences from this district, and one cannot foresee the end of this matter—sadly, this does not require deep contemplation to observe. This problem—the relocation of residences from one district to another—has existed for several years in various places, both in Chicago and in other cities, and the past teaches us about the future.

It is a pity that already three years ago, I believe, I drew your attention to the absolute necessity of opening a branch of the shul and Talmud Torah in the new districts of Chicago, and to do so in good time. Even if it is called a "branch" at the outset, the internal intention must be that this branch should serve as a nucleus and a center from which a proper institution will grow, and within it and its surroundings, those who move from the old locations will gather before they become absorbed into a different environment. On every occasion, I would repeat and reiterate this suggestion, sometimes without regard for the old adage that "one does not listen to advice." May it be the will of Hashem that, at the very least, you now act upon this with the greatest possible energy. And no matter how great that energy may be, it will still not suffice in proportion to the demands of the hour and the spiritual importance for tens upon tens of students—and if one Jewish soul is an entire world, how much more so when it concerns many souls.

Enclosed is what I have published recently, which I am certain will interest you, and you will merit to share its content with those around you as well.

Since you do not mention anything regarding your health or the health of your wife, may they live, I trust that everything is in order and in peace.

With the blessing of the month of redemption, the month of Kislev, and as the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (Rashab) n.e. goes: "Our redemption and the liberation of our souls, the light and vitality of our souls, is given to us."

## 3828

B"H, 8 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, who is involved in communal affairs, R' Nissan
May he live

Greetings and blessings,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your book, *HaTorah VeHaOlam*, volume one. Many thanks for your thoughtfulness in sending it. As I leafed through the pages as time permitted, I was pleased to see that it begins with a saying of the Baal Shem Tov and concludes, in a manner similar to the opening, with a saying of the Tzemach Tzedek. Although the contents of the book have their own inherent purpose, one can—from a much higher perspective—utilize them for a purpose even greater: the dissemination of the wellsprings (*hafatzaat hamaayanot*).

Regarding the anecdote told among Chassidim about the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, R' Hillel of Paritch, who said that all the stringencies he adopts in the observance of mitzvos are for the sake of better absorbing the concept of Chassidus:

Several matters are explained in this vein even in the *nigleh* of Torah, where it is stated that some mitzvos, in addition to their inherent purpose, serve as a preparation for a more comprehensive mitzvah. Ultimately, the entire Torah and its mitzvos are for the sake of the ultimate purpose, as it is written: "And Hashem commanded us to perform **all** these statutes, to fear Hashem our G-d." This period of *ikvesa d'meshicha*—this month and these days—is indeed capable of disseminating the wellsprings outward.

For the sake of interest, I have included a few notes, which are transcribed in the margin.

With blessings that for many more years you will succeed in leading your community on the path that ascends to the House of G-d, in good health, in accordance with the hopes and aspirations of our Rebbe, and to influence them to become more and more Chassidish...

***

Some notes: Although the rule is known that one does not respond to a *drush* (homiletical discourse).

*Parshas Chayei Sara* (page 44 and onwards): The reason given for why women die during childbirth due to a lack of care in lighting the candles. One could explain this according to the *peshat*: that this mitzvah was given as a rectification for what Chava caused regarding the Tree of Knowledge, which brought death into the world. When the rectification is missing, one is punished for the **sin of the Tree of Knowledge**. This is similar to the words of our Sages: "The Holy One, Blessed be He, forgave [the sins of] idolatry, etc., but did not forgive the abandonment of Torah—that they did not recite a blessing over the Torah first." When there is no such love for Torah, the punishment for the more severe sins remains.

It should also be noted that the matter of lighting Shabbos candles was also a point of contention with the Karaites and Samaritans, who interpreted "You shall not kindle fire" as meaning that no fire may be burning on Shabbos. It is known how much [our Sages] were stringent in matters that the Tzedukim did not acknowledge. See also the places indicated in *Torah Shleimah*, part 14, page 320.

*Parshas Vayeitzei* (page 63 and onwards): Thank you for your article against compromises (*pesharot*). This is the most alarming breach in this country and in this period. Not only do they not act according to the instruction of our Torah in cases like these—where one must add a fence—but they add breach upon breach under the pretext that by doing so they will at least save the minority, even though one sees the opposite with one's own eyes. However, the fact that you included in this the matter of a *chuppah* under the open sky, which is done here by means of an opening in the roof of the house, requires further study, for this is not a compromise but the matter in its entirety.

*Parshas Vayishlach* (page 67 and onwards): The story regarding the holy Rabbi R' Michel of Zlotchov—a similar story is found in *Likutei Dibburim* 15, by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. However, it is told there regarding the holy Rabbi R' Meir of Premishlan; perhaps these are two separate matters.

Likewise, the story at the end of page 189—see *Likutei Dibburim* 11, the story regarding the Maggid of Mezritch.

Regarding the conclusion of the book with the saying of the Tzemach Tzedek, one should note the saying of the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory, at the end of his *kuntres*, *Etz Chaim*, beginning of chapter 31.

## 3332

B"H, 7 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was quite alarmed when Rabbi Dehlemitz visited me these past few days (he now resides in Cleveland), and in response to my inquiry, he told me that he had heard nothing regarding a mikveh in the camp, and therefore he fears that the matter has not yet been addressed. Now I have received your letter dated 2 Kislev, and I read in it that this concern is well-founded.

Regarding what you write—that the spiritual state is in a decline, etc.—on the contrary, this is an additional reason and further increases your responsibility to rectify matters, since the others are unaware of the magnitude and gravity of the situation. The same applies to the other deficiencies you mention regarding the community’s affairs. It seems your conclusion from these is that there is no need to work there, whereas the conclusion of sound reasoning should be the exact opposite: since Divine Providence brought you to a specific place as the Rav and Mara D’asra, and you accepted the appointment, the responsibility rests upon you. On the other hand, since our Sages of blessed memory have informed us that the Holy One, blessed be He, does not make demands beyond one’s capacity, it is certain that He has already provided you with all the strength necessary to fulfill the task. This is already a known principle, even regarding a deposit for which one receives no payment: if one intended to incline it toward the stricter view, or in any event, if any action was taken by the trustee, the entire responsibility rests upon him (Bava Metzia 43b).

I believe that since you wrote that the expenses involved in the mikveh project are approximately five hundred dollars, I am prepared, with the help of Hashem, to secure a loan for this amount, with the condition that it be repaid over the course of 20 months. A arrangement such as this will make it easier for you to awaken the point of Yiddishkeit that lies within the heart of **each and every** Jew, in order to bring into actuality the matter of the purity of the Children of Israel, which is also a preparation for the fulfillment of the promise, "I will sprinkle pure water upon you." May it be His will that this happens speedily and completely.

Enclosed is what I have written recently, which I am sure you will merit to share with the many, and the merit of the many is dependent upon you.

With blessings.

***

**Rabbi Dehlemitz:** Rabbi Y.L. Deitsch.

**Mikveh in the camp:** See also above, Vol. 11, Letter 3662.

## 3333

B”H, 7 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, engaged in communal needs, R’ Michael, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from the beginning of the month of Kislev, along with the enclosure... regarding what you wrote about whether to make *tna’im* (engagement conditions), since it is the custom of Israel, it is appropriate to make them at the time that both sides agree upon.

Regarding what you wrote about the *mikveh* in Agadir, it is extremely and profoundly astonishing. If in a city, a mother-city in Israel, there is no *mikveh*... all of Israel is responsible for one another, especially since you have merited to taste, at the very least, from the teachings of Chassidus, and you know from the teachings of the Alter Rebbe that "Love your fellow as yourself" and "Love Hashem your G-d" are one and the same. There is no need to elaborate on a matter that is simple, or at the very least, should be simple.

And as for what you write, that it is difficult to build a *mikveh* there, I am astonished: how is it possible to write such a thing? For it is known that the Torah is eternal—not only in every time, but also in every place. Consequently, the *Bnei Yisrael* in Agadir are also obligated in all its *mitzvos*. And it is known that the *Ribono shel Olam* only demands according to one’s strength. If so, it is simple that a *mikveh* must be built there, and the matter depends only on a person of action who will desire to bring this about...

I am confident that if they truly desire to establish a *mikveh* in Agadir, they will find helpers for this on the spot as well. Knowing the situation that existed in Casablanca—even though there was room to say that the *Beis Din* there might feel slighted, etc., and despite all that, they still assisted in the matter—then *a fortiori* in Agadir, one must do as stated above.

...It is certainly unnecessary to arouse you regarding the appropriate preparations, and preparations in their fullness, in connection with the days of the *Yud* (the 10th), *Yud-Tes* Kislev, and the candle of Hashem of *Chanukah*, in addition to the preparations to utilize the days of *Chanukah*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 3334

B"H, 7 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc., R' Yisrael Aharon, may he live.

Shalom u'Bracha!

In response to your letter of 23 Cheshvan, as you requested, I will mention you, your daughter, and your wife—may they all live—for whatever they need, both in material and spiritual matters. Surely, Hashem will grant you merit, and you will succeed in bringing good news regarding your situation.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you of the Chassidic interpretation of the verse, "From Hashem are the steps of man established, and He delights in his way", as explained in the letter of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, which was printed in *HaTamim*. The implication is that wherever one goes or finds himself, he must remember that he was sent there by Divine Providence. Ultimately, he must illuminate that place with the "candle of a mitzvah and the light of Torah," and with the "light of Torah"—which is the teachings of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs. Furthermore, even when he leaves that place and returns to his permanent residence, he must maintain a connection with his friends in the previous location in a manner appropriate to strengthen the *hisorerus* within them, and to increase it from time to time. Since the Ribono shel Olam only demands according to one's capacity, he has certainly been given the strength beforehand to fulfill this primary and most essential task.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

#### ***3334***

**R' Yisrael Aharon, may he live:** Neprestak, Kfar Chabad.

**As explained in the letter:** *Igros Kodesh* of the Rebbe, Vol. 3, Letter 623; see also the General Index under the entry "From Hashem are the steps of man established."

## 3835

B"H, 7 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent in Torah study,
R' Aharon Elimelech, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I have heard about you for a long time, and therefore it was a pleasure to receive your letter, following the letter from the esteemed R' Yaakov Weiss, may he live. Enclosed is a copy of my response to him.

I will take this opportunity to encourage you—relying on the Sages' teaching that one need not urge the already diligent—regarding the fact that in your region there are many youths attending the educational institutions there. Based on the information I have, and especially since we follow the majority, this youth is in need of encouragement and the uplifting of the spirit of the *Yisrael Sava*. If they find someone to inspire them as is fitting, with words that come from the heart, they are capable of becoming a vessel into which these words will enter, bringing about change and action, even in their daily lives.

If in generations prior to our own there was a mistaken notion that one could fortify the youth to withstand the various winds blowing in the world through the study of Torah alone, two generations ago it became clear that study in matters of *yiras shamayim* and *chovos halevavos* is an absolute necessity for **each and every one**. For study without this has caused many casualties (and if only they had not initially opposed the study of *yiras shamayim*, hundreds and thousands of youths of that era would not have strayed from the straight path; there is no need to dwell on this painful matter).

And if a generation ago there was a mistaken notion that even the study of *mussar* was sufficient, experience has come and slapped the faces of those who claimed this. We saw this tangibly and with our own eyes in Russia during the days of the Bolshevik persecutions and the trials that faced the young men and women in particular. Those who stood firm and were saved from this terrible deluge were those in whom the *Torah* of *Chassidus*, its *hislahavus*, and its *mesiras nefesh* were ingrained through appropriate education.

Unfortunately, the trials of the younger generation have not diminished in these years, even if their form has changed. On the contrary, the change in form—which does not touch the essence—often disguises itself in the garb of a *mitzvah* and begins, and sometimes even draws, from matters of *kedushah* (similar to the Sages' teaching that any lie which does not have some truth at its beginning, etc.). This actually increases the trials, primarily in their quality. It is surely unnecessary for me to elaborate on a situation that is terrifying and alarming even in *Eretz Yisrael*—may it be rebuilt and established—especially considering that it is the land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year; it is not the same as being in the palace of a king, etc.

The conclusion from the above is that it is self-evident that I am not coming to preach, but that the merit and responsibility are yours to utilize all your ability and potential to permeate your entire environment with the light within this *Torah*—the *Torah* of *Chassidus*, its guidance, and its customs. This is especially true regarding the youth, who will soon build homes in Israel; any positive change influenced in them is multiplied many times over, as it is fitting for the homes they will build and for those they will influence.

As you are a descendant of our *Rebbe* the *Alter Rebbe*, the well-known *Baal HaHoraah* whose teaching was that "Love your fellow as yourself" and "Love Hashem your G-d" are one and the same (as is also hinted at in the statement of Rabbi Akiva, "Love your fellow as yourself—this is a **great** principle in the **Torah**"), you will surely succeed in this path. The matter depends only on your will. It is already known that the *Beis Din* on High decreed that because of this *mesiras nefesh*—of our *Rebbe* the *Alter Rebbe*—for the *Torah* of *Chassidus*, they decreed in the *Beis Din* on High that in every matter of *Torah*, *yiras shamayim*, and good character traits, the hand of those who are connected to him and follow in his footsteps shall be uppermost.

Awaiting good news, and signing with honor and blessing.

***

**R' Aharon Elimelech:** Shaulson, Rehovot.

*) See *Shabbos* 68a.

**The well-known teaching:** See also above, letter 3833, and the references in the notes there.

## 3398

B"H, 8 Kislev, 5716

I am pleased to receive from time to time reports from Anash in Paris regarding your assistance, involvement, and efforts concerning the Lubavitch Talmud Torahs in Paris, whose mission is to educate Jewish sons and daughters in a manner that brings them closer to our Father in Heaven. ## 3989

B"H, 8 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 7 Cheshvan, which you sent together with your letter of 5 Kislev, in which you write regarding the visit to your home by Mr. [Name] and his family, may they live, and that you found it difficult to grasp the intent of their visit.

You are surely aware of the content of the letter from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in which he wrote to someone that when a person is hungry and satisfies his hunger with bread and a meal, his thoughts are on the bread, the meal, the food, and the drink. However, the inner essence of the matter and its cause is that his soul craves the Divine spark found within those foods and drinks, as is known regarding the interpretation of the verse, "For not by bread alone does man live, but by everything that proceeds from the mouth of Hashem [that is within the bread]" (Devarim 8:3).

Regardless of what their manifest intention may have been, the inner essence and the cause of their visit is that it is certainly within your power to rectify something regarding their affairs in Yiddishkeit. Their souls orchestrated various reasons and circumstances for them to visit you, and consequently, you should be stirred to fulfill your role in drawing their hearts closer to our Father in Heaven. Elaborating on something so self-evident is surely unnecessary; I have only written this to emphasize that you should contemplate and seek further opportunities to bring all of the above into practice in an appropriate manner. It is understood that everything said above applies also to your neighbor, about whom you wrote. (By the way, since she showed you a mezuzah she purchased, it would be worthwhile to at least superficially check if it is kosher.)

Regarding what you wrote concerning the doctor’s words about the condition of your wife, may she live — there is absolutely nothing to be concerned about. In particular, you should read the note you wrote at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, during a time of favor, and convey this with the appropriate firmness to your wife, may she live.

May Hashem fulfill the days of her pregnancy properly and with ease, and may she give birth to a healthy child at the proper time and in a healthy manner, with ease.

With blessings.

## 3440

B"H, 9 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh, in which you write regarding the commencement of Torah study and the classes at your institution. May it be the will of Hashem that you succeed in this endeavor, and through this, also in the *hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah*—which is one of the matters of these days—and the merit of all those who involve themselves in such things is beyond measure.

From this, it is also understood that the conclusion of your letter—where you write that regarding so-and-so, you hope to give him [the instruction] to study *Toras Chabad* after he returns from the hospital—does not seem correct to me: 1) A matter of *refuah* should be prioritized and utilized in order to hasten the recovery. 2) The matter of *Talmud Torah* in general is a "lost item" each and every day, for *Talmud Torah* has no make-up; every single moment is sufficient to exempt oneself [from the obligation of the moment]. 3) It is well-known, and we see it tangibly, that *yoma garim* (the day causes it) and "merit is brought about through a meritorious person," and all the more so in the days of Kislev, and especially in the coming days of the 10th and 19th of Kislev, the success in *hafatzas hamaayanos* is greater.

Following this, I was also somewhat surprised by the phrasing of your letter regarding your wife, the Rabbanit, may she live, that she "promises to help, with the help of Hashem"—a lukewarm phrasing, to say the least, especially when taking into account her origins and the influence she should have received (and surely has received) from her husband, a student of *Tomchei Temimim*, in these matters, etc., etc. But since our Sages of blessed memory said, "It is not the study that is the essential thing, but the deed," I wish to hope that all of the above will not at all hinder the actual deed, and that you will do everything required to minimize the obstacles, concealments, and obstructions.

You will surely utilize the 19th of Kislev and the fifth candle of Chanukah in particular, and may Hashem grant you success.

With blessings for *Chag HaGeulah*.

## 3951

This break should bring your inner feelings to the fore, whether in the positive or otherwise. With blessings,

## 3443

B”H, 9 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 1 Kislev.

I hope that by the time you receive this letter, you are feeling better, quite simply in terms of physical health, which depends on Hashem Yisbarach. Consequently, this will improve and increase matters of spiritual health, which is in the hands of man, as the Sages said: "Everything is in the hands of Heaven except for the fear of Heaven."

And as is known, the teaching of Rabbeinu HaZaken—whose Chag HaGeulah we will soon be celebrating on the upcoming 19 Kislev—is that Hashem Yisbarach gives Jews gashmius, and they make gashmius into ruchnius. The intention here is not merely the simple meaning—earning merits—but something even more pnimiyusdike: Hashem Yisbarach ensures that the body, and even the nefesh habehamis, which one receives from Hashem Yisbarach, remains whole in its gashmius, and the Jews make that gashmius into ruchnius. As the Rambam writes, the health and wholeness of the body is a way of serving Hashem. This is stated even more clearly in Tanya Kadisha, at the beginning of Chapter [47], regarding serving Hashem with one’s body. This is further reinforced by the directive of our Nasi, the Rebbe, that "You shall love Hashem your G-d" is bound up with "You shall love your neighbor as yourself," which is why one must influence one’s environment to conduct themselves in this way.

And let a person not say, "Who am I and what am I to do in this regard?" For it is known, the verdict from Above, that for the mesiras nefesh (of Rabbeinu HaZaken) for Toras HaChassidus, it was decreed in the Beis Din Shel Maalah that in every matter of Torah, yiras shamayim, and good character traits, the hand of his followers and those who walk in his footsteps shall be uppermost.

With blessings for health and parnassah in abundance, and for good tidings regarding all that was mentioned, including the health of your son, shlita—who visited me with you.

It is self-understood that one must also act *b'derech hateva* according to the guidance of a doctor who is a specialist in this field, but simultaneously with this, have bitachon that Hashem Yisbarach, the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders, will help in this, and you will be able, at the appropriate time and in a good hour, to report good news regarding this.

Surely you are participating in the work of Nshei Ubnos Chabad in... in an appropriate manner, through which one fulfills the will of our Nasi, of blessed memory, and through which the blessing of Hashem Yisbarach is increased.

## 3847

10 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, engaged in communal needs, R’ Yochanan 
Shlita
Gabbai of the Lubavitcher Shul in Lubavitch

Peace and Blessing!

It was a pleasure to receive your letter regarding the birthday and day of passing of our Rebbe the Mitteler Rebbe, son of our Alter Rebbe, along with the enclosure. I was happy to read the opening of your letter—using the language of the Alter Rebbe (in the opening of *Iggeres HaKodesh*)—"We open with a blessing to bless and thank Hashem, for He is good"—and there is no "good" other than Torah, the perfect Torah of Hashem, etc.—regarding the public Torah study in the Lubavitcher Shul in Lubavitch. And a person is obligated to speak in the language of his Rebbe, in the aforementioned *Iggeres HaKodesh*:

"Gratitude for the past and a request for the future; may Hashem grant and add strength to their hearts, like heroes, etc."

And it is possible to explain this based on what is clarified in the *maamar* of the Shabbos on which we bless the month of Geulah —the *maamar* of our Rebbe (the Rashab) and my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—regarding the concept of *gevurah*, which is an intensification of vitality. They bring proof—in the *seder hishtalshelus* from above to below—from the vitality that comes from above, the "mighty rains," to the intensification of vitality within a person, until this also effects an intensification in the ascent from below to above.

May it be the will of Hashem that your public study also be directed toward this aforementioned goal, especially regarding the *pnimiyus* of Torah, whose nature is from above to below; that it should be with an intensification of vitality. Consequently, this will bring about an intensification of vitality in all those participating in the *shiur*, until it reaches the level of *haflagah*—*haflagah* in quality, and *haflagah* in quantity as well, through an increase in the number of participants. Through this, the study will be elevated in intensification, higher and higher, uniting with the lowest of the low—actual practice in daily life, even on weekdays and in mundane matters.

These days between 10 Kislev and 19 Kislev are auspicious, especially the bright day of 19 Kislev, the festival of our redemption and the liberation of our souls, when the light and vitality of our souls was given to us. May there be a beginning in all of the above with success, and may the saying of our Rebbeim be fulfilled: "As one sets oneself up, so it goes."

With a blessing to hear good news regarding all of the above, and with regards to all the participants in the *shiur*. May the ruling of the Heavenly Court be fulfilled for each and every one of them and their families—that in every matter of Torah, *yiras shamayim*, and good character traits, the hand of those who are connected to him and follow in his footsteps shall be on top—in a revealed and manifest good.

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.

It was a pleasure to read in your letter about the beginning of the study with the young women, *tichyena*. Since you have already made a start with *arum fun Chassidus* (general Chassidic topics) and they have expressed interest in studying the subject matter of *Toras HaChassidus*, you should certainly fulfill their heart’s desires for the good. You should certainly utilize, if there are instructions from that time from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding which *maamarim* and topics to study with them. It is understood that starting *Kuntres Uma'ayon* is included in this, but it is obvious that studying the entire *Kuntres* will be difficult for them, especially since several days pass between one study session and the next. Therefore, you should endeavor that every single *shiur* should be, in a sense, a *selik inyana* (a complete topic). In addition to the above, you will find much material in *Sefer HaMaamarim Yiddish* and in the individual *maamarim* that have been printed in some of the *kuntreisim*. In my opinion, it is good that in every *shiur* you should also explain to them some topic of *arum fun Chassidus* or stories of the *Tzaddikim*. And it would be best if there were someone to record what is said regarding *arum fun Chassidus*, as it is likely that they will be able to use this in other places as well, and the merit of the many depends on it.

Enclosed is my contribution as a participation in the repair of the *Sifrei Torah* of the Lubavitcher Shul in Lubavitch.

May Hashem strengthen your health so that you may return to your full strength—to your strength in the literal sense, and to your strength according to the explanation of the Alter Rebbe in the *d'h* "Maskil L'Eisan HaEzrachi" (printed in *Kuntres Limud HaChassidus*)—and may He add strength to your holy work in all of the above. May you also bring good news regarding the health of your wife, *tichyena*, and may you do all of the above from a place of spiritual health, and consequently, physical health as well.

## 3948

B"H, 10 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, occupied with communal needs,
R' Ephraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your postcard, in which you expressed some wonder regarding the two maamarim in Torah Or, *d"h Mayim Rabim*: in the first, it explains that "many waters" refers to the distractions of *parnassah*, while in the second, it refers to *hisbonenus*, etc.

The first maamar corresponds to the interpretation in the *nigleh* of Torah (Sotah 21a) and the *nigleh* aspect of *pnimiyus haTorah*, in the Midrash on Shir HaShirim in its place. The interpretation in the second maamar corresponds to the *pnimiyus haTorah* perspective, as the beginning of the maamar indicates by citing the Zohar.

It can be said that both interpretations evolve one from the other. For the intellect within man (both the *Elyon* and the *Tachton*), the *hisbonenus* regarding the measurements and limitations of the intellect, etc., are precisely what lead to the limitations of the affairs of this world. These cause *parnassah* to become a distraction and a source of concern, to the point that on a lower level still, there is a foothold and nourishment for the *chitzonim*. Consequently, the matters mentioned in Shir HaShirim—the "greatness of the nations," etc.—become possible, and lower still—transgression, as the Gemara expounds.

Enclosed is what you requested. Surely you will merit to bring merit to the many, and the merit of the many depends on you.

With blessings.

#### ***3948***

**R' Ephraim Eliezer:** Yalles. Additional letters to him: above, Vol. 11, 3626, and the references in the footnotes there. Below, 3975, 4056, 4196.

May they establish themselves correctly, as Jewish daughters are meant to build homes now, and in time, future generations among the Jewish people.

I was particularly pleased that you intend to establish contact with the parents of children who study in Talmud Torahs or with private tutors. This is doubly important for the students of the Talmud Torahs and private tutors, and it also brings the parents closer to the subjects being taught to their children, thereby strengthening the children’s chinuch as well. I have requested the office in Paris to provide a subsidy specifically for this work: 15,000 francs.

It would be appropriate to write more often about your work in the newspaper, as this helps attract more members and also strengthens those who are already involved in the work.

With blessings for good news regarding all of the above.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 3550

B"H, 12 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and meticulous in his communal work, a branch of a noble tree, R' Avraham Yehuda, may he live.

Since we are now entering the month of Kislev—the month of redemption, during which He redeemed not only us in peace, but also gave us our souls, and the light and vitality of our souls (as per the language of the Rebbe Rashab, of blessed memory, in his well-known letter)—this is a month of special potential for miracles regarding the soul, and consequently, for miracles regarding the body as well. As is known, the miracle of Chanukah was primarily concerned with the soul, for the Jewish people were dwelling on their land, etc., yet the consequence of this was also a war in the literal sense, as well as [a struggle] regarding their material possessions, etc., as per the language of the Rambam. It is well-known and widely publicized how the verse is interpreted: "And these days are [when they are] remembered [each and every year, all these influences are likewise drawn down] and observed," etc. This is especially true since the health of the body is also a spiritual matter of holiness, for having a healthy and whole body is one of the ways of Hashem.

Enclosed is what was published recently, which I am sure will be of interest to you.

I await good news that you have once again begun spreading the wellsprings during *idna d'ra'ava d'ra'avin* (the time of greatest favor), as well as during the other times of the week, for each and every day has its own task, and that you are doing this with joy and improved health.

With blessing,

## 3852

3852

B"H, 12 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Kislev, in which you write that until now you have studied in the yeshiva all day long, and considering the reality as you describe it, you wish to leave the yeshiva now and begin studying engineering, and you are twenty years old, and you ask for my opinion on this.

If you will listen to my voice, and considering the reality, my opinion and perspective is that for the coming year you should completely put aside any pursuit of worldly goals, and study Torah without calculations, with great persistence and diligence. After a year has passed, you may pose the question again, and if you wish to ask my opinion then as well, it is understood that with the help of Hashem I will inform you of that too.

And do not say that it is impossible for you to study and put aside the aforementioned thought because it is distracting you, for the matter depends only on your will. Especially and particularly because anyone who believes openly, believes clearly that the Ribono shel Olam is the One who sustains and provides for everyone, and specifically with kindness and mercy, at the appropriate time and in the appropriate manner. Our Sages have already said that a person does not know in what he will earn his livelihood, etc., and when the kingdom of the House of David will return, etc.—they are equated to one another. And as is the well-known statement of our Alter Rebbe (Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 22), there is room to think that the king is old and foolish, and that in his affairs he is an expert. He will disguise himself in a cloak of various arguments, and perhaps he will even bring proof for his words from the statements of our Sages, etc., by using them out of context, and consequently, very often, contrary to their intent. And in order to minimize these distractions—regarding which our Sages said, "Were it not for the Holy One, Blessed be He, helping him..."—you should establish a daily study session in the "light of the Torah," which is the inner dimension of the Torah. Be careful with *tevilas Ezra*, and every day before *davening* (the beginning of the middle twelve blessings, which are the request for human needs, is the granting of *Da'as*), give a *prutah* to *tzedakah*, and the Ribono shel Olam will grant you success.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 3853

B"H, 12 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished activists of Yeshivas Ahei Yosef Yitzchak Lubavitch in Melbourne, may they live:

Peace and blessing!

It is surprising that we have not received any letters from the avreichim who visited here during the seventh month, which is saturated with all good; surely they will fulfill this at the earliest opportunity, with the necessary and appropriate details.

I am writing now, in accordance with our Sages' teaching that "one only encourages the diligent," in the certainty that you will utilize the auspicious days of 19 Kislev and the fifth candle of Chanukah to strengthen and develop the affairs of the yeshivah and, in general, all Chabad activities in your camp. May Hashem grant you success. As is known, the ruling of the Heavenly Court is that because of the mesiras nefesh (of our Alter Rebbe) for the teachings of Chassidus, in every matter of Torah, yiras shamayim, and good character traits, the hand of those who are connected to him and follow in his footsteps will be uppermost.

With blessings for success.

P.S. Regarding what you wrote in your letter at the time about a person coming to your country—a man adorned with many virtues, etc.—experience in many places has shown that in such matters, what is needed are energetic individuals who are dedicated to the holy goal of "spreading the wellsprings" and activities in the "outside" of the Chabad vineyard. People who are suited only by their virtues and their ability to "uproot mountains and grind them against each other with pilpulim" do not bring any benefit; often, on the contrary, etc. When I met the avreichim who visited here, and based on my estimation of anash already present in your country, I see that "according to the camel is the burden." You have the ability and the strength to do and accomplish in your country everything that is necessary. The matter depends only on bringing these strengths from a state of concealment—which exists in potential—and even from a state of concealment that is not yet in potential—into actual, tangible revelation.

It is understood that all of the above does not rule out that if a person is found who is full of energy and can act in the aforementioned direction, you should also endeavor for him to travel to your camp; however, for the time being, no person with these virtues is apparent.

3955

B"H, 13 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Dovid, may he live:

From the setting of the sun, when it becomes dark in the world; it is precisely then that one brings light. And as the halachic ruling states, one adds and increases in holiness. When one truly desires to do so, one finds the ways to accomplish this, and Hashem grants success in this. May Hashem, blessed be He, grant you the merit and success to report good tidings regarding all the above.

## 3557

...And just as He redeemed in peace the soul of the *baal hasimcha*, our *Alter Rebbe*—because "there were many with him," for the sake of the many, to whom he did good—

So too may we merit to receive and internalize this *pidyon* and redemption within our innermost selves, through *avodah* of "double good"—good for Heaven and good for the creations—and especially through spreading the *maayanos*, the *maayanos* of *Chassidus*, outward.

For through the dissemination of Torah in general, and the dissemination of the teachings of *Chassidus* in particular, by which *atahpacha chashucha l'nahora* (darkness is transformed into light),

Just as He redeemed in peace the soul of David, King of Israel, because "there were many with him"—even the men of Avshalom—

So too, may each and every one redeem his soul in peace, because "there were many with him"—the angels who guard a person, the *yetzer hatov* and the *yetzer hara*, will be with him.

For through the aforementioned, one empowers the *yetzer hatov* over the *yetzer hara* and sweetens the *gevuros*, and then the *yetzer hara* itself returns and becomes a guardian of the fruit.

And then, also in all matters of this world—and in their totality: children, life, and sustenance—there will be peace and blessing, for "there were many with him" in great abundance, and His word was our support.

**M. Schneerson**

14 Kislev, 5716, Brooklyn, N.Y.

3858

B"H, 14 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and industrious, R' Meir [Gurkow]
Shalom u'Bracha!

In response to your letter of 22 Mar-Cheshvan, along with the enclosure: I have been waiting for some time for news from London regarding what has been happening following the return of the guests who visited here during the "seventh month, which is saturated with all good," [with the intention] of drawing that influence into the entire year. It has already been discussed at several farbrengens that the concept of *divrei b’teilim* (idle words) is not merely the worldly interpretation—that one is speaking about trivial matters—but also its internal interpretation: that if words do not achieve their intended effect and reach the goal of the speech, they become *divrei b’teilim*. It is already well-known in the teachings of Chassidus that even the *maamarim* of Chassidus—and certainly words of *hisorerus* at a farbrengen—have as their ultimate purpose the "therefore" (*habchein*). In our times, this "therefore" relates to actual deed in daily life, and even "outwardly" (*bachutz*). Consequently, if this is lacking, the words of *hisorerus* become, as it were, idle.

Regarding what you write concerning the reasons why the farbrengen was not as successful as it could have been, there is room to say that one of the reasons is the following:

It is explained in one of the *sichos* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that the difference between the Rabbis and the later *Geonim*—who remained in their places and waited for people to come to them to hear their Torah and innovations—and the Baal Shem Tov, was that the Baal Shem Tov would travel to the towns and villages, etc., and bring them the word of Hashem and His Torah. Since you are apparently in a place where people are apprehensive and fearful of the words of Chassidus—which fits the reason given by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the aforementioned *sicha*—one should not be satisfied with a farbrengen where one invites *anash* to come; rather, *anash* must go to them—that is, to the places where they gather. May it be Hashem’s will that this be only for a short time, and that they will soon see the "light that is good," and that the "luminary" has been taken with him, and consequently, they will run to speak of Torah and *mitzvos*.

Enclosed is what I have received recently, and surely you will merit to bring merit to the many, and the merit of the many depends on you.

The *pidyon nefesh* enclosed in your letter will be read at an auspicious time at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

With blessings for the spreading of the *maayanos* outward, and in all three aspects of the adage "they shall spread" (*yafutzu*): *Hafatzah* (spreading, which implies expansion in length, breadth, and depth); *Maayanos* (the springs, which are connected to the "source of living waters" that gush forth); and *Chutzah* (outward, so that the springs reach even the outside). It is already known that because of the *mesiras nefesh* (of the Alter Rebbe) for the teachings of Chassidus, it was decreed in the Heavenly Court that in every matter of Torah, *yiras shamayim*, and good character traits, the hand of his followers and those who walk in his footsteps shall be uppermost.

With blessings for a *Chag HaGeulah* and awaiting good news.

## 3861

3861

B"H, 14 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write that although you have been at Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim for over a year, you do not feel any change within yourself, etc., etc.

It is a known ruling of our Sages that a person cannot testify about himself, for he is too close to himself. Just as in revealed law his testimony is invalid—both for his benefit and to his detriment—the same applies regarding the duties of the heart. In my opinion, this is nothing but a tactic of the *yetzer hara*, which seeks to distract you from ascending the path and the highway that leads to the House of Hashem through various and strange stratagems. Even if it is possible that you could have changed more than you have, G-d forbid to say that there has been no change over the course of twelve months; as it is written, "Keep far from a false matter."

In order for you to begin to feel the change openly (even though, on the face of it, the necessity for this feeling specifically is not understood), and the main thing is that you should change for the better in every way possible, be careful with *tevilas Ezra*, give a few coins to *tzedakah* every weekday before *davening*, and study *pnimius haTorah* before *davening*. Consequently, your *tefillah* will be more readily accepted, for the beginning of a person’s requests for his needs—which are the twelve middle blessings—is "Grant us from Yourself wisdom, understanding, and knowledge," and "if you have acquired knowledge, what do you lack?"

With blessings that you should study the Torah of Hashem with consistency and diligence, with *yiras shamayim*, and for the fulfillment of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*, and for good tidings regarding all that has been mentioned.

## 3862

B"H, 15 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants in the Chag HaSemicha
at Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch
Montreal
May Hashem grant them life

Peace and Blessing!

On the occasion of the **Chag HaSemicha**, taking place on the upcoming 19th of Kislev, I send my greetings and blessings to the Roshei Yeshiva and administrators, the newly ordained students, and all the guests and participants in this Simchas HaTorah.

This celebration at the Lubavitcher Yeshiva, beyond the event itself, is a matter of far-reaching significance and double joy, when one considers the unique character of the Yeshiva and those it educates.

For while in years past, the primary goal of a yeshiva was to instill in its students deep knowledge of the holy Torah, without needing to be concerned about the influence of the surrounding environment, in our current times, the primary task of a yeshiva is to educate not only scholars, but specifically scholars who are G-d-fearing. The intent and approach of a Lubavitcher yeshiva goes even further: to educate not only G-d-fearing scholars who possess good character traits and observe Torah and mitzvos with hiddur, but also to instill in the students a sense of responsibility for the other, permeated with the feeling of Ahavas Yisrael and mesiras nefesh. Therefore, the students and alumni of the Lubavitcher yeshiva are "lamps to illuminate," spreading the light of Torah, mitzvos, good character, and good customs in every place and environment to which Divine Providence leads them.

Everything is by Hashgacha Pratis; thus, it is also significant that the Chag HaSemicha takes place on the luminous day of 19 Kislev, the Chag HaGeulah of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch. On this day, the Alter Rebbe was liberated from the accusations against him, for he had demonstrated actual mesiras nefesh to spread not only the wellsprings of Torah but also the ways of proper conduct. Because of this, he instituted many takanos and spread them even among those who were still "chutza"—on the outside. Surely, this spirit will resonate within the newly ordained students and the participants in this Chag HaSemicha, and in the light of Toras HaChassidus and the customs of Chassidus, they will spread their influence in their surroundings—to everyone around them, both those who are close and those who still stand at a distance—in order to bring them closer to our Father in Heaven.

May the merit of Talmud Torah with yiras shamayim and the merit of our holy Rebbes, of blessed memory, stand by everyone to continue to experience blessing and success for themselves and their families, may they live, in all that they require, both materially and spiritually.

With the blessing of Chag HaGeulah, through which the light and vitality of our souls was given to us.

## 3864

3864

B"H, 15 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Wednesday, which was received with a delay. Regarding what you write concerning the writing of a Sefer Torah, its completion, and its dedication into the synagogue:

It is surprising that you ask about this, at a time when it has been **several** years since a detailed letter from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, was published (I believe in the third volume of *Igros Kodesh*). Does he not study, or at the very least read, the matters of our Nasi that are published? And if he does not do so, then what are the members of his congregation and those he influences supposed to do? I am astonished.

Enclosed is what has been published recently, and surely you will merit the many through its contents, and the merit of the many is dependent upon you.

With blessings that you begin your primary and internal avodah—as is the case for anyone who has merited to study in Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim—which is the dissemination of the wellsprings outward.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 3865

P.S.

It goes without saying that I will fulfill your request and write to him about this. However, I must add that the support the yeshiva provides must take into account not only the current state of the treasury but also the resources it generally requires. Therefore, even if he were to take the full amount from the yeshiva, it would not be enough. I am therefore certain that you, your husband, and your relatives in general will act and help, and do so with a joyful heart.

## 3867

3867

By the Grace of Hashem, 16 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Blessings and Peace!

I have received your letter of 24 Cheshvan, and due to many preoccupations, the response has been delayed until now.

Regarding the content of your letter: As we are instructed, every Jew begins their day with the words, "I offer thanks before You, living and eternal King..." This is not merely the beginning of the day; it sets the tone and should permeate the events of the entire twenty-four-hour period. Since the Torah is a *Toras Chaim* (a Torah of life) that demands this of each of us, it is certain that there is always something to thank Hashem Yisbarach for, every single day, without exception. Therefore, I am surprised by the tone of your letter, as I am certain that you have often reflected upon the words of *Modeh Ani*, and upon the various passages where this thought is repeated throughout the *tefillos* and *brachos* during the day.

It is understandable that no one has everything they desire, not even everything they desire from the perspective of the *yetzer tov*, for this is the entire structure of *Olam Hazeh*. Especially since we are in *galus*, until *Mashiach Tzidkeinu* comes and there is the *Geulah HaAmitis*, there is no complete wholeness, and no one possesses the entirety of their heart's desires. And yet, we have been instructed to say "I offer thanks before You..." and furthermore, the requirement is that this be said with *simcha*.

And not only should the saying of *Modeh Ani* be with *simcha*, but the entire twenty-four-hour period with all its occurrences should be with *simcha*, for upon them all rests the directive to "Serve Hashem with *simcha*." As is explained in many places, one must serve Hashem Yisbarach not only through *davening*, learning Torah, and giving *tzedakah*, but one can and must serve Hashem Yisbarach also through eating, drinking, and performing various tasks, including household chores.

Now, all of this would be what one would say when dealing with someone else. But when it concerns you, if you yourself reflect upon the matters you wrote about, looking into them and seeing the positive side, a completely different calculation emerges—and in my opinion, this is the correct calculation:

Hashem Yisbarach has blessed you with fine children. Regardless of the fact that you are in New York—where only a small percentage of Jewish children receive a Torah education—Hashem Yisbarach has granted you the good fortune that your children receive not just any Torah education, but a *Chassidish* education in a *yeshiva* founded by the *Nesi'ei Yisrael*. And despite the fact that—as you write—your husband, etc., he has not only not hindered such an education, but on the contrary, he even helps, even if not to the extent you feel he should. And regardless of the fact that your husband is a businessman in New York—and unfortunately, we know how the majority of them spend their *Shabbos* and *Yom Tov*, and how they spend their free time, in nightclubs, etc.—Hashem Yisbarach has granted you success in that your husband dedicates a portion of his time to the needs of the community of *Bnei Yisrael*, and naturally, not with the intention of receiving a reward. And you can continue this calculation of the positive side, of which you surely know many details that I do not. By making such a summary, you will see for yourself what the result is.

May Hashem Yisbarach bless you so that from now on, you look only with a good eye upon your husband, your children—*shichyu*—and your entire surroundings. Then you yourself will see how much one can be satisfied and thank Hashem Yisbarach with a full heart for the *chasadim* of the past, and for the *chasadim*—in even greater measure—in the future.

With blessings for good news always, all the days.

3868

By the Grace of Hashem
18 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, who engages in communal affairs,
R' Yitzchak, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 26 Cheshvan: Thank you for what you write regarding the personal message you delivered from your visit here. Surely, the words of the Mishnah are engraved upon the mind of each person: "It is not the study that is the essential thing, but the action." My intent is that you strive to ensure that the personal message—and the words of inspiration that you surely appended to it—should have their effect on the daily lives of those who were gathered, and through them, upon their families as well. It is already known that there is a presumption (*chazakah*) that propaganda (outreach) does not return empty-handed.

I was startled by your question: since you have been accustomed until now to davening on Shabbos with composure and at some length, whether you should continue to do so now, or G-d forbid, the opposite. It is simple that this does not even fall into the category of a question, after what has been explained at great length regarding the matter of tefillah (that only a *toreach tzibbur*—one who burdens the congregation—is excluded from this, as the Sages said regarding Rabbi Akiva, that when he would daven with the congregation, etc., whereas otherwise, etc. [Berachos 31a]). I have no interpretation for your question other than that it surely came so that I would have the opportunity to awaken you: that you should do as mentioned above not only on Shabbos, but—from time to time—also on weekdays. For even on a weekday, one must say "one day **in Shabbos**," etc. Especially since some say this is included in the Ten Commandments (see Ramban, Shemos 20:8, from which it is also proven that the intent is also for the day of Shabbos). Furthermore, Divine Providence has made you a *mashpia* for others. As the rule of "one who is moist [with water] is able to moisten others" (*tofeach al menas lehatfiach*), in order for others to daven at length—at the very least on Shabbos—there must be an increase in this by the *mashpia*. This is simple.

Regarding what you noted in Tanya, Chapter 1, that the interpretation of the Zohar brought in the *hagah* (gloss) is seemingly that which we say in general in the body of the chapter there:

The distinction is explained as follows: what we say "in general" is to be interpreted—as it is explained there—as referring to the matter of reward and punishment. This is not the case in the Zohar, which explains there the matters of "a tzaddik and it is bad for him" and "a rasha and it is good for him."

Surely you will utilize the *eis ratzon* (time of favor) of the bright day of 19 Kislev, the day of our redemption and the liberation of our souls, upon which the light and vitality of our souls was given to us, to disseminate—*hafatzah* specifically—the wellsprings outward, even to those people who for the time being are still on the outside. There is a presumption that outreach is effective, especially during an *eis ratzon* and auspicious days, which acts until it is noticeable even in daily life.

With blessings for a Chag HaGeulah.

The dispatch was delayed, and in the meantime, your letter from Motzaei Shabbos was received with the *pidyon nefesh*.

Regarding the transcripts of the *sichos*, sections will be included in the next *Kovetz* (and I have not yet found the free time for this correction either).

On the afternoon of 10 Kislev, our custom is not to say *Tachanun*.

## 3970

B"H, 21 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write about the idea of traveling here to study, and ask for my opinion on the matter:

In my opinion, if your desire is truly to study in a Chassidic yeshiva, then first and foremost you should study at Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod, for at least one year. Only afterward should you place the question of traveling to the yeshiva here on the agenda. In any event, it is understood that in whichever yeshiva you study, it is your obligation and your privilege to study fixed shiurim—fixed in time and fixed in the soul—every single day in the teachings of the words of the living G-d, which is the Torah of Chassidus. You must conduct yourself according to its guidance and customs, and influence others in this as well. Beyond the inherent greatness of this matter, it also pertains to your own success and ascent in the ways of Chassidus. There is nothing that can stand before the will, and may Hashem grant you success and bring you good tidings in all of this.

Surely you participated in the farbrengen of the auspicious day of 19 Kislev, the festival on which our souls were redeemed in peace and the light and vitality of our souls were given to us, and may this lead to an increase in your efforts regarding Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

A. Quint
Secretary
