## 3992

3992

B"H, 22 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your notification that you are moving into your new home in these coming days:

May it be the will of Hashem that it be at a good and auspicious time. "Change of place, change of fortune"—may it be for the good and for a blessing in all matters.

Surely you are aware of the custom of Anash in recent times: to bring into the new place, first and foremost, a Siddur, Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya. Likewise, to affix the mezuzos immediately—naturally, without a bracha. Upon the completion of thirty days, one should take one mezuzah to be checked. One is then at liberty to replace it with one that is more beautiful, in accordance with the teaching of our Sages, "This is my G-d and I will beautify Him"—beautify yourself before Him with mitzvos. Consequently, one is obligated to recite a bracha, and should have in mind to exempt all the other mezuzos.

Since the days of Chanukah are approaching, it is appropriate to inaugurate the home with a Chassidishe farbrengen in a suitable manner. The saying of our holy Rebbes is already well known: "As one sets oneself up, so it goes." May the home be a Chassidishe home in every respect.

With blessings.

## 3973

B"H, 22 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn

As the saying of our holy Rebbes goes, "As one sets out, so it goes," may you succeed, even after the beginning, to strengthen Judaism through your work and to disseminate it in the widest possible circles—Judaism in its truth, without compromise, and especially through ways of pleasantness. Since this is required of each one of us, and the Holy One, blessed be He, only demands according to our abilities, it is certain and simple that the powers to fulfill the task in practice were given from the outset, and the matter depends only on the will of the person.

This is especially relevant to you, a student of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, to whom our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, gave the title *Tamim*. Over time, this must also become their essential identity. You should contemplate the moral lesson from the story told by the elder Chassidim about the great Gaon, Chossid, and Tzaddik, R' Hillel of Paritch, who explained the reason for his extreme stringencies and extra-meticulous care in mitzvos: his intention in all of this was so that "a word of Chassidus might take root better."

Regarding every one of the *Temimim*, all their affairs must be in order to "become even closer to Chassidus," and that through his way of life, he should justify—even more so day by day—the name *Tamim* that is called upon him. Here, too, the saying holds true: "There is nothing that can stand before the will."

With blessings for the fulfillment of your heart's desires for the good, as you concluded in your letter, to see an abundance of Chassidishe nachas and to be satisfied by it—you and your wife, the Rabbanit, may they live—not only from your children, but from yourselves as well.

With blessings for good tidings in all that was mentioned, and for utilizing the days of Chanukah to their fullest regarding the "candle, light, and illumination," as these matters are explained in the discourses of Chanukah in Chassidic literature.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the questions about Gehinom and Gan Eden—see the indices at the end of Torah Or, Derech Mitzvosecha, and the Sefer HaMaamarim published by Kehot.

## 3974

3974

B”H, 22 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

It was a pleasure to receive your letter, which you began writing on the auspicious day of 19 Kislev—the festival on which our souls were redeemed in peace, and the light and vitality of our souls were granted to us (the language of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe [Rashab], in his well-known Iggeres HaKodesh). I was happy to read that you have seen that the light is good and have begun to put into practice your decision to set fixed times for the study of the words of the Living G-d, which is the Torah of Chassidus. Certainly, as our Sages said, "Study is not the primary thing, but action." The intent here includes its guidance and customs, for regarding this part of Torah as well, the message applies: "Great is study, for it leads to action." May it be the will of Hashem that you succeed in your desire to study and fulfill it with an expanded mind, and may you toil in it, so that the promise of our Sages, "You have toiled and you have found," will be fulfilled for you.

Regarding what you wrote about the order of study, having begun with the first chapters of the Sefer Tanya Kadisha: it would be appropriate to study the third part of the Tanya—Iggeres HaTeshuvah—then the second part, Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah, and after that, the first part. Simultaneously, you should study maamarim from the book Derech Mitzvotecha by my revered ancestor, the Tzemach Tzedek, in those areas that your heart desires. For people’s temperaments are not the same; there are those who find satisfaction in breadth, and there are those who find it specifically in depth, which in the vast majority of cases requires Tzimtzum and focus on a specific subject, etc. It would be best if you could study this in a chavrusa, at least with one other person. If there is no one in your vicinity who understands the study as you do, let it at least be someone who is on a lower level than you, for it is said, "And from my students, more than from all of them."

With blessings for success in all of the above, and for good tidings regarding yourself, your household, and those you influence in your good camp.

P.S. Enclosed is my letter to the member of your shul about whom you write in your letter. Surely, if he requires explanation, you will find the appropriate words to explain to him what is stated in my letter. Thank you for the trouble.

As you requested, the letter is being sent quickly.

## 3995

B”H, 22 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, occupied with communal needs,
Moreinu HaRav Ephraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter following the farbrengen, in which you raise a point regarding what was said—that the open Mem of Atzilus influences the lower worlds, and also the Jewish people, through the process of *hislabshus* (garbing), etc.—and you raise a difficulty based on what is written in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 25 (130b): "However, in *chutz la'aretz* (this is the correct reading, contrary to the change made by the censor, as noted in the *luach hatikun*), the vitality is through the *hislabshus* of the external *sarim* (princes) appointed over the seventy nations, etc." From this, it is implied that in Eretz Yisrael, this is not the case.

Indeed, it is true that in general, "Eretz Yisrael is not governed by any firmament or *chayil achra* (other force), but by the Ribono shel Olam alone" (see Zohar Vol. II, 209, end of side a; see Ta’anis 10a, beginning of side a, and elsewhere, as noted in *Nitzutzei Zohar* there). However, there is a fundamental distinction here:

1) Between the seventy *sarim* discussed in Iggeres HaKodesh—who are appointed over the seventy nations—and the *sarim* and *mazalos* (constellations) through which influence comes into physical manifestation in the affairs of the lower worlds in general, and this world in particular. This is why it is said, "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you do"—specifically [through physical effort], as is explained at length in *Kuntres Uma’ayon* (see there, Maamar 19 and onwards; see also *Sefer Derech Mitzvosecha*, p. 106). It is understood that the same applies to Eretz Yisrael, for regarding it, too, it is said, "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you do," and there, too, the influence must come into physical manifestation, as is explicitly stated in *Likutei Torah*, Parshas Masei, 89b (see there). What was discussed in the *maamar* entitled *L’marbeh HaMisrah* concerns the *hislabshus* in the *sarim* and *mazalos*.

2) There is also a distinction between a strong *klipah* and a weak *klipah*; see *Zohar Chadash*, Vol. III, 140, end of side b.

And in *Or HaChamah* to *Zohar Chadash*, Vol. III, 173a, it is explained that this is why, even in Eretz Yisrael, one must perform *netilas yadayim* upon rising from sleep.

**Note:** Although I have not found this explicitly stated as of yet, based on what is explained in the words of our Sages regarding "the master of the host on high," it follows that except for the time of the First Beis HaMikdash, when Eretz Yisrael was not under the dominion of another nation, in all other periods—since the king of the earth had control, to some degree, in Eretz Yisrael—it must be that this is so regarding his *sar* above. See Iggeres HaKodesh there, 140a: "But when the Jewish people were exiled among the nations, etc." And it is known that the redemption from Bavel was not a complete redemption from exile.

With blessings for good tidings regarding the matter we spoke of during the farbrengen in a parenthetical remark, and regarding which you said you hope to bring good news soon. May the Ribono shel Olam fulfill the desires of your heart for the good, in this as well.

Regarding what you noted about a *sedra* (parsha) that has no break—it should be noted regarding Parshas Mikeitz (*Rambam, Hilchos Sefer Torah*, ch. 8) that "this parsha is connected to the one preceding it" (*Likkutei Torah*, beginning of Parshas Mikeitz)—this week, the 19th of Kislev of this year—and its themes involve the clarification of the seven cows and the seven years of famine through Yosef, *taanug*, the inner dimension of Torah, etc. See at length in *Torah Or* and *Toras Chayim*.

## 3996

3996

B"H, 23 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished scholar,
R' Dovid, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 21 Kislev, in which you write regarding the ruling of our Alter Rebbe in his Siddur concerning the order of *Hachnasas Shabbos*—that the primary opinion is that of the Geonim regarding the time of *bein hashmashos*—and you note the discrepancy with what he wrote in his *Shulchan Aruch*, Orach Chayim 261:5, which follows the opinion of Rabbeinu Tam, and you are in doubt as to which is his final ruling.

His grandson, the Tzemach Tzedek, has already instructed that the Siddur was written a long time after the *Shulchan Aruch* (*Chiddushim* to Maseches Shabbos, end of Chapter 7, 46d), and we follow the rulings of the Siddur for *halachah* and practice, both in this matter and in several other matters where there are differences between the Siddur and the *Shulchan Aruch* (most of which have been collected in the book *Piskei HaSiddur* by the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, R' Avraham Chaim Naeh, of blessed memory, of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt by Mashiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days).

It is also worth noting that in the book *Ketzos HaShulchan* by the aforementioned Rabbi Naeh, at the end of Part 3, he comments on several details regarding the order of *Hachnasas Shabbos* according to our Alter Rebbe.

With blessings for success in your efforts to clarify the words of Torah, and specifically in the laws of *bein hashmashos*, upon which many *halachic* matters depend. And although many great scholars have already delved into this, many of its aspects still require a "carpenter and the son of a carpenter" to explain them and resolve them, based on the points and instructions found in the words of the great Torah authorities of Israel—the early and later *poskim*—up to the greatest of the later authorities, our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe.

May it be the will of Hashem that in these days of *bein hashmashos* of the sixth and seventh millennia—the sixth and seventh days of the days of Creation—whose *bein hashmashos* is on everyone’s lips, and everyone is anxious to complete their work before it becomes dark (Rashi, *Kesuvos* 103a), each of us will succeed in completing our work, the work of Heaven, to make for Him, may He be blessed, a dwelling place in the lower worlds. Through this, the night—the day of the seventh millennium—will shine like the day, as our Sages of blessed memory said regarding the days of Creation, that that light served for thirty-six hours.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***3996***

## 3978

3978

B”H, 23 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 10 Kislev, in which you write your questions regarding matters of your avodah, as well as regarding the matter of the mikveh in...

I write only to offer an observation and an illumination, even though I thought it would be superfluous for an avreich who spent several years within the walls of Tomchei Temimim, and it is this:

It is a well-known saying of Rabbeinu HaZaken—the author of the Tanya, the authority on the nistar of Torah, and the Shulchan Aruch, the authority on the nigleh of Torah—that "You shall love Hashem your G-d" and "You shall love your fellow as yourself" are one and the same. According to what is explained in Tanya, Chapter 3, this love is the root of all 248 positive mitzvos; from it they are drawn forth, and without it they have no true existence (as the mitzvah of fear is also included in the 248 positive mitzvos).

It is understood that the love of Hashem is the foundation and root of the entire Torah and its mitzvos. From this, it should have been obvious that since Divine Providence brought you to... through various circumstances that are above nature, and you found there a breach regarding the mikveh, you should have set aside all your personal calculations and yourself, at least for a short time, to build a fence in this breach. Instead, despite having been there for several months, it appears you have done nothing about this. It seems that even now, you would not have seen it as your concern to do anything about it, were it not for the fact that we are in the *ikvesa d'meshicha*—a period of which it is said, "Many will be purified, whitened, and refined." They showed you through hashgacha pratis, in a way visible even to physical eyes, that the matter concerns you personally—simply and literally, regarding your physical and material livelihood—and only then were you aroused to send a letter posthaste. How can this be?

My hope is that these few lines, small in quantity, will suffice to awaken within you that which was instilled into the depths of your soul within the walls of Tomchei Temimim, and will lead to actual practice, so that you begin to fulfill your role as stated in the Mishnah: "I was created to serve my Maker," as explained in the Rambam, Hilchos Teshuvah, Chapter 10.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

#### ***3978***

**Saying of Rabbeinu HaZaken:** See also above, letter 3933, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 3979

3979

B"H, 24 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

During the farbrengen on the auspicious day of 19 Kislev—the festival that "redeemed our souls in peace, and the light and vitality of our souls were given to us" (in the words of the well-known letter of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe [Rashab]—I was informed of the unfortunate event, may Hashem protect you, concerning you and your wife, may they live.

Since this matter was conveyed during a time of favor (*eis ratzon*), and all the more so—*kal v'chomer*—based on the adage of the Alter Rebbe, which he heard from our Rebbes, that "if one angel were to stand in a gathering of ten Jews together, even if they are not speaking words of Torah..." (*Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 23), then certainly this applies when tens of groups of Jews are gathered in the joy and inspiration of the Nasi of Israel. I am confident that your situation will improve rapidly, in the manner explained in *Likutei Torah* at the end of *Parshas Korach* regarding the concept of "His word runs swiftly."

Certainly, your measure of *bitachon* will not diminish, G-d forbid, for that is the vessel for receiving extraordinary success from Above. I look forward to receiving good news from you soon regarding this, especially as we are on the eve of the days of Chanukah, the law of which is to "increase and add" in holiness, even in the outside world. This is especially true through the dissemination of the wellsprings outward, until the light of the night shines with the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days.

With blessings.

## 3880

3880

B”H, 26 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter—which does not indicate when it was written—in which you write: 1) That you purchased half a house that is nicer than your previous home, and it seems to you that since then, your affairs have not been succeeding as they should.

It would be necessary to clarify whether there was any aspect in your purchase of what our Sages, of blessed memory, termed “one who overturns a cake and another comes along [and takes it],” i.e., encroaching upon another’s territory. It is also appropriate to clarify why the previous owner sold this half of the house. In any case, you should have your tefillin checked, as well as the mezuzos that you use in this house. Furthermore, without a vow, you should set aside a few coins for tzedakah every weekday morning before davening. Through the merit of your involvement in the beis medrash—where you surely use your influence to increase davening and Torah study there—may the blessing of Hashem be great, and may you find success in what you need, both in your personal affairs and in your new home.

2) Regarding the location for the farbrengen on the day of your eldest son’s, may he live, Bar Mitzvah.

You should hold it in the beis medrash where you serve as a gabbai. You should certainly also share a *dvar Torah*, and it would be best if it included something from the teachings of Chassidus. Through this, all three lines will be unified: Torah, avodah (which is tefillah), and gemilus chasadim. This is the inner content of the *pnimiyus haTorah*, as is known from the adage of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe—the arbiter of the *nistar* of Torah—and the Shulchan Aruch—the arbiter of the *nigleh* of Torah—that “You shall love Hashem your G-d” and “You shall love your neighbor as yourself” are one and the same.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

#### ***3880***

**Adage of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe:** See also above, letter 3833, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 3881

B"H, 26 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 23 Kislev, in which you write that you feel a lack of *kabbalas ol* in actual practice, and that this leads to several undesirable outcomes.

It is obvious that this matter depends solely on you, for the *Ribono shel Olam* only makes demands according to one's capacity. In order to implement this in practice as much as possible, first and foremost you must be precise in keeping the *yeshiva* schedule exactly—meaning, even to the point of not deviating from it for reasons that appear to you to be for the sake of *kedushah*. Since it seems that accepting the schedule is difficult for you, the habit of adhering to the *yeshiva* schedules will nevertheless make it easier to accept *ol* in other matters as well. As mentioned, it is highly probable that the *kloginker* (the accuser/inclination) will come with explanations that it is better to study late at night, especially studying *Chassidus*, even if this causes you to be late for *yeshiva* in the morning. However, it is already well-known how much our *Nesi'im*—the founders and directors of *Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim*—insisted that the *talmidim* keep all the schedules. Therefore, any arguments that contradict this have an impure source. It would be excellent if you would also influence all your peers, and certainly those *bochurim* younger than you, so that they too conduct themselves as stated above. Through this, in accordance with the *middah* of the *Ribono shel Olam*—which is *middah k'neged middah*—you will succeed in your work on yourself. And according to the interpretation of our Sages on the verse "lodge here tonight," the test of this is that immediately upon receiving this letter, you should begin this conduct.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 3882

3882

B”H, 26 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 22 Kislev, in which you write that you and your wife, may they live, have settled into the old-age home in...

It is surely unnecessary to remind you of one of the foundations of our faith, which is explained in the teachings of Chassidus: that every matter and event occurs through Hashgacha Pratis, and that in every situation one must serve the Creator of the world. It is understood and simple that this arrangement of yours is also included in what has been said—meaning, that you must view yourself in accordance with the truth: that Hashgacha has brought you to this old-age home so that you may add there to the "candle of mitzvah and the light of Torah," and the "light of Torah" refers to the guidance and conduct (including the teachings) of Chassidus. With the appropriate hisbonenus, you will surely find many pleasant and peaceful ways to bring all of this into practice.

It is already known that the attribute of the Ribono shel Olam is "measure for measure," but even more so: that by increasing the spiritual health of your neighbors in your new place, the Ribono shel Olam will increase your own health, both in spirituality and in physicality, so that you may continue to increase your aforementioned avodah from time to time.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 3883

B"H, 27 Kislev, 5716

In response to your letter, in which you write regarding the marriage proposal for your son... and raise the question in connection with the mother's health, which some time ago was not as it should be.

To uproot the question from the outset, it would be appropriate for you to assemble three of your friends and present the matter to them; let them say, with the power of the collective, that there is no basis for the aforementioned concern and that the proposal is a good one. May it be the will of Hashem that your son increase his fixed times for studying Chassidus and following its guidance and customs, for this will add to the blessings of Hashem and his success in all his affairs.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 3884

B”H, 27 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write regarding the state of your wife’s health, may she live and be well.

It seems that a large part of this is due to nerves—partly her own, and partly those of the people around her. Since one must also find a resolution for matters related to nerves, it is worthwhile to consult a general physician who is also an expert in this field. You should inform him of the results of all the examinations conducted thus far and ask for his professional opinion.

I have already written to several of anash that if they would make the effort and, over time, accustom themselves to writing letters containing good news, it would surely, from time to time, spare them from various unusual matters whose sole purpose is to necessitate the writing of a letter. For we do not know the ways of Hashem, and it is possible that the entire matter exists only so that two Jews might connect once again, in a manner of drawing hearts closer together—a matter that causes great *nachas ruach* Above, as is understood from what is explained in *Likutei Torah*, in the *maamar* beginning *Hechalutzu*, and in *Derech Mitzvotecha* regarding the *mitzvah* of *ahavas Yisrael*, and so on.

It is surprising that in this letter you do not mention anything regarding communal matters, especially considering that you had the merit of being within the walls of *Tomchei Temimim*. Regarding each of them, it was said that one must be a "lamp to illuminate." This is especially true given that since your last letter, we have passed the days of Tishrei, and now we are in the days of the month of Kislev, etc. Elaborating on such a simple matter is unnecessary.

With blessings to hear good news regarding all that has been mentioned.

## 3885

B"H, 27 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned man, a man of character and many accomplishments, who engages in the needs of the community, etc.,
R' Dovid, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

It gave me pleasure to read in your letter that you are striving to strengthen your connections within various circles and with different people, and that you are utilizing these connections as a conduit to bring them the word of Hashem, which is found in our Torah—the Torah of life—and its mitzvos. The attribute of the Ribono shel Olam is "measure for measure"; by strengthening a fellow Jew in any matter, whether in spiritual or material affairs, Hashem strengthens the health of the one who engages in this, both spiritually and materially alike. For the attribute of the Ribono shel Olam is many times over, to an incomparable degree—and this is, of course, also due to the vast disparity, or more accurately, the lack of any comparison, between the Creator and the created.

I derived particular satisfaction from the fact that you have provided several kuntresim and booklets for the library of the sanatorium, which is a matter of the "needs of the many," and the "merit of the many" depends upon it. Please inform me, according to the level of the guests there, which books from the Kehot Publication Society catalog would be suitable for them, and I will endeavor to have them sent there. You will surely be able to see the Kehot catalog with one of Anash.

Thank you for printing the letter to the Rabbis and the letter to the physicians, and for your thoughtfulness in sending me the clippings. I also acknowledge with thanks the receipt of the booklet *HaRokeach* containing your article. I am certain you will continue to do so in the future—sending here what you have printed—since many benefit from the library here.

I am sure you participated in the Yud-Tes Kislev farbrengen in an appropriate manner, especially in Kfar Chabad. Please let me know your impressions, as well as the impressions of the others gathered there, as there are surely things for which this information is needed. It is already known from the saying of the wise that "the past teaches the future," and from the above, it will be possible to know what requires further refinement and improvement.

With wishes for a happy Chanukah to you and your entire family, may they live.

## 3886

B"H, 27 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter—which lacks a date of writing—in which you ask how to prevent a *mikreh lailah* (nocturnal emission), *r"l*.

It is already known to all, first and foremost, that one must divert one's mind from the entire matter—meaning, even from thoughts regarding the *tikkun* (see *Responsa Tzemach Tzedek*, *Shaar HaMiluim*, beginning of Part II). Instead, one should study with consistency and diligence in *nigleh d'Torah* (the revealed Torah) and *pnimiyus haTorah* (the inner dimension of Torah), which provides vitality to the study of *nigleh d'Torah* and the performance of *mitzvos*.

Every day, at the very least, spend a few moments in the morning and a few moments at night increasing the recitation of the letters of Torah and *tefillah*. At the very least, be fluent by heart in some of them; it is best to know some chapters of *Mishnayos* and some chapters of *Tanya* by heart. It is understood that one must be careful regarding *tevilas Ezra*.

May it be the will of Hashem that the statement of our Sages, "He who comes to purify himself is assisted," be fulfilled in you. May Hashem fulfill the requests of your heart for good, and may you have good tidings in all that was mentioned.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe Shlita,
Secretary

## 3898

B"H, 4th day of Chanukah, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter, in which you write about your study schedules, both in Nigleh and in Chassidus. Surely you are fulfilling the ruling of our holy Torah that one must always ascend in matters of holiness, and when one invests effort and toils in this, the ruling is fulfilled: "You have labored and you have found."

And surely this point is engraved within you: that your being in Montreal is to serve as a living proof of how a student of Tomchei Temimim must be. This proof must not be only during the times of learning, davening, and keeping the yeshiva’s schedules with precision, but also to serve as a sample and living proof of how one must conduct oneself in the time between learning and davening. As is explained in Chassidus, a servant serves his master even when the master is nothing more than flesh and blood; how much more so, many times over, when the Master is the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He. The servitude must be evident all day long, and even in sleep.

And regarding this, too, it was said by our Sages, "You have labored and you have found," and "There is nothing that can stand before the will."

With blessings for success in Torah study with yiras shamayim, for the fulfillment of mitzvos with hiddur, and specifically in the avodah of tefillah.

## 3889

B"H, 29 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the third night of Chanukah.

Thank you for writing regarding the farbrengen of 19 Kislev, the festival that redeemed our souls in peace and gave us the light and vitality of our souls. Although your report was brief, it is certain that it did not merely leave an impression on all the *baalei batim*, as you put it in your letter, but that this impression will manifest in practice in matters of Torah and *mitzvos* in general, and in matters of *Chassidus*, its guidance, and its customs in particular. Indeed, there is a *chazakah* that *ta'amulah* (outreach) does not return empty; however, from time to time, one must refresh (*apfrishen*) the farbrengen by recalling some of the points discussed at that time. With words that come from the heart, and certainly with the necessary *hisbonenus*, you will find the appropriate ways to bring this into practice.

This is especially true since this awakening began on the Rosh Hashanah of *Chassidus* and the ways of *Chassidus*. It is already well-known why the term "Rosh Hashanah" (Head of the Year) is used rather than "Tchilas Hashanah" (Beginning of the Year): just as the head contains within it the vitality of all the limbs and from it the vitality is drawn, so too is it regarding Rosh Hashanah in general, and the Rosh Hashanah of *Chassidus* in particular, regarding the rest of the days of the year. May it be the will of Hashem that the desire of Hashem shall succeed in his hand regarding the aforementioned as well—namely, to be constantly increasing and ascending in holiness throughout the days of the year in all those matters that were discussed during the farbrengen.

With blessings and regards to all those who gathered; may they and their households, *shichyu*, stand upon the blessing.

P.S.
It gave me pleasure to read in your letter that you have learned five chapters of *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah* by heart. See *Likutei Torah*, *Kedoshim*, in the *maamar* entitled *VeHadarta Pnei Zaken*, which explains that through this, the Torah and the one who transmitted it—our Alter Rebbe—are permanently engraved in the mind and memory. See there.

## 3990

3990

B"H, 29 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 26 Kislev, along with the enclosure.

It is surprising that in all your letters, you do not mention anything regarding your good deeds—yours and your wife’s, may they live—concerning Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs. My intent is simple: your participation in the shiurim taught in public in both Nigleh and Da"Ch, your participation in Chabad activities in an appropriate manner, and your efforts to disseminate the wellsprings outward, etc. After all, the mitzvah of "love your fellow as yourself"—which includes giving charity in spiritual matters as well—applies to you and your wife, may they live. And after all the explanations that there is "no place" or "no possibility," the fact remains that there is nothing that can stand in the way of the will. Especially when one contemplates the statement of our Sages that the poor person (who receives spiritual charity) does more for the householder than the householder does for the poor person—meaning that all of the above is for **their own benefit**, both materially and spiritually.

May it be Hashem’s will that, at the very least, from now on you will begin to take an interest in what is written above, especially since I have spoken with you and your wife, may they live, about this in person several times. If you begin to contemplate this now, in time it will lead to good deeds. May it be His will that this happens soon.

Enclosed is the Kuntres for 19 Kislev, which I am sure you will merit to use to benefit the many, and the merit of the many is dependent upon you.

With blessings for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires and those of your wife, may she live, for the good, soon.

## 3991

B"H, 29 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

Mrs. Shoshana, may she live,

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter of 23 Kislev, in which you write that you have submitted the responsa of your father, the late Rabbi, may he rest in peace, for publication in *Pardes HaTemimim*. Since the responsa comprise approximately twenty-four pages (it is unclear whether you mean pages or leaves consisting of two sides), there is reason to doubt whether the editors will be willing to print the responsa in a single issue, or if they will divide it into two issues—and who knows when the subsequent issue will be published.

It is understood that I cannot give you a definitive answer regarding this, as the total size of the issue is not yet clear. If it turns out to be smaller than anticipated, you would surely agree that there is no room to allocate so many pages to a single section, as there are several other sections that must be included. Conversely, if it is larger than anticipated, the editorial board itself would certainly not want to divide the responsa into two, as is obvious.

Personally, I believe it requires consideration, as there are several reasons why it might be better for the responsa to appear in two issues; it would then be read by a larger number of people over a longer period of time. It is human nature that when a new issue or periodical is published, the previous one is set aside. However, since you have requested—also on behalf of your brothers, may they live—that it be included in a single issue, I will endeavor to do so, provided that the aforementioned case does not arise where the number of pages in the issue is smaller than anticipated, for the reasons stated above.

Since you do not mention anything regarding the welfare of the entire family, I assume this is a sign that all is well.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 3990

B"H, 29 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing and learned, whose work is the work of Heaven,

Peace and blessing!

After your longest silence, your letter of 22 Kislev was received, in which you write regarding the arrangements for the bright day of 19 Kislev—the festival that redeemed our souls in peace and gave us the light and vitality of our souls—as well as the days preceding and following it. I do not know what your custom has been until now, but based on what is explained and seen tangibly, the benefit of plowing and sowing is only when fruits actually grow. In the language of Chassidus, one must draw this into the inner dimensions specifically, and for it to lead to *uvchein* (and thus), one should have sought ways and means to maintain the connection with the *avreichim* from the other yeshivos who participated in the 19 Kislev *farbrengen*, and to renew (to refresh) within them the inspiration of the *farbrengen*. The main thing is to endeavor that it leads to a matter of *uvchein* appropriate for them. Since among these students there are certainly some with whom you are already in contact, through them one can find out about the others, and there is nothing that can stand before the will.

Surely this year, too, you distributed *Chanukah gelt* on my behalf, just as I requested of the esteemed Chossid R' A. Paris to arrange this, as in previous years, for those who are already studying Chassidus, etc.

## 3993

B"H, 29 Kislev, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of the Reshet,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

...External interference in the spiritual matters of the Reshet is baseless, as has been discussed and agreed upon even by the representatives of the offices. It is understood that if they see weakness in this—and certainly if they act contrary to what is desired due to outside pressure—it weakens the entire position of the Reshet and all of its utility. In the current state of the field of education, if there is no clear benefit, it is a detriment, and a word to the wise is sufficient. In all of this, since the interference is only regarding a negative matter—meaning, they are saying that so-and-so is not fit to fulfill a certain role and should be replaced by someone more suitable, and the more suitable person will be chosen by the Reshet—then this is not of the category mentioned above, and therefore it does not fall under the category of "let the law pierce the mountain."

With blessings for good tidings.

## 3994

B"H, Chanukah, Fifth Candle, 5716
Brooklyn

To all those gathered and participating in the annual United States celebration of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, may Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

To the annual celebration, 3 Teves 5716: I send my greeting and blessing to the askanim of the yeshiva and to all those gathered who have come to participate in the annual Torah celebration of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim in America.

Since this celebration is taking place the day after Chanukah, when the influence of this luminous Yom Tov is fresh in everyone’s memory and will surely illuminate our daily lives throughout the entire year, I wish to emphasize a few essential points regarding Chanukah.

Chanukah reminds us that even something like the Beis HaMikdash, the holiest place for the resting of the Shechinah, can, under certain circumstances, become defiled, even while remaining outwardly intact.

In such a case, Chanukah teaches us that the Beis HaMikdash can be purified only through complete mesiras nefesh: through open and bold resistance against the forces of darkness and tumah, without engaging in calculations of who are the "mighty," who are the "many," and so on.

The lesson from this, in our days, is clear. Our Sages say: "Since the destruction of the Beis HaMikdash, Hashem has nothing in His world but the four amos of halacha." A yeshiva is the holiest place for the resting of the Shechinah. We must ensure that the study of Torah is done on the purity of holiness, with pure fear of Hashem, which in these times, more than ever, requires mesiras nefesh.

This very spirit of mesiras nefesh and Torah study with yiras shamayim permeates the Lubavitcher yeshivos—and it is a mesiras nefesh not only within the four amos of the yeshiva and not only for oneself, but also outside the yeshiva and for the other, for the near and the far. This is one of the specific traits of the Lubavitcher yeshivos, which was implanted in them from the very first day of their founding by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. The students of the Lubavitcher yeshivos are taught to be the Chashmonaim of our generation, the self-sacrificing and tireless fighters for Torah-Yiddishkeit on the purity of holiness in various parts of the world.

Thus, the great merit of all those who take a part in the support and expansion of the Lubavitcher yeshivos is understandable. And in the spirit of Chanukah, this support must be with one’s body and one’s money, and **increasing and continuing**, in order to enable the Lubavitcher yeshivos to be "increasing and continuing" in spreading the "candle of mitzvah and Torah light" and the "light of Torah" from the yeshiva into the street, and from the home into the entire surroundings.

And in this merit, Hashem will also be "increasing and continuing" with an abundance of blessing and success for each person and their household—may they live—in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings for good,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 3995

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 23rd of Kislev, in which you write that you saw a certain book of *segulos* which discusses the wisdom of palmistry, etc.—

Stay away from this path. If you are determined to have a book of *segulos*, there is a *segulah* that is tried and tested, and that is our holy Torah. There is also a wisdom that is tried and tested, and that is the wisdom of the Creator, with which one can unite through the study of Torah—specifically in a wondrous way, as explained in *Tanya*, Chapter 5; see there.

It has already been said, "You shall be wholehearted with Hashem your G-d," and some say (Ramban) that this is also included in the count of the 613 *mitzvos* of the Torah.

It is also understood that what you write—that your activities within the framework of *Tzeirei Agudas Chabad* are almost nil because you are not qualified for this and your health does not permit it—is negated by the Torah. For regarding everyone it is said, "And you shall love your neighbor as yourself," and furthermore, it is a great principle in the Torah. Since you are qualified, and your health permits you to act regarding yourself, it is a positive commandment from the Torah; consequently, the strength is given to fulfill it regarding others. Elaborating on such a simple matter is superfluous, and it is a pity to waste time on *shakla v'tarya* regarding this. When you contemplate this for yourself, you will find many ways and means to spread the *maayanos* outward and to disseminate Judaism within the framework of *Tzeirei Agudas Chabad* in general.

As you requested, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zy"a*.

Regarding what you write about the special pleasantness found in the recitation of *Mizmor Shir L'Yom HaShabbos*, this can be explained according to what is clarified in both the *nigleh* and the *nistar* of Torah: that this is the reception of the holiness of the day of *Shabbos*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 3996

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Teves, 5716
Brooklyn

The Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod
May Hashem preserve them

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letters of the 21st and 24th of Kislev, along with their enclosures... regarding whether one should add another name to the name Tomchei Temimim or Achei Temimim.

Since these primary names were established by our holy Nasi, and despite the fact that there are already dozens of yeshivos, it has not been heard of in any other place that they would add further names. I am therefore puzzled as to why you would be the ones to initiate this change. This is especially true given that it is possible to apply the name "Yisrael" to other matters, such as to the sefarim or the building, and the like. Furthermore, it is also known according to the revealed Torah that when two names are combined for a single subject, the matter is not that each one remains as it was on its own; rather, the two together form a new name (as is also proven from the matter of the names of a bride and her mother-in-law, cited in the Responsa of the Tzemach Tzedek, Even HaEzer, end of Part I).

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 3997

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 17th of Kislev, in which you write about your wandering from yeshiva to yeshiva due to the stubbornness of your heart, etc., and ask for advice regarding this.

The advice is found in the Tur, Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim, beginning of Siman 1—see there—and in several places in Tanya. In short, it is that a yeshiva student must listen to the instructions of the Rosh Yeshiva and fulfill them **completely**. The claim that the yetzer hara does not allow it is no claim at all, for every person possesses a second soul, the nefesh elokis, through which one can overcome the yetzer hara, if one truly desires to do so. May Hashem grant you the merit to do teshuvah for your inappropriate conduct until now, and to do so as soon as possible.

With blessings for yiras shamayim and good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

3999

B”H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Teves, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, man of action, etc.,
R’ Katriel Fishel, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

...On this occasion, I will take the liberty of addressing a personal point, which is this:

The obligation of every individual regarding a mitzvah that cannot be performed by others is well known, as it is distinct from the obligation of other mitzvos—even though all were given by one Shepherd. This applies likewise to the matter of *lehagdil Torah ulehaadir* (making the Torah great and glorious) and to *Orach Chaim* and the customs of Yisrael, which are also Torah.

Now, I have read what you have written on various matters and issues, and I searched among them for the proportion of issues whose subject is the teachings of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs. It is extremely small—at the very least, among the writings of yours that I have seen.

This is consistent with the aforementioned introduction. It is a wonder to me, given that those who occupy themselves with matters pertaining to Chassidus and what relates to it are few, especially when comparing their number to those who discuss and debate other issues. Why should a person exchange the role that is undoubtedly his—since there are few or no others to fulfill it—and dedicate the majority of his time and decisive energy to a matter in which many are already occupied, even if we were to assume it is a clear mitzvah?

This has already been alluded to in the *farbrengen* by the verse, "They made me the keeper of the vineyards, but my own vineyard I have not kept." For even the former are vineyards, and the Torah testifies to this; yet, one complains from the depths of the heart that there is a "vineyard of my own" which I have not kept (even if they "made me" a keeper, and the conditions force it—why did it fall to his lot to be the keeper of vineyards in general?).

Elaborating further is surely superfluous. I only wish to note that we see tangibly that in matters of Chassidus and its customs, in previous generations, one required immense effort and battle against opponents, etc. Yet, in our generation—this orphaned generation—not only are there almost no opponents, but those who seek the teachings of Chassidus have actually increased, both in quantity and quality, begging in a voice that is heard or not heard to be shown the light that is good.

With a blessing, in accordance with the well-known adage, that you should utilize everything with which the Creator of the world has graced you to fulfill your inner, spiritual task: the dissemination of the *maayanos* (the wellsprings) *chutzah* (outward). For, as is the nature of the human soul, then—and only then—will it find its spiritual satisfaction in its fullness.

With respect and blessing.

Regarding your observation on the Rambam, *Hilchos Berachos* 11:5: "Make a parapet for your roof, etc.," which contradicts his own words there in 11:4: "Things that are a matter of danger, one does not recite a blessing over"—yet the obligation of a parapet is as it is written, "And you shall make a parapet for your roof, and you shall not bring blood, etc."

In my opinion, it is simple that for the Rambam, "and you shall not bring blood" is not the providing of a reason for the obligation of making a parapet, but rather a **commandment** in its own right. For the reasons for the mitzvos are not counted in the 613 mitzvos, as he wrote in the Fifth Principle of *Sefer HaMitzvos*. However, "and you shall not bring blood" he included in the count of the negative commandments. What compelled the Rambam to say this is the *Sifri* (Devarim 22:8): "And you shall make a parapet, etc."—a positive commandment; "you shall not bring, etc."—a negative commandment. And if, instead of making a parapet, one made a ramp for the roof or the like, he has fulfilled the negative commandment but has nullified the positive commandment. Note also *Yoma* 72a, and see *Sefer HaMitzvos* there.

## 3300

3300

B"H, 3 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of the Chabad Vocational Schools in the Holy Land, may it be built and established,
May they live,

Peace and Blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 25 Cheshvan, along with the enclosure... Regarding what you wrote concerning the necessity for an additional counselor, and that there is a thought to take some of the students for this position: In my opinion, this does not seem advisable. For surely, if they continue as students, they will become more proficient in their professional training, and it goes without saying that they will study more *limudei kodesh*. This is not the case when you make them counselors; the level of *kabbalas ol* that still remains with them will diminish even further, and "since one is preoccupied with emitting, one does not absorb."

Regarding what you wrote about the commencement of construction and its manner:

One must begin in such a way that, in the final analysis, the buildings will be well-developed. From the proposals suitable for this, it is understood that one must choose the one that currently requires a smaller investment and offers more favorable conditions. Furthermore, one must take into account that, ultimately, at least one of the vocational school buildings must be magnificent. As some of the visitors told me, the current vocational school buildings give an impression of poverty...

Awaiting good news.

I have now received your letter from 27 Kislev. In response: For the time being, the administration of the agricultural school belongs to the administration of the vocational school.

It is surprising that you are continuing so [slowly] in the actual acceptance of students, at a time when alacrity is most necessary for several reasons and concerns.

The curriculum at the agricultural school is, of course, dependent on the level of the students' knowledge. But it is understood that one must ensure—along the lines of what I wrote regarding the vocational school—that the hours of *limudei kodesh* must be more than those of secular studies (especially since the students are younger). The day must begin specifically with *limudei kodesh*, so that the agricultural school does not serve as a temptation and incitement to flee from the *yeshiva*, etc.

The setup of the agricultural school must simply be in a manner that, within a short time, you will be able to expand it both in quantity and in quality.

## 402

B"H, 3 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with the needs of the community, R' Dovid, may he live:

Shalom and Bracha!

Following your long silence, I received your letter from the 15th of Kislev, in which you write about your activities in the area of Bnos Chabad. You are certainly contemplating with the necessary focus how to improve the points you mentioned that are not yet as they should be. This is especially true since, as is apparent from your letter, this depends on a lack of "moisture" and *chassidishe varimkeit* (Chassidic warmth)—a matter that should, by all accounts, be easily found in the village called Kfar Chabad. It is understood and obvious that you did well to begin learning with that particular group again, even after the interruption; on the contrary, the interruption is a pity, but surely this too will be for the good. Since young women in general—and young women who come from one country to another, especially in these years which are years of transition—are more prone to crisis, *chas v'shalom*, all the effort and exertion to improve the situation is worthwhile. The magnitude of the merit is impossible to describe. From this, it is also understood that regarding what you wrote—that perhaps you wrote at too great a length—on the contrary, you were too brief, for no matter how much you write, it will still not be enough relative to the importance of the matter.

I was pleased by what you wrote regarding the activities of N'shei Chabad in Kfar Chabad. Regarding them, and all the more so regarding the young women, it is appropriate that after teaching them, the teacher or lecturer should endeavor to have them ask questions and the like, in order to draw them in and interest them more in the specific subjects being studied.

In these meetings, it is possible that someone might ask an unusual question. It is understood that one should not be discouraged by this, for all beginnings are difficult. And even if someone were to ask something undesirable—that is, something that weakens the authority of matters of *Toras Hashem* and the like—this will surely be in the extreme minority, and perhaps not even that. In any case, you will certainly always find on the spot the appropriate words to dispel the undesirable impression, or if that is not possible, at least words that negate the hypothesis and its reality. *V'dai l'meivin* (a word to the wise is sufficient).

May the *Ribono shel Olam* fulfill the desires of your heart for the good regarding the matters about which you write, and may you bring good news of adding to the aforementioned activities among the N'shei and Bnos Chabad with the energy and strength that are required. May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you success.

With blessings for success in the above.

## 44

B"H, 3 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, 11 Kislev: It is a matter of great wonder and astonishment that there has been such a long gap between one letter and the next, especially at a time when you have holy work upon your shoulders. It is self-understood how much we yearn to receive detailed reports regarding what is happening there, and I hope that from now on, at the very least, you will rectify this.

Regarding what you wrote about the difference of opinion among the doctors: 1) Since the common denominator between them is that there is currently no need for surgery, your hearts should rejoice over this. As for what the doctors conclude regarding what might happen in two or three years, the Ribono shel Olam is the Healer of all flesh and performs wonders; the authority of a doctor is for the immediate, practical management of a situation, not for predicting the future...

And regarding how you conclude—which is, in truth, the main point—as explained in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 7, that all of a person’s affairs depend on the mitzvah in which he must be especially careful: in your case, this is your involvement with the students, upon which depend not only your spiritual matters but also the aforementioned matters.

You write that you do not find satisfaction from the students because they are constantly changing, etc., and what is the benefit in this? Here is the answer: 1) Even if they only study for a few months, you surely teach them in such a way that they will absorb the learning and it will be engraved in their memory, which will certainly lead to results. 2) And this is the main point: you must contemplate how to interest the students more and draw them toward the studies, and primarily toward the matters of Chabad, or at the very least toward the Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch institutions. In doing so, they will naturally see the light, that it is good. This matter depends solely on you and the other Anash who are there, and I look forward to hearing good news regarding this as well.

With blessings.

## D'H

B"H, 3 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and upright individual, who occupies himself with communal needs, R' Shmuel Yosef [Findrik]

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 13 Kislev, we begin with a blessing of Mazal Tov, Mazal Tov, on the occasion of the wedding of your son, the esteemed and upright avreich, R' Yehoshua Zelig, may he live. May they build a home in Israel, an everlasting edifice built upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, as they are illuminated by the "light of Torah"—which is the Torah of Chassidus.

...Since he is in close proximity to the building where he was until now, he should certainly arrange to visit there frequently, though at irregular times. It is a known halachic principle that one who enters and exits [a place] carries the awe of his arrival throughout the entire day, and a word to the wise is sufficient. It is understood that, in addition to this, there must also be fixed times for his visits, such as on days off and the like; and there is nothing that can stand before the will.

Regarding what you write concerning the electric lamp: many who are zealous for the word of Hashem follow the practice in such matters of installing a "Shabbos timer." Although there are those who are extremely stringent and even doubt the permissibility of this, I therefore refrain from giving official advice. However, he, for his part, should endeavor to arrange this without causing a commotion. It would be worthwhile for him to investigate where he can obtain such a timer, as they are certainly available in abundance in Tel Aviv, especially among the G-d-fearing Ashkenazic circles who have followed this practice for generations. He should purchase the timer at my expense; it is understood that I will cover all costs—namely, the price of the timer and its installation in the necessary location in the house where it is situated. After he informs me and carries this out, I am confident that he will succeed in gaining their agreement, and consequently, it will also be easier to implement this in the other Malben institutions, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

I am certain that you have done what is incumbent upon you regarding the celebration of the Festival of Redemption, 19 Kislev—the festival on which our souls were redeemed in peace, and the light and vitality of our souls were granted to us—in every place that your influence reaches. Please write with good news regarding this. Thank you.

With blessings for health and success.

## 406

B"H, 3 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

It is somewhat surprising that no news has been received since late Cheshvan. May it be Hashem’s will that this is a sign for good, indicating that all is well. The path to action is the same as that taken by other G-d-fearing avreichim in such matters: through an intermediary. This is the very thing I have written to you about several times, and it seems you are negligent in this regard. It is in the nature of human beings that in such matters, the longer the negligence persists, the harder it is to be rid of it. However, since one must fulfill the ruling of our Sages that one must "search like a person searching for their lost object," and it is known that the words of our holy Torah are not merely beautiful rhetoric but that the matters correspond precisely to the expressions used, you should know that this is indeed a loss. Every day that passes without this is, to a certain extent, a deficient day. Our Sages have already elaborated on this in the tractate of Yevamos: "Whoever dwells without..." I will await good news as soon as possible.

## 408

B"H, 3 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn

To the G-d-fearing, honorable, and distinguished, etc., R' Shmuel Menachem Mendel, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 7 Kislev.

May it be the will of Hashem that from here on you shall know no more sorrow or anguish, and that you will hear only good news regarding yourself and your entire family.

Regarding what you wrote about an *avel* (mourner) who is leading the *davening* reciting *Hallel*: It is surprising that this is a question, as it has been about five years since our custom was printed in the *Kuntres Chanukah*, in the *maamar* of the Tzemach Tzedek, *Baruch She'asah Nissim*, published by Kehot in 5701...

Regarding the questions: 
1) Whether to hire someone else to recite *Kaddish* for the grandmother, *a"h*, since she has no children, and the grandchildren are already reciting *Kaddish* for their father, *a"h*.

It seems to me that since there is a *ma'alah* (merit) in a grandchild reciting it—especially a son's son—as opposed to a stranger, the grandchildren should recite it. According to what is written in the *Acharonim* (see *Kitzur Shulchan Aruch* 26:16; *Sdei Chemed*, *Aveilus* 53; *Kol Bo*, p. 376), one *Kaddish* can count for two deceased individuals. However, in *Zera Emes* (cited in *Sdei Chemed*, *Aveilus* 158), it says otherwise.

It could be argued that the case there is different, as at least a relative is reciting it, which is not the case with hiring a stranger. This requires further study in the aforementioned *sefarim* themselves, which are not currently at hand.

2) Whether to recite *Kaddish* for the grandmother after the completion of the eleven months since the father's passing, due to the concern that it might appear as if one is making the deceased appear as a *rasha* (wicked person) in the eyes of those listening.

In the *sefer Mishnas Rabbi Akiva* (cited in *Elef HaMagen* on *Mateh Ephraim* and in the *Hashmatos* of the Maharsha in *Yoreh Deah*), it is proven that there is no need to be concerned about this. This is also written in *Kanaf Renanah* (cited in *Kol Bo*, p. 369), and it is implied in the aforementioned *Kitzur Shulchan Aruch*.

Concluding with goodness.

With regards to all the members of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, may they live.

## 4-T

B"H, 4 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

It was a pleasure to see you during the Shabbos farbrengen, and I have just now received your letter from the third night of Chanukah. While it is understood that, in accordance with the teachings of Chabad Chassidus, a brief meeting and a short letter like yours do not constitute the ultimate goal—as they are closer to *makifim* (encompassing lights) than to *pnimiyus* (internalization)—may it be G-d’s will that this serves as a good beginning for a change in your conduct going forward. That is to say, you should return to your practice of some years ago, when you would write in detail and with relative frequency, which is not the case now.

I also wish to comment on the general impression conveyed by your letter, which suggests that you are once again in a state of worry—specifically, the worry that your bread might be lacking, *chas v’shalom*. It is a source of great wonder regarding you, for surely there is more than enough brought in the Torah in general, and in the teachings of Chassidus in particular, regarding the *middah* of *bitachon*, and so on. (Of course, this does not contradict the *hishtadlus* of creating *keilim* for one’s livelihood, as it is written: "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you **do**." However, the "doing" must be as the verse says: "When you eat the labor of your **hands**," and not the labor of the mind, the head, and the heart.) Especially in your case, having seen miracles with your own eyes, it is astonishing that you would suddenly worry whether He who sustains and provides for **all**—which is, relatively speaking, one billion eight hundred million people—will also provide for you and your household, that you may live in a kosher manner and with abundance. It is a pity to spend time elaborating on such a simple matter. May it be G-d’s will that you see the situation as it truly is, and consequently, increase even more in the strengthening of Yiddishkeit and its dissemination in your entire environment. May the Ribono shel Olam increase His measure—which is many times over—regarding your peace of mind, livelihood, and Chassidishe *nachas* from all your children, together with your wife, may they live.

Awaiting good news.

## 410

B"H, 4 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs, R' Chaim Zusia, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from 3 Chanukah, in which you write—albeit very briefly—regarding the farbrengen of 19 Kislev in Kfar Chabad. It seems that this writing was a case of "a pot belonging to partners," and with added "hiddur" at that, where everyone relies on the other, and consequently, only the main points are written based on this. I have already written to several of anash that it is understood that it is better for one report to be received twice than for it to be missing entirely.

I was especially pleased by your efforts to involve yeshiva students in the farbrengen of the bright day of 19 Kislev, the festival that "redeemed our souls in peace" and gave us the light and vitality of our souls. Even more so, that this took place within the walls of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim. My hope is strong that—**each one** who is connected to this—will continue to maintain a connection with those who participated in the farbrengen, so that the hisorerus in their affairs continues in the days following it, and not just for these days, but for weeks and months, etc. In the natural course of events, this hisorerus will also reach their friends who did not participate, and there is a strength in outreach that does not return empty.

It would be good if a list of the participants were sent here—without their knowledge—so that when letters are received from there, one can know if so-and-so participated, and consequently, whether he is familiar with the "environment" of Chassidus at least, or if he is still completely new to it...

I was pleased to read at the end of your letter that you prepared a plan of action for the days of Chanukah. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding this as well, provided that it is with the necessary detail.

With blessings for success in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

## 411

B”H, 5 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, engaged in communal needs,
R’ Alexander Sender shlita,

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter was received some time ago, in which you write regarding your proposal at the Agudas Chassidei Chabad meeting concerning the necessity for each of the leaders and elders of Anash to visit the settlements of the Bnei Yisrael, etc. Your letter was one of the factors that led to what I wrote to Agudas Chassidei Chabad some time ago.

...In our country, in the past, when this involved actual mortal danger, and concealment and hiddenness—even among the Chareidim to a severe degree—they engaged in this regardless of the aforementioned. And when they came to the land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year, and through an arousal from Above the opposition from those who were formerly opposed among the Chareidim diminished and became as naught—not only is there no danger in this, but on the contrary, it involves matters that even in the eyes of the nations of the world are considered good—yet precisely now, the avodah and the energy are diminishing from time to time, a decrease after a decrease, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

It is already known the interpretation of the sin "that we have sinned before You through the yetzer hara," that there are matters for which even the yetzer hara cannot find an explanation or the audacity to incite a son of Yisrael to act in such a way, and through various stratagems they provoke him, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

It is understood that the above is not directed toward any specific individual, but rather to the majority of the leaders and elders of Anash, and consequently, to each one of them as well.

Regarding your notification of the wedding of your son Dovid shlita, I will repeat my blessing. May it be Hashem’s will that it be for a mazal tov, a mazal tov, at a good and successful hour, and for an everlasting edifice built upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, as they are illuminated by the light of Torah—this is the Torah of Chassidus.

With blessings of mazal tov, mazal tov.

## 412

B.H., 5 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 23 Kislev, in which you ask whether you should begin to daven according to the Nusach HaAri. I assume you do not mean Nusach Sefard, but rather the Nusach HaAri as clarified by our Alter Rebbe.

It is unnecessary to elaborate on the virtues of this nusach, some of which are explained in the introduction to *Shaar HaKollel* printed together with the Siddur of our Alter Rebbe—the author of the *Tanya* and the *Shulchan Aruch*—which, according to tradition, our Alter Rebbe compiled from sixty different siddurim and versions. However, you should know that according to what is explained in the responsa *Beis HaYotzer* and *Minchas Elazar* (Section 1), while one may change from Nusach Ashkenaz to Nusach Sefard, and within Nusach Sefard to the aforementioned Nusach HaAri, one may not do the reverse. This means that if you take it upon yourself to daven in Nusach HaAri, it must be with the intention of adhering to this nusach permanently. Therefore, you should reflect on whether this decision of yours is definitive. If it is, may your heart’s desires be fulfilled for the good, to daven in the nusach of our Alter Rebbe, the Nasi of Israel, and may you be blessed.

Regarding what you write about how to organize your learning and divide it throughout the hours of the day, you should consult with the anash in your area. You should detail your current knowledge and schedule to them, and they will guide you.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the matter of "a person should divide [his study] into three," etc.—see the commentaries on the Gemara there. Regarding the practical halacha, see the *Hilchos Talmud Torah* of our Alter Rebbe, Chapter 2. See there.

You surely know of the three daily study portions that are equal for every soul, an enactment of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, and you surely fulfill them. In any event, you should observe them from now on.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 413

413

B"H, 5 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote about how the matter of the well-known nigun came about: it is already explained in many places that in a situation where one must be concerned about *maris ayin* (the appearance of wrongdoing) and what people might hear, any justifications provided by the person involved or the cause of the situation are, at best, slightly altered from the truth, and it is possible that even that is not the case. And as for what you write, that "it was not I who wrote it," etc.—in my own letter, I wrote regarding the yeshivah, and not regarding any specific individual, whoever they may be. For if something is not as it should be, it is not attributed to a specific person, but rather to the name of the yeshivah, which is called by such-and-such a name and was founded by such-and-such a person. And a word to the wise is sufficient.

Regarding your notification of your birthday, it was mentioned at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nevag"m, zia*, on Erev Rosh Chodesh. As our Sages of blessed memory said, "the body derives pleasure from the body," and there is also the interpretation that this is a foretaste of the future era. For now, the vitality of the body comes from the neshamah, whereas in the future era it will be the opposite, and the neshamah will receive its vitality from the body. This is also the meaning of "And Esther—the Community of Israel—was taken to the King—the King of the universe—in the tenth month, which is the month of Teves."

I trust you observed the customs of a birthday, as is the practice of anash in recent times. May it be His will that this be a year of success for you, both spiritually and materially, for you and your family, *sheyichyu*.

With blessings.

## 414

B"H, 6 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write that you feel a decline in your spiritual standing, etc.: It is understood that, first and foremost in such a situation, one must increase in diligence and persistence in the study of Torah, and specifically in the study of the inner dimension of Torah—which provides vitality and light to all of a person’s holy endeavors—for even a little light pushes away much darkness.

Furthermore, one must be careful not to exaggerate, Heaven forbid, the nature of this decline. This is also explained in the *maamar* "Mizmor Shir L'Yom HaShabbos" by the Mitteler Rebbe, which has just been published. Afterwards, you should study with appropriate focus chapters 26–29 of the *Tanya Kadisha*. It would also be beneficial to connect with the *mashpi'im* of *Chassidus* at Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim and speak to them about this concern of yours, thereby fulfilling the teaching of our Sages regarding the verse, "If there is anxiety in a man's heart, let him speak it out," etc.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 415

B"H, 6 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, etc., R' Ze'ev Aryeh, shlita,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge with thanks the receipt of your book, *Raza D'Chayai*, which discusses the immortality of the soul based on the Tanach, Shas, etc. Surely you will act similarly regarding the other works you have published by sending them here to the library, as many derive benefit from them. Thank you in advance.

On this occasion, I would like to add a general observation. Although the dictum "Accept the truth from whoever says it" is well-known (see Rambam, Introduction to *Shemonah Perakim*; *Hilchos Kiddush HaChodesh*, end of chapter 17), it is nevertheless a pity that in the aforementioned book you chose to cite from certain books that are not accepted by many of *anash*, including those in Eretz Yisrael. Because of this, many will distance themselves from this book and, consequently, will not read it or benefit from its contents. This is especially true since the aforementioned citations do not add to the understanding of the subject, but serve only as a "Judah and more to call," to say that so-and-so also agrees with this. It is understood that sometimes, according to our Sages, "from his own wood he is felled," and one may use an opponent's own words against him. However, citations from a few individuals will not be effective when the vast majority of the book is founded upon *sifrei kodesh*. For someone for whom that is not sufficient, these few citations will not be of much help either.

There is another point, and it is a unique one, relevant to our current era—which is particularly afflicted by the blurring of boundaries and the intermingling of good and evil to the point of confusing one with the other. This only increases the necessity of not mixing straw with wheat, and certainly not introducing a "foreign branch" into a vineyard of holiness, even if it is the best of that foreign growth.

With respect and blessing.

With blessings for success in the study of Torah with *yiras shamayim* and in the *avodah* of *tefillah*, and that you may influence your friends, *shiy*, in all of this as well.

## 17

B”H, 7 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Sunday, and your question regarding how a person can determine whether a desire to engage in communal needs, or any other matter involving the merit of the many, is for the sake of Heaven or stems from an ulterior motive:

Here is the answer:

1) It is well known from the *sichos* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that although it is obvious that everyone must be a *ma’arei d’chushbana* (one who keeps an accounting) regarding their actions and speech, there are nevertheless set times for conducting this accounting. It is like a businessman: if he were to be preoccupied with bookkeeping too frequently, not only would it not be beneficial, but on the contrary, it would take away from the time and attention he needs to devote to expanding and refining his business. Sometimes, it even prevents him from engaging in his work as necessary, because an accounting conducted over too short a period is inappropriate. The same applies to conducting an accounting in one’s *avodah* of Hashem; there are set times for this throughout the year, such as during the *Aseres Yemei Teshuvah*, and similarly on the eve of *Rosh Chodesh*, *Yom Kippur Katan*, and so on.

2) It is a well-known saying of the Rebbe (Rashab), the father of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that the litmus test in a situation of doubt as to the source of a particular thought or desire is to see if they are preventing one from performing a good deed. If they are, it is almost certain that their source is not pure.

3) It is well known from the *Sifri* (Parshas Tetzei 29:19) regarding *tzedakah*: if someone lost a coin and a poor person found it, the merit of the *mitzvah* of *tzedakah* belongs to the owner of the coin, even though he did not intend to, did not want to, and did not even know about it. It is understood that the same applies to *tzedakah* performed through involvement in communal needs, assisting a fellow in matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, and the like.

From all of this, it is understood that you should divert your attention from the thoughts that are preventing you from putting into practice your desire to bring merit to the many through involvement in specific communal needs. Engage in this work, and Hashem will grant you success. As our Sages said: a person sanctifies himself a little from below—and the sanctification of *Bnei Yisrael* is through the performance of *mitzvos*, as in the text of the blessing on *mitzvos*, "Who has sanctified us with His *mitzvos*"—and they sanctify him greatly from above.

It is my hope that you are also studying *Chassidus* every day, and may Hashem grant you success to share good news regarding all of the above.

With blessings.
