## 19

B"H, 11 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...It is incomprehensible, even to his own mind, by what authority he wishes to insist upon what seems right to **him** regarding the admission of students to the school. Since this is the responsibility of the principal, as is the custom **throughout** the entire world, it is understood that school principals are also flesh and blood and are liable to err. Therefore, the authority is granted to bring a complaint against them to the one who oversees them. However, "there is room to say" that he, too, is liable to err, and he was not appointed to take the law into his own hands.

May it be the will of Hashem that a spirit from on high be poured upon him, and he may come to the realization that he has not yet reached the level of "my heart is hollow within me," such that all of his actions in every detail are absolutely good and beyond reproach. Consequently, from time to time, he should entertain the doubt that perhaps he ought to consult with his colleagues before taking action in practice...

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 420

B"H, 11 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the N'shei U’Bnos Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may Hashem protect them,
Bnei Brak Branch,
May they live.

Blessings and peace!

We acknowledge receipt of your letter from the beginning of the month of Kislev, the month of redemption. Surely you will continue to do so in the future, and may Hashem grant you success.

Even though, according to halacha, the concept of "encroachment" does not apply to matters of education, there is a concern regarding undesirable competition and becoming involved in politics, etc. You will surely be able to clarify whether there is a basis for this concern, and you should make your decision in accordance with that clarification.

Regarding what you wrote about the proposal to join an existing Bikur Cholim society, with the reasoning that in time, after you become deeply involved, you will be able to take it over:

It is understood that the goal of your organization is not to acquire and conquer societies to make them your own, but rather to perform your holy work, especially in areas that others are not addressing, or are not addressing properly, or even not as thoroughly as is required. Since the aforementioned society is already established and has the capacity to continue existing in the future, it would be more worthwhile for you to utilize your time and energy in other suitable areas.

I am certain you will provide appropriate details regarding how you utilized the days of the month of Kislev and the scope of your work. Thank you in advance.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 422

B"H, 11 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined, etc., R' Dovid Meir, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of the 4th of Teves: As our Sages of blessed memory state, "The body derives pleasure from the body," which is one of the reasons the month is called Teves, from the word *tov* (good). Since the Torah has validated the names of the months that were brought back from Bavel, and this name is included among them, it is understood that the Torah also confirms that the aforementioned is indeed good.

One may explain the inner meaning of this according to what is explained in the teachings of Chassidus: In the time to come, the *neshamah* will receive its vitality from the body, for the highest of the high is precisely that which descended the lowest—down to the body. Currently, however, this is in a state of concealment, and in the time to come, the truth of this will be revealed as well. This is the virtue of "Esther was taken"—*Knesses Yisrael*, which is called "Esther" (hidden) during the time of exile—"to the King"—the King of the world—"Ahasuerus"—He whose end (*acharis*) and beginning (*reishis*) are one, in the tenth month, which is the month of Teves, as mentioned above.

May the Ribono shel Olam lengthen your days and years in pleasantness, in a healthy body, together with your wife, may she live and be well. May the instruction of the Rambam be fulfilled in you, that maintaining a healthy and sound body is among the ways of Hashem.

With a blessing to hear good news regarding all the above.

## 423

B"H, 11 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I have received your request for a blessing for peace of mind and for livelihood with tranquility.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, the Nasi of Israel, regarding the aforementioned.

Just as one must create proper vessels to receive the blessings of Hashem, you should have your tefillin checked immediately to ensure they are kosher according to the law. Furthermore, every weekday before putting on tefillin, you should drop a few cents into a tzedakah box, and after taking off the tefillin, recite at least one chapter of Tehillim. When one puts on tefillin—which must be placed on the head and on the arm opposite the heart—it has a positive effect on the intellect and emotions of the person involved. They bring tranquility to the emotions and greater clarity to the intellect and thoughts. Consequently, your situation will improve, and things will go from good to even better.

Based on the principle and foundation of the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov, which we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—that one can derive a moral lesson for how to conduct oneself in life from everything, especially from matters one encounters day in and day out—there is also a lesson to be learned from your occupation with clocks.

The service and utility of a clock is that through it, a person can organize their lifestyle according to an order and plan they have previously established, and in this way, they will reach the goal and objective for which they strive.

The mechanism of a clock functions through one gear touching and moving the next, and so it continues from one to the next until it reaches the gear upon which the hands are attached. These indicate the minutes, and they move another gear which indicates the hours, according to which a person conducts their affairs as they had planned. In truth, the spring that moves the first gear has no similarity or inherent connection to the person and the work they must do at the designated hour according to the clock's hands. It is simply that through the mediation of the clock—through the gaps and notches that move the hands—the person's work is influenced, and the gears touch one another, thereby bringing plans to fruition.

This above-mentioned analogy removes the question: What connection can there be between putting on tefillin—which are merely pieces of parchment upon which certain letters are written, placed into specifically shaped boxes—and the emotions and intellect of a person? Yet, we know and see that it does influence the person and their actions. The analogy is understood.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

B"H, 11 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

And there is nothing that can stand before the will.

With respect,

## 426

B"H, 12 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and dedicated communal worker, R' Avraham Dov, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 8 Teves, in which you write that you have succeeded in organizing daily davening in the beis medrash since the days of Chanukah, despite having encountered several difficulties: May the statement of our Sages, "all beginnings are difficult," be fulfilled in this as well. Since, as you write, this has materialized literally, the precision of the statement will also come into effect—that it is only the beginning that is difficult, whereas after the beginning, it is otherwise. It is well known that the beginning and the end are the first and last points, and everything in between is outside the category of beginning and end. Since you have succeeded in the aforementioned with relatively little effort, you should draw an *a fortiori* conclusion—a *kal v'chomer ben beno shel kal v'chomer*—regarding the positive results that will follow when you exert all the necessary effort. Based on the above, it is understood that I am pleased with the campaign you are conducting to ensure that women and girls also come to davening on Shabbos, especially since this also involves the aspect of "turn from evil," and a word to the wise is sufficient.

You are doing well by providing refreshments and the like after davening. It would be even better if you were to add to this by having one of the congregants who participates in this give a short talk of about fifteen minutes each time.

With blessings for good tidings regarding what was mentioned, as well as regarding the acquisition of a good home in a good neighborhood, and see also the end of the *hemshech* *Mayim Rabim*.

#### ***426***

**R' Avraham Dov, may he live:** Hecht. Additional letters to him—above 3973, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 427

B"H, 12 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, engaged in communal needs,
R' Shlomo Schneur Zalman, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

Following the gap in your correspondence, I was pleased to receive your letter of 27 Kislev, in which you write about the farbrengen of the auspicious day of 19 Kislev—the festival that redeemed our souls in peace and gave us the light and vitality of our souls. Since it is called the "Rosh Hashanah" for the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus, and the precision of the Holy Tongue is well known—*Rosh* (head) and not *Techilah* (beginning)—it is from there that vitality must be drawn for all the remaining days of the year. You will surely exert effort in this regard as well, in accordance with what is explained: that after the *Kesivah v'Chasimah Tovah* on Rosh Hashanah, there is also the matter of being judged each day, in order to draw down "the matter of the day in its day" (see *Likutei Torah*, end of Parshas Korach; in *Kuntres Uma'ayon*, etc.). It is understood that this is not intended for you alone, but for each and every one of Anash, and for everyone together. It is already known what the Heavenly Court decreed: because of the *mesiras nefesh* (of our Rebbe HaZaken) for the teachings of Chassidus, the Heavenly Court decreed that in every matter of Torah, *yiras shamayim*, and good character traits, the hand of those who are connected to him and follow in his footsteps shall be uppermost.

With blessings.

## 428

B"H, 12 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned R' Shalom Mendel, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your notification that a daughter has been born to you, mazal tov.

May it be the will of Hashem that you and your wife, may she live, raise her—together with all your children, may they live—for Torah, for the chuppah, and for good deeds, in prosperity.

It is known from my father-in-law, the Rebbe [Rashab], of blessed memory, that our custom is to say "for **Torah**, for the chuppah, and for good deeds" even upon the birth of a daughter, based on the words of our Sages (Berachos 17a): "How do women merit? By sending their children to learn Torah... by waiting for their husbands... and by guarding their children..."

With blessings for mazal tov,

**M. Schneerson**

Your letter of 3 Teves was received. Regarding what you wrote concerning the fact that you turned on the electricity without first asking for guidance on the matter—this is the instruction of the Torah of truth, the Torah of life. This is as stated in Shulchan Aruch, beginning of section 328. See also there in the Shulchan Aruch of the Alter Rebbe, section 330, end of section 9, regarding when a woman reaches the ninth month, etc. And there, in section 1, [it discusses] that there is no lamp there, etc., due to fear for the child, etc.

Regarding what you wrote concerning adding names—in regards to the names of the Nasiim, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, did not want others to add another name to their names.

May it be His will, as mentioned above, that very soon reports will begin to arrive regarding good activities in the recent past and in the present, and that these activities will continue to grow from time to time, until the coming of the Master, of whom it is written: "My servant shall prosper, he shall be exalted and lifted up, and shall be very high."

It gave me pleasure to read in your letter about the gathering of the Talmud Torah students organized by N'shei U’Bnos Chabad. Surely, in this too, the principle will be fulfilled: "More than the householder (the giver) does for the poor person (the receiver), the poor person does for the householder." That is to say, the impression and the effect of the aforementioned will be on both sides—to draw more students and parents toward the guidance of Chassidus and its customs, and subsequently, also toward the teachings of Chassidus, and to an increase in activities, both in quantity and quality, on the part of N'shei U’Bnos Chabad, as well as in their own homes and with their own families.

With regards to all Anash, may they and their families stand in blessing and life forever.

## 334

[13 Teves, 5716]

The sending of letters was delayed for a certain reason, and in the meantime, your letters arrived... I do not understand why there is once again such alarm regarding your health. I have already said, and also written to you, many times that my opinion on this is clear. I have also emphasized that, in my view, you should completely divert your mind from thoughts regarding your health, for you are healthy, with the help of Hashem. However, you must fulfill all the doctors' instructions regarding practical matters. I see that even when you were here, you did the opposite in both regards: you dwelled on matters that have no basis whatsoever (without any reason for doing so), and you absolutely refused to keep the schedule for eating and drinking, etc. (also without any logical reason for this). It appears that you are still maintaining this behavior now.

And what good will my writing do again if he insists on doing the exact opposite? The matter depends solely on his own good will.

## 432

B"H, 14 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

It is possible that Mrs. [Name]—may she live and be well—will turn to you with a question, as her state of health is not as it should be, and there are concerns regarding whether her health allows her to conceive (I have written to her that if the doctor says the aforementioned, she should turn to you with the question of how to conduct herself).

Surely you are aware of the ruling of the Tzemach Tzedek on this matter (Responsa Even HaEzer, Siman 89), which is lenient and permits it. I have already said regarding this to those among the Hungarian Anash who are stringent—that in addition to the above, and given that in a place where a Rav has already ruled, the law is established, and we are in the place of our holy Nasi—it is nearly certain that those who were stringent in previous generations (who consequently said to practice abstinence due to the well-known concern) would, upon knowing the situation in our generation—this orphaned generation—have explicitly ruled, for that very same concern, that one should *not* practice abstinence. And since the agreement of both parties is required in this, they would certainly hold by the permission of the Tzemach Tzedek. And a word to the wise is sufficient.

Your letter of 4 Teves, along with the enclosure, has been received.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 33

B”H, 15 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter—which you began writing on Monday of last week.

I have told you several times—as I recall—that you should not delve into or contemplate the matters you write about, namely, the state of your health, your state of mind, and so on, or how such-and-such person relates to you. Instead, you should remember the great principle: "Love your fellow as yourself," which naturally leads one to view others with a favorable eye. You should also remember the statement of the Mishnah: "I was created to serve my Maker," for which the body must be healthy, as the Rambam elaborates in chapters 3 and 4 of Hilchos De’os. Therefore, one must conduct oneself in an orderly fashion regarding eating, drinking, sleeping, and so on, and also perform one’s work faithfully, without entering into deep pilpulim and arguments for and against every matter, whether large or small. In cases where it seems there is a doubt, in the vast majority of instances it is only because one has entered into a pilpul about it; otherwise, one would take the matter in stride. In the rare minority of cases where a doubt remains, even then, it is usually resolved through consultation with friends and good acquaintances. Our Sages have already alluded to this with the saying: "Whatever is straightforward is superior."

The same applies to your shiur in Nigleh and Chassidus. You should not make plans for specific times or calculate where you will find the time and the mood, and so on. Rather, simply begin to fulfill them, and you will see that it is not difficult. As the verse states: "The matter is very close to you, in your mouth and in your heart, to do it."

With blessings for good news regarding all the above, and may peace dwell in your home, and may the statement of our Sages be fulfilled: "The Holy One, blessed be He, found no vessel that holds blessing other than peace."

## 434

B"H, 15 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and diligent worker for communal needs, R' Tzvi Shai [Shusterman]

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 8 Teves, I was very, very pleased (see *Likutei Torah*, *Shelach* 38c, regarding the double expression "very, very") by the awakening regarding improving the situation concerning the mikveh. You must certainly remain vigilant in encouraging the women, may they live and be well, to involve themselves in this, to encourage them from time to time in a diplomatic manner, and also to show them the way to act so that the matter is brought to fruition as soon as possible and in the best possible way.

May Hashem grant you success.

Regarding what you wrote about the Salk vaccine: in general, my opinion leans toward using it. However, one should not separate oneself from the community, and if, as it appears from your letter, they are using it in Chicago, it is good that you should do so as well. May Hashem grant you success, and may you inform me with good news regarding your children, yourself, your communal work, and your inner task of *hafotzas hamaayanos chutzah*.

With blessings—in connection with the birthday of your wife, may she live—for a year of success in *gashmius* and *ruchnius*, and for Chassidishe *nachas* from your children, may they live.

...Regarding a car, it is better to buy a new one. And it is not necessary to investigate; it seems to me that a new 1955 model is as good as a new 1956 model and incomparably cheaper.

## 436

B"H, 17 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent, a man of action, etc., Rabbi Yitzchak, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter, in which you write regarding a letter of recommendation in connection with the work for "Otzar HaPoskim," it seems to me that I mentioned to you during our conversation that, according to the custom of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, such a practice is not our custom.

On the other hand, the great benefit and necessity of the "Otzar HaPoskim" project is understood, especially in our generation—this orphaned generation—in which, on one hand, tens of thousands of copies of books of Halacha and instruction were burned and lost, and on the other hand, the study for the sake of clarifying the final ruling, *halacha l'maaseh*, with its reasoning and rationale, is diminishing and narrowing. You have permission to convey this opinion of mine in the places you visit, and I am confident that *anash*, may they live, who are there, will assist you in this.

With blessings for success.

## 437

B"H, 17 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

It is understood that if, according to your opinion, it will be possible to attract students to a Yeshiva in Tel Aviv as well, and it will be possible to obtain—at least a significant portion of—the funds required for construction, and it is possible to provide legal guarantees through an attorney so that there will be no, Heaven forbid, aggravation resulting from the fact that the plot is registered under two names, then the proposal is sound.

However, regarding the expansion of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod (which is necessary, as you write, and as is also confirmed by reports received from other sources), one must look into relocating it—or at least a significant part of it—to the new village [Kfar Chabad]. It is surprising that you did not suggest this yourselves. It seems you have not taken an interest in clarifying the possibilities in this regard. For it is understood that for several reasons, the primary Chabad educational institutions should be concentrated in one location, or at the very least, in locations adjacent to one another. Especially since there are many matters in this regard that fall under the category of "a light for one is a light for a hundred"...

With blessings to hear good news regarding all of the above,

**M. Schneerson**

## 438

438

B"H, 17 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Kfar Chabad, in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the minutes from Rosh Chodesh, the 7th, 15th, 22nd, and 30th of Kislev, together with the letters from the 25th of Kislev and the 3rd of Teves. May it be the will of Hashem that since the work has entered its proper course, you will continue to proceed forward, following the well-known adage of our holy Rebbes: "from good to even better."

It is surprising and regrettable that the construction of several buildings is being delayed. For we already see tangibly—especially in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily—that once one begins the actual work, various ways and means are found to minimize the difficulties that were anticipated beforehand. Furthermore, and this is the main point, one must think in terms of addition, expansion, and growth; eventually, matters work themselves out over time, and one begins using the buildings sooner—and a word to the wise is sufficient. The witticism regarding this is already well-known: the instruction of our Torah regarding the distinction between *bedieved* (after the fact) and *lechatchilah* (from the outset).

It is surely unnecessary to remind you that it is worthwhile to make an effort to have the train stop in the Kfar more than once a day. The more one increases this, the more praiseworthy it is.

You write regarding the official seal of the Kfar; surely you will inform me of the exact wording. And also—I believe I have already written about this in the past—one must strive with all one’s might to ensure that this includes the area of the Kfar as it has been until now, and the buildings upon it (and even if, for the time being, some of the buildings are not suitable, there is still a vision for the future)...

It is understood that the intent of what is written above regarding the alacrity in construction is not only regarding private residences, but also communal buildings—and even more so regarding them—so that they may also serve as a source of livelihood for several of the Kfar’s residents.

Thank you for your good news regarding the celebration of the auspicious day of 19 Kislev, the festival that "redeemed our souls in peace," and through which the light and vitality of our souls were given to us. I also received the recording; thank you very, very much. Your minds may be at ease, as you have put my mind at ease regarding this. May it be the will of Hashem that, in accordance with the content of this name—the Rosh Hashanah of the Torah of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus—it will draw down upon all the days of the year in all matters of the Kfar, consistent with the name "Rosh" (head), in addition to it being the beginning of the year. And may this be specifically through joy, as one of the foundations of the Torah of Chassidus: "Serve Hashem with joy."

With blessings for great success.

## 440

B.H., 18 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, engaged in communal needs, R' Mordechai Dov, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from Wednesday, it gave me pleasure to read in it the highlights of the farbrengen you held on the auspicious day of 19 Kislev—the festival that redeemed our souls in peace and gave us the light and vitality of our souls. Surely you will seek opportunities to refresh the impressions of that farbrengen throughout the days of the year as well. Regarding what you wrote about the complaints of some of the baalei batim concerning the arrangements at the yeshiva: while it is understood that in matters of holiness in general, and those connected to chinuch in particular, one must improve and refine them as much as possible, regarding the complaints of baalei batim, even though the wise man’s adage is known—"love criticism"—one should not be overly impressed by these complaints. In the vast majority of cases, they come from people whose desire is to criticize and complain, and this desire compels them to search and dig for something to attach their complaint to, as is evident in a tangible way.

As you requested, I will mention you and your entire family, may they live, at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May Hashem grant you success and enable you to share good news regarding all the matters mentioned in your letter, and it is understood that your communal work is included in this.

## 442

442

B"H, 18 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Regarding what you wrote about the unpleasant sight you encountered on your way, and the back-and-forth you had in your thoughts as to whether to look without being affected or not to look at all: this is an old and long-standing debate. There is even a sicha from my father-in-law, the Rebbe (Rashab) n.e., on this, where he concludes simply that one should not look and should not try to perform "tricks," for that is not a person's task. As we pray every day, "Do not bring us into the hands of a trial," and it is surprising that there is even a doubt about this.

The book *HaChashmal L'Or HaHalacha* is in my possession.

Regarding what you wrote about the caution not to make Kiddush between 6:00 and 7:00 on Erev Shabbos: it is understood that the intention is for an hour of sixty minutes, because the movement of the constellations is the same in summer and winter. Also, regarding chatzos, today there is no difference between locations in the south and the north; consequently, the sixth hour means six equal hours after midday.

As for what you wrote, that they are not concerned about this in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and similarly regarding Nittel—surely you will inform me of the reasoning of those who are not concerned about this in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and whether they are an authoritative source.

With blessings for good tidings in all that was mentioned, and it is understood that the activities of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, which are essentially work within the youth, stand at the forefront.

## 443

B"H, 19 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, in which you ask about the order of conduct according to the Chabad way.

It is understood that it is difficult to explain this in a letter, especially since these matters are explained in several of the holy sichos of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in the kuntreisim and Likkutei Dibburim that have been printed, and are available to several of anash in the holy city of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established.

The essential point is that every day—and certainly on Shabbos—there should be a fixed time and a fixed commitment of the soul for the study of the teachings of Chassidus, both by day and by night. Although not everyone is equal in the length of this time, each person should act according to his capacity and according to what he assesses in his heart. You should consult on this with the elders of anash who are present in your location, and they will instruct you. May Hashem grant you success in the aforementioned study, and may the statement "great is study, for it leads to action" be fulfilled in this as well.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 444

B"H, 21 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, the man of action, who engages in the needs of the community, etc., R' Shimshon Refael shlita,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to the notification regarding the entry of your son, Yisrael Meir shlita, into the yoke of mitzvos.

May it be the will of Hashem that he always bear upon himself the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven and the yoke of Torah and mitzvos.

As is known, the precision in the word "yoke" [ol] specifically implies that the fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos must be in a manner of avodah that transcends intellect and reason, for only in such a manner can they be fulfilled as they ought to be.

May you and your wife, shetichye, derive much true nachas from him—nachas that is Jewish—and may the merit of your engagement in strengthening and disseminating Yiddishkeit increase the blessing of Hashem in the aforementioned, both materially and spiritually.

With respect and blessing,

After requesting your forgiveness—and although, on the face of it, the matter has already taken place—I will nevertheless raise a point regarding the fact that the invitation card was printed in Ashuris script, including tagin. It is well known how much the early and later authorities labored to permit the use of square script in letters and the like, and in any case, they strive to alter the script as much as possible from the Ashuris script used in STaM. Surely, elaborating on this to you is superfluous; this is discussed in Yoreh Deah, end of siman 284, in the gloss of the Maharsha there (in Responsa Tzur Yaakov, end of siman 2), and prior to that in the Responsa of the Rambam, cited in the Beis Yosef, siman 283, Responsa of the Radbaz, parts 3 and 4, and elsewhere.

#### ***444***

**R' Shimshon Refael:** Weiss. Additional letters to him—see above, Vol. 11, 3730, and the references in the notes there.

## 445

## 446

B"H, 21 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, etc., R' Eliezer, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter in due time, and now also the two copies of the sefer *Mar'eh Yaakov*; thank you very much. I trust you will continue to act in this manner regarding future matters published by you, as the library here benefits the many.

It was pleasant for me to read in your letter what you wrote regarding an author of a sefer who was devoted to Chassidus and held it in great esteem and reverence in his soul and being, etc. For I wish to learn from this writing of yours that such an attitude finds an echo in his own soul. And since the Mishnah has ruled that "the essential thing is not the study, but the deed," this echo surely exerts an influence on his day-to-day life—especially since, as you wrote, he disseminates Torah and fear of Heaven to both young and old in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, a land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year. From this it is understood that every addition regarding himself (and our Sages of blessed memory have stated that "we increase in holiness"—this is said regarding every single Jew, and "we increase" is a command for the future), this addition is multiplied many times over, for it creates an effect in each of those whom he influences. May Hashem grant him success to increase this further, soon and with greater intensity, and may the blessing be fulfilled in him: "Whoever adds, they add to him."

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

#### ***446***

**R' Eliezer:** Nissenbaum, Manchester.

## 447

B"H, 21 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write about the thoughts that are confusing you regarding the Torah of Hashem and His avodah, and conclude with a description of your daily schedule.

One matter resolves the other, for in your daily schedule there is no study or matter that awakens love and fear of Hashem, and certainly not [the study of] His unity (it being understood that this does not refer to merely saying "Hashem is One" without knowing what the concept of unity entails, as is known regarding that which is said of such a case: "They enticed Him with their mouths... but their hearts were not steadfast with Him" [Tehillim 78:36-37]). For it is understood, and we see it tangibly, that the primary focus and effect of the study of mussar concerns the refinement of human character traits. The way to arrive at the love and fear of Hashem, Yisbarach, is through hisbonenus in His greatness, Yisbarach, and so on—as is also explained in Rambam, Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah, beginning of Chapter 2. When these three mitzvos are lacking—which are among the constant mitzvos (see the introduction to Sefer HaChinuch)—then there is also a lack in tefillah. For "one should only stand to pray with a heavy head" (koved rosh), and the students of Rabbeinu Yonah explain—and it is ruled as halacha l'maaseh in Shulchan Aruch, Siman 98, end of Seif 1—that this refers to hisbonenus in the greatness of the Almighty and the lowliness of man.

Regarding the practical application: You must immediately establish a fixed time and a fixed commitment in your soul for a shiur in the study of pnimiyus haTorah—which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus—a shiur during the day and a shiur at night. At the very least, [dedicate] a few moments before davening in order to fulfill the ruling of the Mishnah regarding the aforementioned tefillah. Likewise, it is understood that you must be careful regarding tevilas Ezra. And in order to increase the siyata d'shmaya, set aside—without a neder—a few coins for tzedakah every weekday morning, as our Sages, z"l, said: "One should give a coin to a pauper and then pray." May it be the will of Hashem that you begin all of the above for your own sake, and promptly, and may Hashem grant you success.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

B"H, 21 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, etc., Moreinu HaRav Shmuel Abba, may he live:

This is in contrast to future events. For it has already been stated: "The hidden things belong to Hashem our G-d, but the revealed things belong to us and to our children **to perform all the words of this Torah.**"

## 449

449

B.H., 24 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter from the first day of Rosh Chodesh Teves: It goes without saying that I did not intend, by writing to you, to frighten you into not writing anymore, nor did I wish to show you that everything in this world is in perfect order and completeness. For until Moshiach comes, there is no completeness in physical matters, as is explained in many places in our holy seforim.

What I emphasized in my letter is that the matters in which there are deficiencies should not obscure, nor diminish, one’s gratitude to Hashem Yisbarach for the portion of good that everyone receives from Him in a **great** measure. Secondly, the way to rectify these deficiencies is not through despair or even *nefilas ruach* (a lowering of spirits); not only does this not help, but on the contrary, it makes the work of rectification more difficult.

In contrast, when one is *b’simcha* (joyful), then the *avodas Hashem* in general, and the aforementioned *avodah* (of rectification) in particular, are accomplished with great success. We see this in practical life, and as is well known, the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that a soldier going to the battlefront must march with a song of joy. This greatly increases the possibility of winning the war. If this is true in a physical war, it is many times more true in the matters one wishes to carry out according to the will of the *Borei Olam*, in which, ultimately, the victory of good is guaranteed, as is explained at length in many places in Chassidus.

I hope that you will accept the guidance of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, as mentioned above, to act and be *b’simcha*, in a joyful frame of mind. May it be the will of Hashem that everyone should have that for which to be *b’simcha*.

With blessings for good tidings and success in all that has been mentioned.

#### ***449***

**Marching song:** See also above, Vol. 8, Letter 2,278.

## 51

B.H., 25 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the 5th of Teves, and as you write following your previous letter from a year and a half ago—it is understood that during this time you could have, and consequently were obligated to have, progressed in your study of the teachings of Chassidus and in following its guidance and customs. I searched for at least the main points regarding this in the four pages of your letter, but I did not find even a hint of it; only, once again, questions.

It is astonishing for a Ben Yisrael who knows that the receiving of the Torah was specifically through the precedence of "we will do" to "we will hear," and in general, as the Mishnah rules at the beginning of the second chapter of Berachos, that the starting point for all matters of a Jewish person is through the acceptance of the yoke [of Heaven]. Yet, it seems you have chosen the opposite path: piling question upon question, and when you receive an answer to the first ones, you dig for new ones.

I have sought to judge you favorably, thinking perhaps that in the time between your two letters you have been studying the teachings of Chassidus and studying in depth for your own benefit, as well as studying the revealed Torah, and thus "great is study that leads to action," but out of excessive humility you do not wish to boast of it. But even so, there should have been some hint of this in your letter. Most importantly, if that were the case, your questions would have been in a different style, and there would have been no need for an introduction stating that your questions are not meant to provoke or be contentious, for the style itself would have proven that. Furthermore, before putting a question in writing, one would search in the relevant places to see if there is perhaps no room for the question at all. Nevertheless, since you have not yet reached that stage, I will address those questions that have practical relevance briefly:

1) In the Sichos of the Chabad Nesi’im, there are several details regarding the earlier periods of Chassidus that are not mentioned in other books. It seems you wish to draw alarming conclusions from this. Like most such questions, they are based on a lack of knowledge, etc. For if not for that, you would know that the very first book on such matters is *Shivchei HaBesht*, which was written primarily based on the words of our Rebbe, the author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*, as explained in the introduction there. And there is no need to elaborate further.

2) Regarding the *Siddur*, how the variations in the text came about and what is the reason for the changes in the *Siddur* on whose title page it is written that it follows the *Nusach* of the Arizal—

You should examine the introduction to *Shaar HaKollel* regarding the history of the printing of the *Siddurim*. Since they were printed by human beings—and of everyone it is said, "Who can discern errors?"—there were errors even in the first *Siddur*. Already in the days of our Rebbe, they compiled a list of corrections, and from time to time they clarified and refined them according to the traditions held among the Chassidim.

3) Regarding the *Shiurim* (measurements).

In the book by the great Gaon and Chassid, Moreinu HaRav Chaim Naeh, of blessed memory, he brings several *shiurim* and notes whether they are based on logical reasoning or whether there is also a tradition for them among the Chassidim.

4) Regarding your third and fourth questions, I do not find any practical difference in them regarding your study of Torah and the fulfillment of *mitzvos*. Consequently, it is a waste of your time to delve into matters that have no relevance to the task of each one of us, as the Mishnah states: "I was created to serve my Creator."

With blessings for good news regarding yourself,

## 452

B.H., 25 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After a very long silence, your letter from Erev Shabbos Parshas Vayigash was received. It contains no explanation for the silence, nor for the brevity of your letter. I trust you will write in detail in your future letters, especially regarding the farbrengens held during the auspicious days of the month of Kislev among Anash, the N'shei Anash, and the students—may they live—and that you will also send clippings from the newspapers, as has been your good custom until now.

It is explained in many places in Chassidus, and also in the maamar delivered this past Shabbos, that the Elokus within every created being contains two opposites: it is both transcendent and also close (meaning, it occupies a place) and invested, since it arose in His will to create it, and yet it is also transcendent. This is the union of the two opposites of Sefiras Malchus: a King over a people—His awe is upon you, and they occupy a place (since His will is to reign over them and issue decrees).

How much more so must this be the case in the conduct of Malchus d’lesata—"Who are the kings? The Rabbis"—and in the conduct of shluchim and Chassidim in general, who are the emissaries of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, to carry out their work wherever they are found according to Divine Providence. Just as closeness and investment are not desirable without transcendence and even separation—knowing that this is not the ultimate intent (as is known the saying, "A householder's [materialistic] approach is a contaminated thing")—so too, transcendence, and certainly separation, without investment, is also not desirable. It appears that among some of Anash, and you are included in this, this line is dominant regarding the Yidden of [your region], and consequently, it makes an impression on the dissemination of the wellsprings outward—the teachings of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs—in that they do not reach all the places where it is necessary and possible for them to reach.

One of the examples I saw last week was when Mr. ... from ... visited me. My impression after our long conversation is that he is a Charedi man and a G-d-fearing person, and his wife—may she live—not only does not hinder him, but on the contrary, even adds to it. It seems that until now, he has not been utilized in Chabad matters in general, and certainly, he has not been "drawn in." He also reminded me of Mr. ..., and it seems that even with him, they have only tapped into a small fraction of his potential. I fear that the reason is as stated above. Regarding what is explained in many places, that the mashpia must estimate the vessel of the recipient and his circumstances, and with appropriate contemplation, arrange the influence in a way that it will be received in its entirety—may Hashem help you to act in the matters mentioned above regarding the Yidden who are in the state of ... and in ... in particular, and may Hashem grant you success.

I could bring more examples of those who were not "drawn in" as much as they should have been, even from those who are closer, but the above is sufficient. It is understood that you have permission to convey all of this to the rest of Anash—may they live—for each one of them must be a "lamp to illuminate," and consequently, this avodah is incumbent upon him as well.

I await good news regarding all of the above.

## 453

[25 Teves, 5716]

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Vayechi and the one preceding it, I am writing to answer you immediately without waiting for my turn, due to the urgency of the matter.

You ask whether it is possible that you will be asked to work in the agricultural school as well, noting as evidence that you have now been approached to travel to the Youth Aliyah camp to select suitable students for that agricultural school, and you are concerned that this will detract from your work at the vocational school.

Regarding the trip to select suitable students: since this is only a one-time matter of a day or two, and it is of great importance that the students be suitable—as is understood—if the administration finds you suitable for this, it is understood that you should fulfill their request.

Regarding permanent work at the agricultural institution: since it is not yet known whether they will offer you the aforementioned position, and certainly the details are unknown, if such an offer does come, you will surely be able to discuss among yourselves how to arrange the work in a way that there will be no damage. After all, the administration of the yeshiva is also interested in the success of the vocational school. It is possible that the agricultural institution, being a new institution, requires special effort, more so than the vocational school, where things have already entered their proper track. It is possible that they will continue as they should even through someone with less experience than you, especially if they remain in awe of you (since you will be able to enter there at the necessary times and intervals—at least for a few moments). Fortunate is your portion that Divine Providence gives you the opportunity to participate in the founding of kosher educational institutions in the spirit of Chabad, and with the objective that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, outlined for them.

Your first letter, in which you write that there appears to be a change for the better in the students, caused me great satisfaction. Surely since then, a change and progress for the better have been evident, in addition to the aforementioned change. It is surprising that you do not write about this...

## 55

B.H., 25 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and meticulous in his work,
R' Yehoshua Shneur Zalman, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

... 4) It is surprising that you do not mention the farbrengen of 19 Kislev, as surely that too was utilized regarding the affairs of the Yeshiva.

5) Regarding what you wrote about the arguments for and against being strict about student tardiness:

It is understood that this depends on the nature of the students, and they are not all the same in this regard; some do so out of necessity, some intentionally, and there are those who fall between these two extremes.

There are two general points to consider: one must maintain discipline and order, yet on the other hand, one must endeavor not to distance students from the Yeshiva. Therefore, there are certainly cases where, if it is **impossible** to correct the matter, one must incorporate it into the framework of order—namely, by creating a class for those who arrive at a certain time because they live at a great distance, etc.

6) Regarding your question that in one class there are students with varying talents, and conversely, it is difficult to split the class since it is not large in number:

This is a problem in every educational institution, for it is impossible to narrow the gap and equalize the talents of the students in every single class. It is up to the local administration to find the middle path so that the classes are not too small and the students do not lose out. It is impossible to set hard and fast rules here, as this itself changes from period to period, in addition to changes in local conditions, etc.

7) I was pleased with the suggestion of the G-d-fearing, etc., R' Moshe Kantor, may he live, that he will enroll his son, may he live, to study for a year at Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch. The benefit in this is far greater than he imagines. This is understood even through human intellect, and especially through contemplation of the fact that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, after whom the institution is named, continues to bestow blessing and success in all the institution's affairs. Anyone who contemplates the history of Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch in Melbourne does not need further proof, even when considering the short time it has existed—which was merely the beginning, and all beginnings are difficult—and certainly this applies from here on out. Happy is the portion of everyone who participates in this, and all those who are educated in this holy institution. It is understood and simple that you may convey to R' Moshe Kantor, may he live, everything written above; and because of Ahavas Yisroel, it is possible that not only can you, but you should. May R' Moshe Kantor, may he live, serve as a guide for other parents as well, so that they may see from him and do likewise...

9) As you requested, we will mention... may he live, at the holy gravesite of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, for a complete and speedy recovery, and that his parents, may they live, should raise him to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds.

In an appropriate manner, one should clarify whether the parents have observed the laws and statutes of Taharas HaMishpacha. If, G-d forbid, there was any matter in this that was not as it should be, then the parents must immediately resolve to observe the laws and statutes of Taharas HaMishpacha from here on, and to influence their surroundings in this as well, which constitutes a form of teshuvah regarding the past.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, and regards to all Anash, may they live.

P.S.
In your letter from some time ago, where you wrote about the efforts of Anash regarding the affairs of the Yeshiva, you mentioned only those living in Melbourne. You should have also stirred those who are in Sydney—and perhaps there are others in other places—for the Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch Yeshiva in Melbourne shines throughout the entire country. All those who are connected, and even those who are only associated with Lubavitch, have the obligation and the privilege to strive for its maintenance and development as much as is necessary. Surely the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, will awaken abundant mercy regarding them and their households, both materially and spiritually.

B"H, 25 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs,
R' Ephraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

In response to your letter from the day of the Hillula of Rabbeinu HaZaken, 24 Teves: May the traditional and sacred formula passed down through generations for such occasions be fulfilled: "May his merit protect us." Your letter was received. Regarding what you wrote in Torah Or (55a): "Malchus of Atzilus, whose root is from the aspect of Malchus of Ein Sof, which is Malchus of Adam Kadmon"—seemingly this is the reverse of the order, for the source of everything is Adam Kadmon, and above that is Ein Sof.

In my view, the matter of **"which is Malchus of Adam Kadmon"** is a parenthetical statement (and therefore it is not in the explanation of the Maamar). It comes only as an additional clarification of how the concept of "growth" applies to the aspect of Malchus of Ein Sof; it explains that this is Malchus of Adam Kadmon, the Will that encompasses the entire Seder Hishtalshelus, as is explained in many places. See Etz Chayim, Shaar 3, Chapter 1: "And the Atik, which is Malchus of Adam Kadmon, etc." See also the beginning of Torah Or by the Mitteler Rebbe, and elsewhere.

## 4057

B"H, 25 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of Wednesday, in which you write that you have been awakened by the "rock from which you were hewn"—that you are of the lineage of Chabad Chassidim—and that you are beginning to walk in the ways of Chassidus and have established a regular study of its teachings, and you are asking for guidance in this matter:

It is understood that the specific details regarding the manner of study, its timing, and so forth, are not the same for every soul and also depend on the circumstances of the time. Therefore, it is good that you consult with the elders of Anash in your vicinity; they will instruct you, relying on what they have learned and heard from the guides of Anash over the years. The general point is that there must be a *shiur* in the study of the teachings of Chassidus at least twice every twenty-four hours—once during the day and once at night. Furthermore, there must be study of this Torah before the morning *davening*, as is the halachic ruling for practical application in *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim*, section 98, end of paragraph 1, for through this study, it is possible to engage in *hisbonenus* in the greatness of the *E-l Yisbarach*; see there.

It is also understood and simple that even in the study of the teachings of Chassidus, the approach must be the same as in other parts of the holy Torah: the priority of *naaseh* (doing) over *nishma* (understanding), and not the reverse. If so, "the integrity of the upright shall guide them," whereas otherwise, etc., as explained in *Maseches Shabbos* (88a). May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you the merit and success to bring good tidings in all that has been said, and may your *siyata d’shmaya* in all this increase by your also influencing your friends to bring them closer to the light and the luminary of Torah, its guidance, and its conduct.

With blessings for success in all of the above.

P.S.
Regarding what you wrote concerning the reason for growing a beard, it is explained at length according to the revealed Torah in *Shu"t Tzemach Tzedek*, *Yoreh Deah*, section 93, and according to the inner dimension of Torah in the *Peirush HaMelizos* of the Tzemach Tzedek on the verse "And He, being merciful, forgives iniquity," printed in *Derech Mitzvosecha*, Part Two, and in the *Miluim* to *Tehillim* with the commentary of the Tzemach Tzedek, page 626. See his words there, for they are pleasant, and [note] how much this matter is relevant, especially for *bochurim*.

#### 4057

**The reason for growing a beard:** See also above, Vol. 8, Letter 2732, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 458

B"H, 26 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Brownsville-East New York Ladies Auxiliary for the Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, may Hashem grant them life.

Blessings and peace!

In response to your notification that your annual banquet will take place tomorrow, Wednesday, Parshas Va’era, 27 Teves.

May the Almighty grant that it be successful, both in material and spiritual matters.

Since the banquet takes place during the week of Parshas Va’era, which recounts the story of Mitzrayim and the Exodus from Mitzrayim of old, and also provides indications regarding the "Exodus from Mitzrayim" of our own time—how to free oneself from galus and from all limitations in material and spiritual matters—

It is especially important for the Jewish woman in general—and for those active in communal work in particular—to remember the special zechus and the special obligations that rest upon the Jewish woman, and the role she occupies in the "Exodus from Mitzrayim" of old and of today.

Chazal tell us that it was in the zechus of the righteous women that the Yidden were redeemed from Mitzrayim. They were not intimidated by the decrees of the king of Mitzrayim, who sought to destroy the Jewish children; rather, they raised, with great mesiras nefesh, a generation of Jewish children who subsequently declared "Naaseh V’nishma" and accepted the Torah.

I hope that you, as dedicated workers for the Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch—which were founded by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and which educate the talmidim to continue with this **Naaseh V’nishma** throughout their entire lives and to ascend in Torah temimah and yiras shamayim—

Will continue to lead your work, and with even greater dedication and mesiras nefesh.

And may the Almighty grant you all success—in this, and also in your personal affairs, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings.

## 459

459

B”H, 26 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter: Thank you for the good news regarding the improvement in the health of [your relative]—may he live and be well. Regarding what you write concerning your spiritual state—that you are complaining about it and are deeply worried, etc.:

You should draw a *kal v’chomer* from the aforementioned. If, regarding the healing of the body—which in itself is not dependent on human beings but rather on the *Ribono shel Olam*—a person must still exert effort through natural means and spiritual endeavors, how much more so is this true regarding spiritual matters, which are entirely dependent on the person. As our Sages of blessed memory stated, “Everything is in the hands of Heaven except for the fear of Heaven,” and “according to the camel is the load,” and “the *Ribono shel Olam* does not demand [of a person] beyond their capacity.” To each and every person it is said, “I am Hashem your G-d,” and likewise regarding the entire Torah and *mitzvos*. From this, it is understood and simple that the matter depends on no one but him. If he exerts himself as is incumbent upon him, he will surely find good, and there is no “good” other than Torah and *mitzvah*.

To assist you with *siyata d’shmaya* in all the above, you should be careful with *tevillas Ezra*, with the three *shiurim* that are equal for every soul—established by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zya*—in the well-known *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*, and with giving a *pruta* to *tzedakah* before morning *tefillah* on weekdays.

With blessings for good news in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*

## 460

*[26 Teves, 5716]*

...Regarding what you wrote about wanting to give lectures on Chassidus Chabad on a regular basis to a regular audience consisting of a mix of men and women, this does not seem appropriate to me. However, on the other hand, several of the activists who...

...visited me assured me that they are not comfortable with such a mix, but that their influence does not reach every place to prevent it. Consequently, when you speak with the activists in our camp, there is room to say that you could easily arrange for the audience of your lecture not to be mixed. There is no contradiction here to the Chabad approach of striving to penetrate all circles to bring them closer to Torah and mitzvos, for this applies when it does not involve a matter of "giving a stamp of approval," and perhaps even more than a matter of approval...

#### ***460***

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 21, p. 406.

## 461

B"H, 26 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 8th of Teves, along with the enclosure, and the *pidyon nefesh* which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding what you wrote about your son... *sheyichyeh*, studying in Montreal, Canada: in general, the reasoning is sound. However, it is necessary to explain to him the ruling of our holy Torah that it is forbidden to leave Eretz Yisrael for abroad except to marry or to study Torah. Therefore, the reason I write that the logic is sound, and likewise the reason his father and brothers-in-law *sheyichyeh* are working toward this, is only based on the aforementioned allowance. If, Heaven forbid, that condition is missing—meaning, if there will not be a significant increase in his Torah study abroad compared to his Torah study in Eretz Yisrael—then the consent and the efforts are nullified, etc., and a word to the wise is sufficient.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 462

B"H, 26 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R' Moshe, may he live.

Shalom u'Bracha!

In response to your letter from the 6th of Teves.

Regarding what you wrote about the *Ketz* (the End of Days), there is no *Ketz* more revealed than the words of our Sages, "All the *Ketz* dates have passed, and the matter depends only on *teshuvah*." From this, there is also a practical takeaway: to know the "call of the hour," which is that every single person must increase their resolve in *teshuvah* and influence their surroundings to do the same. Since the future *Geulah* will not be followed by any exile, G-d forbid, all the *nitzotzos* (sparks) must be refined. You should study the explanation of this, and the distinction between the *Ketz* of "in its time" (*b'eitha*) and the *Ketz* of "I will hasten it" (*achishenah*), in the *sefer Shaarei Orah* by the Mitteler Rebbe, page 173 and onwards.

As you requested, I will mention you, your wife, and your daughter—may they live—at the *Tziyon HaKadosh* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Regarding the three daily study portions established for everyone by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—which you conclude your letter by mentioning: surely, in addition to these, you have a set time for the study of *Toras HaChassidus* in general, which will stand you in good stead for whatever you need, both physically and spiritually.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 465

B"H, 28 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I am pleased to receive news from time to time regarding your work at the Chabad school named after my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, Nasi of Israel, and your success in this endeavor. It is my firm hope that although you surely encounter various difficulties in this work, they diminish from time to time. Most importantly, the space they occupy in your mind diminishes as well, especially as you see the fruits of your labor.

It is understood, as explained at length elsewhere, that every effort—and even toil—in the education of the younger generation is worthwhile. For even a small change for the better in a student at the time of the action can change their entire life in fundamental matters, as is often visible even to the physical eye.

I trust that you have effectively arranged matters in your own home as well, particularly regarding your children, may they live, in such a way that there is no contradiction between your holy work in educating the students of the school and your holy work in educating your own children. After all, one mitzvah assists another, and not, Heaven forbid, the opposite. And surely, according to the measure of the Holy One, blessed be He—which is "measure for measure," only many times over—His blessing and success will be added to your own children, that they may be faithful to Hashem, His Torah, and His mitzvos. May you and your husband, the Rav, may he live, receive from them an abundance of true nachas—which is Chassidishe nachas—with peace of mind and proper health.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 406

B"H, 28 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Chanukah (and the Pidyon Nefesh), in which you ask for advice and guidance in avodah.

The essence of this has already been stated in many sefarim, and especially in the sefarim of Chassidus, Toras Da"Ch. The general points—since the details and the details of the details depend on the conditions of the time and the individuals—are: daily study, both in Nigleh and in Chassidus, both for deep analysis (*iyun*) and for fluent reading (*girsa*); keeping the three daily shiurim that are incumbent upon every soul, established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—the well-known daily portions of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya; care regarding the immersion in a mikveh; and giving—without a neder—some coins to tzedakah every weekday morning before davening.

And since for everything one requires Siyata Dishmaya, as our Sages taught, "If Hashem did not help him, he could not overcome it," one must strive to bring others closer to our Torah and mitzvos. For through this, the one who exerts himself in this is brought closer and closer to the avodah of Hashem, as is known regarding the precision of the teaching: "One who comes to purify himself is assisted."

Surely you participate in the farbrengens of anash, and especially on the auspicious day of 19 Kislev, the festival on which our souls were redeemed in peace, and the light and vitality of our souls were given to us.

With blessings to hear good news regarding all of the above.

## 472

B"H, 28 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...It is already well-known from the explanation of our Sages, of blessed memory, that the Torah uses a circumlocution of eight letters to avoid using the word "impure" (*einena tehorah* — "is not pure"). The simple question arises: the word "impure" (*temeiah*) is used several times in Parshas Shemini without any circumlocution, so what is different about Parshas Noach specifically? The answer is that when the Torah is merely recounting a narrative, it uses a circumlocution, whereas when it concerns a practical instruction, the language must be clear. This, too, is a lesson from the holy Torah, just like the lesson mentioned above regarding the Torah’s circumlocution. This is also the case in the present matter, as it concerns the public and relates to the dissemination of the wellsprings outward, which encompasses the teachings of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs...

#### ***472***

**It is already well-known from the explanation of our Sages, of blessed memory:** See also above, Vol. 11, Letter 3717.

## 475

B"H, 29 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, R' Yoel, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter from the sixth day of Chanukah, in which you write about the song that the Leviim would recite on the sixth day, which corresponds to the general nature of our times. As explained in the Ramban and in many discourses of Chassidus, the six thousand years of the world’s existence correspond to the six days of Creation. The sixth millennium corresponds to the sixth day, on which Adam HaRishon crowned the Creator of the world over all of Creation by saying to them, "Come, let us bow down and kneel before Hashem our Maker." As our Sages of blessed memory state in Pirkei DeRabbi Eliezer, this is the acceptance of His sovereignty, may He be blessed, in a revealed manner, in accordance with the prophecy for the future: "And Hashem shall be King over all the earth; on that day Hashem shall be One and His Name One"—that just as He is written, so is He read. As our Sages of blessed memory state (Pesachim 50a), the preparation for this is the dissemination of the teachings of Chassidus, which teaches every individual how "there is no place void of Him" and "forever, Hashem, Your word stands in the heavens." This is one of the matters that explains the concept that "when your fountains spread outward," then "the Master, Mashiach, will come," as is known from the Iggeres HaKodesh of the Baal Shem Tov.

May the Ribono shel Olam lengthen your days and years in goodness and pleasantness, and may you continue to increase the dissemination of the fountains until we merit, together with all of Klal Yisrael, to greet our righteous Mashiach.

With blessing.

B"H, 29 Teves, 5716

## 477

B"H, 29 Teves, 5716
Brooklyn.

To my dear friend, the distinguished Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., R' Ze'ev Dov, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 5 Teves, in which you write that you repeat maamarim of Chassidus at Seudah Shlishis, and you are in doubt as to how the repetition should be conducted—whether the entire maamar should be repeated, or if it is permissible to skip the difficult-to-understand sections for the sake of those davening in the shul.

Regarding this, it is a well-known principle of our Sages on the verse "And His banner over me is love" (v'diglo alai)—which can be read as "He skips over me in love" (v'dilgu alai)—especially when the skipping is done so that the words of Torah being spoken will be better absorbed. However, in the specific details, we do not know what is in the hearts of others; it is possible that some of the listeners understand even the deeper parts of the maamar, and even for the others, it will act as a *makif* (encompassing influence). As the parable goes, sometimes even when one does not understand the subject matter being heard through intellectual grasp and comprehension, one still senses that it contains a lofty matter, and this, too, has an effect—a great effect.

Furthermore, by omitting the intermediate sections, the connection between what came before and what comes after is sometimes lost. Therefore, one should only act as mentioned above when all the details and the concerns mentioned above are clear. May the Ribono shel Olam grant you the merit and success to be a good conduit for spreading the wellsprings of the teachings of Chassidus in your immediate and distant surroundings.

With blessings for good tidings.

#### ***477***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 23, p. 520, and completed according to the secretariat's copy.

**R' Ze'ev Dov, may he live:** Slonim, Jerusalem.

## 479

B"H, 2 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from 17 Teves, and thank you for writing regarding the farbrengens at various times. Surely you will continue to do so in the future, and will also encourage the anash involved to do the same; thank you in advance.

I was pleased to hear that you have been invited to give lectures before various groups, and you should certainly endeavor, in a diplomatic manner, to be invited more frequently. The reason I write "in a diplomatic manner" is to increase the value of the matter in their eyes, so that it should not appear as if you are forcing yourself upon them. From this, it is also understood that the diplomacy itself is not the main point; the point is that one must spread the wellsprings outward. If it is not possible to do so diplomatically, that does not prevent the matter, provided that it is carried out in practice. This is similar to the well-known saying of the great Gaon, the great Chossid, the great Tzaddik, Reb Hillel of Paritch: "Everything he does is so that a word of Chassidus may be absorbed better."

I am certain, even though you do not mention it, that your wife, tichyeh, is also utilizing her talents for activities in the vineyard of Chabad in an appropriate manner, and in a way that is also appropriate for her health and situation. May Hashem grant you both success, and may you share good news regarding the fulfillment of your hearts' desires for the good, and success in communal matters.

With blessings.

#### ***479***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 21, p. 489, and completed according to the secretariat's copy.

**Saying... Reb Hillel of Paritch:** See also above, letter 3866, and the references in the notes there.

## 481

B"H, 2 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn

Mrs. Mary, may she live,

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter in which you write regarding the nature of a scholarship in the yeshivos.

A scholarship can be structured in various ways, especially in the yeshivos in Eretz Yisrael, which differ from those in America, as there, even married men continue their studies in the yeshivos. The sum for the scholarship can be given to the yeshiva’s fund, and the name of the donor—or another name as requested—is inscribed on a plaque. I believe it can also be arranged to thereby provide an opportunity for one of the more capable students, selected by the yeshiva, to study peacefully and progress. If the scholarship is for several years, it is self-understood that it need not be the same student; it can be transferred to another if it is found necessary for a certain reason.

You do not mention the idea of printing the sefer, *HaRikmah*, or whether you have been in contact with the appropriate institutions in Eretz Yisrael or elsewhere.

With wishes for good news regarding your state of health and regarding everything else, and I hope that if I can be of assistance to you in any of the above, you will give me the opportunity to do so.

With blessings.

B”H, 2 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

Signed by the editorial staff of the publication.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe shlita,
Secretary

Section from a letter of the Rebbe shlita:

Regarding your notification about your birthday: You should certainly follow the custom that Anash have adopted recently for a birthday: an aliyah to the Torah on the day itself if it is a day of Torah reading (or on the Shabbos preceding it if it is not a day of Torah reading); giving to tzedakah before Shacharis and Mincha (and if it falls on Shabbos or Yom Tov, then on the day before); and studying an additional shiur in the revealed Torah and in Chassidus, in addition to the three daily shiurim for every person established by the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, in Chitas (Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya), to be studied on this day.
