## 483

B"H, 2 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and dedicated communal worker, Rabbi Nissan [Nemnov] shlita,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letters from the 5th of Chanukah, the 8th and 27th of Teves, as well as the telegram and their enclosures: Thank you for the good news you wrote regarding the farbrengens. In general, you must strive **more and more** in that which is, to my great sorrow and regret, most lacking among the students: the matter of hiskashrus **to the Yeshiva and its affairs** (although, for the time being, I have not been able to clarify whether the deficiency is only in the hiskashrus to the Yeshiva or also in the study of Torah). This deficiency is evident in the letters I receive, even though they naturally conceal it as much as possible, and one learns to read between the lines. It is understood that effort in this area is absolutely essential, more and more, because ultimately, the time they spend in the Yeshiva is very limited, and their desired role is that they should be "moistening in order to moisten" [i.e., influencing others], and not merely that they should "bring themselves out" [i.e., focus only on their own personal growth]—and the wise will understand.

And if, in general, the conduct of Chassidus is that one does not rely on things happening "on their own" (mimaila), as brought in several sichos of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, how much more so is this the case when one needs to make them *penimiyim* (internalized individuals), and *penimiyim* even in their influence upon others. Further elaboration on this is superfluous. It is understood that in saying this, I refer to all members of the Yeshiva administration, and furthermore, even to those who are occupied with the physical affairs [of the Yeshiva], since it is highly likely that this too influences the students' attitude toward the Yeshiva.

Regarding all of this, it is also said, "It is not hidden from you, nor is it far away... for it is not in heaven." It is known from our Sages that even if it were in heaven, one would have to strive to ascend there in order to fulfill the will of the Creator, may He be blessed. How much more so is the matter "very close to you, in your mouth and in your heart, to do it." This applies to the current matter just as it does to all the above, especially since the merit of our holy Nasiim assists them in this holy work...

## 484

B"H, 2 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from 17 Teves, in which you write of your desire to attach yourself to the Torah and path of Chabad and to be among those who are *mekusharim*.

As has already been stated in several *Igros Kodesh* and is also transcribed in the *Hayom Yom* — 24 Sivan — true *hiskashrus* is through the study of Torah. When one studies *maamarei Chassidus*, reads the *sichos*, and connects with friends among *anash* and the *talmidei hatmimim* (may they live) in their studies and *farbrengens*, and fulfills my request regarding the recitation of *Tehillim* and the keeping of study schedules — this is where *hiskashrus* lies.

The above is a general instruction applicable to every soul. It is understood that here, too, as in all matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, there are specific aspects for each individual according to their own circumstances and what pertains to them — the activity among those they influence in general, and among the *Tomchei Tmimim* in Lod in particular. Since this is their gateway through which Torah, *mitzvos*, and *hemshechos* ascend and descend, one must be extra careful in this regard, as is also understood from *Iggeres HaKodesh*, end of Epistle 7. And words that come from the heart enter the heart.

As you requested, I will mention you at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nevg"m, zy"a*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 485

B”H, 2 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn

To the G-d-fearing, honorable, and distinguished, who engages in communal needs, R’ Boruch, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

It has been quite some time since I have heard from you. May it be the will of Hashem that the reason is that all is well and in order. If that is the case, there is seemingly nothing to write about (although our holy Nasi—may the merit of the righteous protect us—never agreed with that approach, and hoped and expected to be informed of good news as well, especially since one is certainly active in matters of Yiddishkeit, and you, too, are active in this to a significant degree; therefore, there is certainly something to report).

Some time ago, I read about the battle you had regarding the character of your shul, and that the judge ruled in your favor based on the shul’s charter. Since a shul in Pittsburgh is currently facing the same problem due to the stance of some of its members, and according to the information I have, they could also make the same argument that you raised, I therefore think that if you were to send them all the material from your case, including the verdict, it would be of great use to them. This is especially true given the custom of the land, where one judge gives great weight to the opinion and decision of another judge in a similar case. If obtaining this material involves expenses—the clerk’s fees and the like—it is self-understood that Machne Israel will take this upon itself and will send a check for the amount you indicate. You may send the case material to the address of my secretariat to be forwarded to Pittsburgh, or directly to Pittsburgh to Mr. Cohen, as written below. In the latter case, I would be grateful if you would inform me when my request has been fulfilled.

With blessing and regards to Anash in your camp, and also to those who think they are not yet part of Anash—when in truth, all of Klal Yisrael are friends. The only difference is that there are those who know this and feel it, and those who live in error and are waiting for someone to awaken them and tell them that all of Klal Yisrael are responsible for one another.

Awaiting good news.

## 486

B"H, 2 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Following your longest silence, your letter of 28 Cheshvan—which was delayed in transit—has been received. In response, I will address each point in order.

1) You are correct that using the rod for discipline is not the proper way in education. Most frequently, the gain achieved thereby is outweighed by the loss, and a word to the wise is sufficient. One can see tangibly that one achieves much more through the strength inherent in "ways of pleasantness."

2) The thought of exchanging your work in the field of education for a position in accounting, clerical work, or the like, does not seem right to me. As I understand it, that would merely be a matter of material livelihood, in addition to the primary fact that your current work provides spiritual livelihood.

3) Regarding what you wrote about lightning and thunder: have your tefillin checked, as well as the mezuzos in your home. Keep a picture of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, in a place near you—especially at times when you are prone to such feelings. Then, even with a slight bit of hisbonenus, all fear will depart from you, aside from what our Sages have already stated, that these were given to straighten the crookedness of the heart.

5) Regarding your appointment as a maggid shiur for religious soldiers: it is understood that you must utilize this opportunity to its fullest in order to bring them even closer to our Torah—the Torah of life—and its mitzvos, so that their camp may be holy. It is also obvious that you should not be satisfied with the soldiers who are already religious; rather, you should conduct a campaign with energy so that those who are not yet religious in actual practice will also join the listeners. After all, it is said of them as well, "I sleep, but my heart is awake," especially according to what is explained in the book *Derech Chaim* by the Mitteler Rebbe, that the matter of "my heart is awake" is even deeper than the matter of teshuvah (see *Derech Chaim*, Kehot edition, page 182 and onwards). Our Sages have promised us that words which come from the heart enter the hearts of the listeners, and in the end, they will surely have their effect.

6) Regarding what you wrote about moving to..., you must ensure in advance that there will be an organized source of livelihood there, and not rely on mere speculation.

7) Regarding what you wrote at the beginning and end of your letter—that they approached you and your wife to work in the field of education in the spirit of holiness within the vineyard of Chabad, but you did not accept the offer, and you write the reasons for this—what benefit is there for you in the reasons, since in the end, you are not taking part in the institution of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory? Even though it is understood that proper education, wherever it may be, is a vital necessity, one still laments, as it is written, "They made me a keeper of the vineyards; but my own vineyard I have not kept." Even though the Torah testifies that the former are also vineyards, and the wise will understand. Further elaboration is surely superfluous.

8) As you requested, I will mention you and your family—may they live—at the holy gravesite of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, for whatever you need in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all the above.

With blessings for success in chinuch on the purity of holiness.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

## 488

B"H, 3 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined, engaged in communal needs, R' Meir, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 11 Teves, along with its enclosure. Regarding your interpretation of my words in my previous letter to you—that words which do not lead to actual deeds are in the category of "words of vanity," since their purpose was not realized—it seems I did not explain myself sufficiently. My intention was certainly not, G-d forbid, directed at you, but rather at the talks given during the farbrengens **here**.

The practical difference is simple: when you fulfill my request to speak words of hisorerus and the like, and these words come from the heart, then—regardless of the results that come from these words—this is similar to what is explained regarding the blessing for the search for chametz. Even if one does not find chametz, the blessing is valid, because the mitzvah is to perform the search. The same applies to the mitzvah of "rebuke you shall rebuke" (*tochachah*). This is understood from the debate among our Sages as to whether this extends to the point of striking, etc., even though it is obvious that even if it does not reach the point of striking, the rebuke may not be effective; nevertheless, the mitzvah remains in place. This is different from my own talk, which is evaluated on its own merits.

It is my hope that these few lines, small in quantity, will have their effect and achieve their goal: that you will add strength to your *ta'amulah* (outreach), especially since the words of our holy Nasi are well-known, that a *ta'amulah* does not return empty-handed...

With blessings for success in your work in all the aforementioned.

***

**R' Meir:** Gurkow, London. Additional letters to him: above 3958, and in the references noted there.

**Regarding what is explained in the blessing for the search for chametz:** See also below, letter 424.

## 489

B"H, 4 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, [a man of] action, etc., R' Dovid, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

Through the esteemed and distinguished R' Moshe Eliyahu Gerlitzky, may he live, I received the news that you are preparing for a trip to visit our Holy Land—may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days. Since this is the land of which it is said, "The eyes of Hashem your G-d are upon it from the beginning of the year to the end of the year," this should also be felt in the preparations for the trip. This is similar to how one prepares oneself before entering the presence of a great minister, and all the more so before a king, and certainly before the King of Kings. However, the preparation must be in the "garments of the soul"—the internal garments—for "Hashem looks to the heart." This is achieved by increasing one's *shiurim* of study and by increasing the *hiddur* (beautification) in the performance of *mitzvos*. There is nothing that stands before the will when one truly decides to increase in this as much as one is able. It would be excellent if you were to also become a *shaliach mitzvah* on this trip. May it be the will of Hashem Yisbarach that you bring good news regarding all of the above.

With blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.
Surely you are aware of the three *shiurim* that are for every person, established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: 1) Reciting the *shiur* of *Tehillim*—as *Tehillim* is divided for the days of the month—every day after morning *davening*. 2) Studying the *parsha* of *Chumash* with the commentary of *Rashi* from the weekly *sedra* (on Sunday, from the beginning of the *sedra* until the *sheni* portion; on Monday, from *sheni* until *shlishi*, etc.). 3) Studying a *shiur* of *Tanya* every day—as *Tanya* is divided for the days of the year. In any case, you should keep them from now on, and Hashem will grant you success.

## 490

B”H, 4 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the month of Kislev—the month of redemption—in which you describe your current situation and state that throughout your entire life you have never seen any good, and you request that I mention you, your wife, and your children—may they live and be blessed—in prayer.

It seems you do not perceive the contradiction within your own letter.

For a man to whom the Creator of the world has granted a wife and blessed them with children—may they live—and then to say that he has never seen good in his life, is to be ungrateful to an alarming degree.

Certainly, these words will not, Heaven forbid, affect the blessings that Hashem has already bestowed upon you until now. However, the continuation of this influence and blessing, and the increase thereof, should not be dependent on one continuing to be ungrateful.

There are hundreds and thousands of people who pray every single day to be blessed with children, and who would give everything they possess for a single son or daughter, yet they have not yet merited this—may Hashem, blessed be He, grant them the fulfillment of their heart’s desires for good, soon.

And you, who have received this blessing—seemingly without excessive prayer for it—do not recognize the wealth and happiness contained therein, and you repeat this in your letter, as mentioned above! Furthermore, you conclude by saying that you do not believe, Heaven forbid, that you will be helped from Above, because it has been decreed, Heaven forbid, that all your days will be in poverty and misery!

It is understood that I do not mean to say that one’s livelihood should be restricted, or that one’s health should be weak, etc.

Rather, I have come to awaken you to the possibility that this is the very reason for the weakness in health and the lack of expansion in livelihood: because you do not recognize at all the blessing of Hashem, blessed be He, in a matter even more fundamental than perfect health and financial expansion—namely, the blessing of sons and daughters who walk in the way of Hashem. When one does not recognize the visible and revealed good granted from Above—especially when this lack of recognition is so alarming that it leads to the harsh expressions in your letter—is it any wonder if, from Above, blessings are not drawn down in other matters?

It is my hope that these few lines, small in quantity, will suffice to open your eyes to see the situation as it truly is.

When you begin to serve Hashem, blessed be He, with true and inner joy, the blessing of Hashem will certainly increase regarding your health and livelihood as well, as is understood from what is written in many places, among them the Zohar, Vol. II, 184b.

Surely you have a set time for studying the revealed Torah and for studying Chassidus. In any case, you should do so from now on. It is also appropriate to have your tefillin checked, as well as the mezuzos in your home, and every weekday, before the morning davening, you should set aside a few coins for tzedakah.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 494

B"H, 6 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, occupied with communal needs,
R' Yitzchak, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed therein, which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May it be the will of Hashem that your efforts in all the matters you write about be successful, and may you bring good tidings regarding them.

Regarding what you noted in *Tanya*, Chapter 7, concerning the elevation of the *nitzotzot* (sparks), where it is written that they do not ascend from there until their day comes, etc.—you find this difficult, as *Gehinnom* purifies and refines.

The matter, in its simple sense, is that *Gehinnom* refines the soul of a person and the negative matters and stains that envelop it, but it does not elevate these matters. This is also understood from the fact that the subjugation of the kingdoms is the inverse of the concept of *Gehinnom*, as is stated in the *Midrash*, that through this subjugation, a person’s deeds become good, but it is not that the matters of the three completely impure *kelipos* are transformed and elevated.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the matter of lengthening one's *davening*: Heaven forbid, there is no *kapida* (stricture) here at all. May it be the will of Hashem that your prayers be accepted for yourself and for those you influence, especially through the lengthening of your *davening*. As is known from the story told by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that R' Yisrael Salanter asked the Rebbe Maharash why the Chassidim lengthen their *davening* so much, and he replied that there is a known dispute whether *tefillah* accomplishes half or the whole, and therefore they lengthen it so that even the half will be sufficient.

You will surely gather on the day of the *hillula* in an appropriate manner, and may it be the will of Hashem that it be successful.

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 495

B”H, 6 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn, N.Y.

The Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod
May Hashem preserve them and keep them alive

Peace and Blessing!

For the sake of order, I acknowledge receipt of your letters dated 27, 28, and 30 Kislev, and 4, 13, 14, 20, 21, 24, and 28 Teves, along with the enclosures.

1. It is distressing to read in the attached minutes the back-and-forth arguments that get hung up on formal matters, at a time when the welfare of the students is at stake. And what difference does it make [to follow] human laws, when the same mouth that prohibited is the mouth that permitted [i.e., the same authority that created the constraints can remove them]? It appears from certain lines in the minutes that there are those who feel this way, yet the situation remains unchanged.

2. Regarding what you write about new buildings for the yeshiva: in my opinion, the Chabad institutions and buildings should be concentrated—as much as possible—in Kfar Chabad. There are many spiritual and material advantages to this. While it is understood that this cannot be done all at once, in my opinion, this goal should also be kept in mind, and accordingly, a suitable location should be sought for a new and central building.

3. Regarding what you write about publishing Chassidic stories in *Pardes HaTemimim*: it is understood that one must be as precise as possible regarding the authority of the narrator and the subject of the story, and in addition to this, one must note in the printed story who the source of the report is, etc.

4. Regarding the desire to send *shadarim* [emissaries] to Europe: the procedure for this is already known, namely, that one must consult with *anash* there so as not to cause confusion for one another. As for the *shadarim* themselves, this must be clarified on the spot...

I conclude with thanks for sending the recording of the Yud-Tes Kislev celebration in Kfar Chabad, which caused me *nachas ruach* and pleasure. Thank you very much.

With blessings for success,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***495***

**To concentrate... in Kfar Chabad:** See also above, letter 437, and the references in the notes there.

## 496

B"H, 6 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn, N.Y.

The Administration of the Vocational Schools
c/o Yeshivas Chabad Lubavitch
Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily
May Hashem grant them life

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letters of the 5th, 12th, 22nd, 24th, and 25th of Teves.

1. It is puzzling to hear of the request to reduce the number of students in the vocational school, at a time when there is a lack of placement opportunities for youth in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily. Perhaps there is some specific reason for this. It is understood that, based on the principle of "a candle for one is a candle for a hundred," adding students does not mean that expenses increase by the same proportion. Furthermore, one must take into account that in some time, the number of students suitable for such schools will surely decrease significantly, while on the other hand, the number of institutions seeking them will increase; consequently, any advancement in this matter is to be praised. It is understood that, nevertheless, this is not a matter of principle to fight over to the extreme.

2. Regarding the duration of the various study sessions at the agricultural school, one should endeavor—as in the vocational school—to arrange the program such that: (a) the day begins with davening and limudei kodesh, as in your program; (b) the time allotted for limudei kodesh should be at least slightly more than the time for secular studies, if possible...

Surely, since you wrote, you have endeavored to enroll more suitable students for the agricultural school, and I look forward to hearing good news regarding this as well. This letter is being sent urgently, and I am sure you will respond as soon as possible. May it be His will that it concludes for the good, as mentioned above.

With blessing.

#### ***496***

**Study schedules:** See also above, letter 3300.

## 497

## 498

B"H, 7 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the Avreich, Baruch Shalom, may he live.

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter, along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed therein.

Happy is his portion, for he has merited to see fruits from his influence during the *farbrengens* he has organized. As is explained in many places in *Chassidus*, the great *nachas ruach* caused Above by bringing any fellow Jew closer to Hashem, His Torah, and His *mitzvos*. This is also hinted at in the *nigleh* (the revealed Torah) in the well-known statement of our Sages regarding the verse "precious from the vile." From this, one can also understand the opposition of the *sitra achra* to this; therefore, the *yetzer hara* comes in various strange guises. In a place where he has no other counsel, he disguises himself in the cloak of *yiras shamayim*—claiming that this is not the ultimate purpose, that this "wondrous ascent" is actually a descent, and so on.

Our Sages have already stated, "I created the *yetzer hara*, and I created Torah as its spice," specifically the Torah of *Chassidus* and its concepts. Therefore, one should completely divert one’s attention from the schemes of the "old and foolish king" and provoke the good inclination against him, as is explained at length in the *Tanya Kadisha*. May Hashem grant him success.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

## 499

B"H, 7 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write that you are perplexed, etc., and ask what the order of study should be, etc.:

The one is dependent upon the other. When you maintain a set order of study and learn with *hasmadah* and *shekidah*, the rest of your affairs will also fall into place. Just as the receiving of the Torah at the time of *Matan Torah* was contingent upon the precedence of "we will do" to "we will hear," so too is the instruction for our daily *avodah*. As the *Mishnah* rules at the beginning of the second chapter of *Berachos*, one must accept upon himself the **yoke** of the Kingdom of Heaven and the yoke of **mitzvos**. It is self-evident that this applies to you as well: the beginning of *avodah* is through *kabbalas ol*. Then, the *Ribono shel Olam* grants merit and success, so that in time one also finds *taanug* and pleasure, although, as is understood, that is not the main point.

I trust you are keeping the three daily *shiurim* that are equal for every soul, as established by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zi"a*—the well-known *shiurim* in *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*—in addition to your other studies, both in *nigleh* and in *Chassidus*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*

## 400

B"H, 7 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned man, a man of energy and many accomplishments,
R' Moshe Zalman, shlita,

Greetings and blessings!

After a long interval—though I receive regards regarding you and your family, shichyu—I was pleased to receive your letter from Erev Shabbos Parshas Vayechi. In it, you write of your satisfaction with the development of Yeshivas Oholei Yosef Yitzchok in Melbourne. Certainly, this joy brings about, according to the dictum of the Chassidim, "joy breaks through barriers," leading to even greater hishtadlus to strengthen and expand the yeshiva, which is a source of blessing for all Yidden in Melbourne and for the entire country, both in gashmius and in ruchnius.

This is similar to what the Torah tells us, that the deeds of the fathers are a sign for the children: that before Yaakov Avinu traveled to Mitzrayim, "he sent Yehudah ahead of him to Goshen." Our Sages, of blessed memory, say that this was to establish a yeshiva there. Through this, Yaakov Avinu, the founder of the yeshiva, experienced his best years specifically in Mitzrayim, as is known from the question that the Tzemach Tzedek asked his grandfather, our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya, and the answer he gave him (see the calendar Hayom Yom, page 12).

With a wish and hope to receive from you for many more years good news regarding all the above, as well as good news regarding yourself and your entire family, both in gashmius and in ruchnius.

May the merit of the Baal HaHillula—which will be on Monday, the 10th of Shevat, the upcoming year—the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, in whose name the holy institution is called, stand for him and his household in gashmius and in ruchnius.

With blessings for long, good years and for good tidings.

## 101

B"H, 7 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Schneur Zalman, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Rosh Chodesh Shevat, I received the good news that you have finalized matters regarding the apartment and have already paid the deposit.

May it be the will of Hashem that this be a beginning in a good and auspicious hour, and may the continuation be likewise. May your dwelling be a home of joy, both materially and spiritually, and a place for farbrengens regarding Chassidus and for the spreading of the wellsprings.

It is surprising that you do not mention in your letter anything regarding those you influence and your activities among them. I have often reminded many of anash regarding what is brought in Chassidus in many places: that every person has a "gate"—that is, a specific mitzvah or matter through which their Torah, mitzvos, and all their influences ascend and descend. For anash and the temimim, especially in our times, this is the matter of spreading the wellsprings outward. Consequently, any request for a blessing in any matter should be connected to the expansion of that "gate," and so on—and a word to the wise is sufficient.

Surely you will utilize the upcoming yom hilula, 10 Shevat, as is fitting, and may it be the will of Hashem that the hisorerus be drawn down throughout the entire year.

With blessings.

402

402

B”H, 9 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write regarding the Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad in Cleveland.

I was pleased to read in your letter of your interest in the work of the Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad, and more importantly, of your personal involvement and your efforts to bring in your friends and acquaintances as well.

It goes without saying that I agree with you that there is no reason, chas v’shalom, to be despondent. Jews and Yiddishkeit have passed through various difficulties over the course of the thousands of years of their existence, and yet they live on, **clinging** to the Torah and its mitzvos. Meanwhile, many nations that were physically much stronger and far greater in number have left no trace or memory behind.

This teaches us that even in the current state of affairs, one must not be fooled by the yetzer hara according to **his** narrative—that it is difficult to be a Jew. On the contrary, if one truly wishes to be happy—and not only in Olam HaBa, but truly in Olam HaZeh as well—and to have true nachas from one’s children, the only way for Jews is by clinging to and walking in the paths that the Creator of the world and the Guide of the entire world has indicated to us in His holy Torah. When one desires this in truth, not only does one overcome all difficulties and succeed, but the difficulties themselves become smaller than one had imagined, and in the course of the work, they become smaller and smaller.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant you success in finding the appropriate words to explain the above within the circle of all your friends and acquaintances, and through this, to penetrate even more deeply into the work of upholding Yiddishkeit to an ever-increasing and greater extent. May this merit stand by you in all your private affairs.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 103

B"H, 9 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 3 Shevat: Thank you for the good news regarding the improvement in your physical health. May it be Hashem's will that in the future you will also bring tidings of improvement in your spiritual health, which is also dependent upon expanding your activities in the vineyard of Chabad, and specifically within the framework of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad.

Regarding what you wrote—that you feel *hispaalus*, etc.—the advised counsel in such a case is the matter of *hesach hadaas* (diverting one's attention). That is to say, when you feel a thought of the aforementioned nature, banish it by thinking about a different subject—and it is best if it is a subject of Torah. Do not fight against these thoughts when they come to you by engaging in intellectual debate, for a lack of attention to them succeeds far more.

It is appropriate—if your *tefillin* have not been checked during the last twelve months—to have them checked now. Likewise, be careful to fulfill—*bli neder*—the three *shiurim* that are equal for every soul, established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*, which are well known.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 405

B”H, 9 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn

To the Kfar Chabad Committee,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the three sets of minutes from 7, 13, and 19 Teves. I was pleased to learn of your efforts to further integrate the existing village with the new section, in accordance with what I wrote previously: that in my opinion, you should pursue this **with all your might** so that the entire area remains under your jurisdiction. Certainly, every plot of land should be utilized, whether for housing, agriculture, or the like. It is also understood that this requires an effort to increase the number of residents in the village, a matter I have raised several times. I have also written that, in my opinion, this affects both the physical and the spiritual, and to the wise, a word is sufficient...

4) It is surprising that there is no mention of preparations for the Yahrtzeit of 10 Shevat. Surely, the actual work is being done, but perhaps it would be worthwhile to appoint individuals for such tasks who could prepare for their responsibilities well in advance, just as is done regarding Purim, etc.

5) I have heard that in many places, such opportunities are also utilized for matters of livelihood by preparing a special sales area for beverages, food items, etc., in addition to a place for publicity and the sale of printed materials relevant to anash. It is possible that if there were suitable lodging in the village, this too could serve as a source of livelihood.

6) The main point here is that the time has long since arrived to view the village not merely as a place where several individuals happen to be gathered, but as a community—a community that also exerts influence on the outside world. Therefore, it is necessary and essential to address the needs of the community, including its influence on the outside: not just a shul, etc., but a place of hospitality for visitors, a center for providing information about Chabad and anash—both in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt) and abroad, both in the present and the past, etc. One could expand on this with many other points, which would become apparent with a little reflection.

Once again, I add that for me, this is not the main point, but rather that all of this can be a matter of honorable livelihood—physical and spiritual livelihood combined.

With blessings for success and for good news regarding all of the above.

In accordance with my aforementioned approach, I have written to the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva in Lod that, in my opinion, it is most appropriate that the central building of Tomchei Temimim—which must be built—should be established in Kfar Chabad. However, it is understood that to make this possible, the village must allocate a sufficient and spacious area for this in a suitable location.

## 410

B"H, 11 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

## 107

B"H, 11 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of Thursday. At a time of favor (*eis ratzon*), I will mention you, your children, and your grandchildren—may they live and be well—and may Hashem Yisbarach help that you should have *nachas* from them and from everyone together, true *nachas*, which is Jewish *nachas*.

And according to the statement of our holy Torah, "Everything is wondrous from Him," and as is known from the holy books, when one looks with a *ayin yafah* (a generous eye) and a *ayin tovah* (a good eye), it is not only that one notices virtues, but from that very gaze, they receive *chizuk*. Consequently, the negative matters become smaller and fewer. This is especially so according to what is explained in *Tanya*, Chapter 32, and in *Sefer Derech Mitzvosecha*, in the *mitzvah* of *ahavas Yisrael*, regarding the concept of "Love your fellow as yourself," to the point that it is said of Aharon HaKohen—who was the *Kodesh HaKodashim*—that he "loved the creatures," even those who have no particular merit other than the fact that they were created, as explained by Rabbeinu HaZaken in *Tanya* there.

And may Hashem Yisbarach help that, just as *kohanim* are *zerizim* (diligent) and accomplished through their *avodah* that "His word runs swiftly," without any obstacles or delays (as brought in *Likutei Torah* by Rabbeinu HaZaken, end of *Parshas Korach*), may the aforementioned matters come to pass quickly, *lematah me'asarah tefachim*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 108

B"H, 12 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

From time to time, I inquire of the esteemed Rav, the G-d-fearing man of many accomplishments and fine character, our teacher Rabbi Yaakov Ben-Zion Yarkevitch shlita, as to how he is doing and about his activities. He has also informed me of what you write to him regarding your state of mind—or more accurately, your low spirits—and what you write to the aforementioned Rav regarding your spiritual condition.

It is already well-known in such matters, as per the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that the prohibition of *lashon hara* applies not only to others, but also to oneself; it is forbidden to speak *lashon hara* about oneself as well. It is already known from the words of the Rambam regarding the distinction between *lashon hara* and *motzi shem ra* (slander), that *lashon hara* applies even when one speaks the truth, and especially if one exaggerates, and even more so when one does more than exaggerate.

Furthermore—and this is the essential point—according to what is explained in many places in *Chassidus*, in order for a seed planted in the earth to sprout grain and a tree that bears fruit, there must first be a process of decomposition—that is, the nullification of its previous state—which then allows it to sprout even more abundantly. However, when is this decomposition considered a blessing? When it occurs in earth that is suitable for planting and growth, and when it prepares the soil for planting and growth, and one waters it, and so on. But if one leaves a seed on a table and lets it rot, not only is there no benefit or growth, but on the contrary, one has ruined the seed itself.

This is analogous to the distinction between *atzvus* (melancholy) and *merirus* (bitterness), as is understood from what is explained in *Tanya*. The test to avoid deceiving oneself and to discern the nature of this "decomposition" and low spirits lies in the resulting outcomes: if the low spirits lead to an increase in activity in matters of Yiddishkeit, then this is a "decomposition" that causes growth many times over, relative to the seed. But if it causes weakness, and certainly if it leads to the cessation of the aforementioned activities, then it is of the second type.

The analogy is understood. It is essential to set aside time for the study of the teachings of *Chassidus*—a fixed time and a fixed commitment of the soul—and then, ultimately, you will arrive at the fulfillment of the commandment, "Serve Hashem with joy."

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

***

**108**

**He informed me:** See the letter following this one to him.

**Saying:** See also above, Vol. 11, Letter 3795, and the references in the notes there.

## 4109

B"H, 12 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent in communal needs,
R' Yaakov Ben-Tzion, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote about your son, Boruch Boaz, may he live: Please examine the beginning of the Laws of Talmud Torah by our Alter Rebbe. This is based on the glosses of the Rema in Yoreh Deah, siman 245, and is founded upon the Midrash Tanchuma, which states that as soon as a child reaches three years of age, one should teach him written texts in addition to what he is taught orally from the time he begins to speak, as per the well-known words of our Sages.

With this, the difficulty raised in the Biur HaGra there, subsection 19—"I do not understand his discourse," etc.—is simply resolved.

Regarding what you wrote about the esteemed [individual], etc., as to which seforim to instruct him to study: Since you have met him face-to-face, you can certainly gauge his level accordingly and provide him with guidance. As is apparent from the aforementioned letter, he will accept your instructions willingly. May it be the will of Hashem that you succeed in this as well, even though he is located at a distance, in addition to your efforts and toil with those who are in your proximity. The measure of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is "measure for measure," and even more so, to increase Heavenly assistance regarding yourself in both spiritual and material matters.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 4110

B"H, 13 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, involved in communal needs, a man of fine character,
R' Avraham Sender, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 11 Shevat and those preceding it, in which you raise the matter regarding the Chabad version in the recitation of *Kesser*—that it should be *acharis ke-reishis* (the end like the beginning) and not *acharis ke-reishis* [sic]—

One should also examine *Shaar HaKollel*, which writes exactly as I have stated. As for your concluding remark that you are afraid to decide against the version *acharis ke-reishis*, it is puzzling, for the decision has already been made by Rabbeinu HaZaken, the author of *Tanya* (the authority in the hidden aspects of Torah), and the *Shulchan Aruch* (the authority in the revealed aspects of Torah). It is already a known statement of the *Mishnah*: "You are a great sage, for you have upheld the words of the Sages" (*Negaim*, end of chapter 9). It has already been recorded in *Beis Rebbe*—a story of the early Chassidim in the name of the Tzemach Tzedek—that when Rabbeinu HaZaken was clarifying the version for his *Siddur*, he had sixty *Siddurim* before him.

It is unnecessary for you to apologize for writing to me regarding matters such as these, for it is a matter of *Mishnah* (ibid.) that if it is to uphold the words of the Sages, it is certainly appropriate; and the clarification of doubts is included in that upholding.

With blessings for long life and good years—and there is no "good" other than Torah, and one who is *oseik* (engaged) in it, as is explained in many places regarding the precision of being "engaged" in it, rather than merely "learning" it.

***

**R' Avraham Sender:** Nemtsov, Long Beach. Additional letters to him: see above, Vol. 10, 3984, and the references in the notes there.

**The precision of being "engaged":** See also above, Vol. 11, letter 3580, and the references in the notes there.

## 411

B"H, 13 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 10 Shevat, the day of the Hillula of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, Nasi of Israel.

...Since you write that you have spent most of your life in the field of complete Hebrew education, it is surely superfluous to emphasize that the time for education spans all the days of a person’s life. For at both extremes, even one who is, G-d forbid, in the lowest depths, has the ability and power to change from one extreme to the other—sometimes, as the Zohar expresses it, in a single hour and a single moment. Likewise, at the other extreme, even one who has ascended to the highest heights has the ability to learn more and still more, since the good is infinite. Therefore, one who educates others—and in doing so, educates himself as well—must always stand guard to utilize every possibility and opportunity in the aforementioned direction, or even to create such opportunities. According to the well-known statement in the Midrash, "I have learned much from my teachers, and from my students more than from all of them," the effort invested in the education of others—to show them and guide them on the path that leads to the House of G-d—teaches and adds to the positive results in the educator's own education and self-perfection.

It is understood that my intention is not to preach morality, G-d forbid, but rather to awaken [you], that... this does not exempt him in the slightest from utilizing his talents as much as possible to bring the hearts of the sons and daughters of Israel closer to our Father in Heaven through the study of our Torah, the Torah of life, and the fulfillment of its mitzvos. This, too, will certainly increase the blessings of Hashem, may He be blessed, for what is needed for his physical health, as well as what is needed for his household.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

P.S.
I would be interested to know if the lectures you wrote about have been published and if it is possible to obtain them, as they are not in my library.

## 412

B"H, 14 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, and distinguished scholar, engaged in communal needs,
Yehuda Leibush, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to learn, through the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished scholar, a man of character and energy, R' Refael Wilshansky, may he live, of the content of the words of inspiration that you shared at the farbrengen on the day of the hilula of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, the Nasi of Israel.

It is explained in many places regarding the satisfaction caused to the soul of the one whose hilula is being observed through such actions (see Rashi, Yevamos 122a, beginning of the page). This is especially true when the subject is the Nasi of Israel, who "left the life of his spirit, his work in which he labored previously in Israel, the work of a tzaddik for the living, for every living soul that is bound to his soul with the cords of great love and eternal love, etc." (the language of the Alter Rebbe in Iggeres HaKodesh, beginning of Epistle 27). This is a powerful bond, for "he who sees me and is my brother" (Shabbos 153a), and especially when one shares his Torah teachings, with which his soul was uniquely unified (as explained in Tanya, beginning of Chapter 5).

May it be the will of Hashem that the merit of the one whose hilula we observe protect each and every one of us, within the entirety of the Jewish people, to increase the heavenly assistance in fulfilling our role, as the Mishnah says, to serve my Creator.

With respect and blessing.

#### ***412***

**Yehuda Leibush:** Stern, Paris.

## 414

B"H, 14 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Following your longest silence, your letter from Erev Shabbos Parshas Bo was just received, in which I also did not find the reason for the silence. My hope is that, at the very least, it is not a matter of health.

Although you do not mention it in your letter, I hope that from time to time you participate in the farbrengens of anash, which bring about an elevation of spirit and an awakening of memories of days gone by. Regarding matters such as these, if one has stopped for any reason for a period of time, the interruption should cause an even greater desire to participate. After all, the words of Chazal must ultimately be fulfilled: "Throw a stick into the air, and it will land on its base." We see tangibly that the further the stick moves away from the earth—its root and source—the greater the speed of its descent back to the earth.

With blessings for good tidings in all that is stated and written explicitly, and also in that which is found between the lines.

## 155

16 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, who is G-d-fearing and whose work is holy work,
R' Yitzchak, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you raise the following points:

1) Regarding what is written in *Ohr HaTorah* by the Tzemach Tzedek (p. 280b) that the morning *tefillah*, which corresponds to the *Tamid* offering, is until four hours, while *Krias Shema* is until three hours—which is like the division of the *Ketores*, regarding which it is said "every morning, every morning" (*boker boker*) before the *Tamid*—you ask: Since the *tefillah* of the morning corresponding to the *Tamid* until four hours refers to the sprinkling of the *Tamid*’s blood, and the sprinkling of the *Tamid*’s blood occurred before the *Ketores*, and it is also said regarding it "every morning, every morning," why is this presented as a difficulty?

It is surprising that you write this as a difficulty, since in that very same gloss upon which you are questioning, all of this is already written.

Furthermore, the body of the *maamar* explains the matter that the sprinkling of the blood precedes the *Ketores*, and the *Ketores* precedes the limbs. Regarding the essence of the matter—your complaint regarding the language of our Sages (Pesachim 59b), "There is nothing that precedes the *Tamid* of the morning except the *Ketores*"—the actual difficulty of why the time for *tefillah* is until four hours even though the sprinkling of the blood must occur before the *Ketores*, and both are referred to as "every morning, every morning"... this is not the place for that discussion, as it belongs to the *Gemara*, not to the *maamar*.

In accordance with the concepts explained in the *maamar*, it can be said that in the order of *tefillah* as a whole, the sprinkling of the blood relates to *Krias Shema*, whose essence is *ratzo* (running) and enthusiasm in "flames of fire," while the matter of the fats and the burning of the limbs relates to the *Shemoneh Esrei*, regarding which it is said that its time is until four hours. This is understood from the distinction between *Krias Shema* and *Shemoneh Esrei* which is explained in many places in Chassidic discourse.

It should also be noted that the offering of the *Tamid*, which took an entire hour, as per the *Mishnah* at the beginning of *Maseches Tamid*, involved the slaughtering and the sprinkling—which must be done before the blood coagulates—in a very short time. The rest of the time is for the preparations for offering the limbs and the offering itself, as is proven in *Tamid*, chapters 4 and 5. One should not raise a difficulty regarding spiritual matters, for in the *Tamid* of the afternoon there is no *Krias Shema*, even though the sprinkling of the blood took place then as well—because it is explained in Kabbalah, and brought also in Chassidic teachings, that the *Krias Shema* of the morning is effective also for the afternoon *Mincha* (see *Torah Ohr*, beginning of *Parshas Vayechi*, 45c).

2) Regarding what you wrote in the *drush* for the 25th of Kislev, that the refinement of the *middos* is through *Chochma* because they are close to one another, and the refinement of the letters of *Chochma* and *Da’as* is through *Keter*, whose essence in *avodah* is *mesiras nefesh*—and although there are two types of *mesiras nefesh*, *mesiras nefesh* of "One" (*Echad*) and *mesiras nefesh* of "Blessed be the Name" (*Baruch Shem*)—the letters are refined specifically through the *mesiras nefesh* of "One" and not through the *mesiras nefesh* of "Blessed be the Name"—you find the reason for this difficult.

The reason is explained in many places: the *mesiras nefesh* of "Blessed be the Name," which is the love of "with all your soul," is connected to *avodah* that is according to *ta’am v’da’as* (intellectual understanding). This is also understood from the analogy of "pot-roasts"—meaning a food item that the body also enjoys, not just the scent. To refine the letters, whose source is from the "primordiality of the intellect," their refinement can only come from the "primordiality of the intellect" and that which precedes it, not from that which is below it, i.e., *avodah* of *ta’am v’da’as*.

For further explanation, see *Shaarei Orah* by the Mitteler Rebbe in the parallel places, and see there specifically chapters 9 and 10. *Mesiras nefesh* of "One" and the matter of *Ketores*, however, are entirely above *ta’am v’da’as*, like spices that are not fit for food. The matter in *avodah* is also explained in *Kuntres Eitz Chaim* by the Rebbe (Rashab), the father of the Rebbe Rayatz, chapters 8-9, and in many other places. (Perhaps it is possible to say that *mesiras nefesh* according to "Why do you see that your blood is redder" [in the revealed Torah] is similar to *mesiras nefesh* that is according to *ta’am v’da’as*.)

To complete the matter, it should be noted that there is an even higher level, like the superiority of the *Ketores* of Yom Kippur, which is "fine of the fine," over the *Ketores* of the entire year. Even though both are matters of scent, it is like the difference between the right nostril and the left nostril, *chaya* and *chaya d’chaya* (*Zohar*, Vol. 3, 130a). *Mesiras nefesh* of *chaya*, *mesiras nefesh* of *yechidah* (see *Ateres Rosh*, end of *Shaar Yom Kippur*; *Kuntres HaAvodah*, ch. 5; *D’H Lech Lecha* 5637). It is possible to say: *Teshuvah* of the entire year, and *Teshuvah* of Yom Kippur, where the essence of the day atones.

3) In the introduction to *Shaarei Orah* (2b), regarding the superiority of the *mesiras nefesh* of the Ten Martyrs—that the perfection of the *mesiras nefesh* of the Ten Martyrs was that it was not only for the sake of the Torah alone—the intention, simply put, is not regarding the *mesiras nefesh* of Purim and Chanukah, but regarding the *mesiras nefesh* of the Giving of the Torah (although it could be argued with difficulty that in Chanukah there was also the matter of *tefillah*, since the *avodah* in the Beis HaMikdash was nullified, unlike R' Chanina ben Teradyon who was burned with the *Sefer Torah* in his embrace; but in my opinion, that is a **great** stretch). Regarding the superiority of the *mesiras nefesh* of the Ten Martyrs—see *Eitz Chaim*, *Shaar* 39, ch. 4; *Shaar HaNeshamos*, ch. 5. It is possible that the introduction refers to what is written there in parentheses.

4) Regarding what you noted in the *drush* for Chanukah printed at the end of the book *Ohr HaTorah*—which appears to be a slip of the pen, and should be *Derech Emunah*—and you ask who is the author of the gloss on page 10b which begins [with a certain phrase], in my opinion, it is not so.

It seems you have not seen the edition of the *maamar* that we printed a few years ago, separately, for Chanukah.

There it is explained that it is generally by our Rebbe (the Alter Rebbe), and the glosses within it are by the Tzemach Tzedek, but the *maamar* is a transcription by the listener and not the handwriting of the Alter Rebbe himself. Therefore, the Tzemach Tzedek writes regarding the writer that he added, etc. The Tzemach Tzedek’s glosses are found in this manner also in the *drush* *Ta’ar HaSichirah*, in *Likkutei Torah* for *Gimel Parshiyos*, p. 3, and in several other places.

With blessings.

***

*) And so I shall read, for the doubling of "morning" regarding the *Ketores* is written in the place itself, unlike the sprinkling of the blood, which is written in another place.

And it is only that *Adam HaTamid* (Yoma 33b) is mentioned. And there is a reason for this.

## 4116

B"H, 17 Shevat, 5716

This means not only the teachings of Chassidus, but also its guidance and customs—and not only in the "near outside," but also in the "outside" that is currently far away. 4117

4117

B"H, 17 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who occupies himself with communal needs, a man of fine character, etc.,
R' Boruch, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your registered letter of Tuesday with the enclosed document.

Thank you for your prompt reply, although it was written with much *marah shechorah* (melancholy) regarding the *beis knesses* and the battle you are waging to ensure the shul is conducted as it should be. I emphasize the matter of *marah shechorah*, because as we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and as is clearly evident, when one goes into battle, being despondent and in a state of *marah shechorah* itself weakens the conduct of that battle. However, when one realizes that one is going to fulfill the instruction of our holy Torah, which was given to us by the Creator of the world, one does so with much greater vitality, and this itself increases the chances of success and hastens the victory.

I hope you will not suspect me of becoming a *mussar*-giver or preaching *mussar*. My intention in writing the above is only to evoke more action, and to increase the *bitachon* and *simcha* in yet another Yid. It is a well-known Chassidic teaching regarding *Ivdu es Hashem b’simcha* (Serve Hashem with joy) that even on Tisha B’Av—which will speedily be transformed into joy and gladness with the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu—the fasting and the recitation of *Kinos* should, at the time, be accompanied by a feeling of *simcha* as well, because one has the great fortune and opportunity to fulfill the command of the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He. As it is ruled in the Rambam at the end of *Hilchos Lulav*, that one who avoids *simcha* is deserving of punishment, etc., and one who performs this [service] is performing a great *avodah*, etc.—see there.

Enclosed is the letter from the lawyer, and I hope that if you have further news regarding this—and may it be the will that it be good tidings—you will inform me. Thank you in advance.

I am forwarding an excerpt of your letter to Pittsburgh, and I am certain that if they require your assistance in this further, you will provide it. May Hashem grant you success.

With blessing to reach your goals with *simcha* and success.

## 119

119

B"H, 17 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in the Holy City of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

You should certainly proceed immediately to practical activities, in accordance with the ruling of the Mishnah: "It is not the study that is the essential thing, but the deed." This is especially true in light of the Baal Shem Tov’s precise interpretation of the verse, "In a dry and weary land... I have beheld You in the Sanctuary." Since there has recently been a noticeable decline in the activities of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in Jerusalem, this should certainly inspire you to exert additional effort, in the spirit of the aforementioned verse.

In this regard, I wish to draw your attention to what I have written several times to the administration of Yeshivas Toras Emes: that all the married *avreichim*, especially those who have been accepted recently, should dedicate some of their time each day to communal work in the vineyard of Chabad. The administration has replied to me that the *avreichim* are prepared to fulfill this duty and privilege, and they have referred the matter to Tzeirei Agudas Chabad so that you may consult with them regarding the most effective way to utilize their talents, time, and energy. It is surprising that, apparently, nothing has been done about this by Tzeirei Agudas Chabad until now. It would be appropriate for you to meet with the administration of Yeshivas Toras Emes as soon as possible—you have my permission to show them this letter—and to devise a plan for all that has been mentioned.

It is surely unnecessary to point out that, as with any *avodah*, it is proper that the beginning should be calculated with the intent to strengthen existing matters, while adding to them within as short a time as possible, so that the promise of our Sages will be fulfilled: "Whoever adds, they add to him."

With blessings for good tidings.

## 4122

4122

B"H, 19 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from some time ago, and just now the *pidyon nefesh* from the day of the *hilula*, which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy resting place of the *baal hahilula*, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

I was pleased by what you wrote regarding the success in drawing some of our fellow Jews closer to matters of Torah and *mitzvos*. If our Sages taught that regarding a single soul, it is as if one has sustained an entire world, how much more so regarding several souls. It is already known that the effect of a single *mitzvah*, even if performed only once, creates a union Above that is eternal, forever and ever (*Tanya*, end of Chapter 26). This is especially true when, through several good deeds and *mitzvos*, one has merited to be the intermediary for this. May it be the will of Hashem that the ruling that "a *mitzvah* draws another *mitzvah*" be fulfilled in this as well—meaning that his own desire and energy to act in all the aforementioned matters will increase, and consequently, the opportunities will be provided for him to fulfill his heart’s desires for the good, both in his personal family matters and regarding others.

After asking your forgiveness, and prefacing with what is known regarding the greatness of peace—for the sake of which the entire Torah was given, as per the ruling of the Rambam at the end of *Hilchos Chanukah*, and furthermore, it is an explicit *Mishnah* that "a vessel is the only container that holds the blessing of the Holy One, blessed be He"—I will take the liberty of urging and encouraging you to strengthen and increase peace in your home. I mean this in the literal sense, regarding you and your wife, *tichyeh*. It seems, between the lines and also from the nature of the conversation I had here and her state of mind (*shtimmung*), that extra effort on your part is worthwhile to be yielding in your character traits and to exert yourself to the best of your ability in this. The proof of the magnitude of this matter is already well-known, even in the revealed Torah: our Sages of blessed memory said that the Holy One, blessed be He, commanded that His great Name, written in holiness—specifically the *Shem HaMeforash*, and specifically by a *Kohen*—be erased, if only to bring peace between a husband and wife. This applies even when the wife is behaving in a way that is, Heaven forbid, questionable; how much more so with a modest wife who has raised her children to *Chassidus*. Any effort in this is a lofty and exalted *mitzvah*. It is my hope that you will gladden me with good news that you are doing everything in your power in this regard, and that you are acting in accordance with the instruction of our Sages of blessed memory that "women are of a light mind," by gladdening the heart of your wife, *tichyeh*, in a manner appropriate for her—that is, not through tension, but specifically through a pleasant countenance, and so on. Surely these few lines, small in quantity, will suffice, and I will await good news.

With blessings for success in all that has been mentioned.

## 124

124

B"H, 19 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and reliable, occupied with communal needs, R' Shlomo Chaim, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

And not only regarding the matter of *yiras shamayim* and Chassidus, but also regarding the *nigleh*. It is known that the story told by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, is that when the Alter Rebbe began his work of spreading the teachings of Chassidus in Reisin, he utilized students who were outstanding in *nigleh*. The arrangement was that wherever they went, they would astound their listeners with their knowledge of *nigleh*, and they would utilize that astonishment to capture their minds and hearts for the study of the teachings of Chassidus...

Consequently, one must take into account the true desire of the students in this regard.

3) Regarding your question about establishing something akin to a *kollel*: once I receive detailed information on this—namely, how many hours a day those who wish to be accepted into the *kollel* will study, whether they are individuals with sufficient talent such that after studying for a period of time in the *kollel* they will be able and willing to become *mashpiim*, *roshei yeshiva*, and *rabbeim* in the vineyard of Chabad, and also regarding the expenses involved—I will be able to make a decision on this, as I wrote in the letter to the administration in general.

With a blessing to hear good news regarding all that has been mentioned.

## 125

B"H, 20 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn

To the Shomrei Shabbos Gemilas Chasadim Society,
May they live,

Peace and Blessing!

In response to the notification regarding the Society’s annual meeting this coming Sunday:

May it be the will of Hashem that your gathering be successful—successful in material matters and successful in spiritual matters. That is to say, may your activity in Gemilas Chasadim, in its literal sense, in addition to the inherent greatness of the matter itself, also lead to Gemilas Chasadim in spiritual matters.

This follows the path of the Patriarchs, who are a sign for their children—especially Avraham Avinu, whose essence was Gemilas Chasadim. The ultimate goal and purpose of his interaction with those who received from him was the proclamation: "Say, 'Blessed is the G-d of the world, from whose [bounty] we have eaten.'"

In this same way, may it be regarding the work of the Society.

Furthermore, may not only the recipients, but all who see—and even all who hear—that there are those who are Shomrei Shabbos and are also Gomelei Chasadim, understand and be impressed by the connection between these two matters.

In particular, there is also a special connection between them, for the keeping of Shabbos testifies to and establishes the concept of "the renewal of the world, which is the rope that pulls all the foundations of the religion, through the simple Will" (Sefer HaChinuch on our Parsha). That is, through His kindness—a kindness of grace. And man, who was created in the image and likeness [of the Divine] and was commanded to cleave to Him, is to cleave to His ways—to perform acts of kindness. Especially since the Torah was given to them **from His right hand** (see also Tanya, end of Chapter 34; Torah Or 95b, which concludes: meaning that the fire of Torah is also drawn from His right hand. And its reward—in Torah Or 32b, at the beginning).

And just as it is said regarding the "Supernal Man," as it were, "And the throne is established in Chesed," so too is the greatness of the Gemilas Chasadim of the lower man, to influence [the flow of blessing] to him and to all his household, may they live, for whatever they require in material and spiritual matters.

With blessings for success,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.
As is my custom—but without a vow—I have enclosed a check as my participation in the aforementioned Shomrei Shabbos Gemilas Chasadim fund.

## 426

426

B"H, 21 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the Avreich Shlomo, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, in which you write about the tremendous impression made by the gathering, and the speech by [Name], which stirred the spirits toward yiras shamayim, Torah, and mitzvos — fortunate is your portion that you participated in organizing this. From this, my opinion regarding the future is also understood: that you should continue in this work, even though, like any internal avodah, it requires an investment of time, energy, and attention. We have already been promised by our Rebbe, the author of the Tanya (the authority on the hidden aspects of Torah) and the Shulchan Aruch (the authority on the revealed aspects of Torah), that through tzedakah with others, one’s mind and heart become a thousand times more refined.

However, from the very language of this promise—which says that one becomes "refined," not that one becomes a scholar and a yarei shamayim—it is understood that one must study, and also engage in matters that bring about feelings of the heart in the love of Hashem and the fear of Hashem, except that one is blessed with extraordinary success, literally a thousandfold. Therefore, you must arrange your studies in the revealed Torah and in the teachings of Chassidus at a proper time each and every day, as is fitting for an avreich ben yeshiva. And only in the times free from the yeshiva’s schedule—and occasionally from the yeshiva’s time—should you dedicate yourself to the aforementioned avodah. I am confident that in this manner, your father, the Rav, shlita, will also agree with a full heart.

It is understood that all of the above is by way of a fixed order, but in an exceptional case and as an emergency measure, it is necessary—and at times even mandatory—to add time from one’s communal needs to the time for Torah study, and sometimes the opposite: to take from the time of study for communal needs. Especially when considering communal matters such as those under discussion, which at times—in this period—are matters of pikuach nefesh in the literal sense. And surely in this, too, the teaching of the Mishnah will be fulfilled: "A mitzvah leads to another mitzvah," and not, chas v'shalom, the opposite.

Regarding your question as to which individuals to invite to preach before the public, etc.—it is understood that this must be decided by the people who are on the scene, while also taking into account matters of *maris ayin*, what will be heard, and so on.

On the other hand, one must strive to utilize all possible strengths. One should not set hard-and-fast rules about this, even on the spot, and certainly not from a distance, since circumstances change from time to time.

It was pleasant for me to read in your letter that you are studying Chabad Chassidus in a fixed manner. Surely you are familiar with the saying of our Rebbe, that the "fixity" (kavius) must be in time, and also in the soul—which is the main thing. And it is already known that "a fixed thing is not nullified."

And since "every single day does its work," and we recite the blessing on the Torah anew each day, and the phrasing "Giver of the Torah" is in the present tense, the fixity in the study of Chassidus must also be every single day.

With blessings to hear good news regarding all of the above.

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding your questions in your letter from the auspicious day of the 19th of Kislev:

a) Whether to believe with simple faith or to investigate/analyze—both are **necessary**. And not only is there no contradiction between them, but on the contrary, they complement one another.

The beginning of avodah and its foundation is simple faith, and immediately one is obligated in the mitzvah which is the "foundation of foundations and the pillar of wisdom": **to know** that there is a Primary Being, etc. (Rambam at the beginning of his work), and in the language of the Zohar (Vol. II, 25a): "This is the first of all commandments... **to know** Hashem, etc." And "If one says, 'I have labored and not found,' do **not** believe." One is obligated to labor and exert his intellect to contemplate and understand to the extent of his ability—and human ability is limited—and that which is beyond his ability, he shall live by his fundamental and simple faith. See also the mitzvah of the belief in Elokus by the Tzemach Tzedek, *Kuntres Toras HaChassidus*, Chapter 13, and elsewhere.

b) Order of study—in the revealed Torah, in accordance with the schedule of the yeshiva where you study (and it is mandatory, in any case, to study and know the necessary halachos). In Chassidus—you should discuss this with R' Sh. Ch. Kesselman, as it depends on the talents of each individual, etc., etc.

## 127

B"H, 21 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 14 Shevat, which begins with your expression of shame, etc.

It is understood and simple that the goal in this must be a fundamental change regarding **action**. Regarding what you write—that there are matters from which you cannot extricate yourself, etc.—since the Creator demands this from every single Jew, He certainly has already provided the necessary strengths to fulfill that demand. This applies to your situation as well. However, as with all matters, one should not expect a change from one extreme to the other in a single hour or a single moment, for the avodah of a person is from level to level and with appropriate effort; then the promise of our Sages is fulfilled: "You have labored and you have found."

It would be appropriate to have your tefillin checked, as well as the mezuzos in the place where you live. You should be careful regarding tevilas Ezra, and every weekday before morning davening, set aside a few coins for tzedakah. You should learn by heart—so that they are engraved in your memory—words of Torah in general, and in particular, some chapters of Mishnayos and at least one chapter of Tanya. You should strive to learn with a chavrusa, or at the very least in a place where Torah is studied in public, such as a yeshiva or beis medrash. May Hashem grant you success and may you have good news to report regarding an improvement in all the matters about which you write.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 128

128

B"H, 21 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the day of the Hilula, along with the enclosed Pidyon Nefesh, in which you write that the health of your wife, may she live, has improved slightly—may Hashem help that she have a complete and speedy recovery.

Regarding what you write—that you are preoccupied with *parnassah* and so on—this is like someone who is hungry and weakened by hunger, who says that he will not eat until he becomes stronger. For the preoccupation with *parnassah* is as the Mishnah says in *Avos*, Chapter 3, Mishnah 5: "Whoever accepts upon himself the yoke of Torah, they remove from him the yoke of *derech eretz*," and vice versa. Consequently, if one wants the preoccupation with *parnassah* to diminish, accepting the yoke of Torah is one of the primary pieces of advice for this. Further elaboration on a matter that is understood is unnecessary. May Hashem grant you the merit to share good news regarding this, as well as regarding your greatest possible participation in the Yeshivah...

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

B"H, 21 Shevat, 5716

## 4131

B"H, 24 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all friends of *Chinuch HaKasher*, and the participants in the annual *chagigah* of "Beis Sarah," in particular, may Hashem grant them life:

Peace and blessing!

The annual *chagigah* of the Beis Sarah schools, which is scheduled, B"H, for Sunday, the first day of Rosh Chodesh Adar, falls during the week of Parshas Terumah, which recounts the building of the *Mishkan* and the *Mikdash*. This should serve to remind us and emphasize the importance of the Jewish woman and daughter in every detail of Jewish life—as a guiding force and a beacon.

For, as the Torah relates, the women were the first to take a part in building the holy place for the Divine *Shechinah*, and they refused to take any part in the Golden Calf, which was the very opposite of that.

A Jewish daughter, through proper *chinuch* in the spirit of the Torah, feels with an inner, G-d-blessed sense what is holy and must be supported, and what is harmful and must be distanced from Jewish life.

And in these times, when good and evil, light and darkness, are often interchanged, it is, more than ever, a life-necessity that the Jewish daughter receive a Torah-*chinuch* *al-taharas-hakodesh*, so that she may be able to occupy her rightful place as *akeres-habayis*, for in her hands, to a great extent, lies the future of *Beis Yisrael*.

In the Beis Sarah schools, Jewish daughters are prepared from their earliest youth to uphold the *mesorah* (tradition) of our mothers Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah, and all the generations of loyal Jewish mothers who guarded and preserved the foundations of the Jewish home and Jewish life.

I therefore turn with a *kriah shel hisorerus* to all who hold dear the Jewish people and authentic *Yiddishkeit*—which cannot exist one without the other—and who appreciate the importance of *chinuch habanos al-taharas-hakodesh*, and to *anash* in particular, to support the Beis Sarah schools, which were founded by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zi"e*, and to help provide the financial means necessary to maintain these *mosdos* and enable their expansion.

And the *zechus* of strengthening the *chinuch* of the daughters of Israel in the spirit of *Yisrael Saba* will surely stand by the supporters and helpers, that Hashem Yisbarach should help them in all that they need, both *b'gashmius* and *b'ruchnius*.

With blessings of all the best,

**M. Schneerson**

## 4132

B"H, 25 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

With blessings for good tidings,
