## 434

B"H, 26 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Eliezer Steinman
Shalom u'Bracha!

I hereby express my gratitude for your thoughtfulness in sending me the books you have published recently: *Kisvei HaMaggid MiDubno*, *Kisvei Rabbi Nachman MiBreslov*, and *Be'er HaChassidus*, first and second series.

Regarding these books, and specifically the *Be'er HaChassidus* series, I would like to offer two points:

(a) The goal of any author in general, and of one writing on a scholarly subject in particular, is to awaken a desire in the reader to continue taking an interest in the topics presented in the book and to delve into them more deeply—especially if the author is presenting the material in his own language and phrasing, as a "second vessel." In all times, and especially in our generation, efforts are made to facilitate the reader and student by providing "handles for the vessel" and the like. Therefore, in my opinion—and experience confirms this—it is of the utmost importance to indicate the sources immediately in the footnotes, or at the very least at the end of each book, citing the chapter, page, etc. This is especially true when quoting, as it gives the reader and student the opportunity to form their own opinion on the interpretation of the source material and stimulates their desire to delve into the subject. Furthermore, this practice is good and beneficial not only for the reader and student but also for the author, as one’s notes containing the sources are not always preserved, and even if they are, they are not always at hand when one is studying these topics again.

I noticed that these citations are missing in your aforementioned books. However, it is my hope that if my suggestion is accepted, it is not too late to fill this deficiency in your forthcoming books. And it would be even better to issue a supplementary booklet for the books already published, containing the citations for their respective topics.

(b) In conveying the system and concepts of Torah—which is a living Torah and the Torah of life—and especially the part of it that is connected with emotion, and particularly if the intention is to reach a readership for whom these perspectives are new and even foreign: in order for the matter to be presented with greater completeness and closer to their inner selves, it is not enough for the transmitter or author to read the books of this Torah, study them with the necessary depth, and convey their essence. Rather, he must "clothe" himself as much as possible in the spirit of the Torah and in the lifestyle of the system's founders and leaders. And this "clothing" is all the more necessary if the author's goal is to reach practical conclusions regarding life in the present.

I do not know you personally, but I hope you will not take offense at my venturing to suggest that in order to achieve the goal you have set for yourself in your books—as you write in your introduction to *Be'er HaChassidus*—it is appropriate that you internalize their way of life, namely, a life according to the Torah and in actual practice, as these ways of life are explained in the source, in the books of Chassidus. The approach of "the Merciful One desires the heart" is not sufficient; for while this is necessary first and foremost, it is not enough by any means.

You may suspect that my intention in the above is to influence a Jew to become a full observer of Torah and mitzvos, and furthermore, according to the requirements of the teachings of Chassidus.

I will admit that in this, too, our Sages of blessed memory were correct when they said that one is not suspected of something unless it is present in him to some degree.

However, this small part of my intention does not in any way diminish the benefit for the aforementioned goal, and in my opinion, it is also a necessity that these matters—the words of the teachings of Chassidus, which are a "second vessel"—be conveyed with greater proximity to their truth and their inner essence. You may also be surprised by my hope that through a letter I could influence a thinker, who surely has a way of life that is established and bound to the fibers of his soul, to such an extent that upon receiving the letter, he would change not only his perspective but also his conduct.

The explanation for this is that I am not coming with something new of my own, but am suggesting an age-old idea, which is also the concept of our Torah and mitzvos—that every single day is new, and He is the Creator of worlds.

And one who believes in man and his infinite soul-powers—since the soul of a Jewish person is, in the words of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya, "literally a part of G-d from above," which is the Ein Sof—also believes that in a single moment, one can reach the highest heights, regardless of his state and standing the moment before. And the cause of this can be even a small thing or a small spark, since it serves only to open the treasures of the Ein Sof that exist in the soul of the listener or reader.

With respect and blessing.

I am sure you have at your disposal the indices for the Chabad books that I have compiled at various times, which correspond to the first point in my letter above, and which I have found to be of great benefit, as mentioned—not only for others but also for myself.

## 135

B"H, 26 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...You are surely participating in the farbrengen of Anash. Indeed, "great is the drink [of a farbrengen] that brings [people] closer," etc. The end of our exile—which was brought about by baseless hatred—is also dependent upon this closeness. As our Sages of blessed memory have taught, it is understood from this that the rectification must be in a manner that corresponds [to the cause], namely, baseless love, as has been discussed many times.

And even though, on the face of it, the concept of "baseless" (chinnam) is impossible here, since "Love your fellow as yourself" is a great principle of the Torah—therefore, it must be that this refers even to those who are not in the category of "your fellow" who is "your peer" in Torah and mitzvos, and yet one loves them, etc. See Tanya, Chapter 32, and the Sefer HaMitzvos of the Tzemach Tzedek regarding the mitzvah of Ahavas Yisrael, as well as the Tzemach Tzedek’s glosses to Tanya, Chapter 32 (in Sefer Kitzurim VeHe'aros LeTanya, p. 36).

## 4138

B"H, 28 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim
To the Administration of the Vocational School
May they live

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letters of 20 Shevat and 21 Shevat, along with their enclosures. The map of the village grounds has also been received.

1) Regarding the location of the Yeshiva buildings, I have already written that they should be as far as possible from the vocational schools. However, it is also understood that they cannot be placed in an area where there is a risk of flooding. As is my approach in other matters, the buildings and grounds should be planned in a way that allows for further expansion later on.

2) Regarding the shluchim (fundraisers), I have already replied that it is up to the administration to choose them, according to their talents and specific tasks...

3) Regarding what you wrote about the demand to bring a radio, phonograph, etc., into the vocational school: it is obvious that if these things are brought as a demand or a claim, they are to be rejected, even if we were to assume that the matter itself does not carry much risk. Since, on the other hand, one must strive to have the largest possible number of suitable students, and the aforementioned demand may stem from a lack of interesting activities for the students during their free time, one must strive as much as possible to fill this free time with matters of holiness that also engage the *nefesh habehamis*, thereby weakening the aforementioned demand. I cannot refrain from expressing my astonishment at your doubt; for if the aforementioned are permitted in an agricultural school, for what reason would they be forbidden in a carpentry school, and by extension, in Tomchei Temimim in Lod? If you were to take an interest in preparing *sichos* and *farbrengens* with the students, in accordance with their knowledge and talents, this question would certainly be removed from the agenda as a matter of course.

4) Regarding what you wrote in your letter of 21 Shevat about the rumor:

It is simple that those of *anash* who filed claims and a conditional injunction regarding exit permits and the like must immediately cancel these claims and the conditional injunction. For although there is room to make efforts in a friendly manner and through pleasant ways regarding this, it should not be done through methods that are the opposite of common sense. Consequently, you should also strive to ensure that the rumor is debunked.

The attribute of *Chesed* and drawing close will nullify—in the language of *Tikkunei Zohar*—the *Din* which is *Gevurah*, etc. And it is a wonder that even in such simple matters, there is a need for stimulation from across the sea.

Regarding the students for the agricultural school—I have already written that you must increase their numbers as much as possible, especially since it is inevitable that some of those who are accepted will leave the institution due to the difficulty of adjusting to its routines, as is customary in every institution.

With blessings for success and for good tidings.

**M. Schneerson**

## 439

B"H, 28 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned R' Yehuda Aryeh, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of Tuesday, in which you write regarding the difficulty you have with the principle that creation occurs every day and every moment—as we say, "He who renews in His goodness each day, continually, the work of creation"—if so, what is the significance of Shabbos, regarding which it is said, "And on the seventh day He ceased from work and rested," [referring to] the creation of the six days of creation?

The distinction is simple, based on what is written: "And the heavens and the earth and all their host were completed," and it is said, "There is nothing new under the sun," after the conclusion of the six days of creation. For what is renewed thereafter, "continually" each day, is the work of creation, which is a renewal of that which already existed. This is in contrast to the six days of creation, which was a renewal from the very beginning—that is, something that had never existed until then, *yesh me'ayin* [something from nothing]*.

Regarding what you wrote about a curriculum for studying Chassidus, it is understood that this depends on one's knowledge and abilities. Therefore, you should consult with the elders of anash who are in your area; explain your situation to them, and they will guide you.

Surely you are aware of the three daily study portions established by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nevag"m, zi"a*, in the Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, which are known to all. In any event, you should keep them from this point forward.

With blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,
Secretary

***

*) See the *maamar* entitled "Va'ehyeh Etzlo Amon" from the year 5700, Chapter 2 and onwards. There is also a further distinction regarding the above between Rosh Hashanah, Shabbos, and the weekdays, which is explained in many places. Among them is in *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek, in the *mitzvah* of "Do not kindle a fire in all your dwellings."

**R' Yehuda Aryeh:** Palik, Jerusalem.

## 401

B"H, 28 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, and learned man, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Chaim Aryeh, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your *pidyon nefesh* for yourself and for your household, may they live. At an auspicious time, I will read it at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and may it be the will of Hashem that you be able to share good news regarding the matters mentioned therein.

It is surely unnecessary to awaken you to the demands of the hour, especially for one whom Divine Providence has placed in a position to influence the youth—as a *rosh yeshiva* or *rebbe*—to instill in those he influences a spirit of pure *yiras shamayim* and *ahavas Hashem*, even if his official subject is a specific area of study and not the direct instilling of *dichilu* and *rechimu*. For someone like yourself, further elaboration on this is surely superfluous.

My father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, instituted three daily *shiurim* that are accessible to every person: in *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*. They are: 1) Reciting the *shiur* of *Tehillim*—as the *Tehillim* is divided for the days of the month—each day after morning *davening*. 2) Studying the *Chumash* portion with the commentary of Rashi from the weekly *sedra*—on Sunday from the beginning of the *sedra* until the second *aliyah*, on Monday from the second *aliyah* until the third, and so on. 3) Studying a *shiur* in *Tanya* each day—as the *Tanya* is divided here for the days of the year. It is appropriate that you should, at the very least, keep these from here on in.

With blessings for good news.

## 142

B"H, 28 Shevat, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 20 Shevat, in which you write regarding your state of mind, that you lack vitality, etc., etc.

The well-known advice for such a situation is already known: to increase your study of the teachings of Chassidus, which is called the "soul of the Torah," and which adds light and vitality to all of a person’s affairs. Furthermore, increase your efforts in the avodah of the Ribono shel Olam specifically with joy, as the Zohar HaKadosh states (Vol. II, 184b): "If one stands with a shining countenance from below, then they shine upon him from above... the joy of a person draws toward him another, higher joy," see there.

Regarding what you wrote about how to utilize your strengths—

Consult with the anash who are on-site, who know you and the possibilities available in your location, for it has already been said, "In the multitude of counselors there is salvation..."

It is surprising that you do not mention any additional study beyond what is required by the yeshiva’s schedule, for "the mitzvos of Hashem are upright, gladdening the heart"—even the physical heart.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 143

143

B.H., Erev Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5716
Brooklyn

To my dear friend, the eminent Torah scholar and G-d-fearing Chassid, a man of fine character,
R' Yeshaya, may he live and be well, Halevi

Greetings and blessings!

After your longest silence, it was a pleasure to receive your letter, and I thank you for the news regarding the *chavurah* that is with you.

Regarding what you wrote expressing surprise at the mistake of the publisher, who did something improper, and you note subsequently that in the *Siddur* of our Alter Rebbe, in the *Krias Shema She'al HaMitah*, it is written that on Shabbos night one does not say *Viduy* nor *LaMenatzeach*, etc., and there is no mention regarding Rosh Chodesh, Chanukah, or even *Yom Tov*—however, you do not clarify what your complaint is against the publisher. Perhaps you mean what is written there in the *Krias Shema She'al HaMitah* that on Shabbos and *Yom Tov* one does not say *Viduy*—that in any case, he should not have changed the wording of the Alter Rebbe’s *Siddur*, or he should have specified everything necessary, namely: Shabbos night, *Yom Tov*, Rosh Chodesh, Chanukah, etc. Even though your argument is correct in itself, one should judge favorably, as most *Siddurim*—and likewise the *Siddur* published by the publisher—are not typeset anew from beginning to end. Rather, they use *Siddurim* that have already been printed and make changes according to the desired *nusach*. Consequently, they only pay attention to those matters that differ from one *nusach* to another. Furthermore, they do not always notice that there are *Siddurim* prepared for the entire year except for *Yomim Tovim* and the like, which is very common in the *Nusach Ashkenaz* tradition, as they have special *Machzorim* for the *Shalosh Regalim*, etc. It seems that in the publisher’s *Siddur* as well, the *nusach* they printed was inadvertently carried over in a similar fashion—meaning they did it via photography from a *Siddur* of a different *nusach*, which itself was also made via photography from a *Siddur* that preceded it, and thus it was printed as mentioned above.*

It is surprising that you do not mention your communal work, for surely you have a *ayin tova* regarding others, as Hashem has graced you with the power of influence over others, especially in the work of *hafatza*—spreading the wellsprings outward—in accordance with the demand of our Nasi, the Rebbe, *ztzukulalleh, navgum, zya*, and especially since this is the *mitzvah* of the era, as is known from the story of the Baal Shem Tov: "When your wellsprings spread outward, the King Moshiach will come."

With blessings for long days and good years, and for good tidings.

P.S.
You surely meet with *Anash* from time to time and assist them in their activities in the vineyard of Chabad to the best of your ability.

Regarding what you noted about the citation from the *sefer Ohr Ne'erav*—one must search in the first edition of the book, for it is common in such cases that in subsequent printings, several matters are omitted, and for the time being, I have not been able to obtain that edition. The *sefer Ohr Yakar*, I believe, has not yet been printed.

#### ***143***

*) The instruction of our Rebbe, *Rayatz*, regarding this was recorded in the *Hayom Yom* of 28 Adar I, 5743: In *Krias Shema She'al HaMitah*: "Ribono shel Olam, I hereby forgive," and likewise *LaMenatzeach*... *b'vo*—is not said on Shabbos and *Yom Tov*, but it must be said on other days when *Tachanun* is not said. At the conclusion of the three paragraphs, one says the word "Emes." *Ya'alzu Chassidim*—once; *Hinei mitaso*—three times; *Yevarechecha*—three times. In *Tikkun Chatzos*, one does not say *LaMenatzeach*... *b'vo* on days when *Tachanun* is not said.

## 144

B.H., 1 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 25 Shevat, in which you write that you are studying at the Tomchei Temimim yeshiva branch in...

You mention that you have your own reasoning for continuing your studies at the Tomchei Temimim yeshiva in Lod, and you ask whether you should act according to your own desire or not.

It is understood that this phrasing is new to me, for I have never heard of a yeshiva student in general, and a Tomchei Temimim student in particular, asking whether to act according to his own desire. After all, the entire purpose of being a yeshiva student is to ascend in yiras shamayim through the study of Torah in both its revealed and hidden aspects, and in the meticulous fulfillment of mitzvos—not matters of fulfilling one's own desires. It seems that providing room for the aforementioned is also the explanation for your second question, regarding how foreign thoughts are distracting you from your studies, etc.

The advice for both matters together, and their solution, is to accept upon yourself the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven, the yoke of Torah, and the yoke of mitzvos—using the terminology of our Sages, who specifically used the word **"yoke"** in relation to all these. You should listen to the instruction of your Rosh Yeshiva, your Mashpia, and your Mashpia of Chassidus. That is to say, you should present all the reasoning you have before them, but afterwards, you must do whatever they instruct you. It is already well known that the precedence of "we will do" to "we will hear" is precisely how one receives the Torah (even though, on the face of it, it is an intellectual matter), and all the more so is this the beginning and foundation of avodah.

Specifically regarding what you wrote concerning foreign thoughts: you should divert your attention from them through other thoughts. That is, not through a war or a back-and-forth debate with the thought, but rather by anchoring the power of your thought in a good thought—in a matter of yiras shamayim, or in Torah and mitzvos. If you find this particularly difficult, you should bind your thought to the written letters; that is, study the printed text, which will make it easier to expel the negative thought.

I trust that you are keeping the three daily study portions that are incumbent upon every soul, as established by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—the Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—and that you know by heart certain chapters of Tanya and certain chapters of Mishnayos, and that you review them.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 4146

B"H, 2 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...To my regret, I am compelled once again to express my astonishment, with all due respect, regarding the incident that occurred... namely:

In response to my inquiry regarding the plan and the manner of organizing the gathering of the Reshet students on the day of the Hilula...

I was told, to my great astonishment, that while the male students were brought into a storage room immediately upon their arrival and a farbrengen was held with them, etc., the female students were left to wander from place to place for several hours. Consequently, not only was the time not utilized to influence them and bring them closer to Yiddishkeit, Torah, and mitzvos, but on the contrary, an undesirable impression was left, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

When I asked why a suitable place had not been prepared for them in advance, I was told that the initial thought had been for them to gather in the shul, but suddenly, a few individuals stood up and shouted and clamored that they would under no circumstances allow the female students to gather there, citing reasons of... yiras shamayim! I ask that you, as the Mara D’asra, clarify with these individuals: a) Where is the source for this appalling conduct in Nigleh or in Chassidus? b) From where do they derive such "broad shoulders" — *breite pleitzes* — to prevent one hundred students from hearing words of hisorerus and yiras shamayim, given that they are not Rabbanim or *morei hora’ah* in Yisrael? They should merely present their arguments and leave the final decision to the Rav of the community. c) A person knows his own standing in yiras shamayim, which is not always consistent. When they themselves feel a decline, do they also refrain from entering a holy place until they have performed a complete teshuvah, in the language of the Rambam—that the Knower of Secrets will testify that they will not return to folly again—or as explained in the Tanya in Iggeres HaTeshuvah by our Rebbe HaZaken? d) It is an explicit Gemara, Sukkah 51b, that women would enter the Ezrah, and furthermore, initially, the women were inside and the men were outside. The gallery that was instituted for them was only so that they would not come to lightheadedness, since men and women were participating in that same Ezrah, but not because the daughters of Yisrael compromise the holiness of the Ezrah, chas v’shalom. Either way: if these individuals knew of this Gemara, how could they act in opposition to it? And if they did not know of it, then individuals who possess such a lack of knowledge should not be dictating public conduct with such force—conduct that affects one hundred daughters of Yisrael.

In the shul where my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukl”h, nbg”m, zy”a*, Nasi of Yisrael, davened, they held gatherings for female students several times, even during the lifetime of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in this world. And as mentioned in the previous paragraph, if these individuals are unaware of the customs of Chassidim, they should ask, not dictate; and if they do know, how could they instruct to do the opposite...

With blessings.

## 147

B"H, 2 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rav, G-d-fearing, learned, and refined, a man of many accomplishments,
R' Yitzchak Isaac, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your regards through the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and accomplished, R' Shlomo Zalman Hecht, may he live. As he requested, I will mention him and his family, may they live, at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Knowing your relationship with the affairs of Lubavitch and Chabad—and in accordance with the dictum of our Sages, "we ascend in matters of holiness"—and what greater holiness is there than a positive relationship with the Children of Israel, which is a "great principle of the Torah," as Rabbi Akiva said regarding the verse, "And you shall love your neighbor as yourself"—my hope is strengthened that you will increase this relationship. Especially as the time for the discussion regarding the matters of the *Keren Hatzalah* of the camp of the good and the distribution is surely approaching, I am certain you will translate your good intentions into action. This is particularly true given that the need for this assistance is constantly growing, as is surely known to you, to the point that the necessity has breached the boundaries of the newspapers, and even they have begun to take an interest in the situation of the hundreds of thousands of our brethren from the Sephardic lineage.

Regarding matters such as these, I am reminded of a saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, who said upon his arrival in the United States for the second time: although it is the way of the world to avoid competition and imitation, the approach of Lubavitch in general, and my approach in particular, is that "I wish that the number of those who want to work in the areas of his work—and in his manner—would only increase."

It is remarkable that in this work, as in so many points of the activities and affairs of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, we see the consistency of the *Nesi'im* of Israel in our times. For the *Nasi* of our generation—in the language of the *Tikkunei Zohar*, the "extension of Moshe"—even regarding Yehoshua, his servant who would not depart from the tent, nevertheless suggested to him, as it were, "at least as our Sages say, 'cast the burden upon them.'" And in the very same breath, the faithful shepherd of Israel answered, "Would that all of Hashem's people were prophets, that Hashem would place His spirit upon them." This means that he does not insist that it be specifically in the manner previously stated by the Holy One, blessed be He—"I will draw from the spirit that is upon you and place it upon them"—but rather, "that He would place His spirit upon them..."

And as mentioned above, I thank you in advance for your efforts to the best of your ability in allocating assistance for our work in the aforementioned matters, and in the greatest measure possible.

With blessing.

## 4148

4148

B"H, 3 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad in Toronto
May Hashem grant them life

Blessings and peace!

In connection with the news regarding your event on Sunday, Parshas Tetzaveh, 7 Adar, I hereby send my greetings and blessings to all the participants, and to the members of Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad in particular.

Your event takes place at the time of year when we read the Torah portions that recount the building of the Mishkan and the Beis HaMikdash, and the participation of the women in that endeavor.

Surely, the content of these Torah portions will once again remind and emphasize the importance of the Jewish woman and daughter in all details of Jewish life—as a leader and a guide.

For, as the Torah relates, the women were the first to take a part in building the holy place for the Divine Shechinah, and they refused to take part in the Golden Calf, which was the very opposite of that.

A conscious Jewish woman and daughter feels, with an inner, G-d-blessed sense, what is holy and must be supported, and what is harmful and must be distanced from Jewish life.

And in the present time, when good and evil, light and darkness, are often interchanged, it is, even more than ever, a life-necessity that this inner Divine sense of the Jewish woman and daughter should find expression in daily life.

In this consists the main task of the widespread Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad:

To bring out the inner consciousness of the Jewish woman and daughter and their sense of responsibility to occupy their rightful place in the House of Israel, as the *akeres habayis* (the mainstay of the home).

And to always remember that in their hands, to a great extent, lies the future of the House of Israel.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant success to your work and activities, and may you fulfill, to the fullest extent, the aforementioned inner intent that lies at the foundation of the Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad.

And through this, also add and increase the Divine blessings for you and your households, may they live, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings.

## 149

149

B"H, 3 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 26 Shevat, in which you write regarding the concerns [kasad] concerning the new medication, Meticorten, and that there are still doubts as to whether to use it.

In my opinion, you should ask the doctor’s opinion regarding the known medications Hydrocortisone, which are of the cortisone family, but are better; therefore, the doubts regarding their use are less significant. In certain cases, they have been using this here for several months, although I do not know if this is relevant to the treatment of your wife, may she live.

Regarding what you wrote about reviewing Chassidus—that it requires preparation and exertion, and that your preoccupations interfere with this—it is certainly unnecessary to remind you of the words of our Sages, of blessed memory, that the acceptance of the yoke of Torah lightens and removes the matters of the yoke of worldly affairs. We see this tangibly, even—to make a distinction—in intellectual matters: deep immersion in an intellectual subject prepares a person to accept worries and preoccupations in a more calculated manner, and to react to them without exaggerating or magnifying them. How much more so is this true regarding Torah, which brings healing to the world, even in a segulah-like manner.

Regarding what you wrote that you do not have books, and that this also hinders the aforementioned, let me know which books from the Kehot Publication Society catalog that are in the possession of the esteemed R. Avraham, may he live, Paris, you require, and without a vow, they will be provided to you...

With blessings for good tidings.

## 150

B"H, 3 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 24 Shevat, in which you write that you are in doubt as to whether to change your attire to a long coat and black hat, especially since your family members are opposed to this.

Since for the time being you are yourself in doubt about this, there is no reason to rush to a positive decision on the matter. For the present, you should increase your study with consistency and diligence in general, and specifically in the study of Chassidus, which strengthens fear of Heaven and love of Hashem. After some time, you should once again judge the aforementioned question in accordance with your situation then. For a change of attire in such a case must be undertaken in a state of mind where the decision is firm, in order to rule out the possibility of reverting to previous attire due to shame from those who mock. Indeed, we see tangibly that this is one of the great trials, as is also hinted at in the beginning of all four parts of the Shulchan Aruch: "And do not be ashamed before those who mock." See there.

With blessings,

Secretary

## 451

B"H, 7 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all lovers of Torah and mitzvos, and to Anash in particular,
In every place,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and abundant blessing!

The Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim in Lod, in the Holy Land—may it be rebuilt and established—which includes those who have immigrated from Russia and our Sephardic brethren, along with its branches, all of which were founded by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—

Thank Hashem, it has grown and flourished, both in quantity—in the number of students, may they increase—and in quality—in the study of Torah and the "light" within it, with pure yiras shamayim, and in the education of the students, may they live, in accordance with the will of its founder.

And as with all matters of holiness, which, according to the ruling of our Torah—the Torah of life—we must always elevate in holiness, the Yeshiva is growing and expanding. This is especially true in this recent period, due to the vital necessity of opening the doors of the Yeshiva wide for the new immigrants, for the immigrants from Morocco and others; bringing them into the Yeshiva is a matter of literal *hatzalas nefashos*, so that they should not be left outside, Heaven forbid. The command and mandate of the hour is to expand the place of the Yeshiva’s tent—the tent of Torah and the tent of tefillah—and to strengthen its foundations.

It is unnecessary to elaborate on the distress of the times, in which, due to our many sins, it is precisely in the halls of Torah and tefillah that the hardship prevails with greater intensity and force. And if we feel the pain of those who came before, how much more so must we feel the pain of those who come later—those who are knocking on the doors of the Yeshiva.

Therefore, the administration of Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim in Lod has been compelled to send a *shadar* to arouse our brethren, the Children of Israel, to come to the aid of the Yeshiva in this time of distress.

Relying on the statement of our Sages, "One only urges those who are already diligent," referring to those of our brethren, the Children of Israel, whose hearts are awake to Torah and its mitzvos,

I come to them in these lines with a double request and urging: to receive the Yeshiva’s *shadar* with the appropriate countenance and to contribute as the good hand of Hashem is upon them—in action and in deed, with their money and their efforts—to provide real and immediate assistance to Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim in Lod.

The greatness of the merit of supporting the Torah of the many is well known, and in particular, supporting the yeshivos and *talmudei torah* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, who stands and serves on high, bearing song and prayer on behalf of each and every one of those who participate in his holy work.

This participation is a channel and a vessel for the drawing down and receiving of the blessings of Hashem, in all that is needed, from soul to body. And everything is according to the abundance of the deed—with an increase in the vessels comes an increase in blessing and success.

With blessings for all that is good,

**M. Schneerson**

## 451

B"H, 7 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 5 Adar—the month in which we increase in joy—in which you write regarding your *hisorerus* for *teshuvah*, etc., and also write that you wish to atone through *ta'anisim* (fasts), you certainly mean this literally.

My opinion on this is as the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, writes: that in our generations, where fasting leads to illness or physical weakness, *chas v'shalom*, this is not the path of *teshuvah*. Rather, one must increase in learning and *davening* with a *minyan* as is proper, and especially in reciting *Tehillim*. Regarding *ta'anisim*, one should act in accordance with the instruction of the Rebbe Maharash: a *ta'anis* is an *avodah*—spend 15 minutes each day in deep introspection (*adei d'nafshi*) regarding oneself (see *Sefer HaToldos Admur Moharash*, Kehot Publication Society, 5707, Brooklyn, p. 72). Naturally, this contemplation is intended to lead to an increase in Torah and *mitzvos*.

It goes without saying that what is stated above regarding *ta'anisim* does not refer to those fasts which are *al pi Shulchan Aruch*, such as *Ta'anis Esther*, etc. Regarding those fasts, one must consult a Rav, who will issue a *psak* in accordance with one's health.

You should also give a few cents to *tzedakah* every weekday before *davening*, and keep up the three *shiurim* that are for everyone, established by the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory: *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*. 1) Recite the *shiur Tehillim* every day after *davening* in the morning, as *Tehillim* is divided according to the days of the month. 2) Study a *parsha* of *Chumash* with the commentary of Rashi from the *sedra* of the week every day (Sunday from the beginning of the *sedra* until *parshas sheni*, Monday from *parshas sheni* until *shlishi*, and so on). 3) Study a *shiur Tanya* every day, as the *Tanya* is divided according to the days of the year. May Hashem grant you success in all that is mentioned above.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe,
Secretary

## 451

B"H, 7 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 6 Shevat: Thank you for conveying regards to your fellow *chassidim*—may they live and be well. Surely you do not content yourself with mere greetings, but rather inspire them toward greater closeness, which is achieved through matters of Torah and *mitzvos*. These are what connect one Jew to another, as our Alter Rebbe explains in the holy *Tanya*, Chapter 32: that because bodies are separate, those who treat their bodies as primary and their souls as secondary cannot achieve true love and brotherhood; their connection is only dependent on something else, etc. (see there). This is especially true when the *yetzer hara* intervenes through self-importance and self-assertion, which explains how things contrary to love end up overriding the very thing that should foster love. This is in contrast to when one contemplates how the soul of a Jew is literally a part of Hashem from above, and that we all have one Father because the root of our souls is in the One Hashem. We simply need to strengthen our connection to Hashem, our G-d, through Torah and *mitzvah*, which is the straight and easy path to fulfilling the *mitzvah* of "love for every Jewish soul," from the greatest to the smallest. May it be Hashem’s will that your words emerge from the heart, and consequently, they will enter the hearts of those who hear them.

Regarding your question: You were previously engaged in studies, then stopped, and now the desire to study them again has been awakened in you. You ask whether you should fulfill this desire and which subjects you should choose. However, you do not clarify: 1) Since you have much *avodah* before you to influence your friends and your surroundings in general to bring them closer to Torah and *mitzvos*—which surely requires great exertion of the soul, *hisbonenus*, and depth—will there actually be free time for other matters beyond what is required for the success of these activities, which are the increase and elevation in the study of *nigleh* and *Chassidus* and the performance of *mitzvos*? 2) Even if you could, with difficulty, find free time from the aforementioned without it detracting from the success of your activities, in order to answer your question, one must clarify what the purpose is: whether it is to receive a certificate or diploma that could be used to expand your livelihood later on, or merely to increase your general knowledge. The attitude toward and the answer to your question depend on this.

With blessings for success and for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

Secretary

## 4152*

B"H, 7 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 3rd, in which you write regarding your son, shlita.

...Regarding his attire, it is understandable that her husband, the Rav, is correct in his argument: the more his attire remains as it was previously, this in itself will **diminish** the tests he faces, since by virtue of his attire, he will not encounter, or at the very least will not encounter as frequently, undesirable youth.

Regarding his daily schedule, one must strive as much as possible for him to study holy subjects in a *chavrusa*. This is both so that the learning will be more enduring and less difficult for him, and also so that he will not be in isolation. In general, one should endeavor to involve him in activities among the most *chareidi* youth—whether by arranging Shabbos parties, or by having him organize a class of children younger than him to study holy subjects, accompanied by stories of *yiras shamayim* and the like. This will inspire him to strive to be an example in all these matters, and at the same time, it will reduce his times of isolation. Surely, without difficulty, one can find such children, including students from schools who are free after the afternoon hours, and the like.

With blessings for Chassidic *nachas* from your son and for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 453

B"H, 8 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter—which does not indicate the time it was written—in which you write regarding the trait of *zerizus* (alacrity) and the trait of *tokef hada'as* (strength of mind), which you feel are not as they should be:

Regarding the trait of *zerizus*, you should study *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah* by our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, which is the second part of the *Tanya Kadisha*. Following this, you should contemplate what is stated in the *Tur, Orach Chayim* at the beginning, which is also cited by the *Rema* there: that a person’s manner of sitting, his movements, and his affairs when he is alone in his home are not the same as when he is before a great king, etc. If this is true in the Diaspora, it is certainly true in our Holy Land—may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu—for it is not the same to be before a great king when the king is in the field as when he is in his royal palace. After contemplating this for a long time on one occasion, then, whenever you need to strengthen your *zerizus*, you should remind yourself of the main points of this contemplation—in the language of the Alter Rebbe in the beginning of his *Siddur*. Through this, you will remember Hashem standing over you, and you will arise (from your sluggishness) with *zerizus*.

Regarding *tokef hada'as*, you should study *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Vayikra* at the beginning (page 1a), regarding the concept that a person’s (the Supernal) messenger is like him. Contemplate this, and by honoring the *mitzvos*—which are his messengers—you will also be strengthened in *da'as Torah* and *da'as mitzvos*.

Regarding the order of study in *Toras HaChassidus*, you should detail the specifics to the elders of *anash* in your vicinity; they will instruct you accordingly, and you should follow their guidance, and you will be successful.

I trust you are keeping the three *shiurim* that are equal for every soul, established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zya*—the *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*—as is well known. In any event, you should keep them from now on.

With blessings.

## 153*

B"H, 8 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings,

In response to your letter, in which you write about the possibilities of finding employment in the United States as a teacher in a yeshiva or Talmud Torah, or as a shochet of poultry, a chazzan, and the like.

Now, although **in general**, those who come here eventually find their place, it is understood that it is impossible to know how long it will take until one is settled, or whether the nature of that position will be satisfactory. This is especially true for a family man who must settle down relatively quickly, and consequently cannot be selective or wait for an extended period. Here, as in any place, personal connections are also a factor, since in general, the number of candidates exceeds the available and ready positions. If you have acquaintances here who know you personally, it is worthwhile to turn to them and ask for their assessment—based on their knowledge of you and your talents—as to which profession and which location would be easiest for you to settle into.

After all that has been said above, since you are currently in a place where there are very few who can act regarding the preservation and dissemination of Yiddishkeit, and on the other hand, with the appropriate energy it is certainly possible to organize a group of youth and children to be raised with a kosher education (and perhaps even more than that), it requires great consideration whether one should flee from the battlefield—especially since your material and spiritual livelihood are, for the time being, provided for in your current location.

In connection with this, I am interested in knowing the state of Yiddishkeit in Manila, and I would appreciate detailed information regarding this.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 454

B"H, 9 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Adar—the month in which we increase in joy—in which you write regarding the matter of the ingathering of the exiles, the gathering of all the tribes of Israel, and regarding what is said, "Assemble yourselves," and from this you arrive at several conclusions; in response to them:

1) We have nothing but this Torah. Before approaching any action, one must clarify the rulings of the holy Torah to determine if it falls under the category of obligation, or conversely, if it is forbidden, or if it is a matter of optional conduct. This is the touchstone for one’s approach to these activities, specifically regarding what you wrote concerning the non-Jewish Japanese nation and various inquiries regarding their origins, etc.

It is simple that according to the Shulchan Aruch, the laws regarding non-Jews are established, including all their details. From this, it is also understood that all the definitions and conduct prescribed in the Shulchan Aruch regarding the acceptance of converts—and certainly regarding efforts to proselytize—apply to them. From this, the simple conclusion is that there is no place for the activities you write about, and certainly—Heaven forbid—one should not suggest that this would hasten the Geulah, etc.

2) Regarding your inquiry into the delay of our Geulah, it is astonishing to search for hidden reasons and forced explanations, when our Sages of blessed memory have already stated explicitly (Sanhedrin 97b) that all the appointed times have passed, and the matter depends solely on teshuvah and good deeds. As the great teacher, our master the Rambam, states (Hilchos Teshuvah, Chapter 7, Halacha 5): The Torah has **promised** that the Jewish people will eventually do teshuvah at the end of their exile, and they will be redeemed immediately. Instead of searching for ways to influence the Japanese nation, every individual should utilize their strengths and abilities to bring the Children of Israel back in teshuvah. It is not the study that is the main thing, but the action—that they should increase in actual practice in their daily lives, especially all those who are in the land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year.

3) It is also understood that since all of Israel is one complete stature, as it is written, "You are standing today, **all of you**—your heads, etc.—to the drawer of your water," every person who increases within their own four cubits in the study of Torah and the performance of mitzvos with hiddur, automatically adds vitality to the entire stature, similar to the physical human body.

4) Just as in the physical human body, the more the revelation of the soul's vitality increases, the more the health of the body is perfected, so too—and even to a greater degree—as one increases in the "soul of the Torah" through the study of the inner dimensions of Torah and by following its guidance and customs, this adds to the "body of the Torah," and through this, to the body of the Jewish person as well. Elaborating on this simple matter is unnecessary.

With blessings for good tidings very soon, to one who conducts propaganda with the necessary energy for the strengthening of Yiddishkeit and its mitzvos wherever his hand can reach,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 4155

4155

B"H, 11 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent in communal needs, etc.,
Moreinu HaRav Shlomo Yosef [Zevin] shlita,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from the first of the month of "increasing in joy" and the one preceding it.

Regarding what was recorded in the transcript of the sicha of 19 Kislev 5715, that Tosafos in Bechoros discusses that a spring purifies only when it is flowing (zochalin) — this is indeed as you write, that my intent was to Tosafos Bechoros 55b, where two opinions appear (unlike Tosafos Shabbos 65b, which cites the opinion of Rabbeinu Yitzchak simply). You are also correct in what you write regarding my words that the Bahag ruled this way; my intent was to what I wrote, that where a river is dammed, immersion is ineffective.

Regarding what you quote from the commentary Emek She'elah on the She'iltos, siman 96, os 13, which interprets the intent as being that there are not 40 se'ah* present: with all due respect to the Emek She'elah, this is not in the Bahag, not even as a hint. If the words of the Bahag concerned a specific river, perhaps with great difficulty one could interpret it this way, relying on the assumption that the river was known to be a small one. But the words of the Bahag are a general ruling, and it is impossible for a general ruling to omit the **primary** point, obviously.

Incidentally, it is recorded in my memory that I saw in some book that cites this ruling in the name of the Bahag, though I do not recall the name of the book at this moment. I also found in the sefer Mikveh Tahara that it is noted that the sefer Gedolei Tahara discusses this matter, but it is not at hand.

Regarding what I wrote in the aforementioned sicha concerning whether a single witness (eid echad) is believed in matters of prohibitions (issurin) or tumah: it seems there is an error in the transcript, for the discussion was that if Niddah is a matter of tumah, then one could not derive from there the law that a single witness is believed in matters of prohibitions, for we do not derive prohibitions from tumah. See on this matter the Atvan D'oraysa by Mahari Engel, klal 21, and in Yad Malachi, that we do not derive matters of prohibition from tumah...

What was recently published by Kehot has already been sent to you, and as I recall, it was in the package: the Tzemach Tzedek’s additions to Maseches Bava Metzia, the Kovetz Lubavitch (two booklets), and more...

With blessings for a happy Purim and to extend that joy throughout the entire year.

#### ***4155***

*) And I believe the proofreader of the Warsaw edition of the Bahag also says this.

## 456

456

B"H, 11 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the honorable Rabbi, G-d-fearing, etc., R' Shaul Dovid, may he live,
HaKohen

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the 3rd of the month of *Marbin B'Simcha*. Regarding what you wrote concerning the study of Torah for girls, in response to my mentioning our custom—based on the words of our Sages in *Berachos* 17a—to bless girls as well, "for Torah, for *chuppah*, and for *maasim tovim*," [a custom] from the Rebbe (Rashab) *n'e*.

It is well known how precise the words of our Sages are in general, and the Nesi'ei Yisrael in their instructions to the public in particular. Seemingly, one must analyze why the proof for this was brought specifically from the words of our Sages in *Berachos*, and not from other *sugyos* in the *Shas*, particularly those *sugyos* that touch upon the *halacha* where the merit of Torah is discussed.

This can be understood by first noting that, according to all opinions, women must know the actions they are to perform and those they are not to perform—meaning the *halachos* of all the *mitzvos lo saaseh* (negative commandments), and the *mitzvos asei* (positive commandments) where women are equated to men, etc. (See also *Tur Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim*, section 47, regarding the obligation of women to know the Torah, and the commentaries there).

See also the *Hilchos Talmud Torah* of our Alter Rebbe, end of chapter 1: "Women are obligated to learn the *halachos* that they need to know, etc." However, this study is not the *mitzvah* of *Talmud Torah* itself, but rather a preparation for the *mitzvah* of fulfilling the laws. One could attribute many *sugyos* in the *Shas* to this, including those passages you mention in your letter regarding study for girls, etc. But there is no proof from there to say to a girl, "for Torah, for *chuppah*, and for *maasim tovim*," since that is included under *maasim tovim*, and one should not emphasize Torah specifically, as is understood. This is unlike the proof from *Berachos*: "Through what do women merit? Through sending [their children] to learn... through waiting [for their husbands]... and through guarding [their husbands' Torah study]..." This is a participation and a merit in the *mitzvah* of *Talmud Torah* itself, and it is therefore logical to say to a girl also, "**for Torah**, for *chuppah*, and for *maasim tovim*."

With this, the language of the Alter Rebbe in his *Shulchan Aruch* (there) and his *Siddur* is also clarified: "A woman is not included in the *mitzvah* of *Talmud Torah*, etc. Nevertheless, if she helps her son or her husband, etc., she shares the reward **with them**, etc." This is unlike a woman who studied Torah, etc., as she is not commanded [in it], etc. "Nevertheless, women are also obligated to learn the *halachos* that they need to know, etc."

See there. And based on the above, the question you raised is also removed: how can women perform *shechitah* if they are required to learn the laws? For this study is permitted (and is indeed an obligation for women, as stated above).

Regarding your note on our *nusach* in the *Mi Sheberach* for a woman, to say "**in all** her limbs," and your adding to this the point that the *Hamorrim* (the curses) have the *gematria* of twice 248 (his and hers), and that they resolve this by saying that those limbs which do not become *tamei* are not included in the count; and you also note from *Shu"t Elef Lecha Shlomo* to say 248 because a woman is only blessed through what the man has.

Our *nusach* is understood and explained well, because while regarding a curse (*Hamorrim*) one should minimize as much as possible, the opposite is true regarding a blessing, where one should detail and add as much as possible. As for what is written in the aforementioned *Shu"t* that a woman is only blessed through what the man has, this requires study; for since she has additional limbs, it is understood that there should also be an additional blessing.

Incidentally, someone asked me why we say "**in all** her limbs" and not "251." But the answer is simple: in the *Gemara* *Bechoros* 45a, there are several opinions regarding the number of a woman's limbs, and therefore we say "in all her limbs" to include the opinion of everyone.

With respect and a double blessing for the birth of your daughter, that you may raise her for Torah, for *chuppah*, and for *maasim tovim*.

With blessings.

## 459

In response to your letter informing me that you have secured a position as a shochet in the city of... and that you are so preoccupied with this that you do not have enough time to attend to the needs of the community—even though you are certain that several matters there require correction—and that you also have no time for learning or for the avodah of the Creator, as you write in your letter.

When one begins to act, even if it seems that there is no time, it becomes clear within a short period that the ability and possibility exist, and as time goes on, they increase. Since acting for the sake of others is also a positive commandment from the Torah, as it is written, "And you shall love your neighbor as yourself," and "You shall surely rebuke your neighbor," all that has been said applies also to correcting the matters of...

With blessings for good tidings in all that has been mentioned,

## 4162

4162

B"H, 16 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your inquiry regarding my opinion concerning the issue that has come to the fore in recent months on the agenda of the Rabbis in the United States, namely:

Is it permissible for those who observe Torah and mitzvos to participate in organizations that include rabbis who serve as representatives of the Reform or Conservative movements—whether participating as individuals (such as in the New York Board of Rabbis and the like), or participating as organizations (such as the Synagogue Council)? As is known, the arguments of those who favor it and those who oppose it have been publicized by them on various occasions and have also been printed in the newspapers.

In response to the above: In recent weeks, the question and the issue have intensified and taken on a new dimension, in that the general public—and especially the young rabbis and the Jewish youth in the United States in general—have begun to take a special interest in this question. Their perspective is that the resolution of this question and the halachic ruling regarding it is not merely a ruling concerning participation in one organization or another, but rather a ruling regarding the attitude toward the Reform and Conservative movements in general. That is:

Are the aforementioned rabbis—meaning the standard-bearers and representatives of these movements—merely "lenient rabbis," as opposed to the Chareidi rabbis who are "stringent," or—

Does the law accord with the Rambam (Hilchos Teshuvah 3:8): "One who says that the Torah is not from Hashem, even one verse or even one word, if he says that Moshe said it from his own mouth, he is a denier of the Torah; and similarly, one who denies its interpretation, which is the Torah Sheba'al Peh, even a grammatical nuance, etc."

Based on this, it is understood that anyone who has the ability to influence the course of events—and all the more so regarding the instruction and the ruling on this matter, and the phrasing of that ruling—must know and clearly recognize the situation and the consequences involved. That is, this is a question that touches upon the relationship of thousands and tens of thousands of Yidden to the fundamentals of the faith, and the illusory gains about which some write and speak carry no weight in a question of this nature.

And let this be known: Those who wish to find room for doubt, or at the very least for opposition that is not as forceful as required, by claiming that they are not judging the essential question of the fundamental attitude toward the Conservative or Reform movements—this makes no difference at all regarding the instruction, the ruling, and its most absolute phrasing. For the general public and a certain segment of the rabbis will not be interested in the justifications, reasons, and explanations; rather, they will ask for the decision—whether it is for approval or for absolute rejection.

May it be the will of the Ribono shel Olam that, in accordance with our current time, the time of the end, many will be purified, clarified, and refined, to distinguish between the Torah of the words of the living Elokus and the schemes of men.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 463

B"H, 16 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and elevated Mr. Yaakov Yehoshua, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

In due time, I received the news regarding the *shloshim* and the *azkarah* that were held for his father, the late Rabbi Chananya Gavriel, of blessed memory, may his soul be bound in the bond of life. This served as proof that you properly appreciated the deceased, of blessed memory.

I read with spiritual satisfaction that you are taking an interest in the manuscripts left behind by your father, the Rabbi, of blessed memory, which, as you write, are already organized and prepared. Regarding the core question of whether they are suitable for publication and which publishing house could bring the book to light: there are many Rabbis and *morei hora'ah* in Jerusalem to whom the writings should be shown, so they may judge whether the manuscripts are ready for print as they are, or if they still require preparation and refinement, etc. If their opinion is positive, then naturally, such books should be printed immediately in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, for several reasons.

I will take the liberty of adding a personal note, in accordance with the way you wrote regarding the manuscripts and the work invested in them. My hope is that you, together with your brother, may he live and be well, whom you mention, will continue in this direction. I refer not only to the technical aspect regarding the publication of the manuscripts, but also to studying them. This is certainly the author’s primary intent: study in the manner that our Sages, of blessed memory, taught us in their famous statement, "Great is study, for it leads to action." And as our Sages, of blessed memory, stated (*Bava Basra* 116a), "Regarding David, who left behind a son like himself, it is not said that he died." It is surely unnecessary to elaborate on this idea, and there is nothing that can stand before the will—especially when the merit of his ancestors assists you.

With blessings for the improvement of health for his mother, may she live and be well, and success in all that has been mentioned for you and your brother, may he live and be well.

With respect and blessing.

## 4167

4167

B”H, 18 Adar, 5716

Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from some time ago, in which you write regarding the differences of opinion that existed at...

It has already been explained in many places that matters of the past relate to issues of reward and punishment, and as far as the subject himself is concerned—to the avodah of teshuvah. My concern is to be a shaliach to arouse each and every one to utilize all the strengths and opportunities granted to him by Divine Providence to fulfill his role in the present and the future—his spiritual and inner role—as the Mishnah says, “I was created to serve my Maker.” Consequently, what interests me is his conduct in the present and the future: whether it aligns with what was written above—that he is doing everything in his power to disseminate the wellsprings outward, the most direct path for which is within the framework of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad. Especially since those who engage in this are few. It appears that in connection with the upheavals of the past, there is a need for strengthening and an addition of energy, and a word to the wise is sufficient. May it be the will of Hashem that in your return mail you will bring good news regarding all of this—that is, regarding your own activities and regarding the activities of each member of the group. And you should encourage the administration to get into the habit of writing about what is being done by Tzeirei Agudas Chabad frequently, for the very knowledge that the time for writing is approaching has the power to stir up one’s strengths and increase vigor, as is evident in a tangible way.

And lastly, regarding your notification of the engagement of your brother... may he be well, with his bride... may she live, and subsequently of the setting of the wedding date (and surely my letter of response regarding this to your brother, may he live and be well, has already been received), may it be the will of Hashem that their building be an everlasting edifice, a Chassidishe home, and may Hashem grant him success to always report only good news.

With blessings of Mazal Tov,

**M. Schneerson**

## 4168

B”H, 18 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Tuesday, in which you write regarding the state of your health and specifically concerning the condition of your heart.

It is a well-known teaching of our Sages that the 248 positive mitzvos correspond to the 248 limbs, and the 365 negative mitzvos correspond to the 365 sinews. The content of this teaching is that the physical body of a Jewish person—its affairs and its health in general—is dependent upon its spiritual counterpart; that is, upon one’s standing and situation regarding the performance of positive mitzvos and the observance of negative mitzvos. However, because we find ourselves in a world that, by the will of the Creator of the world, was created at the lowest level—meaning, in a physical form, where its conduct appears to the physical eye to be governed by nature—there must be an anchoring in nature for many things and matters. From this, it is understood that even though, in general, one must follow the instructions of a physician, in accordance with the statement of our Sages that “the Torah gave permission to the physician to heal,” one must simultaneously keep the truth before one’s eyes at all times: that the Creator of the world is the One who brings into being, sustains, and gives life to each and every created being. This is especially true for the children of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov, of whom it is said, “You are children to Hashem your G-d.” Since He—the Ribono shel Olam—is the essence of good, and it is the nature of the good to bestow good, there is no place for worry, Heaven forbid. One’s avodah can be carried out with great and genuine joy.

All these things apply to you as well. It is proper that your heart be confident, for your heart is awake to Hashem, to His Torah, and to His mitzvos, and consequently, you will surely live long and pleasant years. However, in order to increase the blessings of the Ribono shel Olam and your success, you should increase in tzedakah toward others—tzedakah in the literal sense, with your money, and tzedakah in its deeper sense—through the exertion of your body and by influencing others to bring them closer to Torah and mitzvos. And there is nothing that can stand in the way of the will.

It is understood that you may write to me whenever you find the time or the need. May the Ribono shel Olam grant you merit and success so that the content of your letters may be joyful, both in spiritual and in physical matters.

With blessings for good tidings in all that was mentioned,

**M. Schneerson**

You should be in *simcha* and learn according to the *yeshiva* schedule, and in your free time, you should also engage in influencing others—but this, too, must be done with *simcha*. It goes without saying that you must follow the instructions of the doctors treating you. May Hashem grant you success in all of the above and may you share good news.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 172

172

B”H, 19 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the end of the month of Teves (which was in transit longer than usual), in which you write the details of your life, your current state of health, and also the state of health of your wife, tichyeh.

In accordance with your request, both of you will be mentioned at the Tziyun HaKadosh of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for an improvement in health—both in gashmius and in ruchnius. For among Yidden, gashmius and ruchnius go hand in hand; the only difference is that health in gashmius is granted by Hashem Yisbarach, while regarding health in ruchnius, Hashem Yisbarach desires that one should desire and act upon it oneself, as Hashem Yisbarach says: “See, I have set before you today life and good... therefore choose life” (Devarim 30:15). This means that one should do as much as possible in the areas of Torah and mitzvos, and also influence one’s children to do the same, and Hashem Yisbarach will grant His blessing and success to fulfill this requirement. And there is nothing that can stand before the will. It is self-understood that Hashem Yisbarach rewards many times over all those who act in this regard.

Regarding your health specifically, it appears that this is primarily a nervous matter. Therefore, you must completely divert your mind from the whole thing and strengthen yourself in bitachon in the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders, the Creator of the world and its Guide. If you do so, the attacks about which you write will become less frequent.

Surely you are aware of the three daily shiurim instituted by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which are appropriate for every soul: 1) Reciting a portion of Tehillim every day after davening, according to the monthly division of Tehillim; 2) Studying a portion of Chumash with Rashi’s commentary every day from the weekly parsha—Sunday from the beginning of the parsha until the second aliyah, Monday from the second aliyah until the third, and so on; 3) Studying a daily shiur of Tanya, according to the annual division of the Tanya. In any case, you should keep these shiurim from now on and moving forward. May Hashem Yisbarach grant you success.

With the blessing of a kosher and happy Pesach,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 173

173

B"H, 19 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your [letter] from the middle of Shevat (which took longer than usual to arrive). I hope that by the time you receive this letter, your health has improved and you have already returned to working in communal affairs with the necessary energy. This is especially true as it is the necessity of the hour: every Jew who is gifted with a feeling for Yiddishkeit must have an *ayin tovah* regarding others and help them understand that *Yisrael, Oraisa, v’Kudsha Brich Hu* are all one.

Regarding your personal matters, this is *b’machel she-kein v’kal v’chomer*: The law is that those who are *oseik b’tzorchei tzibur b’emunah* are, at that time, exempt from other *mitzvos* and Torah study. It is therefore certain that the *Ribono shel Olam* will relieve you of the burdens of material concerns. This is also one of the *segulos* for improving one’s material *parnassah*, ensuring that your *parnassah* and other matters are free from anything that causes confusion.

Surely you utilized the days of Purim. As it is written in the *Megillah*, "many of the people of the land became Jews" (*misyahadim*). One of the allusions in this is that those who, until Purim, were "people of the land"—meaning they occupied themselves only with worldly matters—became "Jews" (*Yehudim*). According to the exposition of our Sages, Israel is called *Yehudim* because they deny *avodah zarah*. The inner meaning of this is that in **every** thing, one seeks—and consequently finds—Divinity. For one who says there is a place empty of Him is a matter of *shtei rashuyos* (two authorities), which is a form of *avodah zarah*. *V’doche*.

With blessings for health, good news, and *hatzlachah* in all your affairs.

## 176

176

B.H., 21 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the illustrious Torah scholar, the G-d-fearing Chossid, who engages in the study of Chassidus,
R. Ephraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, regarding what you inquired: In *Torah Or*, *Parshas Terumah* (71a), in the *dibur hamaschil* "Aval," in the parenthetical note there regarding the time of *galus*, that the aspect of the illumination was withdrawn, etc., "to its root and its source in *Atzilus*," what is its root and what is its source?

This statement corresponds to the statement of the *Zohar*, that in *galus*, *Kudsha Brich Hu* ascends higher and higher. This has been explained in many places: *Kudsha Brich Hu*—*Ze'er Anpin* (the "small face" mentioned in *Torah Or* there); "higher"—*Binah*; and "higher"—*Atik*, which is *Keter*. This is understood based on what is explained in *Tikkunei Zohar*, *Tikkun* 49, that *Binah* is called the "root of the tree," and in *Ra'aya Mehemna*, *Parshas Bo* 42b, that *Keter* is called the "source" (see its explanation in *Likutei Torah*, *Vayikra* 52a). It can also be explained simply through the distinction between the terms "root" and "source," as it is understood that both are mentioned to indicate a difference in levels: the root is found in closer proximity and is of the essence of the matters that come from the root, whereas the source implies a greater distance from that which comes from the source.

Based on the above, that which is brought in the *sefer Gidulei Taharah*, *Responsa* at the end of the book, *Siman* 2, in explaining the names "pit" (*bor*) and "spring" (*ma'ayan*), and concluding that "source" (*makor*) is said regarding the power that is embedded, etc., will also be clarified—that the above corresponds to the order of the *Sefiros*: *Keter*, *Chochma*, and *Binah* are the source, spring, and pit, or the root.

Regarding the *Mishnah* at the beginning of *Megillah*, that when *Purim* falls on a Sunday, the villagers advance [the reading] to the "day of entry," the preceding Thursday—you raise a difficulty: according to the opinion that the reading of *Parshas Zachor* is a Torah obligation, the villagers have gathered anyway on *Erev Shabbos*, and if so, they could read the *Megillah* at its proper time. You did not specify your intent, but it seems you are troubled by the fact that since one must return "in good time"—meaning at the break of dawn—they are necessarily left in the city even after *Shabbos*.

Now, aside from the fact that it is possible for the villages to be in a situation where travel is permitted even on *Shabbos* via *Eruvei Techumin*, and furthermore, the matter of traveling "in good time" is merely good advice and not a rabbinic or Torah prohibition, it is also possible that they could leave the city before the *minyan* gathers for *tefillah*, and especially for the reading of the *Megillah*, the time for which is the entire day (see the *Ran* there, that the reading of the *Megillah* at night was excluded by the Sages). In any case, this observation is not necessarily dependent on the opinion that the reading of *Parshas Zachor* is from the Torah—for the *Krias HaTorah* on Mondays and Thursdays is a *takanas Ezra*, and the villagers are meticulous about it, as brought in many commentators that this is the concept of the "day of entry," that they gather for *Krias HaTorah*. If so, how much more so for the reading on *Shabbos*! It could be said that for *Shabbos*, they arrange for someone who knows [how to read] to come to the villages to fulfill their obligation (unlike weekdays, when the city dwellers are busy with their work). According to this, it is resolved how the villagers arranged the *Krias HaTorah* of *Shabbos*, which is more of an obligation than the reading of Monday and Thursday: for it is obvious that one cannot say that every single *Shabbos* all the villagers (and certainly not for *Parshas Zachor*) would gather in the city to hear the *Krias HaTorah*!

With blessings.

Due to a reason, the sending of the letter was delayed. On *Erev Rosh Chodesh*, before the trip to the *Ohel*, your letter from *Motzaei Shabbos* was received, and I mentioned there the names of the *Bnei Yisrael* whom you mentioned. May it be the will [of Hashem] that it be at a time of favor (*be'eis ratzon*) and with success.

***

 See regarding all this: *Zohar Chadash* 75, *Ra'aya Mehemna* and *Matok MiDvash* there. *Pardes*, *Sha'ar Erech HaKinuyim*, entry *Oy* and entry *Hoy*. The supplement to the *Reshimot* of the *Tzemach Tzedek* on *Tehillim* at its beginning. And see also *Zohar Chadash* 20b.

 According to what is written in *Tosafos*, *dibur hamaschil* "Yichnas" (beginning of *Pesachim*)—it is not [forbidden] for many people traveling on a known path, like the travel of the villagers who are accustomed to travel on this path every "day of entry."
