## 4178

4178

B”H, 22 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter of 8 Adar, in which you write regarding your livelihood situation and your claim to... which naturally leads to the opinion that you should leave your position there, etc.

Regarding this: I have already written to several of anash, and surely you have also seen at least one of those letters, that the time has come when the truth must not be concealed. For all those who have merited to take part in the institutions or activities of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, one should not have to beg them. It is one of two things: either they themselves recognize that this is for their own benefit, or—if they are unwilling to admit this and hold to the opinion that they are doing a favor for my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and through him to all our holy Nesi’im, and through them to the Ribono shel Olam and His entourage—then even moralizing will not help. Although the great pity one feels for them is understandable, and this too falls under the category of "you shall surely rebuke," everything has a limit, especially in this era of ours, where every moment is precious for action.

And if even the young in years, or those who did not merit to be educated within the walls of Tomchei Temimim, require pampering and coddling—as explained in the Rambam’s Commentary on the Mishnah and cited in Chassidus regarding the education of a child—then for those who did merit to study in Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim and have become heads of Chassidic families in Yisrael, there is no benefit in moralizing and pampering. Trying to persuade them with words has no real utility, since after a short time they return to their original opinion, and there is no end to the persuasion and coddling, all while the time could be utilized in a better way. Furthermore, the work they do between one complaint and the next lacks the true taste and appearance...

In any event, one must say the truth as it is. The intention here is that perhaps they will begin to try and look at the other person, realizing that he, too, possesses the ten kochos hanefesh, including Chochma, Binah, and Da’as. On the other hand, they also have their own middos shebalev, which can become emotionally charged and cloud their intellect. Consequently, there is room to say that sometimes one is mistaken and his colleagues are correct, and the only test for this is the instruction that we follow the majority. After one contemplates this for a time appropriate to his soul’s nature, and it becomes a matter of his own personal realization and inner conviction, he will surely begin to see with his own eyes what is written: "Its ways are ways of pleasantness, and all its paths are peace," and he will naturally cooperate in these matters with the rest of anash...

Once again, I repeat what was said before: no one is holding him back from the avodah of the Rebbe, nor are they holding back anyone else. But on the other hand, one feels an immense amount of pity for them—even more so because they have apparently lived for decades in error, saying that they are doing a favor for our holy Nesi’im, rather than the reverse. Naturally, the results of such an attitude toward the avodah are understandable. Therefore, it is incumbent upon you, as it is upon everyone, to try to explain the truth to yourselves once, twice, and several times over. May it be the will of Hashem that they choose the better portion...

With the blessing of a kosher and happy Pesach,

On behalf of the Rebbe Shlita,
Secretary

## 479

B"H, 24 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, involved in communal needs,
R' Shmuel Menachem Mendel, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter in which you write that you have found a suitable house for yourselves and have submitted an application as is customary in such matters:

May it be the will of Hashem that this be a beginning in a good and auspicious hour, and may it be completed in the best possible way, in a manner that is good, visible, and revealed for you and for your entire family, may they live.

It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding the matters of *hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah* (spreading the wellsprings of Chassidus outward), the activities of *anash* in London in general, and your own and your wife’s activities in particular. I am certain you will fill this in at the next opportunity, with the necessary details.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach, and for good tidings regarding all that was mentioned, as well as regarding your mother-in-law, may she live and be well.

Your previous letter was received in due time. It is obvious that one must speak with others about the necessity of studying *Chassidus* (Torah Or/Likutei Torah), for from a lack of speech, there will certainly be no results. However, it is also obvious that the speech must be with pleasant words, tailored to the personal level of Torah and *mitzvos* of each individual listener.

Why the study of *Chassidus* is specifically more necessary now is explained in many places. A point that is relevant and easily understood by everyone: when a new illness, G-d forbid, breaks out in the world, or an old illness intensifies, it is necessary to increase the medication. And even for the healthy—if the illness is contagious, and regarding **everyone**, our Sages said, "Do not trust in yourself."

Why, in our times, the study of Polish *Chassidus* is not at all sufficient is understood from the above: the medicine must be appropriate for the illness. And since the latter is now primarily dependent on intellectual debate and analysis, the medicine must also be through a matter that will occupy and captivate the intellect and the *Chabad* (Chochma, Binah, Da'as) within the soul. And this is easy to understand.

#### ***479***

**R' Shmuel Menachem Mendel, may he live:** Librov, London. Additional letters to him—above, Vol. 9, 2759, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 482

482

By the Grace of Hashem, 25 Adar, 5716
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the chairmen, activists, and participants in the 14th annual campaign for Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in Montreal,
May they live,

Shalom u’vracha!

I was pleased to receive the news regarding the annual dinner event that is scheduled to take place, G-d willing, on Tuesday, Rosh Chodesh Nissan—the month of the Yom Tov of our liberation, **Zman Cheiruteinu**, which is so closely connected with **Zman Matan Torateinu**.

Every event occurs through Hashgacha Pratis, especially a Torah-related undertaking for such an important institution as the Lubavitcher Yeshiva in Montreal. I hope that the timing will add a special significance to this event, which is already of such supreme importance in its own right.

In our times, when Torah-Judaism in general finds itself constrained by various "Mitzrayim and Gevulim" (limitations and boundaries)—apathy and ignorance on one side, and false ideas and opinions on the other—Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch creates not only a "Goshen" within Mitzrayim, but it is also a secure preparation for the liberation from the spiritual "Galus Mitzrayim" of our time.

The Lubavitcher Yeshiva, with its specific character of instilling in and permeating its students with the spirit of mesiras nefesh for Torah and Yiddishkeit, and with a deep sense of responsibility for the surrounding environment—both while they are still in the Yeshiva and especially when they go out into life—is a Divine blessing for a city.

I hope that the Jews of Montreal in general, and the activists and supporters of the Yeshiva in particular, will correctly appreciate their great obligation and the extraordinary zechus of having a part in Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch. I hope they will increase their efforts and support many times over, to give the Yeshiva—their Yeshiva—the possibility not only to maintain its existence, but also to grow and develop, as is the nature of every living thing, and as Chazal have ordained: **"We elevate in matters of holiness."**

May everyone act in this with the appropriate dedication and energy, and the event will surely be successful, and will bring blessing and success to each and every one and their families, may they live, in all that they need, both in gashmius and in ruchnius.

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding what you wrote—that you do not see results from your activities, etc.—it is impossible that this is so, since our holy Nesi'im have informed us that it is a certainty that "propaganda does not return empty." It is certainly possible that the results could be greater, but it has already been said, "Little by little I will drive them out," etc. The main thing is that even regarding the results that do exist, the Yetzer Hara strives to minimize them in one's eyes and conceal them, in the hope that perhaps through this, one will be weakened in his holy work.

From this it is understood that, on the contrary, one must increase his efforts beyond the current measure. "One action is better than a thousand sighs." And this is also the case regarding one's own avodah; see also Tanya, Chapter 26 and onwards.

I was very, very pleased with what you wrote regarding the progress of the avreich... and this, too, is conclusive proof of the above...

Although I will not deny that there is pain in the matter, and also bewilderment, as it is written: "They made me a keeper of the vineyards" (meaning that the Torah testifies that these are vineyards in need of work, yet it laments) "but my own vineyard I have not kept." This is truly the case regarding you and several others, who do not work at all in the vineyard of Chabad (and when they did begin, they ceased working after a short time due to strange reasons), even though in ordinary vineyards they do work and are satisfied, and to the wise, a word is sufficient.

I was pleased by what you wrote regarding the lecture before the N'shei U'Bnos Chabad. Certainly, in the future, this will be continued and even increased. Since our Sages of blessed memory said, "A person should always study in the place that his heart desires," it is all the more so that regarding women, one must arrange the lectures and the study in a way that interests them; then, after a short time, it will be possible to deepen the subjects and expand upon them.

As we approach the festival of Pesach, which is coming upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, may you celebrate it with your family, may they live, in purity and in joy.

## 192

B"H, 1 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...As is known, when there is a conflict, it is impossible that there is not some measure of fault even on the side that is correct in the dispute. This is especially true since the issue at hand is not so much about arguing and pointing fingers to show that so-and-so is to blame for this detail and so-and-so is to blame for that detail. Since the matter concerns the development of the institution and the effort invested in it, as long as the institution is not developing **as much** as is required, then all members of the administration are at fault for this. This is understood and explained even further based on the statement in Tikkunei Zohar, cited in Chassidic discourse, that if there were one tzaddik who would do teshuvah as required, the Geulah would come immediately. How much more so, then, that an improvement in the situation by anyone involved in a joint endeavor brings about a "geulah" within that shared project. There is no need to elaborate on something that is clearly visible and understood by the intellect.

Surely you will arrange for the distribution of the shemurah—in addition to the sale of the shemurah—in accordance with the sicha on this topic from a few years ago. May it be His will that the matters of "food of healing" and "food of faith" be drawn down for the entire year, in all their four amos.

And in anticipation of the festival of Pesach, which is approaching us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, may he and his entire household, may they live, celebrate it in kashrus and in joy.

With blessings.

## 493

B"H, 1 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn

Mrs. Meri, may she live,

Blessings and peace!

After a hiatus, I was pleased to receive your letter of 9 Adar, in which you write regarding the possibility of a fund from which a prize would be distributed each year to an outstanding student.

It is self-understood that such a thing can be arranged. However, it is also understood that this is not a matter of a scholarship, but rather an incentive fund. In this regard, it is not possible to determine the sum of money, as that depends on the person who wishes to establish such a thing (the size of the sum for this purpose, how much should be distributed each year, and to how many people). Once you select one of the possibilities mentioned above, I believe that we will be able to bring this to fruition in one of the Chabad educational institutions in our Holy Land or in Morocco.

I have not written to you about this previously because, among Jews, the distribution of such prizes is not a common occurrence. Although one is not opposed to it, one has also not encouraged such things. Certainly, one of the reasons for this is the consideration that learning in the yeshivos is connected with kedushah—holiness; one did not want to suggest the aforementioned, so as not to emphasize that this is being done—by the students—for the sake of monetary gain or other material benefits. However, in recent years, many yeshivos, especially in Eretz Yisrael, have begun to introduce such things (not through monetary prizes, but through frequent gifts of seforim).

You do not write any details regarding your health, so I hope that it was only a passing matter, and that today you feel even better and will be able to spend the Yom Tov of Pesach in a fitting manner.

With a wish for good news regarding all that was said above, and especially regarding good health.

## 194

B"H, 1 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent in communal needs, R' Moshe Tzvi, may he live.

And if this is the case in the Diaspora, how much more so in the Land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year. Certainly, for one of your stature, elaboration on this is superfluous; I have written these lines only to fulfill the teaching of our Sages that "one only urges those who are already diligent," and it is only necessary to encourage further effort, as mentioned above. May it be the will of Hashem that you succeed in raising students who are G-d-fearing, who study Torah in purity, and who fulfill mitzvos with hiddur.

## 495

B”H, 1 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs, R’ Eliezer, may he live:

Shalom u’Bracha!

It is surprising to hear that your letter from 1 Adar was not received at all.

Regarding what you wrote in your letter from Rosh Chodesh Adar mentioned above, and the one preceding it, concerning the agricultural school: It is understood that since you have entered the field of Chabad education, its spirit must be consistent with this. It is imperative that there be no difference in the conduct and way of life between a school for carpentry, the aforementioned, or a school for printing, G-d willing. I have already replied to this in my previous letter. Even if some students have left, it is obvious that one must not lower or diminish the standards of an educational institution for the sake of a few students—students who are not particular about matters that are contrary to the spirit of Chabad. Consequently, the matters you write about regarding them are ruled out. Rather, as with all Lubavitch conduct, matters must be handled in ways of pleasantness (without compromising). That is, one should not, G-d forbid, expel the students, but rather explain to them the negativity of these matters, and to what extent they are contrary to their own well-being, etc., etc.

And the main point—and this is unlike the approach of the *baalei mussar* who expand their explanations and spend the majority of their time, effort, and commentary on describing the bad—is that the primary effort and explanation should be in describing the superiority of the true good. And to put it simply, you must increase *farbrengens* with them (naturally, on matters appropriate to their level of understanding), involving Chabad stories, *nigunim*, etc., etc. (It is also understood that installing a radio in the school eliminates the possibility of prohibiting the use of radios in their rooms and sleeping quarters, where there is no guardian to ensure what they choose to listen to.)

Since you do not mention your health, I hope it has improved, and may it be Hashem’s will that it improves even further, for you, your wife, and all your household members, may they live.

In anticipation of the festival of Pesach, which is approaching us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, may you and all your household members, may they live, celebrate it with kashrus and joy.

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 496

496

B"H, 1 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter in which you write about the arrangements for the wedding, b’sha’ah tovah umutzlach, and the main points of your current planning. I am interested to hear in detail how you are managing for the upcoming Pesach, may it come upon us for good, and I am certain you will inform me of this as well.

Regarding what you wrote about your conduct: I do not approve at all of your fasting (until midday) on Mondays and Thursdays, etc., for this is not the way of Chassidus. Instead of afflicting the body, one must afflict the *nefesh habehamis*. The meaning of this is: do not compromise the health of the body by abstaining from the food and drink required for health; rather, replace this with the affliction of the *nefesh habehamis*—namely, by refraining from indulging desires in eating and drinking, by avoiding idle chatter, and certainly by avoiding any speech that borders on *lashon hara* or any forbidden speech. [Focus instead on] fulfilling the mitzvah of "love your fellow as yourself," even regarding a person whom you feel does not treat you with love, or who has even harmed you or offended your honor, etc., etc. These behaviors are sometimes harder to implement in practice than fasting from food and drink, and furthermore, they do not weaken one’s health, thereby preserving the ability to study Torah *shiurim* and fulfill *mitzvos* with *hiddur*, without being distracted by bodily concerns.

With blessings to hear good news regarding all that was mentioned, as well as good news regarding the activities of your wife, tichyeh, in strengthening Yiddishkeit—both for yourselves and for your surroundings—and for a kosher and happy Pesach.

With holiday blessings.

## 497

2 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To our brethren, the Children of Israel, and to the *askanim* of *chinuch* in particular, in every place—may Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

The festival of Pesach, the first *yom-tov* given to us, is connected specifically to the concept of *chinuch*, both for *Klal Yisrael* as a whole and for every individual Jew.

For *Klal Yisrael*—the Exodus from Egypt was their birth as a nation and the beginning of the preparation for *Kabbalas HaTorah*. Torah is, by definition, *horah*—instruction and education in a *derech hachaim*, a way of life and conduct.

For every individual Jew—the Torah specifically emphasizes: "And you shall tell your son" (*Vehigadta levincha*), the education of the child, which is one of the essential points of the *yom-tov* of Pesach.

Pesach is therefore an appropriate time to reflect on the methods and approaches of *chinuch*, and how this is carried out in practice, particularly regarding *yomim-tovim*.

*Yomim-tovim*, and Pesach in particular, are connected with many *dinim* and *minhagim*. Beyond their significance at the time they are performed, their influence must extend and permeate daily life throughout the entire year.

As important as this is for every Jew, the influence is even more vital for the youth and for children in particular.

In practice, however, due to various reasons, instead of the influence being strengthened and increased during the days of the *yom-tov*, the children and students—boys and girls—are released from the influence of the *yeshiva*, *yeshiva ketana*, and *talmud torah*, and not only for the days of the *yom-tov*, but also for a certain period beforehand.

In the "old country," the release of students during *bein hazmanim* did not have a harmful effect on their *chinuch*, because the street—and certainly the home—provided the child and the youth with a vibrant, warm atmosphere of *Yiddishkeit* and the observance of *mitzvos* in daily life to the fullest extent. The task of the educational institutions was primarily to provide the students with knowledge of Torah.

In our time, however, and especially in this country, the task of the educational institutions is not only to enrich the students' knowledge of Torah and *Yiddishkeit*, but, most importantly, to implant in them *yiras shamayim*, the observance of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*, and a Jewish way of life in general.

Thus, the severing of the influence of the educational institutions during the times of *bein hazmanim* and the days of *yom-tov* in particular, robs the students of a life-essential influence, and specifically at a time when they need to receive it in the greatest possible measure.

I am therefore turning to everyone who is involved or can be involved in *chinuch hakasher*, and to parents in general, to rectify this regrettable situation through appropriate measures. And most importantly:

a) To arrange that on *erev yom-tov*, or at the very least close to *yom-tov*, the children should once again receive the necessary instructions and guidance in the *dinim* and *minhagim* of the relevant *yom-tov*, and regarding its content and significance.

b) To arrange—which is absolutely necessary—that even during the days of *yom-tov*, at least during the days of *Chol HaMoed*, the *mechanchim* should meet with the children in an appropriate manner, in order to utilize these *yemei segulah* to strengthen the influence on the children in all matters connected with the *yom-tov* in general, and regarding practical application in particular.

Certainly, one can find ways and means to overcome the problems associated with distance or the dispersion of the children, for the gathering during *yom-tov* can be arranged not necessarily in the building of the educational institution. The technical structure of various classes, *mechanchim*, etc., is not as relevant here, because this concerns learning and guidance that can unite students from different classes, etc.

c) Parents should not rely entirely on the educational institutions, but should also take care from their side, recognizing that on one hand, the influence of the street is harmful, and on the other hand, the children have more free time during the days of *yom-tov* and *bein hazmanim*. Consequently, the responsibility of parents for the influence on their children is much greater at that time, but their opportunities are also much greater.

May the *Ribono shel Olam* help that all sons and daughters—all the children of the four types enumerated in the *Haggadah*—should be gathered together at one table with the goal of carrying out "the testimonies, the statutes, and the laws which Hashem our G-d has commanded us," and may they all be good *shoalim* (questioners), asking in order to know and to follow the true answer of the Torah.

And may the beginning of the *kibbutz galuyos*—gathering together at a Torah *seder* even the wayward children—also hasten the *aschalta d'geulah* and the *Geulah HaAmitit VeHaShleimah* through *Moshiach Tzidkeinu*, when the wish with which we begin the *seder* will be fulfilled: "This year we are slaves; next year may we be free men."

With the blessing of a *Chag Pesach Kasher VeSameach*,

**M. Schneerson**

## 198

198

B"H, 3 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...2) Regarding your question as to whether you should daven with your head covered by the tallis, given that in your shul this is not the custom and it will naturally draw attention—in my opinion, one should not overemphasize this. However, since you are the baal kriah, and also the one from whom they hear divrei hisorerus, etc., it will be understandable to them why you daven in this manner with the tallis covering your head, even though they have not yet reached that level themselves; and perhaps others will follow your example.

3) Regarding your question as to why, among the children of [Name], it was precisely the one who was less of a yirei shamayim who remained alive, while the yirei shamayim perished al kiddush Hashem—generally, regarding such questions, it is written: "Why do you inquire into the hidden things of the Merciful One?" One of the explanations found in sefarim for similar cases is that the neshamah still needs to do teshuvah for certain things that were not as they should be, or that its destiny was assigned to perform a favor for so-and-so, and therefore it is kept in the body in the zechus of so-and-so, even if not in its own zechus. And even if the neshamah has not yet done teshuvah until now, then it is as the Sages said: "He is long-suffering and collects what is His." Yet, there is the hope that "no one shall be cast out from Him," and he will return in teshuvah, and he will return and be healed.

And in anticipation of the upcoming Chag HaPesach, may it come upon us and all of Yisrael for good and for blessing, may you celebrate it with all your household members, may they live, in kashrus and in joy.

With blessings.

## 404

B"H, 6 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of Tuesday, in which you write that a respectable proposal has been made to [Name] and the matter is already nearing fruition, but in the meantime someone has come along and cast doubt regarding [her] conduct in the past—even though regarding the present, she has stated explicitly that her desire is to marry specifically someone who is a *shomer Torah u’mitzvos* and to conduct herself according to the laws of Moshe and Yisroel, etc.

Now, since the present is good, and regarding the past, it is a case of "doubtful testimony" which does not even reach the level of a confirmed report—and it is understood that according to *Shulchan Aruch*, one must be very careful about whether such testimony is even credible, especially since *teshuvah* is effective—therefore, in my opinion, you should not be concerned. May Hashem grant success to your efforts, that it may be for the good and at a favorable time.

It is a great wonder that all this time there has been no news from you regarding activities in your surroundings for the strengthening of Yiddishkeit in general, and for the *hafatzas hamaayanos* in particular. After all, regarding each and every one of us, it is said, "In the multitude of counselors there is salvation," and the story of our Sages is well known, that Rav Ashi would gather [the scholars], etc. I wish to remind you of the *chazakah* that "a *shaliach* performs his mission," for every single one of the Children of Israel is a *shaliach* of the *Adam HaElyon* to make for Him, may He be blessed, a dwelling place in the lower worlds through the "candle of a *mitzvah* and the light of Torah," and the "light of Torah" refers to the *pnimiyus haTorah*. Consequently, activity regarding others is also a necessity, for it is only through *tzedakah* that one draws down success for one’s own *avodah* above, as is understood from the statement of our Sages: "Rabbi Eliezer would give a *prutah* to a pauper and then pray" (this also applies to the twelve middle blessings [of the Amidah], which begin with the request for *Chochma, Binah, and Da’as*, etc.). Nevertheless, the *psak din* is that when there is a need to clarify, one must clarify, even if there is a *chazakah*, as is brought in the beginning of *Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah*.

As we approach the festival of Pesach, which is coming upon us and all of Yisroel for the good, may you and your family *shichyu* celebrate it in purity and joy. And may you make an effort to gather all "four sons" to recount (to illuminate) the Exodus from Mitzrayim (limitations and boundaries), for the Torah speaks regarding them all.

With blessings.

## 4101

B"H, 6 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and dedicated to the needs of the community, R' Yissachar Dov, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

Following the long silence, your letter from Rosh Chodesh Nissan has been received. Regarding what you write about the various disturbances in the holy work of educating the daughters of Yisrael in purity—this is the nature of a person’s avodah since we were exiled from our land and distanced from our soil. On the contrary, in recent years the concealments and obstructions have diminished, even if they still exist. This is especially evident to every one of anash who came from our country, as they see this tangibly, with physical eyes, and in their own personal matters. If one were to pause for a brief moment and make a *kal v'chomer* for himself: "If twenty years ago, when I was in such-and-such a situation, I was still involved in matters of Torah and mitzvos—even though there was seemingly danger in doing so—and it was precisely through this involvement that I and my family were saved, how much more so must I thank the Creator of the world and its Guide, who has brought me out from the straits into the expanse, and now I am able to do all that has been mentioned with joy!" Further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

As for the fact that concealments and obstructions arise, you are surely aware that with a small amount of effort relative to the task—and, most importantly, with a firm resolution that the matter must be accomplished—one succeeds. Certainly, this will be the case in the future as well, and our Nasi, the Rebbe, stands and serves and awakens Heavenly mercy so that success will continue in all his endeavors that are conducted according to his spirit and will, as well as in the personal matters of the one who strives and labors in this.

Regarding what you wrote about printing report cards to record the students' grades, etc.—it is surprising that you do not have them yet, as this is standard in all schools. It is understood that it is proper to create them, at the very least, now.

Regarding your question about how to conduct oneself with the students: in general, this must follow two opposing lines. The Gemara says, "Push away with the left," yet regarding a child or a woman, it must be "the right hand draws near," especially in the methods of education.

It is true that there is a place for both approaches. The boundaries for this become apparent during the actual work of education, according to the nature of the student’s soul; one cannot set hard and fast rules. This is especially true since matters change from place to place, from time to time, and from student to student. It is proper that at fixed times, all the teachers should consult together—or at least the majority of them—regarding the conduct of the students and the manner of influencing them. May Hashem grant you success.

Surely you are arranging the conduct of the Seder for Pesach well in advance. It would be worthwhile to clarify in detail the customs they were accustomed to in Morocco while in their homes. Although in essential matters the Seder should be conducted according to Chabad custom, there are surely several details where it is appropriate to allow them to follow their own customs in a manner that is fitting.

The *pidyon nefesh* enclosed in your letter will be read at the holy gravesite of the Rebbe, may the merit of the righteous protect us. Surely, for the time being, her health has improved.

Approaching the festival of Pesach, which is coming upon us and all of Yisrael for good and for blessing, may you celebrate it with all your family, may they live, in purity and joy.

With blessing and regards to the administration and the students, and for a kosher and happy Pesach, both physically and spiritually.

## 4002

B"H, 6 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Mr. Eliyahu, may he live and be well,

Shalom u'vracha!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter, in which you write about your service and request a blessing.

May it be the will of the Creator of the world and its Guide that He bestow blessing upon you in your personal matters and in your general matters—that is, your influence upon your surroundings—for with a Jewish person, these two are interdependent.

For each and every one of us, within the collective of Klal Yisrael, is in need of receiving blessing and success from Above in our daily life, and all the more so for those who are in the army. In order for this blessing and success to be in a maximal measure, one must show that the one requesting the blessing also conducts himself in a similar manner—that is, he provides help and assists all those he is able to help, without seeking reward or compensation for it. The attribute of Hashem Yisbarach, which is "measure for measure," then conducts itself in such a manner with the one requesting the blessing. Therefore, you must utilize your influence upon all your comrades to inform them of the content of our Torah, the Torah of life, and to bring them closer to the fulfillment of its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them." You should not be satisfied with speaking once or twice, but rather [continue] until your words come to fruition and result in actual change. It is already a known adage: "Words that come from the heart enter the heart," and the matter depends only upon one's will.

Especially as we approach the days of the Festival of Matzos, the time of our freedom from the exile of Egypt—a freedom that is bound up with the freedom of the soul. As the verse states, "When you bring the people out of Egypt, you shall serve Hashem upon this mountain"—Mount Sinai and the receiving of the Torah. So too it is in this time, that the true redemption and freedom are dependent and bound up with a firm resolution to study Torah and fulfill its mitzvos, and there is nothing that can stand before the will.

It would please me if you would convey my regards and holiday greetings to your comrades in your surroundings, and may each one of them, and all of you together, celebrate the upcoming Festival of Pesach—which is approaching us and all of Israel for good—in a kosher and joyous manner.

With blessing.

## 403

B"H, 6 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, regarding your questions:

1) Regarding the well-known dispute concerning *bein hashmashos* (twilight), and how women should conduct themselves regarding the *bedikah* (internal examination).

Although in recent times there has been an increase in those debating the matter of *shekiah* (sunset) and the aforementioned *bein hashmashos*, to the extent that books have been printed on this subject in addition to articles in Torah journals, it is understood that for *anash* there is nothing to follow but the *psak din* of our Rebbe (the Alter Rebbe) in his *Siddur*. This *psak* is from his later period, which carries more weight than his *Shulchan Aruch*, and it is known that the opinion of the Gra is also in accordance with this (Orach Chaim, siman 261; Yoreh Deah, siman 262; and in *Shenos Eliyahu*, beginning of *Berachos*; see also *Sefer Gur Aryeh* on *Shabbos* 35).

2) Regarding what you wrote concerning the *onah* (time) for *talmidei chachamim*, which is from one Shabbos night to the next, and the stringency mentioned in *Reishis Chochmah*, *Shaar HaKedushah* (apparently referring to chapter 16), and whether there is room to differentiate between the first year and thereafter.

I have not found this distinction anywhere. While the fact that we have not seen it is not proof in general, in this case, since it is not mentioned in the books that discuss the aforementioned matter, this is indeed conclusive proof. This matter is explained according to the *nigleh* (the revealed Torah) in the commentaries on the *Shulchan Aruch*, Orach Chaim, siman 240, and Even HaEzer, siman 76. See there in the *Pischei Teshuvah* in Even HaEzer, regarding what he cites in the name of *Kerem Shlomo*.

The matter mentioned in *Reishis Chochmah* is based on the words of the *Zohar* in several places; see Part 1, 14, end of side a; there, 50a; and in other places, as noted in *Nitzutzei Zohar* to *Zohar Chadash*, 49b.

Regarding the practical application, we have nothing to follow but what is explained in the writings of the Arizal. Even though there are differences in phrasing between what is brought in *Pri Etz Chaim*, *Mishnas Chassidim*, and *Taamei Mitzvos*, one should prefer the *Taamei Mitzvos* and *Mishnas Chassidim* over the phrasing of the *Pri Etz Chaim*. This is because "the *Mishnas Chassidim* only copied the words of the Arizal; therefore, he presumably saw this in the writings of the Arizal" (*Piskei Dinim* of the Tzemach Tzedek to Yoreh Deah, siman 116). The same applies to the *Taamei Mitzvos* of R' Chaim Vital over the *Pri Etz Chaim*, which also contains the words of the *chaverim*. In *Mishnas Chassidim*, it is in *Maseches Hashkivah*, chapter 11, and in *Taamei Mitzvos*, it is in *Parshas Bereishis* (d.h. *b'inyan hazivug*, 16a in the Vilna edition). [And although the *Hagahos v'Chiddushim* to *Shaar HaMitzvos*, beginning of *Parshas Bereishis*, raises a difficulty against this from the statement of our Sages that the *onah* for *talmidei chachamim* is from Shabbos night to Shabbos night, and they did not make exceptions, it is known that one does not nullify an explicit instruction because of a difficulty.]

Let this be known: all of the above, both according to the *nigleh* and according to the writings of the Arizal, applies only provided that this abstinence does not lead to more severe matters than those mentioned. However, if there is room for such a concern, in my opinion, it is clear that one should refrain from this abstinence. This is all the more so, and *kal v'chomer*, from what is brought in the name of *Sefer Chassidim* in the *Beis Shmuel* to Even HaEzer, beginning of siman 23. I have since found this as well in the *Biur Halacha* to the *Mishnah Berurah* in Orach Chaim, there.

3) Regarding the fact that your wife is particular about customs from Frankfurt that seem strange to you, and were not known in your father's house.

It is simple that in such matters one should conduct oneself only with pleasant ways, and even more so according to the words of our Sages, "the left hand pushes away and the right hand draws near," since it is clear that your question concerns customs that do not involve any prohibition. Even in such cases, it is questionable whether it is worthwhile to change her customs, since it is almost certain that by yielding on your part regarding the aforementioned matters, you will be able to easily influence her regarding customs that do have a tinge of prohibition, or even in matters that are only for the sake of an additional *hiddur mitzvah*. And if some of these customs are truly strange in your environment, then surely, over time, she herself will refrain from them for the sake of those who see.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 405

B.H., 7 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 5th of Shevat, and it is surprising that I have not received any news from you since then.

Regarding what you wrote about the manner of educating your children—whether it is better to place them among children of Sephardic background with whom they are more familiar, or in a Charedi institution even though the students there are mostly Ashkenazic.

Certainly, there are now very Charedi *chedarim* for Sephardic children. However, if such an institution is not available in your vicinity or near your residence, it is understood that *yiras shamayim* takes precedence over everything else. Furthermore, by speaking with the class teacher, you can certainly arrange matters so that the children do not feel isolated.

Regarding what you wrote about learning the craft of a *sofer stam*, the solution to this question depends on his aptitude for it. The test is through actual practice; that is, he should speak with an expert in the field, have him test him in the appropriate manner, and decide based on the results.

Regarding what you wrote about your tight financial situation, which causes you to pay off debts over a longer period than you had initially anticipated:

Heaven forbid that you should become discouraged by this. Surely the lender does not mind; on the contrary, he is satisfied that you are paying in the manner most convenient for you, in accordance with the principle of "you shall not be to him as a creditor." We do not know the hidden ways of the *Ribono shel Olam*, for ultimately, the *Ribono shel Olam* provides the Jewish person with the means to pay all his debts, as this is a *mitzvah*. Seemingly, one might wonder why the ability to do so is delayed, but as mentioned, we have no business with hidden things, and sustenance does not depend on merit, but on *mazal*.

I am certain that you will utilize the days of Pesach with the students as is proper, and that you are also making the necessary preparations to utilize the days of Pesach that are approaching, as well as those before and after it. May it be His will that it be with success.

It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding the arrangements for your mother, *tichyeh*, or what is happening with the rest of the family. I am sure you will fill me in at the next opportunity.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

417

B"H, 7 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter in which you write some details of your life history, and conclude with a complaint that you find it difficult to manage regarding your livelihood, and you express wonder at this. Although the reason is understood even from your own letter, since in past years you established your livelihood in a manner contrary to the observance of the holy Shabbos, and it is already explained in the holy sefarim that through this (forbidden work on the holy Shabbos), not only is there no increase in livelihood, but on the contrary, one damages one’s livelihood.

However, since Hashem, may He be blessed and exalted, has said that teshuvah is effective and can rectify even the past, you should resolve with the greatest possible strength to fulfill the mitzvos of our Torah, the Torah of life, and strive to find a source of livelihood and arrange your affairs in general in a manner that is permitted and kosher according to the Shulchan Aruch. Then there is great and abundant hope that in time things will work out, even if at the beginning there may be difficulties in the matter, and it has already been said, "Though your beginning was small, your end will flourish greatly."

You should see to it that your tefillin are checked, as well as the mezuzos in the place where you live, to ensure they are kosher according to the law. And every weekday, before the morning davening, you should give some coins to tzedakah. After davening in the morning, every day—and also on Shabbos and Yom Tov—you should recite at least one chapter from the Book of Tehillim.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

B"H, 7 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Shushan Purim, I was pleased to read that you have seen the blessing of Hashem tangibly in your business endeavors thus far. Certainly, Hashem will continue His blessing, especially since we have just come from a month in which success was achieved through the principle of "the opposite occurred, that the Jews would rule," and we have entered the month of Nissan, in which, according to the statement of our Sages (Berachos 57a), miracles of miracles occurred. This also extends below ten tefachim, for this is the very concept of the miracle of Purim, which is connected to physical matters, as is explained in many places in Chassidus based on what is written in the Levush, cited in the Taz, Siman 670. Similarly, this applies to the matters of the festival of Pesach, where the servitude at that time was a servitude of the body, in mortar and in bricks, etc., as is also brought in the discourses of Parshas Shemos, Torah Or, and Toras Chayim, etc.

May it be the will of Hashem that success continue in abundance, and may you be able to fulfill the desires of your heart for good, through the mitzvah of tzedakah and in other matters...

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach and for good tidings.

419

B"H, 8 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Professor Avraham Yitzchak Hakohen,

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge with thanks the receipt of your books, as well as the publications of the "Jewish Culture Foundation." They were somewhat delayed in transit, apparently because the package was broken open, and my reply was also delayed due to the pressure of many preoccupations.

It was a pleasant surprise to see your book "Einstein’s Theory of Relativity" among your works, as I was not aware that you were involved in the sciences of mathematics and physics. I was pleased to see on the title page that you did not change your name, and that it is written Katz — Kohen Tzedek.

As is my custom in such matters, I am including in the margins a few comments, at least regarding those points that occurred to me as I leafed through your books, albeit in haste, as time permits.

Surely, by the time you receive my letter, you will have already received news from your sister, may she live, regarding her return together with her son, may he live, safely to the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established.

As the festival of Pesach approaches, I hereby express my blessing that you celebrate it with your family, may they live, in purity and joy.

With holiday blessings and regards to your brother, may he live,

**M. Schneerson**

All those who explain the theory of relativity—naturally—emphasize its most surprising conclusions and place them at the forefront: the negation of absolute space and the negation of absolute time, for both space and time are relative. They present this as having been proven irrefutably—by the Michelson experiment, later during the solar eclipse, by the calculation of a planet’s orbit, etc. Consequently, they incorporate these conclusions into the assets of science, similar to the three well-known laws of Newton and the authority they held before the inaccuracies within them were proven. To my great astonishment, in all the books dealing with the aforementioned theory that I have seen thus far, I have not found **even one** that expresses any reservation regarding this! And among those who study these books, it goes without saying that no one casts doubt on this premise.

For my part, not only is a reservation required here, but since science—in its modern sense, i.e., exact science, which arrives at its conclusions only through measurement, weight, etc.—has no place in its scientific assets, or even within the scope of its inquiry, for dealing with **absolute** concepts. The tools of the trade of exact science "cannot attain" the absolute. Consequently, it cannot negate it (just as it cannot prove its existence).

Furthermore: it is standard that when a scientist finishes experiments and the formulation of their conclusions and laws, he attempts to establish—as a **hypothesis**—a new theory (or to introduce corrections to an existing theory) in the field in which he is engaged. The purpose of this is to add the new conclusions to the scientific assets of that field and to explain their **totality** in a simpler manner, and as much as possible, in a way that is also more understandable to simple logic.

Yet, even in the establishment of this theory—which, as mentioned, is nothing more than a **hypothesis and an attempt** to explain, in a way that is **possible**, a portion of natural phenomena—there is no justification for introducing absolute concepts. Moreover, this contradicts the goal (at least in the present case), because through this, the description becomes "less" understandable (if there is anyone at all who understands it with simple logic and can visualize what it means): there is no absolute space and time, the speed of light is equal in all directions and for all observers, space is curved by the matter placed within it, space (the vacuum of the universe) is limited like a sphere and is expanding or contracting, the speed *c* has a special property—that it is (absolutely) impossible to exceed it, and so on.

***

All the **scientific** experiments that have been conducted, including those regarding the field of relativity, have as their foundation and content: measurement, measuring instruments, and the human who measures and summarizes the results. From this—

All the conclusions reached are only regarding the measurement of space, matter, or light, regarding the "behavior" of the measuring instruments, and regarding the traits of the human and his capabilities.

Regarding the experiments of Fizeau, Michelson, etc.—the hypothesized explanation and the theory that is closest to the experiments and utilizes the fewest assumptions from outside the experiments is the one that must utilize the explanation of Lorentz. And the well-known difficulty (which is also transcribed in your book) as to why the Lorentz phenomenon corresponds **in all** materials precisely to the change in speed, etc.—a difficulty regarding measurement by a human—is minor compared to the difficulty of why all of nature was limited to the speed *c*, no more and no less. And this is not the place to elaborate further.

***

**Regarding your book on Jewish sources in the Koran.**

Page XX: The researchers expressed wonder at the choice of Gabriel specifically.

It can be said simply that this is according to the scriptures in Daniel (8 and 9), where Gabriel explains the vision, informs what will be in the end of days, comes forth to give understanding, etc.—and see also Daniel 12:6 and onwards (and as is known in the words of our Sages, the man clothed in linen is Gabriel).

By the way: see *Shemos Rabbah*, ch. 18:5, that Gabriel also acted as a guardian for Israel. Regarding Gabriel and Avraham—see *Maaseh Avraham Avinu* (in *Otzar HaMidrashim*).

Pages XXII-XXIII: The example of the renewal of the fast from the beginning of Elul does not hold up well, since Elul comes here **together** with the Ten Days of Repentance—meaning a period of 40 days. Its source can be said to be according to the verse (*Devarim* 22:13) and according to the words of our Sages (*Yevamos* 48b), "a month of days of repentance for that sin," etc.

Page 147: The example of the prohibition of intermarriage with the *Netinim* is seemingly unsuccessful—for they are converts, and their prohibition is not related to idolatry. It requires study why you, sir, insisted on this—for there is an entire passage in *Devarim* 7 (and as in *Kiddushin* 68b), and see also *Malachi* 2:11-12.

In such cases, one must ensure that true friends intervene to restore *shalom bayis*. It is self-understood that you, for your part, must undertake—not only to promise, but to actually fulfill in practice—to concede to all of her just demands. And if there are matters that are not sufficiently well-founded, you should defer to the opinion of neutral people. In many cases, when the wife recognizes in her husband that he is truly serious about peace and is prepared to concede, this in itself brings about a closeness of mind. As is known from many *maamarei Chazal*, for the sake of this [peace], it is worthwhile to be *mevater* on many matters, and even to act *lifnim mishuras hadin*. Awaiting good news.

Specifically regarding your memory, you should gradually learn Mishnayos and also Tanya by heart—at least a few chapters of each. Take care not to exhaust yourself in the process of memorization; that is to say, when you see that it is tiring you, leave it for a while and try again after some time. Furthermore, see to it that you observe, from now on, the three daily shiurim—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—that are equal for every soul, as instituted by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which are well known.

With blessings to hear good news regarding all the above, and for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 416

416

B"H, 9 Nissan, 5716

Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh regarding the Geulah **that was established** for Yaakov and his children, and as per the well-known adage of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe: establishment in time and establishment in the soul. Thank you for writing regarding the farbrengens and the main points discussed therein; surely you will continue this good practice in the future, and your mind will be at ease just as you put my mind at ease.

By the way, regarding what you wrote about the statement of our Sages, "This one shall come, etc.," there is a maamar from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Tzemach Tzedek, on this. Although it is in manuscript and has not yet been printed, the general concept is based on what is also explained in Likutei Torah and elsewhere regarding the explanation of the statement of our Sages, "Moshe prophesied with 'this'." In language understandable to all, it can be explained based on all the above: that one can only point with a finger at a matter that has true existence, and therefore it is possible only in matters of holiness, and according to the language of the Rambam, which is the truth of existence, etc.

Regarding what you wrote about the debate among anash concerning the various fundraising campaigns—it is known from our Sages, "Both are completely righteous, etc." (see Likutei Torah, Bamidbar 44b). Even though you are correct in writing that the matters you are occupied with for the Chabad institutions are necessary, your opponent is also correct that it is necessary to arrange matters in a way that there will be room for fundraising for other Chabad institutions as well, whose existence is also necessary. It is understood that it is impossible to visit the baalei batim for the sake of several institutions—all of which bear the name Chabad-Lubavitch—at the same time. The advised counsel for this is to set specific times for fundraising for the different institutions (or to divide the baalei batim, though it is understood that the second way is harder than the first, and it also requires study as to whether the baalei batim will accept the logic that one belongs only to one Lubavitch institution and not the other). There is enough time throughout the year to suffice for all the institutions, and if only they would utilize these possibilities at least.

It is surely superfluous to awaken [you] regarding the precision of our Sages, "Torah scholars increase peace in the world." It is not enough to have mere peace, and it is not enough to have peace in one's home; rather, there must specifically be a *majority* of peace, and specifically *in the world*. As per the interpretation of the word *olam* (world) as *he'elem* (concealment): even in a place where concealment still rules, one must bring peace there, and specifically in a majority. Then all the matters dependent on this will be fulfilled for them, as stated in the Midrash Esther Rabbah at the end. And let the questioner not ask how this difficult avodah is possible; for if one is a student of a wise man, even though one is only asked according to one's strength, one can bring a majority of peace into the world, based on what is explained in the Chavas Daas to Yoreh Deah in the introduction regarding the matter of a Torah scholar.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, and for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 419

B"H, 9 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rav, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, who engages in the needs of the community, R' Yehoshua, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

After the long hiatus, I was pleased to receive your letter from Thursday, along with the *kuntreisim* for Pesach and Shavuos enclosed within it. Thank you for the gift. It is surprising that, contrary to your custom until now, you do not mention your participation in the *farbrengen* of *anash* in your camp.

As you requested, your *petek* will be read at an *eis ratzon* at the *tziyun* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

And since we are moving—and the precision of this expression of our Sages is explained in Chassidus, that a Jewish person becomes a "walker" (*mehalech*), unlike before the soul’s descent below, when it is in a state of "standing" (*omed*)—from the month of Adar, regarding which it is said, "The month that was turned for them" (and the precision of the language "the month" implies that the entire month was turned) into joy, etc., to the month of Nissan, regarding which our Sages said (Shlah on the verse "This month") that every day of this month is in the category of *Rosh Chodesh*. As the verse hints, "This [month] shall be for you the head of the months," and *Rosh Chodesh*, even though work is permitted, is not included in the category of ordinary weekdays. As the language of the verse (Shmuel I 20) implies, the interpretation of this is that the work done during these days is influenced by a more spiritual source, and consequently, the blessing is imbued with success to a greater degree (see *Ohr HaTorah* by the Tzemach Tzedek, 22a and onwards). May it be the will [of Hashem] that from these months, the aforementioned concept be drawn down upon the entire year: that in material matters, the spirituality within them should be more pronounced, which will automatically diminish the constraints and limitations, until the prophecy is fulfilled: "As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show you wonders."

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

4220

4220

B”H, 10 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, scion of a holy lineage,
Rabbi Shalom Yechezkel Shraga, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter, which continues our discussion regarding a metal thread and sewing with it in the context of the laws of Shabbos. You cite several statements from our Sages in your letter where they use the terminology of *tefirah* (sewing) or *chayta* (Aramaic for sewing), even when it involves a metal thread or the like.

It is surprising, however, that you would argue this, for is *tefirah* explicitly written in the Torah as a prohibition of Shabbos? The prohibitions of Shabbos are derived from the work performed in the Mishkan. It is irrelevant whether or not they are called "sewing"; what matters is whether that specific work was performed in the Mishkan, or at the very least, if that is the standard way of performing it. Even though the Mishnah uses the term *tofer* (sewing), it is because "a hundred is included in two hundred, but two hundred is not included in a hundred." Just as with other terms in the Mishnah, it is specifically applicable only when it was done in the Mishkan and in the standard manner—this is simple.

Incidentally, although it is not relevant to the above, regarding your note on the verse, "And they sewed fig leaves"—even though they did not have silk or wool threads or the like, and you therefore conclude that it refers to a type of sewing that is not the standard way of our times—the material is not the issue. If that is the reason, one could just as well argue that they certainly did not have a needle, and therefore they sewed with their fingers—meaning they made a hole with a fingernail, etc.—and on that basis, one would be obligated for a type of sewing that is exempt according to all opinions. As for the practical reality, it is difficult to understand where you derive that they did not have silk or wool threads, etc. It is simply clear that they did not have a metal thread, which is what we are discussing, for the grandson of Adam [Tuval-Cain] was a "forger of every cutting instrument of copper and iron."

Similarly, regarding your statement that there is no difference between *kilayim* and Shabbos as to which material connects the two stitches: in my opinion, the opposite is clearly true. For in *kilayim*, the **manner** in which the connection is made is irrelevant; what matters is the reality that a connection was made. In Shabbos, it is the opposite—the entire prohibition depends solely on whether the manner in which the work is performed is the standard way, etc.

Regarding your comment on my phrasing, "to make [it] from the kosher daughters of Israel, etc.," asking where I derive that this is the custom of the daughters of Israel: I have anchored my position on the *Korban Nethanel* and the authorities that followed him, that this was the custom in Jewish communities. The law regarding a safety pin is certainly the same as it is in our generation, or as in the methods cited in the *Korban Nethanel* and subsequent books.

As we approach the festival of Pesach, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good, may it be the will of Hashem that each of us, within the entirety of the Jewish people, celebrates it in purity and joy.

With respect and holiday blessings.

Regarding what you wrote concerning Shabbos (74b) and elsewhere: if you follow your own logic and equate a safety pin to that, then you must simply conclude that one is liable for a *chatas*, etc. You are forced to admit, even according to your own view, that it is not comparable, and the reason is that there is no "sewing" with a needle; in the Mishkan, there were threads.

From Shabbos (48b), it is proven that one cannot learn Shabbos from *kilayim*, because sewing that is not intended to last is not considered "sewing" or "connecting" in the context of Shabbos (see there in the *Hagahos Maimoniyos*). The reason is as stated above.

Regarding your question on the *Tosafos* (s.v. *d'yada*, Shabbos 69a) as to how it is possible that one knows of the *aseh* (positive commandment) of Shabbos but does not know of the *lo sa'aseh* (negative commandment), since the fulfillment of the *aseh* is through the observance of the *lo sa'aseh*—I did not understand the difficulty, for the meaning there is that he did not know that there is a Torah prohibition (*lo sa'aseh*) regarding this. As for the premise that the fulfillment of the *aseh* of "you shall rest" is only through the observance of the *lo sa'aseh*, see Rambam, *Hilchos Shabbos*, beginning of Chapter 21.

## 4221

B"H, 10 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 28 Adar.

Regarding the package in which a Sefer Torah was placed: in most such cases, one packs it disassembled, in which case the halachic ruling regarding its transport is much more lenient. However, the main point in your case is that since it was placed in a vessel within a vessel—and presumably more than two vessels—and primarily, since it is permitted to send it in such a manner, it is also permitted to **handle** it in such a manner. Therefore, there is no reason for concern. However, merely as a matter of *hiddur*, it would be appropriate for you to donate, from your own funds, a mantle and a *wimple* (mapah) for that Sefer Torah, and also to fast the upcoming *Ta'anis Behab*, but only until *chatzos*, and give the value of the fast to *tzedakah*.

2) Regarding the bottle of wine at the wedding: aside from the fact that the entire matter about which you write is in doubt, this does not fall under the category of *basrei evrei nahara*, in addition to the fact that this is a rabbinic prohibition. And as mentioned above regarding *yeseir se'ah* and *hiddur*, you should give the value of 73 meals to *tzedakah*. It is self-understood that this does not need to be given all at once, and you may do so until the upcoming Rosh Hashanah, may it come upon us for good.

At a time of favor, I will mention the relatives about whom you write at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and it is understood that this includes him as well.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach, and regards to your parents, may they live.

***

**Regarding the package:** He did not know that a Sefer Torah was inside and threw it into the machine.

**Regarding the bottle of wine:** He is in doubt as to whether non-Jews touched it.

***Basrei evrei nahara***: He himself did not drink from them, but rather distributed them among the guests. See *Avodah Zarah* 6b.

## 422

422

B”H, 10 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Yitzchak Koren

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter in due time, and it was a pleasure to read that you participated in the celebration of the auspicious day of 19 Kislev in Kfar Chabad. Even though I had already received reports about this, hearing it from others is not the same as reading a letter from the participant himself, in his own words and impressions.

You are surely familiar with the term commonly used among Chassidei Chabad to describe 19 Kislev as the "Rosh Hashanah of Chassidus." The explanation of this concept is that just as the head influences vitality throughout the entire body, so too must the "head" of the year bestow its spirit upon the entire year. The same applies to the Rosh Hashanah of Chassidus: it must draw additional vitality, light, and enthusiasm into all the remaining days of the year, stemming from that same awakening and state of mind in which one was found on that day. It is well known in such matters that our Sages’ adage, "(Even if one only) passed through the shop of a perfumer, he absorbs its scent," applies all the more so to one who participates in more than just a passing way. My hope, based on our conversation when you were here, is that for you, too, this participation was more than just a passing experience.

Regarding the primary question and issue you touched upon in your letter concerning the mixing of religion and politics—partisanship, as it is called—much has already been discussed about this painful matter. However, in my opinion, the beginning of the rectification must not be as you write in your letter, but rather from the other side. My meaning is this: to our sorrow and regret, it is not only religion that is mixed with politics, but anti-religion is also mixed with it. That is to say, certain circles—unfortunately, even those with significant influence—have inserted the war against religion into the platform of the party to which they belong, even though there is no ideological or intellectual connection between the two matters; furthermore, on certain points, they actually contradict one another.

It is understood that they were forced to introduce this war in an unofficial manner, and even more so for the reasons mentioned. Nevertheless, they utilize the party apparatus and its influence to wage this war, and not always through fair means, as is customary in party warfare.

My reason for saying that the beginning must come from the other side is simple: because they are the majority, and the apparatus of their organization is stronger; therefore, it is they who must take the first step. There is also a more internal and fundamental reason for this, as the popular saying goes: "No one has ever spoiled a kosher piece of meat, even one who does not care for salted meat for an hour"—whereas the opposite is not the case.

Surely, for one of your stature, there is no need to explain these things further. I only wish to add—even if in your eyes I may be suspect regarding this issue—that in my opinion, it would be a blessing for the parties of the aforementioned "other side" if they were to remove the war against religion from their platform. And this is not only a blessing for the World to Come, but quite simply regarding the development and deepening of the party’s affairs in terms of quality.

I will conclude regarding the end of your letter, where you ask for forgiveness for having "pushed your way into the parlor," etc. There is no place for such a request for forgiveness. On the contrary, as is known from the approach of Lubavitch and Chabad since time immemorial, all the children of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov are religious in the inner recesses of their souls. The difference lies only in the partition between the inner and the outer—whether it is a partition of iron, a partition of silk, or how many windows it has, or if the partition has been removed entirely. Therefore, you did not "push your way" into the parlor of religion; rather, you have been in it since the day your soul descended below, regardless of all the upheavals you have experienced throughout your life. Furthermore, regarding you specifically, since you are in a position to influence the many, even a slight effort on your part in the desired direction will succeed greatly, for the merit of the many assists you.

It is understood that if there is any development regarding the aforementioned issue, I would be interested in knowing the details, and I thank you in advance for your trouble in this.

With respect and blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach, and for good tidings regarding general matters in good health.

## 4223

B"H, 10 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, occupied with communal needs, may his light shine,

As is well known, the Sages interpret the verse, "Educate the child according to his way," to mean that from the age of sixteen, etc., until twenty-four, the parents bear responsibility for their son (though the ruling of our Alter Rebbe in his Hilchos Talmud Torah, Chapter 1, end of paragraph 6, requires further study, as he seemingly straddles two opinions regarding the period from sixteen to twenty-four). May you derive from him and from all your descendants, may they live and be well, much true nachas—nachas that is Chassidishe—for long, good days and years.

May you celebrate the upcoming festival of Pesach in purity and joy.

P.S. My letter in response to your previous one has surely arrived by now.
