## 425

425

*[11 Nissan 5716]*

Regarding what you wrote concerning the Iggeres HaKodesh of the Alter Rebbe, that tefillah is *de'oraisa*, etc. (see the transcription in *Mishnas Yoel*—by R. Y. Diskin—and the notes made there).

Seemingly, this is difficult to reconcile with what is written in his *Shulchan Aruch* (Orach Chaim, 106, end of subsection 2), "And such is the essential ruling." One could resolve this according to what is written in *Shaar HaKollel* at the beginning. However, see *Piskei Dinim* of the Tzemach Tzedek, *Chiddushim al HaRambam*, *Hilchos Tefillah*.

And it is clear that the Alter Rebbe’s intent in the aforementioned Iggeres HaKodesh is **not** to render a definitive halachic ruling **at all** as to whether tefillah is *min haTorah* (and therefore he did not write that those who say it is *derabanan* are "mistaken," but rather that "they have never seen the light of day"). Rather, the content of the letter is to demonstrate the error of those who wanted to daven in haste, etc., because they claimed tefillah is *derabanan*. It is to this that the response and the explanation of the magnitude of their error is addressed: because **in this time**, for those who daven in haste and those who mock, etc., it is the foundation of the entire Torah, etc. See there. And examine carefully *Zohar* Vol. III, 202b.

#### ***425***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 14, p. 223.

## 426

11 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I received a pleasant surprise in your letter confirming the receipt of the chiddushim of the Tzemach Tzedek on Maseches Bava Metzia, and I read with special satisfaction about the study sessions on this tractate.

Great is the power of studying our Torah, the Torah of life, which "leads to action." Surely the teaching "one mitzvah leads to another" will be fulfilled as well. And since we increase in matters of holiness, my hope is that the aforementioned will continue to grow and increase, both in quantity and in quality.

Some are puzzled by the statement of our Sages, "Rabbi honored the wealthy."

To me, this is understood and explained according to one of the fundamental points of the Baal Shem Tov’s approach: that every matter in the world, even the smallest of the small, is by Divine Providence, and especially general matters that affect many.

Wealthy people—those whom Divine Providence has placed in a position to have the means to accomplish much good in the world of the Ribono shel Olam—surely possess soul-powers suited to fulfilling this role, a role that far exceeds the role of the average person, and certainly that of a poor person. And our holy Rebbe, whose era was a transitional period in the life of the Jewish people—from a relatively peaceful life to a life of decrees and persecutions—had to mobilize all his strength so that the Jewish people would withstand this trial and emerge whole and fortified. It was his task to contemplate each and every individual and strive to utilize all the potential within them. Therefore, he expressed a feeling of respect toward those who were given greater possibilities from Above, which were surely also utilized to protect everything holy in Israel, just like all the other actions of our holy Rebbe.

However, it is consistent with the general conduct of the world that every Jew is given free choice, and Hashem Elokim tests him to know whether he loves Hashem, etc., and keeps His mitzvos and listens to His voice, etc. In this, too, the choice is given to every wealthy person, as it is said, "See, I have set before you today life and good, etc.," to fulfill through his choice, as the verse concludes, "and you shall choose life," or, G-d forbid, the opposite.

It is simple that if this applies to those wealthy in gold and silver, it applies all the more so to those wealthy in the power of influence over their immediate and distant surroundings.

It is also understood that since there is a Leader for this world and there is nothing in it in vain, an active and positive utilization of wealth is mandatory; it is not sufficient at all that one simply does not use the wealth in an undesirable direction.

For even the lack of utilization disrupts the order of creation, since its purpose is that **all** its parts must actively assist the general and unified goal.

I have heard much about you, your soul’s qualities and character traits, and your attitude toward the traditional holy matters of the Jewish people.

In this era of ours, you have been given special possibilities, similar to what was mentioned above, to influence your immediate and distant surroundings—an influence that can bring about far-reaching results. Especially in preserving the true character of our people, who became a nation through the receiving of the Torah. This is the scarlet thread that runs through all the periods of our people’s existence and unites them, even though during this time many nations—nations with the most developed cultures—have ruled the world, etc., and were doomed to destruction and had no recovery. Yet Israel falls and rises—through the connection with the Creator of the world and its Leader—and He says, "For I, Hashem, have not changed, and you, sons of Yaakov, have not been consumed" (Midrash Tanchuma, Parshas Nitzavim).

And if in many periods it was necessary to mobilize all the strength of the Jewish people to guard and protect the Torah and its mitzvos—the secret of the Jewish people's existence—in our time, this is certainly true, for this is a time of the world’s birth and a time of crisis and trial, one of the greatest trials for our people, Israel. Those who are wealthy in ability and possibility, for whom the responsibility is also many times greater, have a holy obligation—and also the privilege—to utilize these possibilities to their fullest to protect what is holy to the Jewish people: our eternal Torah and its mitzvos. This is especially true in the King’s palace, the land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year until the end of the year. And since this task has been placed upon you, surely all the matters required to fulfill the task in its entirety were provided from the outset; it is only the Creator’s will that this be through choice—"and you shall choose life."

Relying on what I have heard about you, my hope is strong that you will not be offended by my lines above, even though this is my first letter to you, and that the words will be received with the same feeling with which they were written.

May it be His will that I merit that these words do not remain mere words.

With respect, appreciation, and wishes for a kosher and happy Pesach.

It is possible that the following paragraph should have come at the beginning of the letter: a request for forgiveness for opening my letter without preceding it with titles, etc. In this, too, I relied on what was described to me regarding your character and soul’s qualities, that you would understand my intent.

From the day I began attending "cheder," and even before that, a picture of the future Redemption began to form in my imagination—the redemption of the Jewish people from their final exile, a redemption such that through it the sufferings of exile, the decrees, and the persecutions would be understood. As part of this bright future and as part of this redemption, there will be a "Nasi who is a king—not a Nasi of a tribe, but one over whom there is none but Hashem his G-d" (Horayos 11a, end). Everything will be in such a way that with a whole heart and full understanding, "You shall say on that day, I thank You, Hashem, **for You were angry with me**." Therefore, it is so difficult for me to use this title in connection with the Jewish people at a time when Yaakov is small and the Jewish people are "sick, driven, crushed, and scattered, and sufferings come upon them." I could have used this word superficially, but since I have heard that you are "authentic," I did not want to be false in my soul. Please accept my apology.

## 427

B"H, 13 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., R' Yitzchak Yaakov, shlita,

Shalom u'Bracha!

I received your letter with pleasure, and subsequently your book, *Responsa Minchas Yitzchak*. I thank you very much for this gift. Although time does not permit me to study it with the necessary depth, out of appreciation for the work, I have noted down in haste a few comments, which are transcribed below in the margins. As our Sages of blessed memory said, "And Vahev in Suphah..." 

In anticipation of the festival of Pesach, which is approaching for us and for all of Israel for good and for blessing, I offer and receive a blessing for a kosher and joyous Pesach, and for the continuation of that joy throughout the entire year, in accordance with the statement of the Arizal, cited in the commentaries to the Shulchan Aruch, that whoever is careful [in the observance of Pesach] influences the entire year.

With respect and holiday blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

**Regarding Responsa, Section 1, Subsections 1-2:** If the term **"assur"** (forbidden) is used without qualification, does this imply a prohibition for all time, or only when it is explicitly stated **"assur l'olam"** (forbidden forever)? Your honor cited various places and books.

Seemingly, one must distinguish between the language of the Sages in the words of our Sages of blessed memory and legal rulings, and the language of ordinary people.

Furthermore, if one needs to remove [something] from a status of *heter* (permissibility), one must say so. It is possible that the books you cited discuss this, but they are not currently at hand.

**Section 6-33. The law regarding one who asks a question [regarding the status of a woman] concerning his wife's sister or a yevamah for the marketplace:** In *Responsa Mar'eh Cohen*—by Rabbi S.M. Adler of London, 3rd edition—there is an extensive discussion on this. He also transcribes there letters from the great halachic authorities of the previous generation on this matter.

**Section 65. "Yachel" (he shall profane), its meaning in the Torah:** See *Responsa of the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek*, *Shaar HaMiluim*, Section 8; *Piskei Dinim* of the aforementioned to *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim*, Section 666; *Sdei Chemed*, *Pe'at HaSadeh*, *Asifat Dinim*, *Ma'arechet Bein HaMetzarim*, Section 2, Subsection 3; *Responsa Tzafnat Paneach* by the Gaon of Rogatchov, Vol. 2, Section 31.

**Section 83.** There is a discussion on this in the book *Mo'ed Kol Chai*; it is transcribed in *Yalkut Dat V'Din* by Rabbi Asaf, p. 90.

**Section 89.** The practice followed in the house of the Rebbe—my father-in-law, the Rebbe—is in accordance with the instruction of his father (the Admur Moharashab) and those before him in holiness, that (except for the door leading outside) the placement of the mezuzah is determined solely by the *hiker tzir* (the hinge side).

***

**427**

**R' Yitzchak Yaakov:** Weiss, Manchester.

**Placement of the mezuzah:** See also *Sefer HaMinhagim - Chabad*, p. 81. Below, *Igros* 437, 451.

## 4228

B"H, 13 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 6 Nissan and the one preceding it, in which you write regarding the state of your son’s health, may he live and be well: at an auspicious time, I will mention him at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May it be Hashem’s will that you soon have good news to report regarding him. It would be appropriate to have his tefillin checked, and you should endeavor, in pleasant ways, to ensure that he puts them on every weekday, wherever he may be, as it is known that this is a shield and protection for a Jewish man.

Regarding what you wrote about your livelihood: the advice of our Sages to increase in tzedakah is well-known, for then the blessing of Hashem is fulfilled, "Give a tithe so that you may become wealthy." The word "increase" is precise here, as one must remove the constriction of the channels, which is accomplished through an action at the other end. This is similar to what is brought in Rambam, Hilchos Deios, chapter 3, and follows the principle that the conduct of a person below awakens a corresponding conduct from the Person upon the Throne, as it were, for the measure of the Holy One, blessed be He, is measure for measure.

It is surely unnecessary to urge you to instill yiras shamayim in your students and to teach them the halachos necessary for daily life, for this is the whole of man, as it is written, "Keep His mitzvos," and there is nothing that can stand before the will.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

B"H, Erev Chag HaMatzos, 5716

And since the good and the holy are infinite and boundless, the more the study increases, the more the action will increase as well.

## 4,233

B”H, 17 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, engaged in the needs of the community, Rabbi Chaim, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 8 Nissan, in which you write regarding your holy work in the Talmud Torah for the masses in the neighborhood where you are located, and that the *shiurim* are increasing in both quantity and quality.

May it be the will of Hashem that you do not settle for the work you have done until now, but rather increase your strength to the best of your ability. Through this, the success from Above will be multiplied many times over, in accordance with the statement of our Sages, “A person sanctifies himself a little from below, [and he is sanctified much from Above].”

Happy is your portion that Divine Providence has placed you to teach Torah to the children of Israel. You surely do this by first introducing the external keys, “The beginning of wisdom is the fear of Hashem,” by speaking words of *hisorerus* to those who listen to your teachings, and through *shiurim* in the *halachos* that they need to know for their daily lives. In the vast majority of cases, those who learn deep *shiurim* in *Shas*, *poskim*, and *rishonim* are actually lacking more in the knowledge of the necessary *halachos*. Furthermore, there is the statement of our Sages that “an error in study is considered intentional,” and it is simple that there is no matter of shame in this, *chas v’shalom*. As is known from the custom of many of the great figures of Israel, they had a fixed time for learning the *halachos* that are necessary—*halacha l’maaseh* specifically. This is repeated in the Written Torah and doubled in the Oral Torah, as it is written, “Fear G-d... for **this** is the whole man,” and as our Sages said, “The study is not the essential thing, but the action.” Elaboration on a matter that is understood is superfluous; I have only come to remove the misconception from the hearts of those who are mistaken and wandering—and this is certainly true in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, where many *halachos* dependent on the land have been added.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

Due to the holiness of the *moed*, the Rebbe shlita did not sign, and I am signing on his behalf.

The Secretary

P.S.
It is surely known to you regarding the three *shiurim* for every soul, established by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in the *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*, as is well known. In any event, you should observe them from here on.

## 4,234

B"H, 17 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

...I was pleased to read in your letter about the improvement in your financial situation, and I hope that the verse "Open your mouth wide and I will fill it" will be fulfilled for you, and that you, for your part, will fulfill the saying of our Alter Rebbe: that Hashem Yisbarach gives Jews gashmius, and they transform that gashmius into ruchnius.

It goes without saying that it is necessary to renew the discussions among yourselves regarding matters of yiras shamayim and Chassidus. Regarding what you say—that one must first demand it of oneself—while this is a valid argument, in this time one must not postpone any avodah b’kodesh. One must do both things simultaneously: demand it of oneself and of others, and not wait until one has perfected oneself entirely. ## 4235

B"H, 18 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the brilliant Rabbi, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, who engages in the needs of the community,
Rabbi Meir Hakohen, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you inform me that you have been appointed, with the help of Hashem, as a dayan: May it be the will of Hashem that you fulfill this holy position with all your ability and with all your strength. As is well known from the words of our Sages, of blessed memory, there is a great responsibility in this, alongside the privilege. The primary point regarding this is understood from the well-known statement of our Sages, that the reason the Halacha follows Beis Hillel is because they were gentle and humble, etc. (Eruvin 13b). The foundation of this level is understood from the statement of our Sages, that in such a case the Halacha follows him because Hashem is with him (Sanhedrin 93b; and see Sotah 5a).

And on a deeper level, the distinction between "these and those are the words of the living G-d" is as the language used in Eruvin: *Elokim* has the same numerical value as *HaTeva* (nature)—meaning, Elokus as it is clothed within the ways of nature, as explained in *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, Chapter 6. This is in contrast to *Havayah*, which is Elokus as it is in revelation—meaning, that one's avodah is in the manner of "I have set **Hashem** before me always." This is the beginning and the foundation of all four sections of the *Shulchan Aruch*, which is why the *Tur* and the *Rema* begin with this. And this is well understood.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

Due to the holiness of the festival, the Rebbe shlita did not sign, and I am signing on his behalf.

The Secretary

***

**Rabbi Meir:** Kaplan, Jerusalem.

Secretary

## 4,237

B"H, 18 Nissan, 5716

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the end of Adar and the one preceding it: Thank you for the good news regarding the improvement in your health. May it be Hashem’s will that you continue to go from strength to strength, and in accordance with the ruling of our holy Torah, we increase in matters of holiness. Certainly, in addition to increasing your study of Chassidus, you are also increasing your activities within the framework of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, through which you will also increase the blessing of Hashem and your success in all that you require.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the manner of affixing a mezuzah on a balcony (gizoztra): Generally, regarding the affixing of a mezuzah, there is an instruction in the name of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, that we follow the "hiker tzir" (the side of the door hinge), in accordance with the opinion of the Rishonim on this matter.

It is added in this regard that they asked: What should one do if all the doors in a room have their "hiker tzir" opening toward another room, and if so, in what manner should one enter the room? They answered: One should enter through the window. However, the above applies except for doors that lead to a courtyard or to the public domain. It is worthwhile to ascertain the details from the elders of Anash in your vicinity, who surely are also aware of this.

Regarding what you wrote about the night of Nittel—whether to fulfill the mitzvah of onah when it is permitted before halachic midnight: Let it be known that: a) On the night of tevilah, as the Mishnas Chassidim (Maseches Seder Leil Pesach, at the end) states, there is no prohibition except on the night of Tisha B'Av and Yom Kippur. b) Regarding what you wrote—before halachic midnight—it is brought in many places that the fulfillment of the mitzvah of onah should always preferably take place after halachic midnight. See Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim, section 240, paragraph 7, and the commentaries there. c) Regarding the night of Nittel, although the Sefer Darkei Chaim V'Shalom (section 825) notes this stringency, citing the Sefer Zecher Tzaddik Livrachah in the name of the Rebbe of Munkatch, I have not heard an instruction on this. The basis for being stringent after midnight requires further study. I do not have the Sefer Zecher Tzaddik Livrachah at hand to see the reasoning. However, the difficulty is that since the fulfillment of the mitzvah of onah involves the sanctification of thought, and thought has a profound effect, there is room for concern that the subject of Nittel might enter one's mind, and this is a detriment, as is understood, even when one is thinking about the negation of the matter. Perhaps this is also the reason for the aforementioned stringency.

As you requested, I will mention you and your wife, shetichyeh, at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the fulfillment of your hearts' desires for good in the near future.

With holiday blessings,

Due to the holiness of the festival, the Rebbe shlita did not sign, and I am signing on his behalf,

A. Quint
Secretary

## 429

B"H, 20 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 10 Nissan: there is no need to ask forgiveness for writing here. On the contrary, it is a source of satisfaction if one can be of assistance to anyone in any way. Especially in your case: despite all the reasons you write, there is no "fleeing from the battlefield" here. As experience has shown, this is not the case. Every Jew—and especially one whom Hashem has graced with the talent for chinuch and for influencing others—can certainly influence his surroundings. It is just that the words must come from the heart, for then they enter the hearts of the listeners. And even though in the vast majority of cases the results are not immediately visible, the adage of our Nasi is well known: that there is a chazakah that propaganda [efforts to influence] does not return empty. This is especially true given that, even by your own admission, there are currently almost no G-d-fearing activists in your location.

Regarding what you write—that your firstborn son has reached the age of chinuch, while on the other hand your success with the community is in doubt:

The instruction of Chazal is well known in this regard as well: a person must do his part in accordance with the command of our holy Torah, the Torah of life. The command is, "You shall surely rebuke [your neighbor]..." [Vayikra 19:17], even to the point of reprimand, even to the point of striking. It is clear and simple that it is impossible for the fulfillment of one Torah mitzvah to cause damage, chas v'shalom, to the fulfillment of a second mitzvah—the mitzvah of "And you shall teach them to your children," the mitzvah of chinuch. On the contrary, one mitzvah leads to another. Especially since in this matter, there is also the principle of Hashem’s attribute of "measure for measure" (only many times over). When one brings others closer to the Torah of Hashem and His mitzvos, the Creator of the world will certainly grant him even greater success in bringing his own son closer to Torah and mitzvos.

May it be the will of Hashem that He guide you in the best way for you, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 440

440

B"H, 23 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letter of 5 Nissan, regarding your *cheshbon hanefesh* and the fact that you have come to the conclusion that you do not feel within yourself the levels of *avodah* and *yiras shamayim* commensurate with your Torah study.

It is well known that there is a teaching of our Sages (*Avodah Zarah* 19a) that there are two stages in Torah study: "He meditates in the Torah of Hashem" and "in His Torah"—the latter being the ultimate goal of study. Seemingly, one might ask: how is it possible for the "Torah of Hashem" to become "his Torah"? After all, there is no comparison whatsoever between the Giver of the Torah and the student of the Torah, between the Creator and the created. If it is impossible to pass an elephant through the eye of a needle (even in a dream), even though both are finite, how much more so is this true regarding the Creator, who is the true Infinite, and of whom it is said that He, His knowledge, His wisdom, and His Torah are one (as the Rambam elaborates on this at length, and as is explained in *Tanya*, specifically in *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah*). Rather, it is through the kindness of the Holy One, Blessed be He, who is all-powerful, and for whom nothing is impossible.

From this we can also understand that in order for the "Torah of Hashem" to become "his Torah," it is essential that one be an *oved Hashem*; study through the intellect alone is not sufficient at all. This is as the *Mechilta* (*Yisro*) states: "Accept My sovereignty, and afterwards you shall accept My decrees." And in *Berachos* (beginning of ch. 2), it is stated that **every day** one must first accept the **yoke** of the Kingdom of Heaven, and only afterwards the **yoke** of Torah and *mitzvos*.

From all of this, it is understood that if the preparation is not as described above [all of which is encapsulated in the brief adage of our Sages that the acceptance of the Torah was through the **precedence** of *naaseh* to *nishma*], and if the study is not conducted in this manner, then it lacks a true connection with the person studying. Consequently, its effect is not apparent. Nevertheless, so as not to negate the concept of free choice, one is permitted to study Torah and understand it if he is a person of intellect, as this is one of the ways of nature—similar to the teaching of our Sages (*Mishnah Avodah Zarah*, ch. 4) that "his world will be destroyed because of..." And especially since, according to the promise that "none shall be cast away from Him," the words of Torah will eventually work to return him to the desired path. But the tragedy is that this might happen in another *gilgul* (*Tanya*, end of ch. 39), and in the meantime, tens of years have been lost, etc.

The conclusion from all the above is that one must study Torah in purity (by being careful with *tevilas Ezra*) and with the prerequisite of *yiras shamayim* and the acceptance of the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven. And since, even after all this, one still requires *siyata d’shmaya*, there must also be the matter of "giving a *prutah* to a pauper." For then, according to the measure of the Holy One, Blessed be He—which is "measure for measure"—they grant him success in his study, regardless of whether he is poor or rich.

It is understood that it is impossible to explain everything necessary in a letter, but I hope that these few lines, small in quantity, will suffice if you study them as required.

You surely know of the three daily *shiurim* that are appropriate for every soul, established by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in the *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*, and that you keep them. In any event, you should keep them from here on in.

With blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

With blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

## 4244

B"H, 23 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from before the holiday of Pesach: it is clear, based on what is explained in several places, that the *cheshbon hanefesh* regarding which you write—that you have not accomplished anything and do not see results, etc.—stems from an impure source. As the test for this, brought down by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe (Rashab) *n.e.*, and transcribed in *Hayom Yom*, states: if this *cheshbon* interferes with your *avodah*, then the *baal davar* is involved. As is evident from your letter, this entire *shakla v’tarya* has resulted in a lowering of your spirits, and consequently, a weakening in your activities.

I have already written to several of *anash* that the ruling of our Torah, even in the *nigleh* of Torah regarding the *biur chametz* of the physical, is well known: a person must search for it, and if he finds it, he must burn it. Even if, with his own powers, he does not find it—and consequently has nothing to burn—he has nonetheless performed his *mitzvah* according to the *halacha*, because he did what was incumbent upon him. The Torah was not given to ministering angels. From this, it is understood that even if you were correct in your claims, you have still performed the *mitzvah* according to its *halacha*—the *mitzvah* of "You shall surely rebuke," and even more so, the *mitzvah* of "Love your fellow as yourself." Consequently, you must strive to improve him. And since it is **highly probable** that you are mistaken in your *cheshbon*, as mentioned above—and regarding this it is also said, "One action is better than a thousand sighs"—you should continue your activities in your environment. Since you are thereby fulfilling a *shlichus* from Above, for which nothing is impossible, eventually, things will work out in the desired direction.

Regarding what you write about the transfer of assets that the administrators require: it seems that this is also the custom in the United States. Those who enter to reside in such places and do not have a son or daughter are required to stipulate that after one hundred and twenty years, the assets will pass to the institution. Surely, their requirement does not extend to preventing one from giving gifts, etc., during one’s lifetime, for long and good years.

I trust you will inform me how you utilized the days of the holiday of Pesach, the time of our freedom. May it be the will [of Hashem] that it serves as good preparation for the upcoming holiday of Shavuos, as it is written: "When you bring the people out of Egypt, you shall serve Elokus on this mountain."

With blessings for good tidings.

#### ***4244***

**The test for this:** See also above, Letter 4017, and the references in the notes there.

**I have already written:** See above, Letter 4088.

## 4246

B"H, 24 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing and learned, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Boruch, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

It is surprising that for a long time there have been no letters or news from you, especially since your work is in the field of chinuch on the purity of holiness, teaching the children of Israel the Torah of Hashem, etc. It is already well-known that regarding matters of Torah in particular, in the language of the Zohar, one must "increase it every day." This is especially true when the teaching or the supervision of the students takes place in a Chassidishe institution, where the spirit of its founders and directors—our holy Nesi'im—hovers over them in a way that is both encompassing and internalized, with the teachers and mashgichim serving as the conduit through which these influences are drawn down. And a word to the wise is sufficient.

Regarding what you wrote concerning my opinion on the "erasing of the remembrance of Amalek," I wrote some time ago to the esteemed Rabbi, etc., R' Chaim Naeh, of blessed memory, regarding what appeared to me to be the case, and he included his opinion in the Luach HaKollel. It is based on a maamar of our Alter Rebbe (printed in Boneh Yerushalayim and cited in the sefer Ketzos HaShulchan, Part 4, by the aforementioned).

Regarding what you wrote about placing the tefillin shel yad case over the tefillin for the entire duration of davening in order to protect the corners—this is how I conduct myself. It is understood that the part of the case opposite the yud is cut out, so that the yud does not shift from the bayis, in accordance with the words of the holy Zohar. However, in the tefillin of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, this part (opposite the yud) is intact, from which it is understood that the case was not there during the duration of davening.

And surely the Rebbe (his father) also conducted himself in this manner.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write that you see a sign of blessing in your learning, but regarding the rectification of the known matter, it seems to you that there is no improvement in the situation.

Now, regarding the hidden ways of Hashem, etc., a person must do what is incumbent upon him. Furthermore, it is impossible that there is not some movement toward improving the situation. This is nothing other than the tactics of the yetzer hara, attempting to induce a sense of lowliness and despondency in order to prevent you from progressing in your avodah of Hashem. You should also study Tanya, Chapter 29 and onwards.

In any event, you should strive to completely divert your attention from the aforementioned matter, and even from its rectification, as much as possible. Instead, strive to increase your influence on others, bringing them closer to Torah and its mitzvos. Through this, you will increase the blessing of Hashem for your own progress, in accordance with the measure of the Ribono shel Olam—measure for measure—only many times over.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 450

B"H, 24 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

...With blessings for good tidings in both general and personal matters. It is understood that the "vineyard of Chabad" takes precedence over all else, for this is a mitzvah that cannot be performed by others—unlike a mitzvah that is not specifically in the category of "my own vineyard." The magnitude of the distinction here is understood from the words of our Sages, of blessed memory, that even "matters of Heaven"—meaning mitzvos—are not equivalent to even one word of Torah study. Therefore, [regarding] a mitzvah that can be performed by others, etc. [it is secondary to Torah study], but if it cannot be performed by others, it is not only equivalent, but it even takes precedence. It is a source of great wonder regarding many of anash that they do not contemplate this, even though there are many instructions from our Nesi'im regarding such matters; based on the above, this is also an explicit ruling in the revealed Torah.

With blessings.

## 4251

B"H, 24 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, occupied with communal needs, R' Yaakov, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

A matter regarding the laws of mezuzah has come to my attention, specifically when there is a contradiction between the "hinge side" (*heker tzir*) and the "majority of usage" (*rov tashmishem*). There is a tradition circulating among the elder Chassidim regarding the ruling of our holy Nasi on this (and some say it is from the Alter Rebbe). Since I have heard various versions of this here, I would be grateful if you could inform me what you have heard regarding this, the details of the version, etc. The more detailed, the better.

With blessing.

#### ***4251***

**R' Yaakov:** Landau. Additional letters to him appear above, Vol. 5, 1238, and in the references in the notes there.

**A matter has come to my attention:** See the letters above, 4227, 4237.

**Inform me:** In his response, he writes: "I merited, through the kindness of Hashem, that during all the time I took shelter in the shadow of the holy holiness [...] our Rebbe, of blessed memory, would call me each time he affixed mezuzos to accompany him, and he would teach me the order of their placement... This rule he transmitted to me in the name of the Rebbe Maharash—he never mentioned in this regard any tradition in the name of the Alter Rebbe—that for any door other than the primary entrance that is obligated in a mezuzah, one must consider only the hinge side (*heker tzir*). However, for the primary entrance itself, one affixes it on the right, even if it opens outward."

He added and related that in his apartment, before they added to it, there was a room—the room where he would later receive people for yechidus—where all the doors opened outward. The Rebbe Maharash himself affixed the mezuzos on all those doors according to the hinge side. This meant that, according to this, there was not a single door that was an "entrance" into the room. Our Rebbe asked his father, "If so, how will people enter?" To which his father, the Rebbe Maharash, replied: "What does that bother me? Let him jump through the window." See also what Rabbi Marz"sh Dworkin wrote regarding this in the book *Kovetz Raz"sh*, p. 57.

453

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After a very long interval, your letter was received, and I thank you for the good news regarding the improvement in your health.

Regarding what you wrote about the farbrengens, and that even to the physical eye they appear to bear fruit: they are not comparable to the true fruits, even though the yetzer hara confuses one with strange tactics, among them casting doubt on whether there is any benefit in a farbrengen, as its ways in this are explained in the maamarim of Chassidus and in the sichos.

...Regarding what you wrote about the words of the doctor treating you concerning your state of health, and how the work of... is difficult for you, especially when you are also occupied with the affairs of Chabad, and therefore you fear that you must reduce this involvement, etc.

It is astonishing that you apparently do not feel the double and redoubled darkness of the time of galus, even when it is pointed out to you with a finger. Moreover, you reach conclusions that are the opposite of what they should be, and which are also contrary to common sense. Had you contemplated what I wrote to you in my letter... and read them at the time of receiving the letter without the bribe of an incorrect desire, you would have seen then that the matter of... is not suitable for you now. But since I did not merit that my words be accepted, naturally a doctor came and told you the same as above, only in sharper terms. It is understood that he attributed the matter to the body and not to the soul. Not only did this also not help, but your honor—after asking your forgiveness—came to the **opposite** conclusion of the aforementioned intentions: that you must abandon even your participation until now in the affairs of Chabad, and only hold on to the affairs of...

I do not know if further words on this will add anything, after it has been pointed out and is being pointed out to you **with a finger** what you should be occupied with. May it be Hashem’s will that very soon, and with kindness and mercy, you will begin to fulfill your true role in the place where you are now—which was your role immediately upon your arrival there—and all other matters are secondary to the secondary. May you do this with joy and a good heart, for finally, one has grasped what is meant. Simply put, the matter of physical livelihood is not hidden from me either, but the yeshiva... has the ability to support you and your family with dignity. Furthermore, you will bring much more benefit than the salary you will receive. If only you had done this two or three years ago, when you were healthier physically and the entire environment was healthier spiritually. The matter depends on nothing but your own will.

With blessings for good news regarding all the above.

P.S.

It is not ruled out that, since this is a "worldly" matter, you will find several wise businessmen among Anash who will try to explain to you that my aforementioned opinion does not seem right to them, and that "it is not proper for a person of standing," etc. You have my permission to explain to them, and in my name as well: that in truth, my opinion is that **all** of Anash who came from Russia... should receive their livelihood in a direct manner through involvement in the yeshiva... (since in any case, the influence is drawn to them in the merit of the yeshiva; it is only that because they insisted on clothing their livelihood specifically in material garments, through negotiations in the marketplaces and streets with a terrifying distraction of the soul, naturally, further concealments and hidings are added, since the influence must descend through several more levels. Furthermore, waste is added, namely, unwanted expenses—such as doctors' bills, etc., G-d forbid). If only they, too, would at least now choose a livelihood in the aforementioned manner, the reduction of the concealments and hidings that would be added would suffice for their needs and those of their families—even their physical needs—with much satisfaction, not to mention less distraction of the soul. In addition to this, they would be investing their knowledge, strength, and energy in true matters. There is no need to elaborate on the **obvious**, except that the trouble is that one understands and explains when reading these things in a book, and even when explaining them regarding someone else, but when one begins to speak regarding oneself, all the reasoning and negotiation become as naught, and the wise will understand.

It is understood and simple that there is no element of strictness, etc., in any of the above, but finally, it is time to recognize the truth, even if it were only lying on the table, and certainly when it is emphasized and highlighted, as stated above.

With blessings for good news.

Brooklyn.

In response to your letter, as you requested, I will mention you and your family—may they live and be well—at the holy resting place of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May it be the will of Hashem that He fulfill your heart’s desires for the good, with sons, and that you raise them, together with your daughter—may she live—for Torah, the chuppah, and good deeds. Great is the merit of your involvement in the chinuch of the children of Yisrael in accordance with the purity of holiness, which will surely assist in the fulfillment of your aforementioned request, for the attribute of the Holy One, blessed be He, is "measure for measure," and whoever teaches his fellow’s son Torah or exerts himself in this, etc.

Regarding what you write concerning the friction that occurred between you and the teacher, and the father of one of the students—

While you are correct that it is necessary to maintain discipline and supervision, and consequently one must distance oneself from anything that weakens or undermines that, on the other hand, one must seek a path and a method whereby others, from the outside, can influence the aforementioned father to continue sending his son to the Talmud Torah (in a way that it will not be known that the initiative came from you, in order to preserve the discipline). Regarding this, too, it is said: "In the multitude of counselors there is salvation."

It is my hope, even though you do not mention it, that you participate in the farbrengens of anash—may they live and be well—which bring light and vitality to the study of Torah and the observance of mitzvos.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 4161

B.H., 28 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the avreich, the G-d-fearing, etc., Naftali, may he live, HaKohen.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter, in which you inform me of your holy work in guiding the children of Bnei Yisrael in yiras shamayim, through the study of Torah and the fulfillment of mitzvos: fortunate is your portion to have merited this, for the magnitude of the matter of bringing Bnei Yisrael closer to our Father in Heaven cannot be fully expressed. Regarding what you wrote concerning the curriculum you use with them, it is understood that it must include the study of the halachos required for the daily lives of those you influence. This must take precedence, as our Sages said, "The study is not the primary thing, but the deed." You can surely clarify which details are most necessary, and regarding this, too, it is said, "In the multitude of counselors there is salvation."

There is another point here: since the time you spend with them is limited, you must arouse in them a desire that even when they leave you, they will continue—in their homes or in the beis medrash—with the very matters you speak of and influence them with. This is achieved by starting a topic and telling them that the continuation can be found in such-and-such a sefer, in such-and-such a place, and the like. And since, as you have already written, you have succeeded in influencing some avreichim regarding the minhagei Chassidus, how much more so will you succeed in the aforementioned manner with those you influence.

Regarding what you wrote about wearing a tallis gadol before marriage: regarding such a matter, it is said that one should follow the custom of the environment in which one is located. However, it is obvious that nesias kapayim must be done while wearing a tallis, and I believe there are no differences of custom regarding this.

With a blessing to hear good news regarding all of the above.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

A. Quint
Secretary

It is obvious that sleep should be at night (according to both the revealed and the hidden Torah, and apparently also according to the nature of the world), and only in exceptional cases should there be a light sleep during the day (though this requires further study regarding what is written on this in the *Sefer Minhagei HaChatam Sofer*). Regarding Shabbos, see the *Shulchan Aruch* of our Rebbe, section 281, and *Pri Etz Chaim*, *Shaar HaShabbos*, chapter 1, and this requires further study.

The method of study should be appropriate to the order of the yeshiva where you are studying, and within that very framework—in accordance with the words of our Sages of blessed memory—in the place that one's heart desires.

## 4,268

B"H, 29 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In due time, I received the note from the *Anshei Maamad*, and I hope that since then, in accordance with the instruction of our Sages of blessed memory that "we elevate in matters of holiness"—meaning that one must increase in matters of holiness, specifically Torah and *mitzvos*—the same has been the case for you. This is the true growth of a Jew: not merely that months and years are added to the calendar, but that there is an increase in the 248 *mitzvos asei* (positive commandments), which correspond to the 248 limbs, and in the observance of the 365 *mitzvos lo saasei* (negative commandments), which correspond to the 365 sinews of a person—the limbs and sinews of the *neshamah*, and likewise the limbs and sinews of the body (*guf*). And as there is an increase in general health, as stated, Hashem Yisbarach adds His blessings in the areas where one is in need.

I hope it is superfluous to draw your attention to the absolute necessity in this time and in this generation, which has passed through so many storms, to also have a *kevius* (fixed time) for that part of Torah which strengthens *bitachon* in Hashem Yisbarach and helps one better fulfill the instruction of Hashem Yisbarach, "Serve Hashem with joy," and according to the language of the verse, "You shall serve Hashem your G-d with joy and goodness of heart." This is attained through the study of *Toras HaChassidus* (*Da"ch*). I would be grateful if you would inform me of good tidings regarding all that has been mentioned above.

With blessings,

P.S.
Surely you are aware of the *takanah* to recite *Tehillim* every day after *davening* in the morning, as the *Tehillim* is divided according to the days of the month. Hopefully, you will observe this from now on and moving forward.

## 4190

B"H, 29 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and industrious, engaged in communal affairs,
R' Yehoshua Shneur Zalman, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Your letter from the end of Adar was received in due time, and last week I also received a detailed personal report via your son-in-law, the esteemed R' Virdiger, may he live. The magnitude of the achievements you have been privileged to bring into reality in your location is beyond measure or adequate description. It is my hope that Anash in your area also perceive this—and not merely as a superficial observation, but in the sense brought in Chassidus: that a powerful, focused gaze leads to an internal stirring, to a yearning and a drive to increase these efforts to the fullest extent of one’s ability. Indeed, the success in the increased number of students is sufficient proof of all that has been said above, and it is beyond any doubt.

Regarding what you wrote about the limited time dedicated to holy studies: surely there are subjects in the curriculum labeled as secular studies that can be infused with holy content. For example, history should be taught through the lens of Tanach (Yehoshua, Shoftim, Shmuel, Divrei Hayamim, and the like). However, it is understood that this is not enough. Therefore, the approach you suggest is very sound: to lobby the Ministry of Education, based on the unique nature of the Yeshiva—especially since it is the only one of its kind in the entire country that provides a proper education in Torah and mitzvos. Since there is no other Yeshiva, it is imperative that even in the lower grades, as they serve as preparation for the higher grades, they must increase their holy studies.

Certainly, you must find connections (*bakantshaft*) within that Ministry, so that you will know the most effective way to phrase the request, and most importantly, so that your request will be granted. This is especially true since in the country of Australia, religious affairs also fall under the government (unlike in the United States), and consequently, they—the government—bear the responsibility to provide for the necessary requirements, particularly regarding the number of study hours. It is highly likely that letters from Rabbonim will be helpful in all of the above. It is understood that it is not always desirable to publicize this lobbying effort, as it is best not to alarm some of the parents by suggesting that the administration’s intention is to absolutely abolish secular studies. I rely on your discretion in this.

It is simple that there is no room at all for the idea of canceling the Talmud Torah for those who come after school hours, especially since, in any case, some of them will eventually begin studying in the Yeshiva before noon.

Regarding the question of administration in general, and the financial situation in particular: I believe I have already written about this a few times. All technical matters should be offloaded onto others as much as possible. On the other hand, you should be the head and the overseer of all matters that carry responsibility. In order for the oversight, management, and supervision to be as they should, it is proper that you not be distracted by technical matters—which includes even teaching a class that you happen to be mentioning, and certainly bookkeeping or writing receipts. Since your authority will be felt by them, it is not strictly necessary that these tasks be done by Anash, provided they are done by someone who will listen to your orders and instructions.

Regarding your question as to whether it is possible to open a department of the Yeshiva for girls in the aforementioned building: surely you must arrange matters so that there is no concern that the department will slip out of your control, and in that case, it is a proper thing.

I was pleased by what you wrote about hiring a teacher for the girls, etc. As for your question about whether to incorporate this into the Yeshiva’s operations and inform the board members, etc.—this should be judged according to the mood of the board members. Although, in general, it is correct that it should align with the truth—that this, too, is an activity of Anash—one should not alarm them by suggesting that expenses will increase in an extraordinary manner. In general, in our times, it makes the best impression when people see G-d-fearing individuals striving in the education of girls as well.

Regarding what you wrote about the involvement of Agudas N'shei Chabad in this: this is also correct, and perhaps it will engage them further in Chabad activities in general, and consequently, many of the members will become closer and closer.

With blessings for overwhelming success in all of the above, in good health and with high spirits appropriate to the state of affairs.

## 470

B”H, 29 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn

To the avreich Aharon, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letters of 24 Nissan (and the three preceding ones) with the Pidyon Nefesh enclosed therein, which was read today at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May it be the will of Hashem that just as you were the messenger to bring the request, the Almighty should grant success so that you will also be the messenger to bring good tidings regarding this.

I was pleased to read in your letter that you are preparing to utilize the upcoming Lag B’Omer in a special way. This year, it falls on a day when parents are free from their work and students from their secular studies. Consequently, it is worthwhile to make an effort to have their fellow students join them—meaning, even those who, for the time being, do not yet study at Oholei Yosef Yitzchok. The same applies to the special minyan you are organizing for the students; it is worth making an effort to ensure that those who do not yet study with them also attend. Naturally, you must arrange supervision in a way that, G-d forbid, those coming from the outside will not have a negative influence, and I am certain you will write about all of the above with the necessary detail.

With blessings for success in your holy work, through which success will surely increase in your personal matters as well.

The details are in accordance with the instruction of our Alter Rebbe, that through tzedakah, one’s mind and heart become refined a thousand times over (Torah Or, at the beginning). It has already been explained in other places that the aforementioned "thousand times" is not an exaggeration, but literally so (Hagahos HaTzemach Tzedek, ibid.).

With blessing.

I am sure you are continuing with the chazarah of Chassidus, for it is a very proper thing (and surely it also influences the attitude toward you on the part of the students of Oholei Yosef Yitzchok).

Organizing a summer camp is very, very necessary (and in time, it may also become a source of income)...

## 4271

B"H, 29 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Kfar Chabad,
May they live,

Peace and Blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the minutes from the meetings held on 26 Shevat, 15 Adar, and 5 Nissan. Thank G-d, it appears that matters are beginning to move in the right direction. May it be His will that this proceed quickly and without any delays, concealments, or obstructions, both in material and spiritual matters.

You do not mention details regarding the method of constructing the mikveh, but from your letter it is evident that it is in an old building, etc., and I am concerned that you might not be paying sufficient attention to the external appearance of the mikveh and the surrounding rooms. It is already well known how meticulous our holy Rebbes, the Nesi'im, were in such matters, for the internal essence and the core of the matter depend upon this externality. It would be worthwhile to consult specifically with experts in such improvements regarding this issue, and you should endeavor to ensure that, as much as possible, even the exterior is of the highest quality and even beautiful. Needless to say, this applies to cleanliness (which depends to a significant degree on the appropriate materials for the flooring and walls, etc.), which is not merely an external matter but an internal one as well...

I was pleased to read that you saw tangible success in the Purim celebration in Kfar Chabad. May it be His will that the success in other matters also be tangible, which will naturally lead to increased courage and effort in the other affairs of the Kfar. In connection with this, I will once again raise what I have already written: that in connection with every celebration, you should also arrange matters of sustenance in the Kfar, such as providing refreshments, fruits, etc., for the guests who arrive (since they spend several hours in the Kfar), and the like. With some reflection, you can surely expand this framework, and there will be great spiritual benefit in this, beyond the material benefit—even though the saying is well known: "Someone else's material is, for me, spirituality..."

I am certain that you baked matzah shemurah in the Kfar, and I am interested in knowing the details regarding this and the success you had with it.

With a blessing for success in your holy work, through which success will also be drawn down in your personal affairs, and for each and every one who exerts themselves in this, he and his entire household, may they live.

#### ***4271***

**What I have already written:** See Letter 4105.

## D'Reb

B"H, 29 Nissan, 5716
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, occupied with communal needs, R' Eliezer, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from the conclusion of the festival of Pesach and thereafter; likewise, your letters from the 9th of Shevat and the one preceding it were received in due time. And since we have just emerged from the days of the festival of Pesach, the time of our freedom—freedom in the sense of our Torah, the Torah of life, which is the Torah of truth—may it be the will of Hashem that very soon you will bring good tidings that, in good health and with peace of mind, you are increasing your shiurim in the study of our Torah, both in Nigleh and in Chassidus. And may you also have a "good eye" regarding others, to inspire them as well in these studies, in accordance with the well-known adage, "May your springs spread outward," and may we speedily merit the fulfillment of the promise that "the Master is coming"—the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With blessings for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

*D'Reb*

**R' Eliezer:** Krasik, Tel Aviv. Additional letters to him—see above 3908, and the references in the footnotes there.
